# M04 Phase 9 — Cluster Synthesis — structural input

**Date:** 2026-05-19
**Cluster:** M04 — Joy, Gladness and Delight

---

## §1 — Cluster overview

M04 (Joy, Gladness and Delight) holds 7 inner-being characteristics:

| Char | Short name | One-line definition |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Exultation | The soul's active, surging, triumphant inner state directed at what is glorious or transcendent — above all at God. |
| 2 | Joy | The active inner experience of rejoicing — the soul's engaged, participatory delight in what is worth celebrating. |
| 3 | Gladness | The inner state of settled, warm, positive brightness — the heart that is glad, the soul whose inner condition is light and well. |
| 4 | Delight | The inner state of treasuring and taking pleasure in a specific object — the soul's resting satisfaction in what it loves. |
| 5 | Pleasure | The inner-being experience of pleasantness — the felt quality of agreeableness received from persons, relationships, creation, and material or sensory experience. |
| 6 | Wonder | The inner state of astonishment and awe before what exceeds ordinary comprehension — the soul arrested and overwhelmed by what it cannot fully grasp. |
| 7 | Suffering-Joy | The paradoxical inner capacity to find genuine joy in and through suffering — not merely alongside it, not despite it, but as an inner state that suffering itself produces or occasions. |

Each characteristic produced 189 findings in its Phase 9 batch (1,323 rows total in `cluster_finding`).

---

## §2 — Confirmed cluster observations (with resolution notes)

These four observations were raised at characteristic-mapping time and confirmed during Phase 9. They name the boundaries already validated and are direct inputs to the synthesis.

### Observation #1 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 2)

**Title:** Joy/Gladness inter-relationship within M04-B and M04-C

**Description:**

> M04-B (Communal/Festive Rejoicing) and M04-C (NT Joy in Christ) carry BOTH the active-rejoicing register (Joy, Characteristic 2) and the settled-warm register (Gladness, Characteristic 3) within their verse corpora. The characteristic map assigns these sub-groups to Joy as their dominant phenomenon; the Gladness dimension within them is expected to emerge from VCG-level analysis. This inter-relationship between Joy and Gladness is anticipated as one of the significant findings of Phase 9 for M04.

**Confirmed resolution:**

> CONFIRMED via Char 2 Phase 9 self-check. The Joy/Gladness boundary surfaces as one of the most significant analytical findings of Characteristic 2's Phase 9. Evidence: (a) sa.mach and sim.chah appear in close synonymous parallelism throughout M04-B; (b) the formulaic "joy and gladness" pairing is the most common co-occurrence pattern; (c) the boundary is clearest at the extremes (Hab 3:18 type Joy is not Gladness; Lam 3:26 type Gladness is not Joy) and most porous in the middle register. To be primary finding in Session D cluster-scope synthesis.

---

### Observation #2 — SPLIT_SUBGROUP (cluster-wide)

**Title:** M04-E serves both Characteristic 2 (Joy) and Characteristic 7 (Suffering-Joy)

**Description:**

> M04-E (Promised and Eschatological Joy) carries two distinct registers within its 35-verse corpus. Its eschatological forward-rejoicing register (sa.s.von — gladness promised as reversal of sorrow) belongs under Characteristic 2 — Joy. Its NT suffering-paradox register (agalliao — rejoicing in trials; joy that suffering itself occasions) belongs under Characteristic 7 — Suffering-Joy. The VCG structure within M04-E will show which VCGs serve which characteristic. Phase 9 should apply the 189 prompts to M04-E under both Characteristic 2 and Characteristic 7 separately, where the evidence permits.

**Confirmed resolution:**

> CONFIRMED via Char 2 Phase 9 self-check. The split is validated by the evidence: M04-E-VCG-01 (sa.s.von corpus - OT restoration joy) belongs to Char 2 as eschatological-Joy register; M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao - NT exulting-beyond-circumstance) belongs to Char 7 (Suffering-Joy) in its paradox-of-joy-in-suffering register. Several verses (1Pe 1:8; Mat 5:12; Rev 19:7) carry evidence for both characteristics simultaneously. Char 7 Phase 9 should treat M04-E-VCG-02 as primary evidence base.

---

### Observation #3 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 4)

**Title:** Delight's breadth — affective/volitional/obedience/relational/corrupt inter-relationships

**Description:**

> Characteristic 4 (Delight) spans five sub-groups (M04-G affective, M04-H volitional, M04-M obedience, M04-N relational, M04-P corrupt) covering 247 verses. The inter-relationships between these registers — particularly between M04-G (affective delight in God) and M04-H (volitional delight as directed will) — are expected to be analytically significant in Phase 9. The single characteristic carries both the soul's affective orientation toward what is treasured and the will's directed pleasure; Phase 9 should examine how these dimensions of the same characteristic relate.

**Confirmed resolution:**

> CONFIRMED via Char 4 Phase 9 self-check; the breadth-integration surfaced as the central analytical finding of the batch. (a) M04-G affective and M04-H volitional are not separate but the affective and volitional faces of a single orientation-toward-object (Psa 37:4; 40:8; Rom 7:22 show the integration in single instances). (b) M04-M obedience is M04-H's directed will operating in the obedience-toward-God register (Joh 8:29 fully integrates M04-H and M04-M in Christ). (c) M04-P corrupt operates through the same faculty as the healthy registers (Isa 66:3 nephesh + cha.phets) - corruption is a question of object, not faculty. Delight is the most volitionally-constituted and agentively-powerful characteristic in M04; Isa 53:10's cha.phets makes divine Delight the inner mechanism of the atonement.

---

### Observation #4 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 3)

**Title:** M04-L evaluative-cognitive face integrates with M04-O circumstantial under Gladness

**Description:**

> M04-L (Evaluative Goodness) and M04-O (Circumstantial Gladness) together form Characteristic 3 — Gladness. M04-L is the cognitive face (the soul's inner appraisal that something is good — the assessment that produces and expresses gladness); M04-O is the experiential face (the warm inner response to beneficial circumstance). Phase 9 findings for M04-L should be integrated with M04-O's findings under Characteristic 3, recognising these together name the cognitive + experiential aspects of one inner-being characteristic.

**Confirmed resolution:**

> CONFIRMED via Char 3 Phase 9 self-check. Integration surfaced as the structural key to Char 3: M04-L cognitive-evaluative (Mic 6:8, Gen 1:31 ontological baseline) + M04-O experiential-circumstantial together form Gladness. The evaluative act (M04-L) produces the cognitive recognition that enables and grounds the experiential warmth (M04-O). Char 3 is the most cognitively-constituted positive characteristic in M04 - distinguished from Joy / Exultation / Delight / Pleasure by its unique cognitive-evaluative primary dimension. Status: analytically validated.

---

## §3 — Per-prompt synthesis matrix

For each of the 189 prompts (T0.1.1 … T7.3.4), the 7 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim below. Read all 7 before authoring the cluster-scope row in your output.

### T0

#### T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected

##### T0.1.1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The verse evidence directly attributes exultation to God himself, revealing it as a genuine divine characteristic before it is a human one. God rejoices over restored Israel with gladness (Zep 3:17 — su.s and gil_verb: "he will rejoice over you with gladness; he will exult over you with loud singing"), takes delight in prospering his people (Deu 30:9 — su.s), rejoices in Jerusalem (Isa 65:19 — gil_verb and su.s), delights in doing Israel good with all his heart and soul (Jer 32:41 — su.s), and rejoices over Zion as a bridegroom over a bride (Isa 62:5 — su.s). This evidence reveals God as a being whose inner life includes triumphant, exultant delight — his exultation is not incidental but flows from his relational investment in his people and the restoration of right order. The human capacity for exultation reflects this divine character: the person who exults in YHWH images the God who exults over his people.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence explicitly attributes Joy to God across multiple registers. God is named as the one who produces and multiplies Israel's joy (Isa 9:3 — "you have increased its joy; they rejoice before you"); creates Jerusalem to be a joy and her people a gladness (Isa 65:18 — gi.lah); rejoices in his people's festive songs (Judg 9:13 — "wine that cheers God and men"); rejoices over his people with gladness (Zep 3:17 — sim.chah); rejoices in Jerusalem (Isa 65:19 — sa.mach); and rejoices over the repentant sinner (Luk 15:7 — "more joy in heaven"; Luk 15:10 — "joy before the angels of God"). In the Johannine corpus, Jesus has his own joy (Joh 15:11 — "my joy may be in you") and declares his joy fulfilled in the disciples (Joh 17:13). The evidence reveals God as a being whose inner life participates in Joy — he rejoices over his people, over restored covenant, and over recovered sinners. Joy is not merely a human response to God but a divine inner state that God himself inhabits and directs toward his creation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The M04-L-VCG-01 corpus (32 verses) is the most concentrated evidence for Gladness as a divine attribute. God's evaluative-goodness declarations across Gen 1:4–31 (seven "God saw that it was good / very good" appraisals) reveal God as a being whose inner life includes the capacity to perceive, assess, and register gladness/satisfaction in what is genuinely good. Beyond creation: God is declared good in character ("good and upright" — Psa 25:8; "good and forgiving" — Psa 86:5; "The Lord is good to all, and his mercy is over all that he has made" — Psa 145:9; "The Lord is good, a stronghold in the day of trouble" — Nah 1:7). The ki-tov declarations throughout the Psalms (100:5; 106:1; 107:1; 118:1, 29; 135:3; 136:1) establish God's goodness as an intrinsic character attribute, not a situational response. Gladness is the inner state of one who recognises and inhabits what is genuinely good — and God's character is the archetype of that goodness. In M04-O: God's covenantal goodness produces Gladness in the people (Neh 2:18 — God's good hand upon Nehemiah becomes the testimony that stirs communal resolve; Ezr 6:22 — "the Lord had made them joyful" at the Feast of Unleavened Bread). God is the origin and exemplar of the Gladness the characteristic describes.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The evidence reveals Delight as a profoundly divine characteristic across three registers: (1) **Volitional-sovereign delight** — M04-H-VCG-01 establishes that God's delight is his sovereign will operating without external constraint: "Our God is in the heavens; he does all that he pleases" (Psa 115:3); "whatever the Lord pleases, he does, in heaven and on earth" (Psa 135:6); Isa 46:10 — "My counsel shall stand, and I will accomplish all my purpose" (che.phets); Isa 55:11 — God's word accomplishes what he purposes. Divine delight and divine sovereignty are identical: God's inner pleasure is the operative principle of all his acts; (2) **Relational delight in persons** — M04-H-VCG-02 shows God's delight directed personally and redemptively: "he rescued me, because he delighted in me" (Psa 18:19; 2Sa 22:20); God delighted in Solomon and set him on the throne (1Ki 10:9; 2Ch 9:8); Isa 62:4 — God's delight in Zion becomes her new name; "I have no pleasure in the death of the wicked, but that the wicked turn and live" (Eze 18:23; 33:11); God delights in steadfast love, justice, and righteousness (Jer 9:24); "he delights in steadfast love" (Mic 7:18); (3) **Affective delight in God's own word and wisdom** — Pro 8:30–31 — Wisdom was daily God's delight before creation; Jer 31:20 — Ephraim is God's "darling child," sha.a.shu.im, his cherished treasured one; Mat 3:17; 12:18; 17:5; Mar 1:11; Luk 3:22; 2Pe 1:17 — "this is my beloved Son, with whom I am well pleased" (eudokeo at baptism and transfiguration); Mat 12:18 — "my soul is well pleased" — delight located in God's own soul directed toward the Son.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Three divine registers: (1) **Divine beauty as Pleasure** — Psa 27:4 names the no.am (beauty/pleasantness) of the Lord himself as the supreme object the psalmist seeks — "to gaze upon the beauty of the Lord and to inquire in his temple"; the pleasantness is an intrinsic quality of God's own being, not merely of his acts; (2) **Divine responsive Pleasure at worship** — M04-K-VCG-01 (the ni.cho.ach corpus, 38 verses) reveals God as one who receives the soothing aroma of correctly-offered sacrifice with inward satisfaction; Gen 8:21 — "the Lord smelled the pleasing aroma, the Lord said in his heart" — God's inner response to Noah's offering is a settling, calming pleasure that moves him to covenant resolve; Num 28:2 — "my pleasing aroma" — God describes the offering as his own food, claiming the pleasure-relation personally; (3) **Divine covenantal pleasantness as character** — Psa 36:8 names "the river of your delights" as flowing from God himself; Psa 90:17 — "the favor/pleasantness of the Lord our God be upon us" — divine pleasantness as gracious character directed outward toward the community; Zec 11:7, 10 — the shepherd's staff named No'am (Pleasantness/Favour) representing the quality of divine covenantal grace toward the flock.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the most explicitly theocentric characteristic in M04 — virtually the entire M04-I-VCG-01 corpus (61 verses) is a catalogue of divine acts that produce wonder. The evidence reveals three dimensions of God's character: (1) **God as the exclusive worker of wonders** — Psa 72:18 ("who alone does wondrous things"); Psa 86:10 ("you are great and do wondrous things; you alone are God") — Wonder is not a response to a powerful class of beings but is uniquely and exclusively evoked by the one God; (2) **God's acts exceed human comprehension** — Job 5:9; 9:10 ("great things and unsearchable, marvellous things without number"); Job 37:5 ("God thunders wondrously… great things that we cannot comprehend"); Psa 40:5 ("they are more than can be told") — the incomprehensibility of God's acts is constitutive of Wonder; (3) **God's name as Wonderful** — Isa 9:6 ("his name shall be called Wonderful Counselor") — the coming child's identity inherently evokes awe; Wonder is an essential quality of Christ's being, not merely a reaction to his deeds.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two primary evidences for the divine dimension of Suffering-Joy: (1) **Jesus' agalliao in the Holy Spirit** — Luk 10:21 ("In that same hour he rejoiced in the Holy Spirit and said, 'I thank you, Father...'") — this is the clearest instance of the characteristic operating in the divine-human person; Jesus' exultation occurs in the context of the disciples having been exposed to opposition and the suffering of itinerant ministry; his Spirit-located rejoicing is not despite the context of difficulty but in and through it; (2) **Heb 12:2** — "for the joy that was set before him [he] endured the cross, despising the shame" — the cross is the suffering context; the joy set before Christ is the eschatological ground that enabled endurance of suffering. Together these reveal God's own inner life as encompassing the capacity to hold joy and suffering together without the suffering cancelling the joy. The characteristic reflects the divine image as the capacity to inhabit genuine rejoicing when circumstances press against it, because the inner being is grounded in a reality that transcends circumstances.

---

##### T0.1.2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, explicitly and repeatedly. Deu 28:63 shows God taking delight in ruin as he formerly took delight in doing Israel good (su.s); Deu 30:9 shows God again taking delight in prospering the restored (su.s); Isa 62:5 portrays God's delight in Zion as a bridegroom's delight (su.s); Isa 65:19 has God rejoicing in Jerusalem (gil_verb + su.s); Jer 32:41 locates God's rejoicing in doing good "with all my heart and all my soul" (su.s); Zep 3:17 pairs God's rejoicing (gil_verb) and exulting (su.s) over his restored people with gladness and loud singing. The attribution reveals that exultation is not a merely creaturely emotion but participates in the divine life — when the human person exults in God, they are responding with the same category of inner state that God exercises toward them. This makes exultation a fundamentally relational and reciprocal characteristic: God exults over his people; his people exult in him.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, explicitly and extensively. Beyond the references in T0.1.1: God gives joy directly into the heart (Psa 4:7 — "you have put more joy in my heart"); makes people joyful (Ezr 6:22 — "the Lord had made them joyful"); is himself the source of fullness of joy (Psa 16:11 — "in your presence there is fullness of joy"); commissions Jesus to carry joy (Heb 12:2 — "for the joy that was set before him"); and God as the master whose joy the faithful servant enters (Mat 25:21, 23). The attribution reveals that Joy is not incidental or peripheral in God's inner life but is bound up with his covenantal relationship with his people, his redemptive purpose, and his own eschatological gladness at restoration. For the human person, this means Joy is not merely an emotional bonus but an image-bearing capacity — the person who rejoices genuinely participates in a mode of being that God himself inhabits.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, explicitly and foundationally. Gen 2:18 — "it is not good that the man should be alone" — God evaluates and declares a deficiency; this is the evaluative-gladness faculty operating in its negative register: the good that is absent is recognised and named. The Gen 1 series (VCG-01) is the positive register: God perceives and declares goodness in what he has made. Psa 119:68 — "you are good and do good" — explicitly joins divine being-good (ontological Gladness-quality) and doing-good (action arising from it), a model the programme observation OBS-026 identifies as the being/doing pattern. Neh 9:20 — "you gave your good Spirit to instruct them" — the Spirit's quality of goodness is an attribute of the divine Gladness-character extended outward. The attribution reveals: Gladness in its evaluative-cognitive form (the recognition and declaration of what is truly good) is first God's own inner act before it is the human person's. The human capacity for Gladness-as-evaluative-recognition is an image-bearing participation in God's own goodness-perceiving inner life.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, more extensively and programmatically than any other M04 characteristic. The attributions span five different registers: (1) God's sovereign volitional delight (Psa 115:3; 135:6; Isa 44:28; 46:10; 53:10; 55:11; Ecc 8:3; Jon 1:14) — his pleasure is his will; (2) God's relational delight in persons (Psa 18:19; 22:8; 37:23; 41:11; Num 14:8; 1Ki 10:9; Isa 62:4; Deu 30:9) — his pleasure motivates rescue, exaltation, and restoration; (3) God's moral delight — what he takes pleasure in and what he does not: "you delight in truth in the inward being" (Psa 51:6); "God does not delight in wickedness" (Psa 5:4); he takes no pleasure in sacrifice without inner transformation (Psa 40:6; 51:16; Isa 1:11; Heb 10:6, 8); he delights in steadfast love rather than sacrifice (Hos 6:6; Jer 9:24; Mic 7:18); (4) God's trinitarian delight — the Father's soul well pleased with the Son (Mat 12:18; eudokeo — the most explicit soul-location of divine Delight in Scripture); (5) God's creative delight — Wisdom as God's daily delight before creation (Pro 8:30); Jer 31:20's cherishing of Ephraim as a darling child. The breadth of attribution reveals: Delight is not incidental to God's character but is the integrating inner disposition that drives his will, his relational choices, his moral preferences, and his creative pleasure. Human Delight is a participation in the most comprehensive and fundamental feature of the divine inner life evidenced in M04.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, in two primary registers: (1) **God's being as pleasant/beautiful** — Psa 27:4 (no.am as God's own character-quality perceptible in worship); Psa 36:8 (river of delights flowing from God); (2) **God's inner responsive pleasure at worship** — Gen 8:21 (God's heart moved by the soothing aroma); the entire ni.cho.ach corpus of M04-K-VCG-01 names an inner divine state of calmed, settled reception — God experiences the pleasing aroma as genuinely soothing to his regard. The attribution reveals: human Pleasure as the soul's positive receptive response to what is pleasant is grounded in a God who himself experiences pleasantness in his own being and in rightly-directed worship. The human capacity for pleasure in beautiful persons, agreeable speech, and material goodness images back the divine pleasure in his own beauty and in worship that is rightly offered.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is not directly attributed to God as a characteristic God himself possesses in this corpus — rather, God's deeds and character are the objects that produce Wonder in those who encounter them. The partial exception: Zec 8:6 ("if it is marvellous in the sight of the remnant… should it also be marvellous in my sight, declares the Lord?") — God distances himself from the wonder-response, implying his own perspective transcends wonder rather than experiencing it. Isa 9:6's "Wonderful" (pe.le) as a name/title for the coming child is closest to attributing Wonder-quality to God, but this names his character as wonder-inducing rather than as one who experiences wonder. The attribution reveals: in Scripture, Wonder is primarily a human response to God rather than a divine characteristic — it belongs to creatures confronting the incomprehensible Creator.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, most fully in the person of Christ. Heb 12:2 names the joy set before Christ as the ground of his endurance of the cross — the divine-human person exercises Suffering-Joy in its purest form: suffering as extreme as crucifixion held alongside and through joy set before him. Luk 10:21's Jesus rejoicing in the Holy Spirit acknowledges the hiddenness of kingdom realities from the world (a form of the disciples' vulnerability/suffering in the mission context) while exulting. The attribution reveals: Suffering-Joy is not merely a human coping mechanism for unfortunate circumstances but participates in the divine inner life as Christ exercised it — the capacity to hold eschatological joy as more real and determinative than present suffering. For the human person, Suffering-Joy is an image-bearing participation in Christ's own suffering-to-glory pattern.

---

##### T0.1.3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, what does that silence suggest about the characteristic's place in the divine image?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Scripture is not silent; it is explicit. There is no silence to interpret. The opposite observation is more significant: the breadth and intensity of divine exultation in the evidence — spanning six distinct passages, employing two primary terms (su.s, gil_verb), and grounding the divine exultation in relational faithfulness and restorative action — suggests that exultation is among the most fully attested divine inner states across the characteristic's corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Scripture is not silent — divine joy is extensively evidenced. The more significant silence is in the VCG-06 (inverted/corrupt/absent joy) register: God's withdrawal of joy from the community (Deu 28:47; Hos 2:11; Jer 7:34; 16:9; 25:10; Joe 1:16) is the silencing of what God himself possesses and intended — the removal of the community's joy is shown as the most complete act of covenantal judgment precisely because joy belongs to the life God designed. The absence of divine joy toward a people (Isa 9:17 — "the Lord does not rejoice over their young men") is itself a severe verdict. The evidence thus shows divine joy as the norm and its absence or withholding as the exception under judgment.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Scripture is not silent on divine goodness — it is extensively evidenced. The more analytically significant observation is the asymmetry within the corpus: M04-L-VCG-01 (divine character goodness) has 32 verses, making God the subject of goodness more prominently than any sub-group's human subject. This dominance reveals that Gladness-as-evaluative-recognition of the good is not primarily a human characteristic that God also happens to possess; it is a divine attribute that humans reflect. The human evaluative-gladness of M04-L-VCG-02 (moral appraisal of persons and actions) is the image-bearing participation in what God first exercises. No silence; instead, a positive finding about origination.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

Scripture is not silent; divine Delight is the most extensively attributed characteristic in this cluster. The analytically significant observation is not silence but selectivity: God explicitly withholds delight in specific contexts (ritual sacrifice without inner transformation, wickedness, faithlessness — Psa 5:4; 40:6; Isa 1:11; Mal 1:10; Heb 10:6–8) and explicitly directs it toward others (steadfast love, justice, righteousness, the Son, repentant persons). The pattern of divine delight and divine withholding-of-delight together reveal that Delight is a morally structured characteristic in God's inner life — not indiscriminate pleasure but directed toward genuine goodness and relational faithfulness.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The evidence is not silent about divine Pleasure — but the divine pleasantness is more restricted in scope than the human. God's ni.cho.ach pleasure at worship is bounded by covenant conditions: Lev 26:31 ("I will not smell your pleasing aromas") shows divine Pleasure withheld from disobedient worship; Eze 20:41's future-oriented "as a pleasing aroma I will accept you" shows it restorable. The bounded quality of divine Pleasure at worship reveals that divine pleasantness is morally structured — it responds to genuinely correct worship and withdraws from its corruption (M04-P-VCG-01's misdirected ni.cho.ach). The human capacity for Pleasure has the same bounded quality: genuine pleasantness is appropriate to right objects; misapplied, it becomes luxury-curse (Deu 28:54–56) or illicit indulgence (Pro 9:17).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The near-silence about God experiencing Wonder is analytically significant. Zec 8:6's rhetorical question ("should it also be marvellous in my sight?") implies God does not stand in wonder at his own deeds — he is their originator and therefore understands them fully. Wonder is the creature's response to encountering what exceeds its comprehension; God is not a creature and does not encounter incomprehensible reality. The silence reveals Wonder as characteristically creaturely: it is the inner response appropriate to finite beings encountering the infinite. The human person who wonders is exercising a characteristically creaturely capacity — the capacity to be genuinely overwhelmed by what is greater than oneself — which is an image-bearing capacity but not one God exercises in the same way.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The silence in the M04-E-VCG-01 sa.s.von restoration corpus (which is primarily about God reversing suffering rather than God experiencing suffering-with-joy) is analytically significant: the OT does not primarily present God as experiencing suffering-that-he-rejoices-through; rather, God is the one who reverses suffering. The characteristic in its paradoxical form (joy through suffering, not merely after it) emerges most fully in the NT through Christ's incarnate suffering and the Spirit's enabling of the church under persecution. This is not silence about the characteristic's divine grounding but about its location — Suffering-Joy's divine archetype is the incarnate Christ, not the transcendent Creator.

---

#### T0.2 — Created Purpose

##### T0.2.1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence consistently shows exultation functioning as the appropriate inner response of the created person to the reality of God's reign, salvation, and presence. Psa 2:11 commands "rejoice with trembling" before the enthroned Lord; Psa 32:11 commands the upright in heart to be glad in the Lord and rejoice; Psa 97:1 calls the earth to rejoice because "the Lord reigns." The purpose exultation serves is alignment: it orients the whole inner being — soul (Psa 35:9), heart (Psa 13:5; 32:11; Zec 10:7), whole being (Psa 16:9) — toward God as its rightful object. Exultation is the inner-being mechanism by which the human person participates in the truth of God's sovereignty and goodness. It equips the person to live from a true account of reality.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence reveals multiple created purposes: (1) **Alignment with God's reality** — joy is the appropriate inner response to divine sovereignty and goodness; the commanded feast-rejoicings (Deu 12:7, 12, 18; 16:11, 14, 15; 26:11; 27:7; Lev 23:40) establish rejoicing before God as the designed posture of the covenant community in God's presence; (2) **Relational completion** — Deu 24:5 (the husband exempted from military service to make his wife glad) shows that joy serves the completion of human relational bonds; Pro 10:1; 15:20; 23:24–25; 29:3 (wise children gladding parents) show joy functioning as the inner fruit of right-ordered human relationships; (3) **Communal cohesion** — M04-D (sunchairo) shows joy functioning as the mechanism of communal solidarity — the body that co-rejoices is the body that is bound together; (4) **Worship** — joy is the inner quality that animates and is the purpose of worship; Deu 28:47 makes failure to serve with joyfulness and gladness of heart the root cause of judgment, revealing joy as the designed inner disposition of the worshipper; (5) **Sustained engagement with life** — the Ecclesiastes evidence (Ecc 8:15; 9:7; 11:8–9) shows joy commended as the inner companion of mortal life across its whole span.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The evidence reveals three created purposes: (1) **Moral orientation** — M04-L-VCG-02 shows Gladness-as-evaluation guiding decisions, conduct, and community life (Jethro's assessment of Moses, Exo 18:17; Naomi's assessment of Ruth's best course, Rut 2:22; the repeated "not good" verdicts on injustice in Proverbs). The evaluative faculty equips the person to navigate moral reality accurately; (2) **Relational assessment** — M04-L-VCG-02 includes comparative evaluations of relational worth (Rut 4:15 — Ruth's love surpassing seven sons; 2Sa 18:3 — David's worth ten thousand soldiers) — the faculty serves honest relational perception; (3) **Receptive recognition of circumstantial goodness** — M04-O shows Gladness as the soul's warm inner response to genuinely good news, beneficial states, and received blessedness (Pro 12:25 — good word counteracting anxiety; Pro 15:30 — good news refreshing bones; Neh 2:18 — God's good hand motivating communal action). The characteristic equips the person to recognise and receive the good when it is genuinely present.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The evidence reveals four created purposes: (1) **Alignment of the will with what is genuinely good** — Psa 40:8 ("I delight to do your will, O my God; your law is within my heart") — the will directed by Delight toward God's law enables natural, willing obedience rather than reluctant compliance; 1Ch 28:9 — "a willing mind" as the right orientation for serving God; (2) **Sustaining the inner person through adversity** — Psa 119:92 ("if your law had not been my delight, I would have perished in my affliction") — Delight in God's word is a life-preserving inner resource; similarly Psa 119:77, 143 — delight sustains through trouble and anguish; (3) **Orienting the inner being toward its proper object** — Psa 37:4 ("delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart") — Delight in God aligns the will with his giving, restructuring what the heart desires; (4) **Equipping moral discernment** — Psa 1:2 ("his delight is in the law of the Lord, and on his law he meditates day and night") — the delight-in-law faculty drives the sustained engagement that produces wisdom; the Preacher who "sought to find words of delight" (Ecc 12:10) names the inner faculty as a vehicle for discovering and expressing truth.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Three created purposes: (1) **Receiving the goodness of creation and persons** — M04-J-VCG-02 shows Pleasure as the soul's receptive faculty for what is genuinely agreeable: wisdom pleasant to the soul (Pro 2:10), wisdom's ways as pleasantness (Pro 3:17), gracious words nourishing soul and body (Pro 16:24), the beloved's beauty received in wonder (Song 1:16; 7:6), Jonathan's companionship deeply pleasant (2Sa 1:26) — the human person is equipped to register and receive genuine agreeableness; (2) **Rightly ordering the pursuit of material good** — M04-K-VCG-03 (the wisdom better-than comparatives) shows the faculty of Pleasure being trained in wisdom to prefer modest integrity over corrupt abundance (Psa 37:16; Pro 15:16, 17; 16:32; 17:1) — the wise person's Pleasure is properly calibrated toward what is genuinely good, not merely materially satisfying; (3) **Participation in right worship** — M04-K-VCG-01 shows Pleasure as the relational mechanism of correct sacrifice: the ni.cho.ach that rises to God and evokes his inner settled reception is the human person's rightly-directed worship-expression participating in a genuine relational exchange.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Three created purposes: (1) **Acknowledgment of God's incomparable greatness** — Exo 15:11 ("who is like you, O Lord, among the gods? Who is like you, majestic in holiness, awesome in glorious deeds, doing wonders?") — Wonder is the appropriate inner acknowledgment of God's incomparability; the person who genuinely wonders at God's deeds is rightly calibrated about the relation between Creator and creature; (2) **Worship and praise as the overflow of Wonder** — Psa 9:1 ("I will recount all of your wonderful deeds" — alongside wholehearted thanks); 1Ch 16:24 ("declare his glory among the nations, his marvellous works") — Wonder produces proclamation and praise; (3) **Cognitive humility before the incomprehensible** — Job 42:3 ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — Job's recognition that he spoke of what he could not comprehend; Wonder's purpose is to keep the human mind appropriately humble before what exceeds it (Psa 131:1 — "I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me").

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The evidence presents Suffering-Joy as primarily a **response-to-fallen-condition** capacity rather than an original-creation capacity (see T0.2.2) — it equips the person to: (1) **Maintain inner-being coherence under persecution** — Mat 5:12 ("rejoice and be glad, for your reward is great in heaven") equips the persecuted to sustain their inner orientation despite suffering; (2) **Participate in Christ's own suffering-to-glory pattern** — 1Pe 4:13 ("rejoice insofar as you share Christ's sufferings, that you may also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed") — Suffering-Joy equips the believer to enter the same suffering-glory trajectory Christ entered; (3) **Produce proven character** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy when you meet trials of various kinds") frames Suffering-Joy as the inner faculty that enables the trials to accomplish their formative work; (4) **Ground the inner being in eschatological reality** — 1Pe 1:6 ("in this you rejoice, though now for a little while... grieved by various trials") — present suffering is contextualised by the eschatological inheritance; Suffering-Joy equips this recontextualisation.

---

##### T0.2.2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence shows exultation operating in both registers. Its function in the creation narrative is implicit in the cosmic-rejoicing passages (Psa 96:11; 97:1; 1Ch 16:31 — the heavens, earth, and coastlands called to rejoice because the Lord reigns), which presuppose exultation as part of the creation's designed response to its Creator's reign. Its operation in the fallen condition is most explicit in the salvation-exultation cluster (Psa 9:14; 13:5; 35:9; 61:10; Isa 25:9; 61:10; Hab 3:18) — where exultation arises specifically from divine rescue and deliverance. The eschatological exultation passages (Isa 65:18–19; 66:10; Zec 9:9; Jer 32:41; Zep 3:17) show the characteristic moving toward its fullest expression in the age of restoration. Exultation is therefore part of original design, given a particular form by the condition of redemption, and moving toward eschatological completion.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Both, with strong evidence for original design. The feast-commandments in Deuteronomy, Leviticus, and Numbers presuppose joy as the designed inner response of the covenant community before God. The cosmic-rejoicing passages (1Ch 16:31; Psa 96:11; 97:1) place joy as the appropriate response of all creation to divine sovereignty — not a fallen-condition remedy but the inherent response of the creature to the Creator's reign. The NT evidence adds the response-to-fallen-condition dimension: M04-C's emphasis on joy through suffering (Jas 1:2; 1Pe 1:6; 2Cor 6:10; Rom 5:3) and amid persecution (Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23) names joy specifically as the counter-intuitive inner posture required in the fallen world. The Ecclesiastes evidence (commending joy in the face of vanity and mortality) similarly frames it as the fitting inner posture amid creaturely limitation. Joy is both an original-design characteristic and one that takes particular forms in the fallen condition.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Strongly original design. The Gen 1 series (VCG-01) establishes the evaluative-gladness faculty as operating at creation itself — before the fall, God's own perception of the good in his work is the archetype. Gen 2:18's "not good" — the only negative in the creation narrative — shows the evaluative faculty precisely identifying a genuine lack (solitude) in an otherwise good creation. The M04-L-VCG-02 corpus in Proverbs, however, shows the evaluative faculty operating extensively in the fallen condition (assessing injustice, corruption, moral deficiency) — these uses are responses to the fallen world's moral complexity. M04-O's circumstantial Gladness similarly spans both: the soul's warm response to good news and blessing is a created-design capacity; its deployment in scenarios of exile, judgment, and adversity (Lam 3:26–27; Jon 4:3, 8; Hos 2:7) reflects operation in the fallen condition.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Both, with strong original-design grounding. (1) **Original design** — Pro 8:30–31 shows Delight operating before creation as Wisdom's daily pleasure before God and in the children of man — pre-fall, pre-human, grounding Delight as a created-design capacity anterior to the fall; Psa 37:4's promise ("delight yourself in the Lord… he will give you the desires of your heart") implies that properly directed Delight is what the person was constituted to experience; M04-H-VCG-03's volitional-preference idiom throughout the historical narratives shows human delight as a normal created capacity for personal judgment and preference; (2) **Response to fallen condition** — M04-P (corrupt delight — Eze 23:12; Hab 3:14; Isa 66:3) and M04-H-VCG-04 (negated and misdirected delight — Isa 65:12; 66:4; 2Th 2:12) are specifically fallen-condition phenomena — the misdirection of a created good toward wrong objects; M04-M (pleasing God as obedience orientation) in contexts of cultic correction (Lev 1:17; 1Sa 15:22; Hos 6:6) is also fallen-condition remedial; Delight-in-God's-word as a sustained life-preserving resource (Psa 119:92) is specifically operative in the fallen world's suffering.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Both, with strong original-design grounding: (1) **Original design** — Pro 3:17 ("her ways are ways of pleasantness") places wisdom's pleasantness in the created order; Psa 16:6 ("lines have fallen for me in pleasant places") describes a God-given inheritance of pleasant provision; Psa 36:8 ("river of your delights") is an attribute of God's house; the Song of Songs' celebration of bodily beauty and pleasantness (Song 1:16; 7:6) is original-design relational appreciation; (2) **Response to fallen condition** — the ni.cho.ach corpus (M04-K-VCG-01) is explicitly cultic and sacrificial, which is a fallen-condition institution addressing sin; Lev 4:31 (pleasing aroma alongside atonement) shows ni.cho.ach operating in a forgiveness-seeking context; M04-K-VCG-02's luxury-curse register (Deu 28:54, 56 — the delicate person's comfort destroyed) is entirely a fallen-condition phenomenon; (3) Pro 9:17 (stolen bread called pleasant) is the fallen-condition distortion of Pleasure: the same faculty that receives genuine pleasantness is deceived by illicit appearance.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Both, but with important distinctions by register: (1) **Original design** — M04-I-VCG-01's wonder at God's marvellous works (creation, redemption, providence) is an original-design capacity; Psa 139:14 ("I am fearfully and wonderfully made") — the wonder evoked by human embodiment itself is a created-design reality; (2) **Original design but fallen-context deployment** — most VCG-01 wonders are performed in the context of Israel's history (Exodus, wilderness, conquest) — these arise from God's redemptive responses to the fallen condition, but the wonder-capacity itself is original design; (3) **Fallen condition distortion** — M04-I-VCG-03's dark wonder (Job 10:16 — wonders worked against Job; Dan 8:24; 11:36 — the king's fearful destruction and astonishing blasphemy; Gal 1:6 — Paul astonished at the Galatians' defection; Rev 17:6 — wonder at the harlot) is specifically a fallen-condition phenomenon; wonder-as-dread, wonder-at-evil, and wonder-at-apostasy are not original-design states.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Primarily a **response to the fallen condition**. The M04-F corpus (ba.lag/mav.li.git — Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13; Jer 8:18) depicts fragile cheerfulness sought under extreme adversity that arises from the brokenness of creation under the curse: Job's suffering, the psalmist's mortality-distress, Jeremiah's grief over the people's ruin. None of these would arise in an uncorrupted creation. The M04-E-VCG-02 agalliao passages (Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23 — rejoicing under persecution; 1Pe 1:6; 4:13 — joy amid trials; 2Cor 6:10 implied by the adjacent characteristic-1 and 7 shared registers) arise from the conflict between the gospel community and a hostile world — again a fallen-condition context. That said, the characteristic anticipates its own eschatological resolution (1Pe 4:13 — "also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed") — suggesting it is a transitional capacity that serves the fallen condition while pointing toward the restoration where suffering-joy gives way to unqualified joy.

---

##### T0.2.3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, strongly. The Isaianic exultation passages are concentrated around eschatological restoration: Isa 65:18 commands "be glad and rejoice forever in that which I create," grounding the exultation in a new creative act; Isa 65:19 places God's own rejoicing in Jerusalem in the new-creation context; Isa 66:10 calls all who love Jerusalem to rejoice with her at her vindication; Zec 9:9 directs Zion's exultation at the coming of her king. Jer 32:41 and Zep 3:17 both locate divine exultation over Israel in the final-restoration context. The current experience of exultation — the psalmist's "my soul will rejoice in the Lord" (Psa 35:9) — anticipates a fullness not yet arrived: the "I will rejoice" of Psa 9:14 is future-oriented; Psa 14:7 / 53:6 cast Jacob's rejoicing as awaited. The characteristic is eschatologically open.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, strongly — this is one of Joy's most prominent features. M04-E-VCG-01 (OT restoration joy) is entirely forward-oriented: Isa 35:10 / 51:11 ("everlasting joy shall be upon their heads"); Isa 51:3 (joy and gladness found in restored Zion); Jer 31:13 (God turning mourning into joy); Jer 33:9, 11 (Jerusalem as a name of joy in restoration); Zec 8:19 (fasts becoming seasons of joy). M04-C-VCG-04 extends this: Joh 16:22 ("your hearts will rejoice, and no one will take your joy from you"); Rev 19:7 (commanded corporate rejoicing at the Lamb's marriage); Jude 24 (great joy at blameless presentation before God's glory); Heb 12:2 (the joy set before Jesus that sustained his cross). Within Characteristic 2 itself, fullness of joy is a recurring eschatological goal: Joh 15:11 ("that your joy may be full"); Joh 16:24 ("that your joy may be full"); 1Jo 1:4; 2Jo 12 (joy made complete). Present Joy is consistently experienced as partial and anticipatory.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Partially. M04-O-VCG-04's covenantal-promise goodness register (Jer 29:10; 33:14; Jos 21:45; 23:16) shows God's good promises as the ground of present endurance — the soul's gladness in the present is anchored in future-fulfillment confidence. The makarismos verses (Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15 — in M04-O-VCG-04) present blessedness as a declarative eschatological state. Lam 3:26 ("it is good to wait quietly for the salvation of the Lord") frames the present inner disposition of gladness-in-waiting as oriented toward a salvation not yet arrived. However, Gladness lacks the concentrated eschatological trajectory of Joy (Characteristic 2) — it is more characteristically present-responsive than future-oriented.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in several registers: (1) **Eschatological delight in YHWH** — Isa 58:14 ("then you shall take delight in the Lord, and I will make you ride on the heights of the earth") — delight in the Lord as the eschatological fruit of Sabbath faithfulness; Job 22:26 ("for then you will delight yourself in the Almighty") — restored delight in God as the future state of the person brought back; (2) **Jerusalem as a land of delight** — Mal 3:12 ("you will be a land of delight, says the Lord of hosts") — the restored nation inhabiting its fullest delight-quality as the eschatological goal; Isa 62:4 — Zion renamed "My Delight Is in Her" as the eschatological reversal; (3) **Father's good pleasure giving the kingdom** — Luk 12:32 ("it is your Father's good pleasure to give you the kingdom") — divine delight as the willing eschatological gift; (4) **Isa 11:8's nursing child playing over the cobra's hole** — carefree sha.a in the eschatological age of peace when natural enmity is removed, pointing toward a fullness of fearless delight not yet present.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 16:11** — "at your right hand are pleasures forevermore" — the clearest eschatological statement for Pleasure in the corpus: pleasures in God's presence as a permanent eschatological reality; (2) **Eze 20:41** — "as a pleasing aroma I will accept you, when I bring you out from the peoples and gather you" — future divine acceptance-as-pleasantness as the eschatological restoration goal; (3) **Zec 8:19** — former fasts becoming "cheerful feasts" — the transformation of mourning into Pleasure as eschatological reversal; (4) **Job 36:11** — "if they listen and serve him, they complete their days in pleasantness" — pleasantness as the fruit of faithful obedience with eschatological overtones; (5) **Psa 36:8** — river of delights as the eternal supply in God's house, pointing toward the New Jerusalem's river of life.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Isa 29:14** ("I will again do wonderful things with this people, with wonder upon wonder") — the escalating wonder of God's future acts promises a fullness that surpasses even the Exodus wonders; (2) **Mic 7:15** ("as in the days when you came out of the land of Egypt, I will show them marvellous things") — the new exodus's marvels pointing toward eschatological fullness; (3) **Joe 2:26** ("the Lord your God, who has dealt wondrously with you") — restoration's wonders as a foretaste of the fullness; (4) **Isa 9:6** — the Wonderful Counselor's coming as the ultimate wonder-event; (5) **Dan 12:6** ("how long till the end of these wonders?") — the apocalyptic wonders as the transitional events leading to the final state.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes — this is one of Suffering-Joy's most prominent features. (1) **Eschatological reward as the ground** — Mat 5:12 ("your reward is great in heaven"); (2) **Transition to glory** — 1Pe 4:13 ("that you may also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed") — present Suffering-Joy is explicitly oriented toward a future unqualified rejoicing at Christ's revelation; (3) **Inexpressible and glorious** — 1Pe 1:8 ("joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory") — the present form of Suffering-Joy already participates in the glory-filled quality of eschatological reality; (4) **Heb 12:2** — Jesus' joy-set-before-him is the eschatological ground that enabled the cross. The characteristic is inherently eschatologically-structured: the suffering is present; the joy is eschatologically anchored.

---

#### T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression

##### T0.3.1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation expresses the divine image in the human person as the capacity for God-directed inner triumph — the ability to respond to divine reality (reign, salvation, presence, goodness) with an inner state that rises toward its source. The evidence shows this as a correspondence between God's exultation over his people (Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41; Isa 62:5) and the human person's exultation in God (Psa 35:9; 21:1; Isa 61:10; Hab 3:18). The image is not merely formal (humans can exult as God can exult) but relational: the divine-human exultation pair is structured as mutual delight — God delights over the person, the person delights in God. The divine image in this characteristic is the capacity for that particular relational orientation of triumphant, Godward inner joy.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy expresses the divine image as the human person's capacity to actively engage and participate in what is worth celebrating — a capacity that mirrors God's own inner rejoicing. The most direct image-evidence is the parallelism between God's joy over his people and the people's joy in God: God "makes them joyful" (Ezr 6:22); the people rejoice "in him" (Psa 40:16; 70:4; 86:4). The image-bearing quality is the directionality and the object-relatedness: just as God's joy is directed toward his people in covenant relationship, the human person's joy is designed to be directed toward God. The NT deepens this: Jesus' own joy is to be in the disciples (Joh 15:11; 17:13) — the transfer of Christ's joy into the human inner being is the fullest expression of Joy as an image-bearing capacity. Joy in the human person is the response-face of the same inner-state that God has toward them.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness expresses the divine image as the human person's capacity for evaluative recognition of genuine goodness — the inner faculty that can perceive, name, and be settled in what is truly good, mirroring God's own perception of goodness in creation. Mic 6:8 — "He has told you, O man, what is good; and what does the Lord require of you but to do justice, and to love kindness, and to walk humbly with your God?" — is the most explicit statement: God has declared what human goodness is, and the human person's capacity to recognise it (evaluative Gladness) and inhabit it (moral Gladness) is the image-bearing response. Psa 119:68's "you are good and do good; teach me your statutes" shows the divine being-good as the pattern the human person is being formed toward. The image is expressed as a correspondence in evaluative-moral faculty: God sees and declares good; the human person sees and declares good (or not-good) in imitation of that divine evaluative act.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight expresses the divine image through two primary image-bearing patterns: (1) **Volitional delight as the image of divine sovereignty** — God's cha.phets is his sovereign will (Psa 115:3; 135:6); the human person's cha.phets/che.phets is a creaturely participation in the capacity for directed inner willing that resembles the divine. Gen 34:19 (Shechem's delight driving urgent action), Psa 40:8 (the psalmist delighting to do God's will), and 1Ch 28:9 (the willing mind) show human volitional delight as the image-bearing analogue of divine purposeful willing; (2) **Affective delight as the image of divine relational pleasure** — God's delight in persons (Psa 18:19; Isa 62:4; Jer 31:20) is the divine pattern; the human person's delight in God (Psa 37:4; Job 22:26; Isa 58:14), in God's word (Psa 119; Rom 7:22), and in fellow persons (1Sa 19:1; Psa 16:3; 1Th 2:8) images back the divine relational-pleasure capacity. Mic 6:8's "he has told you what is good" applies here: human Delight directed at God, his word, and righteous character is the created-image response to the divine inner pleasure that first directed itself toward humanity.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure expresses the divine image as the human person's capacity to receive and register genuine agreeableness — imaging the God who himself experiences his own beauty as pleasant (Psa 27:4's no.am as God's quality) and who receives correct worship with inner satisfaction (Gen 8:21's ni.cho.ach moving God's heart). The human person's Pleasure in beautiful persons (Song 1:16; 7:6), agreeable speech (Pro 16:24), wisdom's ways (Pro 3:17), brotherly unity (Psa 133:1), and the pleasantness of God himself (Psa 27:4; 16:11) images back the divine capacity for pleasurable reception. The image is specifically expressed in the receptive-appreciative dimension of the inner being — the person who can receive beauty, goodness, and agreeableness and respond to it inwardly is imaging the divine pleasure in his own beautiful and good character.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder expresses the divine image as the creature's capacity to rightly acknowledge what infinitely exceeds its own comprehension. The image-bearing significance: a person formed in God's image is not merely intelligent and volitional but is constitutively open to what exceeds them — Wonder is the experiential evidence of this openness. Psa 139:14 ("I am fearfully and wonderfully made") shows that Wonder can be directed inward — the person who genuinely wonders at their own creation is acknowledging that they themselves are made by and for a God infinitely greater than themselves. The specifically image-bearing quality of Wonder is that it is the inner state appropriate to a finite being encountering the infinite: God made the human person as a finite image of the infinite, and Wonder is the characteristic that keeps the image-bearer aware of its own created finitude before the Creator's infinity.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy expresses the divine image as the capacity to participate in the Christ-pattern: the suffering-toward-glory trajectory that Christ himself embodied (Heb 12:2). The human person who genuinely rejoices amid suffering — not performing relief, not denying the pain, but genuinely finding joy through the suffering — is imaging the inner life of the incarnate Son who endured the cross for the joy set before him. 1Pe 1:8's "joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory" names this participation: the present experience of Suffering-Joy is already filled with the glory that belongs to the age to come, because the inner being is participating in the risen Christ's life through the Spirit (Act 16:34 — the jailer's entire household rejoiced in God despite having just been delivered from an earthquake crisis; Luk 1:47 — Mary's spirit exulting in the Savior despite her vulnerable unmarried-mother-in-a-suspicious-society situation).

---

##### T0.3.2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence supports genuine sharing rather than merely analogical relation. The same primary terms (su.s, gil_verb) are used for divine exultation (Zep 3:17; Isa 65:19; Jer 32:41) and human exultation (Psa 35:9; Isa 61:10; Hab 3:18). The same preposition structure ("exult in / over") is used in both directions. Jer 32:41 grounds God's rejoicing in "all my heart and all my soul" — constitutional language applied to God in a passage describing mutual restoration. This suggests the characteristic is genuinely shared across the Creator-creature boundary, with the creaturely form being a real participation in the divine inner life rather than a mere analogy.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Genuinely shared. The same terms (sa.mach, sim.chah, chairo, chara) are used for both divine and human joy in the same passages. Psa 104:31 ("may the Lord rejoice in his works" — sa.mach) applies sa.mach to God. Jer 32:41 applies su.s to God. The NT adds: God rejoices over the repentant sinner (Luk 15:7, 10) using the exact same register as human rejoicing. The most decisive evidence is Joh 15:11 — "my joy may be in you": Christ's own joy (chara) is to indwell the disciples, making their joy a participation in divine joy rather than a mere analogy to it. The sharing is constitutive: Joy in the human person is described as the Lord's joy being present in them (Neh 8:10 — "the joy of the Lord is your strength").

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Genuinely shared at the level of the evaluative faculty. The same term (tov) is used for God's evaluative declarations ("God saw that it was good" — Gen 1:4–31) and the human person's evaluative declarations ("it is not good that the man should be alone" — Gen 2:18; "the thing that you are doing is not good" — Exo 18:17; "Ruth's love is more to you than seven sons" — Rut 4:15). The human evaluative faculty is a real participation in the divine evaluative capacity, not merely a pale analogy. The programme observation OBS-026 (Psa 119:68) makes this explicit: God's being-good generates doing-good; the human person who evaluates correctly is participating in the same moral-recognition structure. In M04-O, God's covenantal goodness (good hand, good promises) is what produces the human person's gladness — confirming that the human Gladness-response corresponds to a genuine divine goodness-reality.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Genuinely shared, most extensively of any M04 characteristic. The same root terms appear for both: (1) cha.phets — used for God's sovereign will (Isa 53:10; Psa 115:3; 135:6), God's relational delight (Psa 18:19; 37:23; Eze 18:23), and human volitional delight and desire (Gen 34:19; Psa 40:8; Job 13:3); (2) eudokeo — used for the Father's delight in the Son (Mat 3:17; Col 1:19; 2Pe 1:17), and for human willing generosity (Rom 15:26–27), preference (2Cor 5:8), and contentment (2Cor 12:10). Pro 8:30–31 is unique: the same sha.a.shu.im term names both God's delight in Wisdom and Wisdom's delight in the children of man, creating a shared-delight architecture — God delights in Wisdom, Wisdom delights in humans, humans are constituted as delight-objects of God and delight-bearing agents. The sharing is thorough.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially shared. The no.am/na.im/no.am vocabulary describes both: God's own beauty (Psa 27:4 — no.am as God's attribute); human pleasantness (2Sa 1:26 — Jonathan's na.em to David; Pro 3:17 — wisdom's no.am ways; Psa 133:1 — na.im of brotherly unity). The ni.cho.ach vocabulary is explicitly relational — it names an inner divine response that corresponds to a human worship-act: the human offers, God receives with pleasure; this is a shared-pleasure structure at the worship interface. God's own inner beauty (no.am) is not shared with humans in the same direct sense as cha.phets (volitional Delight) — but human Pleasure in God's beauty (Psa 27:4) is the creaturely analogue of God's delight in his own character.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primarily creaturely, with the important exception of Isa 9:6's "Wonderful" as a divine name/title. The evidence consistently positions Wonder on the human side of the Creator-creature divide: God does wondrous things (active side); humans marvel at them (receptive side). Zec 8:6 explicitly distinguishes the human "marvellous in the sight of the remnant" from what would be marvellous "in my sight" — suggesting the divine perspective is not wonder but understanding. Wonder is therefore primarily and characteristically creaturely — the response of the finite to the infinite — though "Wonderful" (Isa 9:6) as a divine title shows that God's character and presence are inherently wonder-inducing.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Genuinely shared, through Christ. The same term (agalliao) is used for: Jesus' rejoicing in the Holy Spirit (Luk 10:21); Abraham's anticipatory exultation at Christ's day (Joh 8:56); Mary's exultation in God her Savior in the vulnerable context of her pregnancy (Luk 1:47); the disciples' inexpressible glorious joy in believing the unseen Christ (1Pe 1:8); the jailer's household's exultation at coming to faith (Act 16:34). The sharing is through the Spirit who enables the same quality of rejoicing in the human person that Christ exhibited (Luk 10:21 — "he rejoiced in the Holy Spirit"). Suffering-Joy in the human person is a Spirit-enabled participation in Christ's own joy-through-suffering pattern.

---

##### T0.3.3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The inverted exultation passages (M04-A-VCG-02) provide the most direct evidence. Pro 2:14 shows those who "rejoice in doing evil and delight in the perverseness of evil" — exultation directed at evil is explicitly contrasted with wisdom's way, indicating that the characteristic's object determines whether it images God or distorts the image. Hos 9:1 commands Israel "rejoice not" because their joy is built on spiritual prostitution; Hos 10:5 shows idolatrous priests who rejoiced over a golden calf now mourning its departure — their exultation directed at an idol is now ended. The evidence shows that exultation directed toward God reveals the divine image functioning; exultation directed toward evil, idols, or another person's calamity (Pro 24:17; Psa 13:4) reveals the image distorted or corrupted. Absence of exultation before God — as in Job 3:6–7 (the wished-barrenness of the birth-night) — marks a state of such extremity that even the capacity for directed inner joy is temporarily overwhelmed.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The inverted and absent joy evidence (M04-B-VCG-06, M04-C-VCG-05 corrupt elements) is the most diagnostic: (1) **Image corrupted** — Pro 2:14 (those who "rejoice in doing evil and delight in the perverseness of evil"); Eze 25:6 (Ammon's joy arising from "malice within your soul" at Israel's ruin); Eze 36:5 ("wholehearted joy and utter contempt" of those who seized God's land) — joy directed at evil, at others' ruin, or at one's own pride reveals the image severely distorted; (2) **Image silenced by sin** — Psa 51:8, 12 (David's joy silenced by his sin, requiring restoration through confession and forgiveness); the loss of joy is a diagnostic of sin's damage; (3) **Image emptied by judgment** — Deu 28:47 (failure to serve with joyfulness as the root of covenant curses); Joe 1:16 (joy cut off from God's house under judgment) — the absence of joy before God reveals the covenant relationship broken; (4) **Image functioning** — Psa 97:11 ("joy for the upright in heart") — the presence of genuine joy in the uprightly-oriented inner being signals the image in its designed operation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Presence reveals the image functioning: the person who accurately evaluates what is genuinely good (Mic 6:8's trio of justice, loving kindness, walking humbly; Naomi's wisdom in evaluating Ruth's best course; the Psalms' steady recognition of God's goodness as the ground of thanksgiving) shows the image in its designed operation. Distortion reveals the image degraded: the people who judged return to Egypt as "better than dying in the wilderness" (Num 14:3 — M04-O-VCG-02) are evaluating from fear rather than faith; the craftsmen who say "it is good" of their idol's soldering (Isa 41:7 — M04-L-VCG-02) show the evaluative faculty applied to a self-congratulating work that cannot respond or act; Jeremiah 44:17's people who attributed former wellbeing to idol-worship show the evaluative-gladness faculty seriously distorted by false memory. Absence reveals the image silenced: Eze 36:31 ("your deeds that were not good, and you will loathe yourselves") shows the evaluative faculty turned against the self in moral revulsion — the image partially restored through recognition of past failure, but accompanied by shame.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

**Presence** of rightly directed Delight reveals the image functioning: Psa 40:8 (delighting to do God's will with the law within the heart — image functioning at its most direct, Heb 10:7 applies this to Christ); Psa 1:2 (delight in the law driving sustained meditation — the blessed person's image operating through will and mind); Rom 7:22 (delight in God's law "in my inner being" — even in the struggling person, the deepest layer of the image is directed toward God's law). **Misdirected Delight** reveals the image distorted: Isa 66:3 ("their soul delights in their abominations") — the same delight-capacity directed at the opposite of its proper object; Jer 6:10 (no pleasure in God's word — the image closed to its proper object); 2Th 2:12 (pleasure in unrighteousness — the image inverted). M04-F (fragile horizontal delight in beast-captivation — Rev 13:3; 17:8) shows the most complete image-distortion: the delight faculty captivated by an antichrist figure rather than by God. Jer 6:10's uncircumcised ear that takes no pleasure in God's word is the diagnostic of a heart sealed against its proper object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

**Presence of rightly directed Pleasure** reveals the image functioning: the person who finds wisdom genuinely pleasant (Pro 2:10 — "knowledge will be pleasant to your soul"), who appreciates the pleasantness of brotherly unity (Psa 133:1), who gazes on God's beauty (Psa 27:4), and whose worship genuinely soothes God's regard (M04-K-VCG-01) is an image-bearer receiving the world rightly. **Absence / distortion**: Neh 9:17 (Israel failed to register God's wonders — wonder absent); Pro 9:17 (stolen bread called pleasant — the Pleasure faculty deceived by wrong objects); Deu 28:54–56 (the delicate person's Pleasure destroyed by the curse — the image's receptive capacity collapsed under judgment); Job 20:18 (the wicked getting no enjoyment from his profits — the image's natural Pleasure capacity blocked by moral corruption). The diagnostic: the person who finds genuine pleasantness in wisdom, in persons, and in God's presence has a functioning image; the person whose Pleasure has been captured by wrong objects or collapsed under judgment shows the image degraded.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**Presence of genuine Wonder** reveals the image rightly oriented: (1) Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law") — the person who seeks to see wonder in God's law has a properly humble, receptive image-orientation; (2) Psa 139:14's self-wonder confirms an image properly aware of its own created dependency; (3) Job 42:3's wonder-humility after the whirlwind-encounter shows the image restored to its right creaturely orientation. **Absence of Wonder** reveals the image degraded: Neh 9:17 ("did not consider your wondrous works; they… rebelled") — failure to wonder at God's acts hardened into stiff-necked rebellion; Psa 78:11, 32 ("forgot his wonders… despite his wonders, they did not believe") — wonder-failure correlating directly with unbelief; Psa 106:7 ("did not consider your wondrous works") — wonder-absence leading to Red Sea rebellion. The diagnostic: the person who has stopped wondering at God has begun to treat themselves as the measure of all things.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

**Presence** reveals the image being renewed by the Spirit in the Christ-pattern: the person who genuinely rejoices amid suffering (1Pe 1:6–8; Jas 1:2) demonstrates that the Spirit is at work producing a quality of inner life that transcends circumstances — a deeply eschatologically-oriented inner being. **Absence / distortion** is most sharply evidenced in M04-F: Job 9:27 (Job considers attempting cheerfulness but immediately recognises he cannot maintain it — the image's capacity is there but overwhelmed by suffering's weight); Psa 39:13 (the psalmist's request for a little smile before death — the barely-flickering of the capacity under extreme mortality-distress). M04-F's fragile and barely-attainable cheerfulness shows the image's Suffering-Joy capacity as genuinely present but requiring the Spirit's enabling (M04-E-VCG-02) to function in its fuller form.

---

#### T0.4 — Typological Significance

##### T0.4.1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate (covenantal, eschatological, christological)?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The most direct typological deployment is Zec 9:9 ("Rejoice greatly, O daughter of Zion! Behold, your king is coming to you") — the commanded exultation at the arrival of the humble, saving king is the OT type fulfilled in Christ's entry into Jerusalem (Mat 21:5). The pattern of Godward exultation established in the Psalms (Psa 2:11; 9:14; 21:1; 32:11; 35:9) also functions typologically: the psalmic exultation in YHWH's salvation participates in a larger pattern of divine-human restoration that Christ's coming fulfils. Isa 61:10's "I will greatly rejoice in the Lord; my soul shall exult in my God, for he has clothed me with the garments of salvation" is a passage Jesus quotes as fulfilled in his ministry (Luk 4:18–21), making the exultation of Isa 61 christologically significant.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, extensively. Several clusters: (1) **Feast joy as type of eschatological joy** — the commanded feast rejoicings (Deu 16:11, 14, 15; Lev 23:40) are the OT type of the eschatological feast (Rev 19:7; Mat 25:21, 23 — "enter into the joy of your master"); (2) **The lost-found parables** (Luk 15:6–7, 9–10) deploy joy typologically: the shepherd's joy over the recovered sheep is the type of heaven's joy over repentance; (3) **Abraham's joy** (Joh 8:56 — "your father Abraham rejoiced that he would see my day") frames OT faith as typological joy that Christ's day fulfils; (4) **The oil of gladness** (Psa 45:7; Heb 1:9) — the king's anointing with the oil of gladness is applied to Christ, making the royal joy of the OT king a type of Christ's pre-eminent anointed joy; (5) **M04-E's sa.s.von corpus** — the restoration joy promised (Isa 35:10; 51:11; 61:3) functions typologically as the OT anticipation of the NT and eschatological joy brought by Christ's work.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, in specific registers: (1) **The Gen 1 creation-goodness as type** — God's "very good" declaration over creation (Gen 1:31) is the OT type pointing forward to the new creation (Isa 65:18 — God creates Jerusalem to be "a joy" and her people "a gladness" — gi.lah); the created goodness of the first creation is the type of the consummated goodness of the new; (2) **Psa 45:7's oil of gladness** (sa.s.von) applied christologically in Heb 1:9 — the anointed king's gladness beyond his companions is the OT type for Christ's eschatological anointing; (3) **The makarismos typology** (Rom 4:6, 9 — Abraham's blessedness as the type of the justified person's blessedness declared apart from works) — the OT blessedness pattern (in M04-O-VCG-04) is the type for NT declarative righteousness; (4) **God's good promises** (Jos 21:45; Jer 29:10; 33:14) as types of the final fulfillment in Christ — every good promise not one of which has failed finds its ultimate Yes in Christ (2Cor 1:20).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, richly: (1) **Christological — the Father's eudokeo** — the divine delight declared at baptism (Mat 3:17; Mar 1:11; Luk 3:22) and transfiguration (Mat 17:5; 2Pe 1:17) is the OT covenant-pattern of divine pleasure in the servant (Isa 42:1 — "my beloved with whom my soul is well pleased" — the servant-song's divine pleasure typologically fulfilled in Christ); (2) **Redemptive typology — Isa 53:10** — "it was the will of the Lord to crush him; the will of the Lord shall prosper in his hand" — the most theologically charged divine-cha.phets in the corpus: God's delight directed toward the servant's suffering-for-sin as the mechanism of redemption; this is divine Delight as the hinge of atonement; (3) **Wisdom's delight as type of Christ** — Pro 8:30–31 (Wisdom as God's daily delight, delighting in the children of man) is the type that the NT applies christologically; (4) **The "land of delight" and "My Delight Is in Her"** (Mal 3:12; Isa 62:4) — OT types of the eschatological community that the NT's "body of Christ" fulfils; (5) **Luk 12:32** — "the Father's good pleasure to give you the kingdom" fulfils the OT pattern of divine delight as the ground of covenantal gift.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, in the ni.cho.ach register most clearly: (1) **Cultic ni.cho.ach → Christ's self-offering** — the entire Levitical pleasing-aroma system is the OT type that the NT applies to Christ's sacrificial death (Eph 5:2 — "a fragrant offering and sacrifice to God" — not in this corpus but the type is established here); each Levitical offering producing ni.cho.ach is a type of the final offering that fully satisfies divine regard; (2) **Psa 27:4's gazing on no.am → eschatological vision** — the one thing the psalmist seeks (gazing on God's beauty in his temple) is the type of the final face-to-face beatific experience (Rev 22:4 — "they will see his face" — not in corpus but anticipated by Psa 27:4); (3) **Zec 11:7, 10's No'am staff → covenant pleasantness revoked** — the breaking of the Favour/Pleasantness staff typologically anticipates the rejection of the Good Shepherd (the NT applies Zec 11 to the thirty pieces of silver and Christ's betrayal — Mat 27:9–10); (4) **Psa 36:8's river of delights → the river of life** (Rev 22:1) — the eschatological typing of divine pleasantness.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Exodus wonders as type of redemption** — the VCG-01 corpus is heavily dominated by remembrance of Exodus wonders (Exo 3:20; 15:11; 34:10; Neh 9:17; Psa 78:4, 12; 105:2, 5; 106:7, 22; 136:4) — these are the foundational type of all divine wonder-working, the OT archetype that NT redemption in Christ fulfils and surpasses; (2) **Isa 9:6 "Wonderful Counselor"** — the OT type (the coming child's wonder-name) points to Christ whose identity is inherently wonder-inducing; (3) **Isa 29:14 "wonder upon wonder"** — the OT promise of escalating wonders typologically points to the NT's "greater works than these" (Joh 14:12); (4) **Psa 118:23 ("this is the Lord's doing, it is marvellous in our eyes")** — the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone as marvellous — Psa 118:22–23 is quoted in the NT as explicitly christological (Mat 21:42), making it a formal OT typological text for Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Abraham's anticipatory Suffering-Joy as type** — Joh 8:56 ("your father Abraham rejoiced that he would see my day") — Abraham's exultation across the gap of non-fulfilment is the OT type of NT faith-joy in the unseen Christ (1Pe 1:8 — "though you do not now see him, you believe in him and rejoice with inexpressible joy filled with glory"); (2) **The prophetic exultation under judgment as type** — M04-F's Jeremiah (Jer 8:18 — "my joy is gone; grief is upon me") is the OT sufferer whose inability to maintain cheer anticipates the fuller articulation of Suffering-Joy in the NT through Christ; (3) **Psa 39:13 as type** — the psalmist's request to "smile again before I depart" anticipates the resurrection-grounded joy that the NT's Suffering-Joy provides as the answer: believers will not merely smile briefly before death but will fully rejoice when glory is revealed (1Pe 4:13).

---

##### T0.4.2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology — does the human instance point toward the divine, or does the divine instance establish the pattern for the human?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The primary direction is human-to-divine: the human instance of commanded exultation at YHWH's salvation (Zec 9:9; Psa 2:11) points forward toward the eschatological-messianic reality Christ fulfils. The secondary direction is divine-to-human: God's exultation over his people (Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41) establishes the pattern for the restored community's exultation in him. The two directions are constitutive of the same relational structure: divine exultation calls forth human exultation, and human exultation points toward the eschatological reality in which God and his people exult in each other permanently.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Both directions are evidenced: (1) **Human-to-divine / present-to-eschatological**: The OT feast joy points forward to the eschatological banquet; the OT restoration promises (sa.s.von) point to the NT gospel joy; Abraham's faith-joy points to Christ's day; (2) **Divine-to-human / heavenly-to-earthly**: Joh 15:11 and 17:13 establish the downward direction — Christ's own joy is transferred into the disciples as the pattern the human joy approximates. The master's joy (Mat 25:21, 23) sets the divine-relational joy as the destination into which the faithful servant enters. The two directions form a circular pattern: God's joy descends into the human person; human joy rises in response; both are oriented toward the eschatological fullness of the kingdom feast.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Both directions: (1) **Human-to-eschatological**: Gen 1:31's "very good" creation points forward to the new creation's perfected goodness; the OT blessing declarations (makarismos) point forward to NT declarative righteousness; (2) **Divine-to-human pattern**: Psa 119:68 ("you are good and do good") establishes the divine being-good/doing-good as the pattern the human person is formed toward; God's evaluative "good" in creation establishes the standard by which all creaturely evaluations operate.
