The bidirectional typology confirms Gladness as a characteristic that participates in the divine evaluative life and moves toward eschatological consummation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Both directions operate: (1) **Divine-to-human** — the divine eudokeo (Father's delight in the Son) establishes the pattern for the human person's delight in God (the human response images back the divine originating pleasure); Isa 53:10's divine cha.phets is the originating sovereign act that the human appropriation of redemption participates in; (2) **Human-to-eschatological** — Psa 37:4's "delight yourself in the Lord" is the present human act that anticipates the eschatological fullness of Job 22:26 and Isa 58:14; the present Delight in God's word (Psa 119) is the type of the eschatological resting in God. Isa 42:1's servant-delight is the human-typological figure pointing to Christ; the divine eudokeo at the baptism confirms it.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primarily **OT-type → NT/eschatological fulfilment**: the cultic ni.cho.ach system points forward to Christ's offering; the Zec 11 No'am staff points forward to the Good Shepherd's rejection; the Psa 27:4 / 36:8 divine-pleasantness language points forward to eschatological vision and the river of life. The direction is historical-typological: the OT forms of Pleasure-in-worship and divine-pleasure establish the pattern that the NT and eschatological realities fulfil and surpass.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primarily **OT-type → NT/christological fulfillment**: Exodus wonders → Christ's miracles; Psa 118:23 (rejected stone becoming cornerstone as marvellous) → Christ's resurrection and rejection; Isa 9:6's Wonderful Counselor → the incarnate Christ. Also **progressive escalation**: Isa 29:14 ("wonder upon wonder") shows the typological direction as always toward a greater wonder — the pattern is not merely repetition but surpassing.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Primarily **human-to-eschatological**: (1) M04-F's fragile OT cheerfulness → NT Spirit-enabled suffering-paradox joy; (2) Abraham's anticipatory agalliao → NT faith-community's present agalliao in the unseen Christ; (3) The Psalmic barely-maintained cheer → the fully-articulated Suffering-Joy of the NT epistles. The direction of typology is: OT fragile/anticipatory form → NT Spirit-enabled fully-realised form, with the eschatological fullness still to come (1Pe 4:13; Rev 19:7).

---

##### T0.4.3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Typological use is evidenced (see T0.4.1–T0.4.2). No silence to note.

---

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Typological use is extensively evidenced (see T0.4.1–T0.4.2).

Typological use is evidenced; not silent.

Typological use is the most extensively evidenced typological pattern in M04; not silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Typological use is evidenced in the ni.cho.ach and No'am staff registers; not silent.

---

## T1 — Definition and Structural Analysis

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Typological use is extensively evidenced, especially in the Exodus-wonder type and Psa 118:23; not silent.

---

## T1 — Definition and Structural Analysis

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Typological use is evidenced; not silent.

---

## T1 — Definition and Structural Analysis

---

### T1

#### T1.1 — Name and Naming

##### T1.1.1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The characteristic is called Exultation. The name signals three things: (1) intensity — exultation is a heightened inner state, not a mild positivity; (2) directionality — exultation is always toward an object worthy of the surging response; (3) triumph — the term carries the sense of victory and vindication, appropriate to the primary register of the evidence where exultation follows divine rescue (Psa 9:14; 35:9; Isa 25:9; 61:10; Hab 3:18). The name also distinguishes this characteristic from Joy (participatory rejoicing) and Gladness (warm inner brightness) by naming the upward surge rather than the sustained warmth or engaged participation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The characteristic is called Joy. The name signals: (1) **Active engagement** — joy is participatory; it rejoices *in* something; it is directed and engaged, not a passive inner warmth; (2) **Inner-being scope** — the name is a recognisable inner-being state, distinct from Exultation (which surges), Gladness (which is warm and diffuse), and Pleasure (which is receptive). Joy as a name names the whole person's active rejoicing capacity; (3) **Communal resonance** — unlike Exultation (which is more individually intense), Joy has a communal dimension built into its common usage — one "rejoices with" others, and the commanded feast-joy of Deuteronomy is inherently social. The name correctly orients the enquiry toward an active, participatory, engageable inner state.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The characteristic is called Gladness. The name signals: (1) **Settled warmth** — gladness is a positively-coloured inner condition rather than an active surge (Exultation) or engaged participation (Joy); (2) **Cognitive-evaluative dimension** — gladness includes the soul's recognition that something is good, which the name captures by its diffuse, non-directed quality (one is glad rather than exulting at something); (3) **Inner condition rather than inner act** — the name points to a state rather than an event; the glad person inhabits gladness rather than performing it. The two sub-groups (M04-L and M04-O) fill the name: M04-L contributes the evaluative-cognitive face (the assessment that things are good); M04-O contributes the circumstantial-experiential face (the warm inner response to what is recognised as good). Together they name the settled, bright inner condition of a person or community that has accurately assessed and is responding to genuine goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The characteristic is called Delight. The name signals: (1) **Object-focus** — Delight is always delight *in* something or someone; the name implies a specific treasured object that the inner person rests in and returns to; (2) **Receptive orientation** — unlike Exultation (active upward surge) or Joy (participatory engagement), Delight implies a resting, returning, orienting movement toward the beloved object; (3) **Affective-volitional integration** — the name in English carries both the emotional quality (it feels pleasurable) and the volitional quality (one chooses to delight, one finds and returns to what delights); this dual quality is exactly what the corpus confirms — M04-G is the affective face and M04-H is the volitional face; (4) **Scope across good and evil** — English "delight" can apply to both legitimate and illegitimate objects, which is consistent with M04-P's corrupt-delight register.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The characteristic is called Pleasure. The name signals: (1) **Receptive quality** — Pleasure names what is received and felt, not what is generated or directed; it is the soul's positive receptive response to what is pleasant; (2) **Agreeableness** — the name implies a felt quality of fit or agreeableness between the inner person and the object; (3) **Less directional than Delight** — Delight is always toward a specific treasured object; Pleasure is more ambient, received from surroundings, persons, and circumstances rather than focused on a single treasured object; (4) **Less active than Joy** — Pleasure is the inner being at ease in what is agreeable rather than actively exulting or rejoicing.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The characteristic is called Wonder. The name signals: (1) **Arrested quality** — Wonder names an inner state that is stilled rather than surging; the person in Wonder is arrested by what they encounter, not actively exulting; (2) **Receptive-perceptive** — Wonder is specifically a response to encounter, not an initiation; the inner being encounters something beyond itself and Wonder is the result; (3) **Breadth of register** — the single word "Wonder" covers the positive (marvelling at God's deeds), the cognitive (encountering the incomprehensible), and the negative (appalling dark astonishment); the name's breadth is a programmatic signal that the characteristic spans all three; (4) **Distinctness** — the name distinguishes this from Exultation (which surges), Joy (which participates), Gladness (which settles in the good), Delight (which rests in the beloved), and Pleasure (which receives the agreeable).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The characteristic is called Suffering-Joy. The hyphenated name signals: (1) **Paradox** — the name holds two apparently contradictory states together as a single inner-being reality, not as a compromise between them; (2) **Directionality** — "Suffering" precedes "Joy" in the name, indicating that suffering is the context within which Joy arises; (3) **Distinctness from Joy and Gladness** — the name signals that this is neither Joy (which rejoices in what is good) nor Gladness (which is the warm inner state of one whose circumstances are assessed as good) but a third positive inner-being state that specifically arises through suffering. The name correctly orients the enquiry toward a paradoxical inner capacity, not a surface emotion.

---

##### T1.1.2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The primary OT terms are: **gil_verb** (H1523 — to rejoice, exult; verbal form of the root that names spinning or leaping movement, capturing the kinetic energy of the inner state); **su.s** (H7797 — to rejoice, exult, take delight in; used both for human and divine exultation, with a strong affective-volitional force); **re.na.nah** (H7445 — triumphing joy, joyful crying, exultant sound; the sonic-expressive form of exultation); **cha.dah** (H2302 — to rejoice, be glad, more infrequent; used notably for Jethro's rejoicing at hearing of God's works, Exo 18:9); **te.ev** (H2868, Aramaic — to be glad, used in Dan 6:23 of the king's exceedingly glad response at Daniel's safety). No primary Greek term appears in this characteristic's corpus — M04-A is entirely OT. The root meanings consistently emphasise movement (spinning, leaping — gil), affective intensity and relational direction (su.s), and sonic expression (re.na.nah) — suggesting exultation is constitutively outward-moving, not merely interior.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Primary terms across the four sub-groups:

**OT (M04-B, M04-E):** **sa.mach** (H8055 — to rejoice, be glad; verb; the dominant term with 147 instances in M04-B, appearing across every literary register); **sim.chah** (H8057 — joy, gladness; noun; 89 instances in M04-B; names the state that sa.mach produces); **sa.me.ach** (H8056 — joyful, glad; adjective; 21 instances in M04-B; describes the person in the state of joy); **ma.s.vo.s** (H4885 — joy, exultation, rejoicing; noun; 16 instances in M04-B; often associated with festive and communal contexts); **sa.s.von** (H8342 — gladness, joy, exultation; noun; 22 instances in M04-E; strongly restoration-oriented); **gi.lah** (H1525 — rejoicing, exultation; noun; 2 instances in M04-E); **ched.vah** (H2304 — joy, gladness; Aramaic/Hebrew; 2 instances in M04-C-VCG-01 and M04-D-VCG-01).

**NT (M04-C, M04-D, M04-E):** **chairo** (G5463 — to rejoice, be glad; verb; 58 instances in M04-C; the primary NT rejoicing verb); **chara** (G5479 — joy; noun; 57 instances in M04-C; names the state); **agalliao** (G0021 — to exult, rejoice greatly; verb; 11 instances in M04-E-VCG-02; a more intense exultant-joy term); **agalliasis** (G0020 — exultation, joy; noun; 4 instances in M04-C); **eufrosune** (G2167 — gladness, good cheer; 2 instances in M04-C); **sunchairo** (G4796 — to rejoice with, co-rejoice; verb; 8 instances in M04-D); **eucharistia/eucharistos** (G2169/2170 — thanksgiving/thankful; M04-C-VCG-06); **euthumeō/eupsucheō** (G2114/2174 — to be cheerful, encouraged; M04-C-VCG-04).

At the definitional level, the primary roots consistently name an inner state of positive, engaged, participatory gladness (sa.mach/chairo — active rejoicing; sim.chah/chara — the resulting inner state of joy). The Aramaic ched.vah and Greek eufrosune confirm the characteristic's cross-linguistic stability.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **tov** (H2896A) — the dominant term across both sub-groups (83 M04-L instances + 50 M04-O instances = 133 total). Tov as noun/adjective/verbal-function names the quality of genuine goodness — pleasant, beneficial, agreeable, right, fitting. At the definitional level it reveals Gladness as rooted in objective goodness rather than subjective preference; (2) **makarismos** (G3108) — blessedness; 3 NT instances in M04-O-VCG-04 (Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15). Makarismos names the inner state of one who has received divine favour; (3) **sa.s.von** (H8342) — appears in the M04-E-VCG-01 corpus which overlaps with Characteristic 3 at the VCG-01 level (sa.s.von as gladness-of-restoration). At definitional level: tov's breadth (moral, relational, circumstantial, divine-character goodness) establishes Gladness as the widest-scope positive inner-being characteristic in M04 — broader than Joy (which has its own primary vocabulary), though the two share the experience.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Primary terms span a wide vocabulary: (1) **sha.a.shu.im** (H8191) — delights, cherished things (noun, plural of intensity): used of God's darling child Ephraim (Jer 31:20), Wisdom as God's daily delight (Pro 8:30–31), the psalmist's delight in God's testimonies (Psa 119:24, 77, 92, 143, 174), Isa 5:7 (Israel as God's pleasant planting), Jer 31:20. The plural-of-intensity form signals the full, rich, multiple-faceted quality of treasured pleasure; (2) **sha.a** (H8173B) — to delight, play, carefree enjoyment: Psa 94:19 (God's consolations cheer the soul); Psa 119:16, 47, 70 (delight in statutes); Isa 11:8 (nursing child playing over cobra); Isa 66:12 (bounced on knees in peace); the root carries a carefree, playful quality of delight; (3) **a.nog** (H6026) — to be delicate, to delight oneself: Psa 37:4, 11; Job 22:26; 27:10; Isa 55:2; 58:14; 66:11; Deu 28:56 — the term implies a luxuriating, resting, pampered quality of inner satisfaction; (4) **o.neg** (H6027) — delight as noun (Isa 58:13); (5) **cha.phets** (H2654A) — verbal: to take delight in, to be pleased, to desire — the dominant M04-H verbal form covering both divine volitional pleasure and human desire/delight; (6) **che.phets** (H2656) — noun: delight, desire, matter — the dominant M04-H nominal form; (7) **cha.phets** adj (H2655) — delighting in; (8) **eudokeo** (G2106) — to be well pleased, think it good, take delight: 17 NT instances across M04-H-VCG-01 (divine pleasure in the Son) and VCG-02 (human willing-pleasure); (9) **arestos** (G0701) — pleasing, acceptable: M04-M-VCG-02 (Joh 8:29; Act 6:2; 1Jo 3:22); (10) **sunēdomai** (G4913) — to delight together with: Rom 7:22 (delight in God's law in the inner being); (11) **ta.a.nug** (H8588) — daintiness, delight: Mic 1:16 (parental delight); (12) **che.med** (H2531) — desire, delight, covetousness: Eze 23:6, 12, 23 (lustful captivation); (13) **a.li.tsut** (H5951) — exultation, predatory joy: Hab 3:14; (14) **ni.cho.ach** (H5207) — soothing aroma: M04-M-VCG-01 (correct worship) and M04-P-VCG-01 (misdirected worship); (15) **thaumazō** (G2296) — to marvel, wonder: Rev 13:3; 17:8 (beast-captivation). At definitional level: the vocabulary spans from playful carefree pleasure (sha.a) through luxuriating satisfaction (a.nog) through cherished treasuring (sha.a.shu.im) through directed volitional willing (cha.phets/eudokeo) through obedient-pleasing orientation (arestos) through corrupt-lustful desire (che.med) to predatory elation (a.li.tsut).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **na.im** (H5273A) — pleasant, agreeable, lovely; 8 instances in M04-J; root na.em — to be pleasant, agreeable; the quality of what is fitting and agreeable to the inner sense; Psa 133:1; 135:3; 147:1; Psa 16:6; Job 36:11; Song 1:16; 2Sa 1:23; Pro 22:18; (2) **na.em** (H5276) — to be/feel pleasant; 7 instances in M04-J; the verbal experience of pleasantness; 2Sa 1:26 — "very pleasant have you been to me"; Pro 2:10 — "knowledge will be pleasant to your soul"; Pro 9:17; 24:25; Song 7:6; Psa 141:6; Isa 32:12; (3) **no.am** (H5278) — pleasantness, beauty, favour; 5 instances in M04-J; the noun naming the quality: Psa 27:4 (Lord's beauty); Psa 90:17 (Lord's favour); Pro 3:17 (wisdom's ways); Pro 15:26; 16:24; Zec 11:7, 10; (4) **na.a.man** (H5282) — pleasant plants: Isa 17:10; (5) **ni.cho.ach** (H5207) — soothing, pleasing (aroma); 38 instances in M04-K-VCG-01 — the dominant term for the sacrificial-worship Pleasure register; root: to rest, settle, give rest; the quality of the worship-aroma that calms and settles God's regard; (6) **a.nog** (H6026) — to be tender/delicate/luxuriant: Deu 28:54, 56 (the pampered person); Isa 47:1 (Babylon's delicateness); (7) **a.las** (H5965) — to exult, delight (in pleasure): Job 20:18 (the wicked gets no a.las from profits); Pro 7:18 (seductress's carnal a.las); (8) **ta.a.nug** (H8588) — daintiness, luxury: Pro 19:10 (luxury unfit for fools); Ecc 2:8 (concubines as "delight of the sons of man"); Mic 2:9 (delightful houses); Song 7:6; (9) **ed.nah** (H5730B) — pleasure, luxury: 2Sa 1:24 (luxurious scarlet); Psa 36:8 (river of delights); Jer 51:34 (Jerusalem's delicacies consumed); (10) **tov** (H2896A) in the M04-K-VCG-03 better-than-comparatives; (11) **thambeō** (G2284) — to be amazed: Mar 10:24 (disciples amazed at Jesus' teaching). At definitional level: the vocabulary cluster reveals Pleasure as covering a spectrum from the lightest agreeableness (na.im — pleasant, fitting) through the sensory-luxury of delicate living (a.nog, ta.a.nug, ed.nah) through the worship-pleasantness of correctly-offered sacrifice (ni.cho.ach) through the moral-comparative Pleasure of preferring integrity (tov better-than).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **pa.la** (H6381) — to be extraordinary, surpassing, beyond ordinary; 47 instances in M04-I; the dominant term; root meaning: to be distinct, separated out from the ordinary; at definitional level: Wonder is the response to what is 'separated out' from ordinary reality — what cannot be accounted for by normal categories; (2) **pe.le** (H6382) — wonder, marvel; the nominal form: Exo 15:11 ("doing wonders"); Isa 9:6 ("Wonderful Counselor"); Psa 77:11 ("wonders of old"); Isa 25:1; 28:29; Lam 1:9; Dan 12:6; 7 instances; (3) **miph.la.ah** (H4652) — wondrous work: Job 37:16 ("the wondrous works of him who is perfect in knowledge"); (4) **thambeō** (G2284) — to be amazed/seized with astonishment: Mar 1:27; 10:24; 10:32; the NT wonder term involving being seized with astonishment at Jesus' teaching and advance; (5) **thauma** (G2295) — wonder, marvel: 2Cor 11:14; Rev 17:6; (6) **thaumazō** (G2296) — to marvel, be astonished: Gal 1:6; Rev 17:6, 7, 8 (M04-N-VCG-02 cross-assigned). At definitional level: pa.la/pe.le names Wonder as the response to what is categorically extraordinary; thambeō names Wonder as the inner state of being seized/arrested by what is confronted; thauma names the wondering itself as an experience.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **agalliao** (G0021) — to exult, leap for joy, rejoice greatly; 11 instances in M04-E-VCG-02. Root meaning: to exult, from agan (very much) + hallesthai (to leap) — the intensified-leaping form of joy. At definitional level: agalliao names an intense, outward-reaching, Spirit-enabled rejoicing that is characteristically present when circumstances offer no natural ground for joy. Its appearance in suffering contexts (1Pe 1:6; 4:13; Mat 5:12; Act 16:34) is not despite its intensity but because of it — the intensity is required to leap over the suffering context; (2) **ba.lag** (H1082) — to smile, to be cheerful; 3 instances in M04-F-VCG-01 (Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13). Root meaning: to gleam, smile; connotes a fragile, brief brightening — the opposite of agalliao's intensity; (3) **mav.li.git** (H4010) — consolation, comfort (1 instance: Jer 8:18). Root meaning related to comfort and solace. At definitional level: the three terms together span the full range from fragile attempted cheerfulness (ba.lag) through grief-without-comfort (mav.li.git) to Spirit-enabled exultation (agalliao) — the characteristic has a wide phenomenological range within its suffering-context definition.

---

##### T1.1.3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, all three. Directional: the evidence shows exultation consistently moving toward an object — "exult in your name" (Psa 89:16), "rejoice in the Lord" (Psa 32:11), "exult in his salvation" (Psa 35:9), "rejoice over you" (Zep 3:17). The characteristic is inherently directional. Relational: the dominant register is the divine-human relation — exultation is the inner state produced by and directed toward the covenant relationship. Constitutional: the evidence explicitly names the soul (Psa 35:9; 63:5; Isa 61:10), the heart (Psa 13:5; 32:11; 66:14; Zec 10:7), and the whole being (Psa 16:9) as constitutional loci, and extends to the bones (Psa 51:8) as the body's participation in the state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

All three. **Directional**: joy consistently requires an object — "rejoice in the Lord" (Deu 12:7; Psa 32:11; Phili 4:4); "rejoice at his birth" (Luk 1:14); "rejoice in hope" (Rom 12:12). The name implies directionality. **Relational**: the sunchairo corpus (M04-D) and the Pauline joy (1Th 2:19–20; Phili 4:1; 3Jo 3–4) show joy as constitutively relational — persons are described as the content of joy. The name carries the implication of joy-between-persons. **Constitutional**: the heart is the most frequently named constitutional locus across both OT and NT (Exo 4:14 — "glad in his heart"; Psa 4:7 — "more joy in my heart"; Psa 33:21 — "heart is glad in him"; Pro 15:13 — "glad heart makes a cheerful face"; Jer 15:16 — "joy and the delight of my heart"; Joh 16:22 — "your hearts will rejoice"; Song 3:11 — "gladness of his heart"). Joy is constitutionally located in the heart.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Moderate directional, strong cognitive, moderate relational implications: (1) **Cognitive-directional**: tov consistently points toward an object that is good — the glad person is glad about or in something; M04-L's evaluative appraisals ("better than," "not good," "good to those who wait") always name an object or situation; M04-O's circumstantial responses always have an occasion; (2) **Relational**: the "good man" (Pro 12:2; 13:22; 14:14) and the relational comparatives (Rut 4:15; 2Sa 18:3) show Gladness as relationally-embedded — it arises in and from relationships; (3) **Constitutional**: unlike Exultation and Joy, Gladness's primary constitutional language is not "heart" first — the tov corpus is more frequently directed at objects, circumstances, and character than at the heart's location. The heart is named in specific instances (Ecc 5:20; Jer 15:16 — but these are M04-E sa.s.von rather than M04-L/O tov), revealing Gladness as somewhat more cognitively-distributed than heart-centred.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Directional**: Delight always has an object it is directed toward — the directional implication is the most distinctive feature; Psa 73:25 ("there is nothing on earth that I desire besides you") shows Delight at its most purely directional — entirely toward God; (2) **Relational**: the relational implications are pervasive — Delight in persons (parental: Jer 31:20; Mic 1:16; interpersonal: 1Sa 19:1; Psa 16:3; 1Th 2:8; divine-human: Psa 18:19; Isa 62:4) shows that Delight is fundamentally relational in most of its registers; (3) **Constitutional**: Rom 7:22 ("in my inner being") is the most explicit constitutional location statement in the corpus — the deepest layer of the self; Mat 12:18's "my soul is well pleased" locates divine Delight in the soul (psychē); (4) **Volitional**: the cha.phets/che.phets vocabulary implies an act or orientation of the will — Delight is not merely felt but chosen and directed.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Receptive rather than directed** — the na.im/na.em vocabulary consistently describes a quality the inner person receives or recognises rather than generates or directs; (2) **Relational** — most M04-J instances are relational: Psa 133:1 (brotherly pleasantness), 2Sa 1:26 (Jonathan's pleasantness to David), Song 1:16; 7:6 (beloved's pleasantness), Pro 2:10 (wisdom pleasant to the soul), Pro 16:24 (gracious words nourishing soul and body); (3) **Constitutional** — Pro 2:10 names the soul explicitly ("pleasant to your soul"), Pro 16:24 names both soul and body ("sweetness to the soul and health to the body"); Pleasure is constitutionally distributed across soul and body in a way that no other M04 characteristic is as explicitly.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Directional** — Wonder is consistently directed toward God's acts and character (VCG-01 and VCG-02) or toward extraordinary events (VCG-03); it always has an object that exceeds ordinary categories; (2) **Cognitive** — Wonder specifically engages the cognitive-perceptive faculty; Job 37:5 ("great things that we cannot comprehend") names the cognitive limit as the trigger for Wonder; Wonder is constitutionally located at the boundary of comprehension; (3) **Relational-asymmetrical** — Wonder is not a symmetric characteristic; it is experienced by the lesser before the greater; the creature wonders at the Creator; Mar 10:32 (thambeō at Jesus' advance toward Jerusalem) shows Wonder as a response to one who is greater than oneself and who one cannot fully understand.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Directional** — agalliao is consistently directed toward a specific ground: God my Savior (Luk 1:47), the Father's gracious revelation (Luk 10:21), the unseen Christ believed in (1Pe 1:8), the future glory (1Pe 4:13), Christ's day (Joh 8:56). The name implies a Godward or eschatological direction for the joy component; (2) **Relational** — Act 16:34 (the jailer and his entire household) and Mat 5:12 (the persecuted community) show the characteristic operating in relational and communal contexts; (3) **Constitutional** — Luk 1:47 ("my spirit rejoices") explicitly names the spirit level; Luk 10:21 ("rejoiced in the Holy Spirit") confirms Spirit-level constitutional location as primary for agalliao.

---

#### T1.2 — Kind

##### T1.2.1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence shows exultation operating as both an **act** and a **disposition**. As an act: Psa 35:9 ("my soul will rejoice") and Hab 3:18 ("yet I will rejoice") are volitional, deliberate acts of exultation chosen despite circumstances. Psa 118:24 ("let us rejoice and be glad in it") is a commanded act. As a disposition: Psa 89:16 describes exulting "all the day" — a sustained inner orientation, not a momentary act. The commands throughout (Psa 2:11; 32:11; Isa 65:18; 66:10; Zec 9:9) presuppose that exultation can be a cultivated orientation, not only a spontaneous response. The characteristic is primarily **an act that can become a sustained disposition** — the volitional-affective surge that, when habituated, orients the whole inner life Godward.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence shows Joy operating as all four, but primarily as a **disposition that generates acts**: (1) **Disposition** — "Rejoice in the Lord always" (Phili 4:4; 1Th 5:16) names joy as a standing inner orientation, not a momentary act; (2) **Act** — the commanded feast-rejoicings (Deu 16:11, 14; Lev 23:40) and the responsive rejoicings (Exo 4:14; 1Sa 6:13; Dan 6:23; Mat 28:8) are discrete inner-being acts; (3) **Condition** — "fullness of joy" (Psa 16:11; Joh 15:11; 16:24) names Joy as a state of being the person can inhabit fully or partially; (4) **Quality** — "joyful heart is good medicine" (Pro 17:22); "receiving food with glad and generous hearts" (Act 2:46) — joy as an inner quality that colours the whole of a person's engagement with life. The dominant register across the corpus is joy as a disposition that expresses itself through acts of rejoicing in specific circumstances while remaining the standing inner orientation of the covenant person.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness operates as a **condition and a quality** more than as an act: (1) **Condition** — "it is well with the man who deals generously" (Psa 112:5); "it shall be well with you" (Deu 19:13); Saul "was refreshed and was well" (1Sa 16:23) — these name an inner state of being-well, not an act of doing; (2) **Quality** — "a good man" (Pro 12:2; 13:22) names goodness as a stable character quality; "the Lord is good" (Psa 100:5) names divine goodness as an intrinsic attribute; (3) **Evaluative act** — M04-L-VCG-02's "better than" comparatives (Rut 4:15; 2Sa 18:3; Pro 8:11; 16:16) show Gladness as an act of judgment; but even here the act is a cognitive recognition rather than an affective surge. Gladness is primarily a condition/quality that the evaluative faculty perceives and the inner person inhabits.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is a complex phenomenon spanning four kinds: (1) **Disposition** — the most common form: a stable inner orientation toward a specific object (sha.a.shu.im in Psa 119 series — the law as the psalmist's settled delight; Psa 1:2 — the blessed man's delight in the law as a defining character disposition; Psa 73:25 — God as the exclusive object of directed desire); (2) **Act** — cha.phets frequently marks a specific act of will: Gen 34:19 (Shechem's delight driving immediate action); Psa 40:8 (delighting to do God's will); the diplomatic "as it pleases you" idiom throughout M04-H-VCG-03; (3) **State** — a.nog (Psa 37:4, 11) and sha.a (Isa 66:12) name a resting, luxuriating condition of the inner being; (4) **Quality** — arestos (pleasing, acceptable) and ni.cho.ach (soothing aroma) name a quality of what the inner being produces or embodies before God. Delight is therefore an inner-being phenomenon that is simultaneously a disposition directing the will, an act of the will choosing its object, a state of resting satisfaction in the found object, and a quality of the person before God.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is primarily a **quality** and **condition** rather than an act or disposition: (1) **Quality** — na.im/na.em/no.am name a quality of what is pleasant (Psa 133:1 — unity is pleasant; Pro 3:17 — wisdom's ways are pleasantness); (2) **Condition** — the state of pleasantness enjoyed or inhabited: Psa 16:6 (lines fallen in pleasant places — an inherited condition); Job 36:11 (years in pleasantness — a condition of life); Psa 16:11 (pleasures at God's right hand — a permanent condition); (3) **Receptive experience** — Pro 2:10 (knowledge "will be pleasant to your soul" — a felt inner experience received when wisdom enters); Pro 16:24 (gracious words as received nourishment); (4) **Divine inner state** — Gen 8:21 (God's inner calmed response to ni.cho.ach — a state of settled reception). Pleasure is primarily the quality-condition of what is agreeable, received and inhabited by the inner person, rather than an act directed outward.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is primarily a **state** (a perceptual-cognitive inner condition) that is **momentarily arrested**: (1) **State** — "they were all amazed" (Mar 1:27 — thambeō); "I am fearfully and wonderfully made" (Psa 139:14 — an ongoing recognition, not a momentary act); "things too wonderful for me" (Job 42:3 — an inner state of humility before the incomprehensible); (2) **Response-event** — thambeō in Mark is consistently a sudden inner seizure: Mar 1:27 ("they were all amazed"); Mar 10:32 ("they were amazed"); (3) **Sustained contemplative orientation** — VCG-01's "tell of / proclaim / remember / meditate on" verbs (Psa 26:7; 71:17; 119:27; 145:5) show Wonder as sustained contemplative engagement, not merely a momentary flash; (4) **Cognitive-humility condition** — Psa 131:1 ("I do not occupy myself with things too marvellous for me") — Wonder as a sustained epistemological posture of not overreaching one's cognitive capacity.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is primarily an **act with dispositional grounding**: (1) **Act** — Mat 5:12 ("rejoice and be glad"); 1Pe 4:13 ("rejoice insofar as you share Christ's sufferings") — commanded active responses requiring volitional engagement; Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") — a deliberate cognitive-volitional act of reframing; (2) **State** — 1Pe 1:8's "joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory" names an ongoing inner state, not a momentary act; the jailer's rejoicing (Act 16:34) is a state that encompasses his entire household in a moment of post-crisis stability; (3) **Fragile attempted condition** — M04-F (ba.lag in Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13) shows Suffering-Joy attempted as a desired condition that the sufferer cannot fully reach. The characteristic therefore spans from the attempted (M04-F) through the commanded-volitional (Mat 5:12; Jas 1:2) to the Spirit-produced state (1Pe 1:8; Luk 10:21).

---

##### T1.2.2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence reveals constituent elements: (1) **the object** — exultation requires a specific object toward which it is directed; in this corpus it is overwhelmingly YHWH, his salvation, his name, his judgments, his reign; (2) **the inner state** — the affective surge of triumph and delight; (3) **the expressive dimension** — re.na.nah (triumphing cry, Psa 63:5; 100:2) and the repeated pattern of rejoicing-and-shouting show that exultation is constitutively expressive, moving from inner to outer; (4) **the volitional element** — the commands and the "yet I will rejoice" of Hab 3:18 show exultation also involves the will's active engagement. These four elements are always present though weighted differently per context.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy has multiple constituent elements evidenced across the 15 VCGs: (1) **Object-directedness** — a specific cause or object of joy is almost always named or implied (God's salvation, the Lord himself, the restored community, the gospel, the repentant sinner, the festival, the spouse, the child's wisdom); (2) **Volitional element** — the commanded nature of feast-joy (Deu) and NT commands ("Rejoice always" — 1Th 5:16; "Count it all joy" — Jas 1:2) show the will as a constituent; (3) **Affective element** — the heart and soul's gladness is the inner state itself; (4) **Communal element** — feast-joy is inherently social; sunchairo is inherently shared; Pauline joy is consistently relational; (5) **Expressive element** — joy consistently moves outward into singing, shouting, dancing, praise; (6) **Eschatological element** — sa.s.von and agalliao in M04-E show joy as forward-oriented toward restoration. Joy is structurally complex but coherent — these elements are not in tension but constitute the full inner-being experience of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Complex — two clearly distinct constituent elements map to the two sub-groups: (1) **The evaluative-cognitive face** (M04-L) — the inner faculty of moral and relational appraisal that perceives, names, and settles in what is genuinely good; this includes the divine evaluative act (VCG-01), human moral appraisal (VCG-02), and wisdom's surpassing-worth recognition (VCG-03); (2) **The experiential-circumstantial face** (M04-O) — the warm inner response to beneficial circumstance, good news, covenantal promise, and received wellbeing. The two faces are linked: the evaluative act (M04-L) produces the recognition that enables the experiential warmth (M04-O). A person who correctly evaluates that God's good promises are reliable will inhabit the warm inner gladness that such confidence produces. The integration_note carry-forward (M04-L as cognitive face, M04-O as experiential face) is confirmed as the structural key to Gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The most structurally complex characteristic in M04 — five distinct constituent registers correspond to the five sub-groups: (1) **Affective-receptive delight in God's word and God himself** (M04-G) — the soul's pleasurable orientation toward its divine object, sustained through meditation and resistant to adversity (sha.a.shu.im, sha.a, a.nog, sunēdomai); (2) **Volitional delight as directed will** (M04-H) — both divine sovereign pleasure and human directed desire; spans four VCGs: divine sovereignty (28), God's relational pleasure in persons (31), human volitional willing (105), negated/corrupt pleasure (20); (3) **Obedience-delight: the inner orientation toward what pleases God** (M04-M) — the soul directed toward what is acceptable (arestos, ni.cho.ach, tov-in-obedience); (4) **Relational horizontal delight** (M04-N) — pleasantness between persons (ta.a.nug, tov, thaumazō); (5) **Corrupt and misdirected delight** (M04-P) — the disordered face (ni.cho.ach misdirected, che.med lustful, a.li.tsut predatory). The structural complexity is itself analytically significant: Delight is the characteristic most fully showing the range from rightly-ordered inner pleasure to its complete corruption.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Two distinct constituent elements mapped to the two sub-groups: (1) **Relational-personal pleasantness** (M04-J) — the agreeableness of persons, bonds, speech, wisdom, and God's own beauty; the inner being's capacity to register and inhabit what is genuinely pleasant in relationships and in God; (2) **Sensory-material pleasure and worship-pleasure** (M04-K) — spanning four registers: (a) the soothing-aroma worship-Pleasure of correctly-offered sacrifice (VCG-01 ni.cho.ach, 38 verses); (b) sensory luxury and pampered ease (VCG-02 — a.nog, ta.a.nug, a.las, ed.nah); (c) the wisdom better-than comparatives (VCG-03 — tov) where material Pleasure is calibrated against moral worth; (d) the cross-assigned instances (Psa 34:8 taste-and-see, Zec 8:19 cheerful feasts, Mar 10:24 disciples' amazement). The characteristic is therefore structurally more complex than its "Pleasure" name implies: it spans the most refined relational warmth (Jonathan's companionship) through the most formal worship-Pleasure (ni.cho.ach) through the morally-calibrated better-than comparatives.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Three constituent registers mapped to the three VCGs: (1) **Proclaimed and proclaimed-remembered Wonder** (VCG-01, 61 verses) — wonder at God's extraordinary acts in history and creation, expressed in proclamation, thanksgiving, memory, and praise; the dominant and most positive register; (2) **Wonder as incomprehensibility** (VCG-02, 13 verses) — the pa.la/pe.le family used to name what is too extraordinary/impossible for human cognitive reach: Gen 18:14; Deu 17:8; 30:11; Jer 32:17, 27; Isa 29:14; Job 42:3; Psa 131:1; 2Cor 11:14; (3) **Dark wonder** (VCG-03, 10 verses) — Wonder inverted into dread, appalling shock, or troubled astonishment: Job 10:16 (wonders worked against Job); Dan 8:24; 11:36 (fearful destruction, astonishing blasphemy); Lam 1:9 (terrible fall); Mar 10:32 (awe-mixed-with-fear); Gal 1:6 (Paul's troubled astonishment); Rev 17:6, 7 (John's great marvelling at the harlot).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two constituent elements map directly to the two sub-groups: (1) **The Spirit-enabled exultation register** (M04-E-VCG-02 agalliao) — the intense, outward-reaching joy that arises through and within suffering, produced by the Spirit (Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6 — adjacent), grounded in eschatological reality (Mat 5:12; 1Pe 4:13), and participatory in Christ's own suffering-to-glory pattern (Heb 12:2); (2) **The fragile-composure register** (M04-F-VCG-01 ba.lag/mav.li.git) — the barely-attainable, desired but elusive inner comfort under extreme adversity, the tenuous attempted cheerfulness of the deeply suffering person. These two registers represent the same inner-being capacity at its Spirit-empowered fullest (agalliao) and its unaided fragile minimum (ba.lag) — the full range of Suffering-Joy from empowered paradox to fragile attempt.

---

##### T1.2.3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is the soul's active, surging, triumphant inner act of rising toward God in response to his reality — his reign, salvation, presence, goodness, and acts of deliverance. Constitutionally located in the soul and heart, and expressed through the whole person including the body, it is a volitional-affective act that can become a sustained inner orientation. It is inherently directional (always toward an object), inherently relational (arising from and directed at the divine-human covenant), and inherently expressive (moving from inner state to outer declaration). Its most concentrated constitutional home is the heart-soul axis; its most characteristic expression is the triumphing cry.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is the active inner experience of rejoicing — a volitional-affective inner state that engages the whole person (heart, soul, whole being) in response to what is genuinely good and worth celebrating. It is constitutionally located primarily in the heart, expressed outwardly through singing and shout, directed toward a specific object (God himself, restored relationship, the gospel, the beloved community), cultivated as a standing inner disposition, capable of transcending adverse circumstances, and oriented toward an eschatological fullness in which all partial present joy is completed. It is distinguished from Exultation by less surging intensity and broader scope of occasions; from Gladness by its active-engaged rather than warm-diffuse character; from Delight by its orientation toward celebration and participation rather than treasuring; from Pleasure by its communal and directed rather than receptive character.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is the inner state of settled, warm, positive brightness arising from accurate evaluation and recognition of what is genuinely good — in God's character, in circumstances, in persons, and in received blessedness. It is constituted by two integrated faces: an evaluative-cognitive face (the soul's assessment that something is good, better, or surpassing, grounded in moral and relational discernment) and an experiential-circumstantial face (the warm inner response to beneficial news, covenantal goodness, and circumstances assessed as genuinely good). It is less active than Joy (which rejoices in something) and more diffuse: it pervades the inner condition as a quality of being rather than an act of doing. Its primary constitutional home is distributed across cognitive and affective faculties without strong dominance of either.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the inner state of treasuring and taking pleasure in a specific object — the soul's resting satisfaction in what it loves. It is more object-focused than Gladness (which is a diffuse evaluative warmth) and more receptive than Exultation (which is an active upward surge). The person who delights has found an object that satisfies their inner being: they rest in it, return to it, orient themselves toward it. The characteristic operates in two primary integrated modes: an affective-receptive mode (sha.a.shu.im, sha.a, a.nog — the soul's pleasurable resting in a specific treasured object: God's law, God himself, wisdom, restored Zion) and a volitional-directive mode (cha.phets/che.phets/eudokeo — the will's directed inner pleasure that motivates action and expresses sovereign purpose). These two modes are not separate characteristics but the same inner-being capacity operating through different faculties — affect and will — on a treasured object. Constitutional primary location: the inner being (Rom 7:22), the heart (Psa 40:8; 1:2), and the soul (Mat 12:18). The characteristic also carries an obedience-orientation face (M04-M), a relational-horizontal face (M04-N), and a corrupt face (M04-P).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is the inner-being experience of pleasantness — the felt quality of agreeableness received from persons, relationships, creation, and material or sensory experience. It is the soul's positive receptive response to what is pleasant. Less directed than Delight (which focuses on a specific treasured object) and less active than Joy — Pleasure is the inner being's sense of agreeableness and satisfying ease in what surrounds it. The primary modes: (a) relational pleasantness — the agreeableness of persons, bonds, and speech; (b) worship-pleasure — the soothing reception of correctly offered sacrifice by God; (c) sensory-material pleasure — the comfortable ease of pampered living, properly calibrated by wisdom; (d) morally-calibrated comparative Pleasure — the wisdom verdict that modest integrity is more genuinely pleasant than corrupt abundance. Constitutional location: the soul (Pro 2:10), the body (Pro 16:24), and by extension the whole person in creation (Psa 16:6; 36:8).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the inner state of astonishment and awe before what exceeds ordinary comprehension — the soul arrested and overwhelmed by what it cannot fully grasp. Wonder is the inner being stilled rather than surging: it confronts what is too great to simply rejoice at. In its primary register (VCG-01), it is a contemplative and perceptive response to God's marvellous works — expressed in proclamation, memory, thanksgiving, and meditation. In its incomprehensibility register (VCG-02), it is the inner acknowledgment of cognitive limits before what is too extraordinary to grasp. In its dark register (VCG-03), it is appalling awe before what is terrible or wrong. Constitutional location: primarily engaged at the perceptive-cognitive level, involving memory and proclamation as its primary expressive modes. Distinguished from Exultation by its arrested, contemplative character; from Joy by its perceptual-receptive rather than participatory character; from Pleasure by the scale and incomprehensibility of what it encounters.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is the paradoxical inner capacity to find genuine joy in and through suffering — not merely alongside it, not despite it, but as an inner state that the suffering context itself occasions or enables. In its Spirit-enabled form (agalliao, M04-E-VCG-02), it is an intense, outward-reaching exultation grounded in eschatological reality (the reward in heaven, the glory to be revealed, the unseen Christ believed in) that enables the inner being to genuinely rejoice even when present circumstances offer no natural ground for joy. In its fragile form (ba.lag, M04-F-VCG-01), it is the barely-attainable attempt at inner brightness under extreme adversity — the awareness of the capacity while feeling unable to access its fullness. Constitutional location: primarily at the spirit level (Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21), with heart and tongue as secondary (Act 2:26).

---

#### T1.3 — Boundary

##### T1.3.1 — What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence provides multiple structural opposites: (1) **joylessness as curse** — Job 3:6–7 wishes the birth-night to be barren of rejoicing (re.na.nah absent); Job 3:22 describes those who rejoice at finding the grave — a total inversion of the normal directedness of exultation; (2) **grief, weeping, distress** — Isa 65:19 sets rejoicing against "the sound of weeping and the cry of distress" as its explicit opposite; (3) **mourning** — Isa 16:10 names joy and gladness stripped from the fields as desolation; Joe 1:16 shows joy cut off from God's house; Jer 48:33 names gladness removed from Moab as judgment; (4) **absent-joy as curse** — Deu 28:63 shows that the same divine su.s that delights in doing Israel good can operate in bringing ruin. The structural opposite of exultation is the condition of the person or community from whom joy has been stripped or who has never been able to direct their inner being toward the true object.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple structural opposites are named across the corpus: (1) **Mourning** — Jer 31:13 ("turn mourning into joy"); Isa 61:3 ("oil of gladness instead of mourning"); Psa 30:11 ("turned my mourning into dancing"); (2) **Sorrow/grief** — Joh 16:20 ("you will be sorrowful, but your sorrow will turn into joy"); Jas 4:9 ("let your joy be turned to gloom"); (3) **Sighing** — Isa 35:10; 51:11 ("sorrow and sighing shall flee away" as joy arrives); (4) **Weeping and lamentation** — Joh 16:20 ("you will weep and lament, but the world will rejoice"); (5) **Groaning** — Heb 13:17 (leaders doing work "with joy and not with groaning"); (6) **Fear/dread** — Joe 2:21–23 (fear displaced by joy through God's acts). The structural opposite of Joy is the cluster of mourning-grief-sighing-weeping that Joy displaces and replaces, most fully in the eschatological reversal passages.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple structural opposites evidenced: (1) **Not-good / moral deficiency** — the most frequent, through tov's negation: "it is not good" (Exo 18:17; 1Sa 2:24; 2Sa 17:7; Neh 5:9; Pro 17:26; 18:5; 20:23; 24:23; 28:21; Eze 18:18; 20:25; Eze 36:31; Isa 65:2) — the structural opposite of moral gladness is moral deficiency or wrong; (2) **Sorrow, grief** — in M04-O's circumstantial register, the opposite of gladness as wellbeing is sorrow: Lam 3:26's "wait quietly" implies prior anguish; Jon 4:3, 8's despairing "better to die" is the extreme inversion of circumstantial gladness; Hos 2:7's nostalgic "better then than now" shows the absence of present gladness; (3) **Mourning** — M04-E-VCG-01's sa.s.von corpus which overlaps Gladness shows gladness as what replaces mourning: Jer 31:13 ("I will turn their mourning into joy"); (4) **Self-loathing** — Eze 36:31 shows the not-good evaluation turned inward producing self-loathing, the negative terminus of the evaluative-gladness faculty when applied to one's own past conduct.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple structural opposites: (1) **No delight / absence of pleasure** — the most frequent: God "has no pleasure in the death of the wicked" (Eze 18:23; 33:11); "my joy is gone" (Jer 8:18 — mav.li.git, the gone-comfort); "they take no pleasure in it" [God's word] (Jer 6:10); "I have no pleasure in you" (Mal 1:10); Ecc 12:1 — old age when pleasure drains away; (2) **Disgust and rejection** — the opposite of God's delight in persons: "like a vessel no one cares for" (Jer 22:28; 48:38 — che.phets negated as total rejection); (3) **Self-directed pleasure without God** — Isa 58:13 — "seeking your own pleasure" on the Sabbath as the opposite of delight in God; (4) **Corrupt delight** — M04-P shows delight directed at wrong objects: Isa 66:3 ("their soul delights in their abominations"); 2Th 2:12 (pleasure in unrighteousness); (5) **Mourning as loss of delight** — Deu 28:56 (the delicate woman losing her delicateness); Jer 7:34; 16:9 (voice of gladness silenced). The structural opposite cluster is: no-delight (total absence), rejected-delight (object withheld), and misdirected-delight (object corrupted).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple structural opposites: (1) **Harshness/roughness** — the na.im/na.em vocabulary implicitly stands against harshness; 1Sa 25:3 (Nabal's harsh inner character contrasted with Abigail's discernment — adjacent); Pro 15:26 (gracious/pleasant words pure vs. wicked's abominable thoughts); (2) **Denied pleasure** — Job 20:18 ("no enjoyment" — a.las absent); Deu 28:54, 56 (delicate person's pleasure destroyed by judgment); (3) **Unacceptable worship** — Lev 26:31 ("I will not smell your pleasing aromas") — the ni.cho.ach withheld when the covenant is broken; the structural opposite of worship-Pleasure is God's non-reception; (4) **Folly's false pleasantness** — Pro 9:17 (stolen bread "pleasant" — the structural opposite of genuine Pleasure is deceived pleasure that masquerades as genuinely agreeable but leads to death); (5) **Strife and hatred as the opposite of relational Pleasure** — Pro 15:17 ("better a dinner of herbs where love is than a fattened ox and hatred") — hatred is the structural opposite of the relational pleasantness that makes community agreeable.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple structural opposites: (1) **Failure to consider / forgetting** — the most frequently evidenced structural opposite in the corpus: Neh 9:17 ("not mindful of the wonders"); Psa 78:11 ("forgot his works and the wonders"); Psa 106:7 ("did not consider your wondrous works"); the structural opposite of Wonder is not denial but simply not-attending, not-registering, not-remembering; (2) **Unbelief** — Psa 78:32 ("despite his wonders, they did not believe") — Wonder-failure immediately preceding unbelief; the structural opposite runs from not-attending to not-believing; (3) **Presumption/Overreach** — Psa 131:1's restraint ("I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me") implies its opposite: the person who presumptuously occupies themselves with things beyond their comprehension — overreach as the structural opposite of humble Wonder; (4) **Dark wonder's opposite is true worship** — the dark wonder at the beast (Rev 17:6–7) is structurally opposed to the genuine Wonder of the redeemed who marvel only at God's acts.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The structural opposites evidenced: (1) **Grief/mourning as the dominant context** — 1Pe 1:6 ("grieved by various trials" stands alongside the rejoicing); Mat 5:12's context is persecution; Jas 1:2's context is trials. The structural opposite is not merely the absence of Suffering-Joy but its replacement by grief, mourning, and lament; (2) **Absent cheerfulness** — M04-F: Jer 8:18 ("my joy is gone; grief is upon me; my heart is sick within me") — the total absence of the characteristic's fragile register; (3) **Worldly rejoicing over wrong** — in the structural contrast of 1Pe 4:13 ("you may also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed" vs. the world that rejoices when Christ's witnesses are silenced — Rev 11:10) — the world's gloating over suffering is the inverted structural opposite of Suffering-Joy.

---

##### T1.3.2 — What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation excludes: (1) **self-directed triumph** — nowhere in M04-A-VCG-01 does exultation produce pride directed at the self; the consistently named object is God, his salvation, his name; (2) **enemy-triumph over the righteous** — Psa 13:4 expresses the psalmist's prayer that his enemy should not rejoice over his defeat; (3) **rejoicing at another's fall** — Pro 24:17 explicitly prohibits the heart's gladness over an enemy's stumbling; (4) **hollow joy on false grounds** — Hos 9:1 prohibits Israel's rejoicing because it is built on unfaithfulness; (5) **premature joy in the face of judgment** — Eze 21:10 ("shall we rejoice?") exposes the impossibility of exultation under the sword.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy explicitly excludes or resists: (1) **Rejoicing at evil** — 1Cor 13:6 ("love does not rejoice at wrongdoing"); Pro 24:17 ("do not rejoice when your enemy falls"); Job 31:29 (Job denying he rejoiced at enemy's ruin); (2) **Hollow festivity without covenant ground** — Isa 22:13 ("let us eat and drink, for tomorrow we die" — reckless joy-without-substance condemned); Ecc 2:1–2 (pleasure tested and found vain); (3) **Illegitimate joy** — Hos 9:1 ("rejoice not, O Israel, for you have played the whore"); (4) **Premature joy** — Isa 14:29 (Philistia warned not to rejoice at the broken rod); (5) **Self-focused delight** — Luk 10:20 (Jesus redirecting joy from power over spirits to the deeper ground of names written in heaven); (6) **Shallow surface-level joy** — Mat 13:20; Mar 4:16; Luk 8:13 (rocky-ground hearer receives word with joy but lacks root). Joy resists being rooted in wrong objects, shallow grounds, or morally corrupted directions.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness explicitly excludes: (1) **False evaluation** — Num 14:3 (preferring Egypt as better is fear-distorted evaluation, not true gladness); Jer 44:17 (misattributing former wellbeing to idol-worship); Isa 41:7 (the craftsman's self-congratulatory "it is good" over an idol) — Gladness resists evaluation that is not grounded in reality; (2) **Self-righteous entitlement** — Deu 9:6 ("not because of your righteousness") directly corrects the inner assumption that the good land was merited; (3) **Premature or shallow evaluation** — Hezekiah's self-serving reception of Isaiah's word as "good" (Isa 39:8) because it means peace in his own lifetime — Gladness resists the cognitive shortcut of evaluating as good only what benefits the self; (4) **Despair-assessment** — Jon 4:3, 8 (Jonah's "better to die") is the extreme distortion of the circumstantial-gladness faculty. Gladness resists any inner assessment that is not grounded in genuine moral and covenantal reality.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight explicitly excludes: (1) **External ritual without inner transformation** — Psa 40:6; 51:16; Isa 1:11; Heb 10:6, 8 — God's delight is not engaged by sacrifice and offering without the accompanying inner reality; "to obey is better than sacrifice" (1Sa 15:22; M04-M-VCG-02); Hos 6:6 — God's desire is steadfast love, not sacrifice; (2) **Self-seeking pleasure on holy time** — Isa 58:13 — "not going your own ways, or seeking your own pleasure" on the Sabbath; (3) **Delight in wrong objects** — Psa 5:4 — "you are not a God who delights in wickedness"; Isa 65:12; 66:4 — the people "chose what I did not delight in"; 1Cor 10:5 — God was not pleased with most of Israel in the wilderness; Heb 10:38 — God's soul has no pleasure in the one who shrinks back; (4) **Impulsive desire without knowledge** — Pro 19:2 — "desire without knowledge is not good"; (5) **Misdirected worship-delight** — M04-P-VCG-01 (ni.cho.ach aroma to idols — Eze 6:13; 16:19; 20:28).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure explicitly excludes: (1) **Worship without covenant faithfulness** — Lev 26:31 (God will not smell pleasing aromas from the unfaithful) — the ni.cho.ach pleasure-relationship is bounded by covenant obedience; (2) **Corrupt luxury** — Isa 47:1 (Babylon's delicateness about to be stripped — pampered ease built on evil must end); Pro 19:10 (luxury unfitting for fools); (3) **Illicit sensual pleasure** — Pro 7:18 (the seductress's a.las as carnal indulgence); (4) **Excess of pleasant things** — Pro 25:27 ("not good to eat much honey") — even genuine pleasantness becomes not-pleasant in excess; (5) **Self-serving pleasant words without moral reality** — Isa 58:2 (adjacent — delight to seek God but without justice) — Pleasure in worship without moral correspondence is explicitly rejected.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder explicitly excludes: (1) **Overreach** — Psa 131:1 ("I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me") — Wonder, rightly oriented, also restrains; not everything that is marvellous should be grasped at; (2) **Complacency** — the VCG-01 proclamation-commands ("tell of all his wondrous works"; "sing to him, sing praises; tell of") resist the complacency of forgetting; Wonder resists the drift toward treating God's extraordinary acts as ordinary; (3) **Dark wonder at evil** — the Rev 17:6–7 sequence where John wonders at the harlot and is immediately questioned ("why do you marvel?") — genuine Wonder resists marvelling at evil or at the adversary's apparent power without understanding; (4) **Wonder-failure under accumulation** — Isa 29:14 ("the wisdom of their wise men shall perish, and the discernment of their discerning men shall be hidden") — when human wisdom accumulates to the point of no longer recognising the extraordinary, Wonder resists this closure.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy explicitly excludes: (1) **Performed or hollow cheerfulness** — M04-F makes clear that ba.lag is not easy or automatic; Job 9:27's attempted cheerfulness immediately collapses — the characteristic is not a performance of happiness; (2) **Joy based on wrong grounds** — Joh 5:35 ("you were willing to rejoice for a while in his light") — the crowds' transient agalliao in John's light was real but shallowly grounded and did not endure; Suffering-Joy resists joy that lacks the depth to hold through difficulty; (3) **Denial of suffering** — 1Pe 1:6 ("though now for a little while, if necessary, you have been grieved") explicitly acknowledges the grief alongside the rejoicing; Suffering-Joy does not pretend suffering away; (4) **World-aligned rejoicing** — Rev 11:10 (earth-dwellers rejoicing over the prophets' deaths) — this is joy rooted in opposition to the gospel, not in participation in it.

---

##### T1.3.3 — What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is not Gladness (M04-O, M04-L), which is the settled warm inner brightness without the surge and directional intensity. Exultation is not Pleasure (M04-J, M04-K), which is the receptive agreeableness without the upward movement. Exultation is not Wonder (M04-I), which arrests and stills the inner being rather than surging it. The evidence clarifies the boundary with Joy (M04-B, M04-C): Psa 14:7 uses both gil_verb and sa.me.ach — "let Jacob rejoice (gil), let Israel be glad (sa.me.ach)" — in synonymous parallel, suggesting the boundary is porous in some usages; but the overall evidence pattern shows exultation (gil, su.s) as more intense, more directional, and more expressive than the broader gladness vocabulary.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is not: (1) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Gladness is the warm, settled, positive inner brightness; Joy is more active, directed, participatory, and commands engagement. The two co-occur frequently (Psa 51:8 — "joy and gladness"; Isa 35:10 — "gladness and joy") but are not identical. Gladness is the inner state of one who is well; Joy is the inner state of one actively rejoicing. (2) **Exultation** (Characteristic 1) — Exultation is more intense and surging, specifically Godward. Joy is broader in its occasions and less exclusively upward-directed. (3) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — Delight is the receptive inner state of treasuring a specific object; Joy is the active state of rejoicing in what is celebratable. Delight rests in its object; Joy engages with it. (4) **Pleasure** (Characteristic 5) — Pleasure is the inner-being's receptive agreeableness; Joy is engaged and participatory. (5) **Thanksgiving** — the eucharistia sub-corpus (M04-C-VCG-06) within this characteristic is adjacent to Joy but specifically concerns Godward gratitude; thanksgiving is an act of the will directed Godward; Joy is the inner state that thanksgiving often accompanies and expresses.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is not: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Joy is active, participatory, engaged; Gladness is settled, warm, and diffuse. The "joy and gladness" formulaic pairing (confirmed in Char 2 Phase 9) places them adjacent but distinct. Joy rejoices *in* something; Gladness is the inner condition of one whose assessment is settled in what is good; (2) **Exultation** (Characteristic 1) — Exultation surges upward; Gladness is warm and level; (3) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — Delight is the soul's treasuring orientation toward a specific object; Gladness is more broadly distributed across circumstances, persons, and evaluations; (4) **Pleasure** (Characteristic 5) — Pleasure is receptive agreeableness through sensory and material channels; Gladness is cognitively-grounded warm inner brightness; (5) **Suffering-Joy** (Characteristic 7) — Suffering-Joy arises paradoxically through suffering; Gladness is characteristically the inner state of one whose circumstances or evaluation confirm that things are genuinely well.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is not: (1) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Gladness is the warm, cognitively-grounded inner state of one who has accurately assessed that things are genuinely good; Delight is more object-focused and more explicitly directed at a specific treasured person or thing; the distinction is that Gladness is diffuse recognition, Delight is specific attachment; (2) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Joy is active participatory engagement; Delight is receptive resting satisfaction; Joy exults in, Delight rests in; (3) **Exultation** (Characteristic 1) — Exultation is the upward surge of the inner being; Delight is the inward settling toward the beloved object; (4) **Pleasure** (Characteristic 5) — Pleasure is the receptive inner agreeable sensation through sensory and material channels; Delight is more specifically object-oriented and includes the volitional direction of the will; (5) **Love** — Love's choosing and cherishing overlaps with Delight but Love carries a stronger volitional commitment; Delight is the pleasurable dimension of Love; (6) **Mere preference** — the M04-H-VCG-03 "as it seems good to you" diplomatic idiom is preference and practical judgment, not Delight's deeper affective-volitional anchoring in a treasured object; the spectrum within M04-H is wide, and the surface preference instances (Est, Neh diplomatic formulas) are at the thinner edge of Delight's range.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is not: (1) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — Delight is focused on a specific treasured object and is more volitionally directed; Pleasure is more ambient and receptive — it is the quality of what is agreeable rather than the orientation toward what is treasured; (2) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Joy actively participates; Pleasure passively receives; (3) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Gladness is the cognitively-evaluated inner warmth of settled goodness; Pleasure is more immediately sensory and relational in its receptive quality; (4) **Wonder** (Characteristic 6) — Wonder is the inner being arrested by what exceeds comprehension; Pleasure is the inner being at ease in what is agreeably familiar; (5) **Luxury or hedonism** — M04-K-VCG-02's luxury register (Deu 28; Isa 47; Ecc 2) shows Pleasure in its excessive or cursed form; the characteristic itself is the genuine reception of what is genuinely pleasant, not the self-indulgent pursuit of pleasure; (6) **Mere sensory stimulation** — the ni.cho.ach corpus shows God's Pleasure at worship as an inner settled response, not mere sensory input; divine Pleasure at the soothing aroma is a theologically substantial inner-being event, not primitive sensory reaction.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is not: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Joy actively participates; Wonder is arrested and contemplative; (2) **Exultation** (Characteristic 1) — Exultation surges upward in active response; Wonder stills the inner being before what exceeds it; (3) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Gladness is the settled warmth of one who has evaluated and found things genuinely good; Wonder is the arrested astonishment before what is too great to simply evaluate; (4) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — Delight rests in a specific treasured object; Wonder is arrested before what cannot be fully grasped or contained; (5) **Pleasure** (Characteristic 5) — Pleasure receives what is agreeably pleasant; Wonder is overwhelmed by what exceeds ordinary categories of agreeableness; (6) **Fear** — closely adjacent but distinct; Mar 10:32 shows them paired (amazed + afraid) but they are distinguished; Wonder is specifically the astonishment-component, not the threat-response.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is not: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Joy rejoices in what is genuinely good and celebratable; Suffering-Joy specifically arises through suffering rather than from the presence of the good; the overlap is in the agalliao term (shared across both characteristics' evidence), but the determining context is different; (2) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Gladness is the warm inner state of one whose circumstances are assessed as genuinely good; Suffering-Joy arises precisely when circumstances are not good; (3) **Resignation or stoicism** — the ba.lag fragile cheerfulness of M04-F is not stoic acceptance; it is a desired but barely-attainable inner brightness, not a philosophical detachment from feeling; (4) **Masochism** — the suffering-context is not sought for its own sake; 1Pe 4:13's "insofar as you share Christ's sufferings" frames the suffering as the context of kingdom participation, not as desired in itself.

---

#### T1.4 — Modes of Operation

##### T1.4.1 — In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Four distinct modes appear in the evidence: (1) **spontaneous response** — Jethro's rejoicing (Exo 18:9, cha.dah) on hearing of God's acts is an immediate inner response to external information; the king's exceeding gladness at Daniel's safety (Dan 6:23, te.ev) is a direct relief-and-delight response; (2) **volitional act** — Hab 3:18 ("yet I will rejoice") and Psa 118:24 ("let us rejoice") are deliberate inner choices made independent of circumstances; (3) **sustained orientation** — Psa 89:16 ("who exult in your name all the day") names a perpetual orientation rather than a punctual act; (4) **commanded cultivation** — Psa 2:11; 32:11; Isa 65:18; Zec 9:9 are commands that presuppose the inner state can be directed and sustained by will and formation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Five distinct modes: (1) **Spontaneous responsive joy** — Aaron's heart-gladness at seeing Moses (Exo 4:14); the people of Beth-shemesh at seeing the ark (1Sa 6:13); the disciples at seeing the risen Lord (Joh 20:20) — immediate inner response triggered by a direct encounter; (2) **Commanded and cultivated joy** — Deuteronomic feast-joy; "Rejoice in the Lord always" (Phili 4:4); "Count it all joy" (Jas 1:2) — joy directed and sustained by volitional practice; (3) **Spirit-produced joy** — "filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit" (Act 13:52); "joy of the Holy Spirit" (1Th 1:6); joy as the Spirit's fruit (Gal 5:22) — joy as a directly Spirit-imparted inner state; (4) **Paradoxical suffering-joy** — "sorrowful, yet always rejoicing" (2Cor 6:10); joy in affliction (2Cor 8:2); co-rejoicing in Paul's imprisonment (Phili 2:17–18) — joy co-existing with and transcending suffering; (5) **Relational co-joy** — sunchairo throughout M04-D; Paul's joy over specific communities (1Th 2:19–20; 3Jo 4) — joy produced by and existing in the bonds between persons.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Four modes: (1) **Divine-evaluative** — M04-L-VCG-01 (God's "it is good" appraisals across Gen 1; the ki-tov praise declarations) — Gladness operating at the highest level as the divine inner recognition of genuine goodness; (2) **Moral-comparative appraisal** — M04-L-VCG-02 (the human person weighing conduct, character, and choice against the standard of genuine goodness: "better than," "not good," "a good man") — Gladness as the cognitive-moral faculty; (3) **Wisdom's evaluative recognition** — M04-L-VCG-03 (Pro 8:11, 19; 16:8, 16, 19 — wisdom declared better than gold) — Gladness as the inner recognition of value hierarchies; (4) **Circumstantial warm response** — M04-O (all four VCGs — good news refreshing, wellbeing as flourishing, covenantal promise-gladness, makarismos blessedness) — Gladness as the affective inner warmth produced by receiving genuine goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Five distinct operational modes corresponding to the sub-groups: (1) **Affective-receptive mode** (M04-G) — the inner being luxuriating in and sustained by a specific treasured object (sha.a.shu.im in Psa 119's law-delight series; a.nog in Psa 37:4; sha.a in Isa 66:12's bounced-on-knees image); (2) **Sovereign-volitional mode** (M04-H-VCG-01) — delight as purposeful directed will: God's cha.phets producing action (Psa 115:3; Isa 53:10; 55:11); the king's volitional pleasure as his sovereign act (Est 6:6–11); (3) **Relational-delight mode** (M04-H-VCG-02) — delight directed toward persons: God's redemptive pleasure in persons producing rescue and exaltation (Psa 18:19; Isa 62:4); human relational delight (1Sa 19:1; Psa 16:3; 1Th 2:8); (4) **Obedience-orientation mode** (M04-M) — the inner being directed toward what pleases God, producing acceptable worship (arestos in Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22; ni.cho.ach in Lev 1:17); (5) **Corrupt mode** (M04-P) — the same faculty misdirected: lustful captivation (che.med — Eze 23:12), misdirected worship (ni.cho.ach — Eze 20:28), predatory elation (a.li.tsut — Hab 3:14).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Four operational modes: (1) **Perceptive-receptive mode** (M04-J-VCG-02) — the inner being receiving and registering what is pleasant in persons, speech, and creation: Psa 27:4 (gazing upon beauty), 2Sa 1:26 (Jonathan's pleasantness received by David's soul), Pro 2:10 (knowledge pleasant to the soul), Pro 16:24 (gracious words nourishing), Song 1:16; 7:6 (beloved's pleasantness perceived and appreciated); (2) **Worshipful-receptive mode** (M04-K-VCG-01) — the ni.cho.ach quality of correctly-offered sacrifice evoking God's inner settled pleasure; this is the worship-interface mode in which human offering evokes divine receptive Pleasure; (3) **Luxury-comfort mode** (M04-K-VCG-02) — the inner ease of refined, pampered existence: a.nog in Deu 28:54, 56; ta.a.nug in Pro 19:10; Ecc 2:8; Mic 2:9; (4) **Wisdom-calibrated comparative mode** (M04-K-VCG-03) — the tov better-than comparatives: training Pleasure to prefer modest integrity over corrupt abundance; Pleasure here is the inner faculty being formed by wisdom to assess what is more genuinely pleasant.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Four operational modes: (1) **Proclamatory Wonder** (dominant VCG-01 mode) — the marvellous work is encountered, wonder arises, and the inner response overflows into proclamation/declaration: "tell of all his wondrous works" (1Ch 16:9, 24; Psa 26:7; 71:17; 78:4; 96:3; 105:2; 145:5); (2) **Remembering-Wonder** — the deliberate inner act of calling to memory God's wonders and thereby refreshing Wonder: "remember the wondrous works" (1Ch 16:12; Psa 77:11; 105:5; 111:4); (3) **Contemplating-Wonder** — the sustained meditative engagement with what is marvellous: "meditate on your wondrous works" (Psa 119:27; 145:5); (4) **Humble-epistemological Wonder** (VCG-02 mode) — the recognition that something is beyond one's comprehension and the appropriate suspension of claims to know: Job 42:3; Psa 131:1; the "too hard for God?" rhetorical questions (Gen 18:14; Jer 32:17, 27) which challenge the human inner sense that anything could exceed God.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Four modes: (1) **Spirit-exultation** — the agalliao mode: Spirit-produced, intense, directed toward God/Christ/glory, operating at the spirit level (Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21; 1Pe 1:8 — "inexpressible and filled with glory"); (2) **Volitional-cognitive reframing** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") — a deliberate cognitive-volitional act of viewing trials through the lens of their formative-gladness output; Mat 5:12's command to "rejoice and be glad" addresses the will to direct the inner state; (3) **Communal sharing in mission-suffering** — Act 16:34 (jailer and whole household rejoicing together at coming to faith in a post-earthquake, post-imprisonment context); Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing that they were counted worthy to suffer — a communal inner orientation); (4) **Fragile desired brightness** — M04-F's ba.lag mode: the attempted, barely-sustained cheerfulness of Job and the psalmist — the inner person reaching for a brightness it cannot fully access.

---

##### T1.4.2 — Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, in two observable ways. First, **by object**: exultation directed at God's salvation (Psa 35:9; Isa 25:9; Hab 3:18) has an explicitly eschatological quality — it follows rescue and anticipates fullness. Exultation directed at God's reign (Psa 97:1; 1Ch 16:31) has a cosmic-declarative quality — it participates in the universe's recognition of divine sovereignty. Second, **by inversion**: when exultation is directed at wrong objects (evil — Pro 2:14; idols — Hos 10:5; an enemy's fall — Hab 1:15), it operates as the same inner-state capacity but distorted in direction and morally condemned. The constitutional locus does not appear to differ by context — the heart and soul are consistently named regardless of whether the exultation is spontaneous or cultivated.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. (1) **By context**: Festival/feast contexts produce a communal-structured joy (M04-B-VCG-01); personal narrative contexts produce a spontaneous-responsive joy (M04-B-VCG-04); persecution contexts produce a counter-intuitive commanded joy (M04-C-VCG-05); restoration contexts produce a forward-oriented promised joy (M04-E-VCG-01). (2) **By direction**: Joy directed at God is the normative and most sustained form (M04-B-VCG-05; M04-C-VCG-03); joy directed at persons (M04-B-VCG-04; M04-D) has a different character — more relational and completable; joy directed wrongly (M04-B-VCG-06) is morally condemned. (3) **By constitutional level**: The heart is the primary seat across all registers; the soul (Luk 1:47 — Mary's spirit/soul rejoices; M04-E-VCG-02 agalliao passages) is named in more intense or Spirit-mediated registers; the whole being (Psa 16:9) appears in sustained-joy states.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **By direction**: the evaluative mode (M04-L-VCG-02) is primarily outward-directed — it assesses persons, actions, and circumstances; the wellbeing mode (M04-O-VCG-03) is inward-received — "it will be well with you"; (2) **By object**: moral evaluations produce the gladness of moral clarity; covenantal promise-gladness (M04-O-VCG-04) produces the gladness of anchored trust; circumstantial good news produces the gladness of refreshment; (3) **By constitutional emphasis**: the evaluative modes (M04-L) engage the cognitive faculty more prominently; the circumstantial and wellbeing modes (M04-O) engage the affective faculty more prominently; (4) **By register**: the divine-character declarations (M04-L-VCG-01) are doxological; the moral appraisals (M04-L-VCG-02) are practical-ethical; the wisdom-comparative (M04-L-VCG-03) is wisdom-formation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)
