Yes: (1) **By object**: when directed toward God and his word (M04-G), Delight operates as the soul's resting orientation, producing sustained inner life; when directed toward persons (M04-H-VCG-02, M04-N), it operates as relational affection motivating care and action; when directed toward wrong objects (M04-P), the same faculty produces corruption and judgment; (2) **By constitutional level**: the affective-receptive mode (M04-G) engages the inner being (Rom 7:22) and heart (Psa 40:8) most deeply; the sovereign-volitional mode (M04-H-VCG-01) engages the will; the diplomatic-preference idiom (M04-H-VCG-03 surface instances) engages judgment and practical discernment at a shallower level; (3) **By register**: the divine sovereign mode operates without constraint (Psa 115:3); the human volitional mode operates under moral constraint — desire without knowledge is not good (Pro 19:2); the obedience mode (M04-M) operates under the frame of divine approval; (4) **By direction (God to human vs. human to God)**: God's delight toward the person (M04-H-VCG-02) is redemptive; the human person's delight toward God (M04-G, M04-H-VCG-03 in its righteous registers) is worshipful and volitional.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **By direction**: the ni.cho.ach mode moves from human to God (the worshiper offers → God receives with pleasure); the na.im/no.am mode moves from persons/creation to the inner being (what is pleasant in the world is received inwardly); the luxury mode is self-referential (the person's own inner ease in pampered conditions); (2) **By constitutional level**: na.im/no.am registers primarily in the soul (Pro 2:10 — "pleasant to your soul"); ni.cho.ach operates at the worship-level interface between human and divine; a.nog/ta.a.nug registers in the bodily dimension (Deu 28:54, 56 — somatic delicateness; Pro 16:24 — "health to the body"); (3) **By register**: the relational register (M04-J) is warm and personal; the worship register (M04-K-VCG-01) is formal and covenantal; the luxury register (M04-K-VCG-02) is private and bodily; the wisdom-comparative register (M04-K-VCG-03) is evaluative.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **By direction**: VCG-01's Wonder is directed toward God's acts in history and creation; VCG-02's Wonder is directed toward the boundary of human comprehension (what cannot be known); VCG-03's dark Wonder is directed toward what is terrible or wrong; (2) **By constitutional level**: VCG-01's proclamatory Wonder engages the voice and memory; VCG-02's incomprehensibility Wonder engages the cognitive faculty at its limits; VCG-03's dark Wonder engages the affective faculty in its disturbed-astonishment register; (3) **By register**: positive (VCG-01 — marvellous works of God producing praise); neutral-humble (VCG-02 — epistemological limit-recognition); dark (VCG-03 — dread and appalling astonishment).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **By constitutional level**: Spirit-level (agalliao in Luk 1:47; 10:21) produces the most intense and paradox-sustaining form; heart-level produces the fragile form (M04-F — ba.lag as attempted inner brightness); (2) **By eschatological grounding**: when Suffering-Joy is explicitly grounded in eschatological reality (Mat 5:12 — reward in heaven; 1Pe 4:13 — glory to be revealed; Heb 12:2 — joy set before him), it is more durable; when it is sought in the present (M04-F's "let me find a little cheer before I die"), it is fragile; (3) **By Spirit-agency**: Spirit-produced agalliao (Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6 adjacent) is more consistent and intense than unaided attempts at cheerfulness (ba.lag).

---

##### T1.4.3 — Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, strongly evidenced. re.na.nah (H7445) is the triumphing cry or joyful shout — an explicitly sonic-expressive form of exultation (Psa 63:5; 100:2; Job 3:7 by negation; Job 20:5; 23:582). Psa 32:11 commands "shout for joy, all you upright in heart." Psa 100:2 instructs "Come into his presence with singing." Zep 3:17 shows God himself "exulting over you with loud singing." Isa 49:13 calls the mountains to "break forth into singing." Zec 9:9 parallels "rejoice" with "shout aloud." The evidence shows exultation as constitutively expressive — its natural movement is from inner state to voiced proclamation, making the shout of joy and the triumphing song intrinsic to the characteristic rather than optional additions.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, prominently. The sim.chah/sa.mach register consistently moves into voice: Neh 12:27–43 (gladness expressed through singing, cymbals, harps, lyres); 1Ch 15:16 (David appointing Levites to "raise sounds of joy"); Jer 31:7 (singing aloud with gladness for Jacob); Joel 2:21–23 (rejoicing paired with praise). In the NT: chairo naturally moves into thanksgiving and praise (Act 13:48 — "began rejoicing and glorifying the word of the Lord"); Phili 4:4's commanded rejoicing is paired with prayer (4:6). In M04-E-VCG-02: Mary's spirit rejoices and her mouth proclaims (Luk 1:47 → 1:46 Magnificat); Act 2:26 — "my heart was glad, and my tongue rejoiced." Joy is inherently communicative — it moves from inner state to voiced expression as its natural overflow.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, in two forms: (1) **Doxological declaration** — the ki-tov praise formulas (Psa 100:5; 106:1; 107:1; 118:1, 29; 135:3; 136:1) are verbal declarations of divine goodness that simultaneously express and reinforce inner gladness; the "give thanks" command consistently paired with the "for he is good" formula shows that gladness-declaration is intrinsic to worship; (2) **Good word/news** — M04-O-VCG-01 (Pro 12:25 — "a good word makes him glad"; Pro 15:23 — "a word in season, how good it is!"; Pro 15:30 — "good news refreshes the bones"; Isa 52:7 — the good-news herald; Zec 1:13 — gracious comforting words) — speech is the medium through which gladness is communicated and received; the apt, timely word is itself an instance of Gladness reaching the inner person through the channel of speech.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in two forms: (1) **Divine speech declaring delight** — the baptism/transfiguration declarations (Mat 3:17; 17:5; Mar 1:11; Luk 3:22; 2Pe 1:17) — "this is my beloved Son, with whom I am well pleased" — are the most programmatic speech-acts of Delight in Scripture; the Father's eudokeo is declared by a voice from heaven; (2) **Diplomatic and practical speech** — the M04-H-VCG-03 "as it seems good to you" / "if it please the king" idiom throughout the historical books (Esther, Nehemiah, Samuel, Kings) is a speech-mode of Delight: the speaker verbally defers to or invokes the other's inner pleasure as the governing standard; this is communicative Delight in the relational-volitional sense. The communicative mode is thus both the highest divine declaration and the most ordinary human relational deference.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, in the speech-Pleasure register: (1) **Pro 16:24** — "gracious words are like a honeycomb, sweetness to the soul and health to the body" — speech as the medium through which Pleasure is communicated and received; the gracious word is itself an instance of pleasantness reaching the inner person; (2) **Pro 15:26** — "gracious words are pure" — pleasantness characterising speech as morally wholesome; (3) **Psa 45:1** — "my heart overflows with a pleasing theme" — the inner pleasantness expressing through speech in the form of praise poetry; (4) **Pro 22:18** — "it will be pleasant if you keep them within you, if all of them are ready on your lips" — wisdom's pleasantness residing within and ready to flow through speech. The speech-Pleasure link is the most distinctive communicative mode for this characteristic: genuinely pleasant speech is itself an inner-being state of pleasantness expressed outward and received inward.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, extensively — proclamation is the dominant expressive mode of VCG-01: (1) **"Tell of"** — 1Ch 16:9 ("tell of all his wondrous works"); Psa 9:1 ("I will recount all of your wonderful deeds"); 1Ch 16:24; Psa 26:7; 71:17; 78:4; 96:3; 105:2 — proclamation as the characteristic speech-act of Wonder; (2) **"Remember" + speech** — "remember the wondrous works" implies both inner memorial and outward declaration; (3) **"Meditate"** — Psa 119:27; 145:5 — the inner speech of contemplative Wonder; (4) **Questions** — the rhetorical "is anything too hard for the Lord?" (Gen 18:14; Jer 32:17, 27) and "who is like you?" (Exo 15:11) — Wonder expressed through the questioning mode that acknowledges God's incomparability. Wonder is uniquely the M04 characteristic that most consistently moves from inner response to outward vocal declaration.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: Act 2:26 ("my tongue rejoiced" — agalliao) — the tongue as the expressive organ of inner Spirit-joy; Luk 1:47 (Mary's Magnificat is the vocal expression of her spirit's rejoicing); Luk 10:21 (Jesus' Spirit-rejoicing immediately moves into voiced prayer — "I thank you, Father"); Act 16:34 (the jailer's communal rejoicing presumably involved voiced expression). The communicative mode is prayer and praise, not merely verbal declaration — Suffering-Joy in its Spirit-enabled form consistently moves into worshipful, Godward speech.

---

#### T1.5 — Immediate Response

##### T1.5.1 — What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Where the evidence names an occasion for exultation, the immediate response is the surging of the inner state itself: Exo 18:9 (Jethro hears of God's acts → he rejoiced); Isa 25:9 (God's salvation arrives → "let us be glad and rejoice in his salvation"); Dan 6:23 (king sees Daniel unharmed → "was exceedingly glad"). The immediacy is notable — exultation is not described as arising after reflection but as the direct inner response to the encounter with divine reality. Where exultation is commanded rather than spontaneous (Psa 32:11; Zec 9:9), the command implies the will can initiate the state rather than merely waiting for it.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence across the corpus shows the immediate inner response to the occasion of joy is the arising of gladness in the heart before its expression outward: Exo 4:14 (Aaron "will be glad in his heart" — gladness in the heart is the immediate response); 1Ki 8:66 (people go home "joyful and glad of heart" — the gladness is located in the heart as the first response to what they experienced); Psa 4:7 (God has "put more joy in my heart" — the inner reception is the primary event); Act 12:14 (Rhoda's "joy" at recognising Peter's voice is so immediate it overrides action — she runs in without opening the gate). The heart's gladness is the first movement, before voice or action.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The immediate responses vary by mode: (1) **Good news register**: Pro 12:25 — "a good word makes him glad" — the immediate inner shift from anxiety to brightness; Pro 15:30 — good news "refreshes the bones" — physiological-inner penetration; Zec 1:13 — gracious words bring inner reassurance; Gen 40:16 — the baker's immediate inner opening to disclosure when he perceives the interpretation as "favorable"; (2) **Evaluative register**: no strong immediate-response language; the moral appraisals of M04-L-VCG-02 are deliberative rather than immediate; (3) **Wellbeing register**: 1Sa 16:23 — Saul "was refreshed and was well" — the immediate inner calm produced by music when the harmful spirit departed; (4) **Covenantal register**: Neh 2:18 — the people's resolve strengthened when they heard of God's good hand — immediate motivational response to gladness-testimony.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Varies significantly by mode: (1) **Affective-receptive mode** (M04-G): immediate inner animation and sustained orientation — Psa 94:19 ("your consolations cheer my soul" — sha.a producing immediate inner brightening when cares overwhelm); (2) **Volitional mode** (M04-H): immediate action — Gen 34:19 ("the young man did not delay to do the thing, because he delighted in Jacob's daughter") — the most immediate response: delight translating directly and instantly into action; (3) **Relational-delight mode** (M04-H-VCG-02): immediate rescue and action — Psa 18:19 ("he rescued me, because he delighted in me") — divine delight in the person produces immediate saving action; (4) **Obedience mode** (M04-M): immediate appropriate action — Joh 8:29 ("I always do the things that are pleasing to him") — the person oriented toward what pleases God acts immediately in alignment with that pleasure.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The immediate responses differ by mode: (1) **Relational pleasantness** — an immediate inner recognition and warm reception: 2Sa 1:26 (David immediately experiencing Jonathan's companionship as pleasant); Song 1:16; 7:6 (the lover's immediate appreciative response to the beloved's beauty); (2) **Good words/speech** — immediate inner animation: Pro 12:25 (good word making glad); Pro 16:24 (gracious words providing immediate nourishment — honey simile implies instant effect); (3) **Worship-Pleasure (ni.cho.ach)** — Gen 8:21 (God's immediate responsive resolve in his heart upon smelling Noah's offering); the divine response to the pleasing aroma is immediate and decisive; (4) **Divine beauty** — Psa 27:4's longing to gaze on God's beauty is an aspiration rather than an immediate response, but the assumption is that the encounter with divine no.am produces immediate worshipful reception.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The immediate responses differ by register: (1) **VCG-01 positive Wonder**: immediate arrested attention — Job 37:14 ("stop and consider the wondrous works of God") — the first response is to stop; Mar 1:27 ("they were all amazed, so that they questioned among themselves") — thambeō seized them immediately; Psa 118:23 ("this is the Lord's doing; it is marvellous in our eyes") — immediate recognition of divine agency; (2) **VCG-02 incomprehensibility**: immediate epistemological humility — Job 42:3 ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — immediate recognition of the limit of one's knowledge; (3) **VCG-03 dark Wonder**: immediately unsettled and disturbed — Mar 10:32 ("they were amazed, and those who followed were afraid") — astonishment mixed with fear; Rev 17:6 ("I marvelled greatly") — overwhelmed inner seizure.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The evidence shows varied immediate responses: (1) **Spirit-gift form**: immediate Spirit-produced exultation — Luk 1:47 (Mary's spirit immediately exults upon the angel's announcement, despite her vulnerable situation); Act 16:34 (the jailer's rejoicing is immediate upon coming to faith); Act 2:26 (Peter quotes David's immediate heart-gladness at the resurrection promise); (2) **Fragile-sought form**: the immediate response is desire and attempt that may or may not succeed — Job 9:27 (considers attempting cheerfulness but the context makes clear he cannot sustain it); (3) **Commanded form**: the immediate response is volitional reorientation — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy when you meet trials") — the command assumes the immediate response will not be joy but the will can redirect the inner state.

---

##### T1.5.2 — Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The spontaneous pattern is consistent: when God acts in salvation or deliverance, the immediate inner response is exultation (Psa 9:14; 35:9; Isa 25:9; Hab 3:18). The volitional-initiated pattern is also consistent: when commanded, the command addresses the will directly. No evidence shows exultation arising from a slow reflective process — it is presented throughout as a direct inner-state response.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Consistent in kind, varied in intensity and occasion. The heart-gladness response is universal across the corpus. What varies is: (1) Intensity — from the overwhelming joy that causes Rhoda to forget to open the gate (Act 12:14) to the quiet gladness of Solomon's people eating and drinking (1Ki 4:20); (2) Occasion — from cosmic events (the Lord's reign calling the earth to rejoice) to personal moments (Aaron's heart glad at seeing his brother); (3) Presence of volition — some responses are spontaneous (Exo 4:14) and others are commanded and require volitional engagement (Deu 16:11; Phili 4:4).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Varies by mode. The good-news register (M04-O-VCG-01) shows the most consistent and immediate inner response: words of genuine goodness produce immediate inner brightening (anxiety → gladness; weariness → refreshment). The evaluative register (M04-L-VCG-02) is more deliberative — its "better than" comparatives presuppose prior assessment rather than immediate reaction. The wellbeing register (M04-O-VCG-03) shows immediate response to relief (1Sa 16:23; 1Sa 11:9 — men of Jabesh glad when they heard of deliverance). The divine-character declarations (M04-L-VCG-01) produce immediate doxological response (the ki-tov formula is simultaneously recognition and declaration).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Varies by mode, with a consistent directional pattern: in all registers, Delight when present produces movement toward the object — whether immediate action (Gen 34:19), sustained meditation (Psa 1:2; 119:16), rescue (Psa 18:19), worship (Psa 37:4), or generosity (1Th 2:8). The immediate response is always a movement of the will or affect toward the object of Delight. The sovereign-volitional mode produces immediate sovereign action (God does what he pleases — Psa 115:3); the relational mode produces relational movement toward the beloved; the affective-receptive mode produces inner orientation and sustained engagement. What varies is the faculty (will vs. affect) not the directionality (toward the object).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Generally consistent in direction (inner reception, warmth, nourishment) but varies in intensity and constitutional level: the relational pleasantness response is warm and affective; the worship-pleasure response (ni.cho.ach) on God's side is settled and resolving; the speech-pleasure response is nourishing; the sensory-luxury response is comfortable ease. All involve a positive receptive inner movement toward what is pleasant, but the depth, faculty, and duration vary by register.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The constant across all registers is the arrested quality: the inner being stops its ordinary flow of activity and is seized by what it encounters. Beyond this, the immediate responses diverge: positive Wonder produces questions, proclamation, and thanks; incomprehensibility Wonder produces humility and suspension of overconfident claims; dark Wonder produces disturbance and questioning ("why do you marvel?"). The arrested quality is the consistent feature; the direction of the subsequent inner response varies.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The immediate response varies by mode: Spirit-enabled agalliao produces immediate intense exultation (Luk 1:47; Act 16:34); ba.lag is explicitly an attempted state that may fail (Job 9:27); the commanded forms (Mat 5:12; Jas 1:2) presuppose that the immediate natural response is grief/complaint rather than joy, requiring deliberate volitional redirection. The inconsistency is itself analytically significant: this is the one M04 characteristic where the immediate response is explicitly not guaranteed to be the characteristic itself — it requires either the Spirit's production or the will's deliberate act.

---

##### T1.5.3 — Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The VCG-02 (inverted/absent exultation) and VCG-03 (relational and natural) verses are largely silent on the immediate response pattern — they address the object or absence of exultation rather than its mechanism of arising.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

M04-E's sa.s.von corpus is largely future-oriented and thus describes promised joy rather than immediate inner response. Similarly, the VCG-06 (inverted/absent joy) corpus by definition describes the absence or distortion of the immediate response rather than its presence. The inverted joy passages (Pro 2:14; Eze 25:6) do show the immediate inner response to wrong objects — but they are morally condemned precisely because of the wrongness of the object rather than the wrongness of the inner response mechanism itself.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

M04-L-VCG-02's moral appraisals and M04-L-VCG-03's wisdom-comparative evaluations are largely silent on immediate inner response; they describe the cognitive judgment rather than the felt first reaction to encountering the characteristic. The Eze 36:31 recognition of "not good" deeds produces self-loathing (an immediate negative response), but this is the inverted register.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

The M04-P corpus (corrupt delight) is silent on immediate response in the formal sense — it describes the corrupt inner state but does not trace an immediate response sequence. The beast-captivation (Rev 13:3; 17:8) shows collective astonishment-following as the immediate response to the beast's apparent resurrection, but this is the immediate response to the stimulus, not an unpacking of the inner sequence of Delight itself. M04-M's obedience-orientation (ni.cho.ach aroma) is similarly silent on the sequence of inner response.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

M04-K-VCG-03 (the wisdom better-than comparatives) does not evidence an immediate response to Pleasure — these are evaluative verdicts about what is more genuinely pleasant, not descriptions of a felt immediate response. Similarly, M04-K-VCG-01 on the human side (the person offering the sacrifice) is silent on the person's immediate inner state — the focus is on the divine reception. The luxury register (M04-K-VCG-02) is also largely silent on the immediate experiential response of the person enjoying luxury, focusing instead on the curse (Deu 28) or the catalogue (Ecc 2:8).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

The dominant VCG-01 corpus (61 verses of "tell of his wondrous works," "remember his wonders," "his wondrous works in the deep") largely describes Wonder in its retrospective-proclamatory mode rather than tracing the immediate inner response at the moment of encounter. The immediate encounter-response is most visible in the Mark thambeō instances (Mar 1:27; 10:24; 10:32) and in the negative cases (Neh 9:17 — failure to respond) rather than in the Psalmic proclamatory corpus.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Joh 8:56 (Abraham's anticipatory rejoicing at seeing Christ's day) and 1Pe 1:8 (inexpressible joy in the unseen Christ) describe a sustained inner state rather than an immediate response to a specific moment. The ongoing-state form of Suffering-Joy is not captured by the "immediate response" framework.

---

#### T1.6 — Sustained Effect

##### T1.6.1 — What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The sustained-exultation passages (Psa 89:16 — "all the day"; Isa 65:18 — "forever") and the eschatological-joy passages suggest that sustained exultation produces: (1) a settled Godward inner orientation — the person whose exultation is habituated orients all of life toward God as its ground and object; (2) stability under adversity — Hab 3:18's "yet I will rejoice" in the face of total material loss shows that practiced exultation produces an inner stability not dependent on circumstance; (3) proclamation — sustained exultation generates the ongoing declaration of God's greatness (Psa 40:16; 70:4: "may those who love your salvation say evermore, 'God is great!'" — the continuous triumphing cry).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The sustained-joy evidence produces: (1) **Strength** — Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength") — sustained Godward joy produces inner resilience; (2) **Health** — Pro 17:22 ("a joyful heart is good medicine") — the joyful heart has a medicinal effect on the inner being; (3) **Generosity** — 2Cor 8:2 (joy in severe affliction and extreme poverty overflowing into generous giving) — sustained joy expands the person's giving capacity; (4) **Stability in suffering** — 2Cor 6:10; Col 1:11; Phili 2:17 — sustained joy enables endurance; (5) **Prayer and worship** — the commanded feast-joy (Deu 16:11; Neh 8:12) over time forms the person into a worshipper; sustained joy produces and sustains the inner posture of worship; (6) **Completeness** — 2Jo 12; 1Jo 1:4; Joh 15:11; 16:24 — sustained joy in community moves toward fullness; it grows toward completion.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Sustained Gladness produces: (1) **Moral formation** — M04-L-VCG-02's persistent evaluative engagement with what is good and not-good forms the inner person's moral discernment capacity over time; Pro 2:20 ("walk in the way of the good") — sustained recognition of goodness as the standard shapes the path one walks; (2) **Covenantal stability** — M04-O-VCG-04's "good hand of God" awareness (Ezr 7:9; 8:18; Neh 2:8, 18) produces stable confidence in divine providential care; sustained recognition of God's good faithfulness builds inner resilience; (3) **Doxological orientation** — sustained engagement with the ki-tov declarations produces a person whose default inner posture toward God is thanksgiving and praise; (4) **Generosity** — M04-O-VCG-03: Psa 112:5 ("it is well with the man who deals generously") — sustained wellbeing produces generous disposition.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Sustained Delight produces: (1) **Life-preservation under adversity** — Psa 119:92 ("if your law had not been my delight, I would have perished in my affliction") — the single most striking sustained-effect statement in the corpus; (2) **Aligned desires** — Psa 37:4 ("delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart") — sustained Delight in God restructures the heart's desires to align with his giving; (3) **Sustained meditation and wisdom** — Psa 1:2 (delight in the law → meditating day and night → the blessed man's formation); Ecc 12:10 (the Preacher seeking words of delight → finding truth in delightful form); (4) **Productive will** — Isa 44:28; 46:10; 55:11 — God's sustained sovereign cha.phets producing accomplished purpose; (5) **Moral integrity** — Joh 8:29 (always pleasing the Father — the sustained effect of Delight-in-God's-pleasure producing consistent moral integrity); (6) **Corrupt formation** — Isa 66:3 ("their soul delights in their abominations") — sustained misdirected Delight forms a person deeply embedded in the wrong object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Sustained genuine Pleasure produces: (1) **Relational depth** — 2Sa 1:26's sustained friendship with Jonathan is the deepest relational pleasantness evidenced in the corpus; sustained experience of genuine relational Pleasure deepens the bond and its inner satisfaction; (2) **Nourishment and health** — Pro 16:24 ("sweetness to the soul and health to the body") — sustained gracious speech and its Pleasure nourishes the inner and outer person; (3) **Wisdom formation** — Pro 2:10's "knowledge will be pleasant to your soul" presupposes wisdom already dwelling in the heart; sustained Pleasure in wisdom produces the person formed by its ways (Pro 3:17 — "ways of pleasantness"); (4) **Worship relationship** — the twice-daily ni.cho.ach corpus (Exo 29:38–41 — morning and evening) sustains an ongoing relationship of divine favour; sustained right worship produces a continuous pleasantness of divine reception; (5) **Eschatological orientation** — Psa 16:11 (pleasures at God's right hand forevermore) implies a sustained present orientation toward God's presence producing the eschatological fullness.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Sustained Wonder produces: (1) **Praise and proclamation** — the entire VCG-01 corpus shows Wonder producing proclamation as its sustained expression: "I will recount all of your wonderful deeds" (Psa 9:1); "I still proclaim your wondrous deeds" (Psa 71:17 — from youth to old age); (2) **Faithful memory** — 1Ch 16:12; Psa 77:11; 105:5 — Wonder sustains faithful memorial of God's acts through the inner act of deliberate remembrance; (3) **Epistemological humility** — Job 42:3; Psa 131:1 — sustained Wonder produces a stable inner posture of not-overreaching, recognising the limits of human knowledge before God's incomprehensibility; (4) **Moral faithfulness** — conversely, the absence of sustained Wonder correlates with moral failure: Neh 9:17 ("not mindful of the wonders… they rebelled"); Psa 78:32 ("despite his wonders, they did not believe") — sustained Wonder is implied as the condition for sustained faithfulness.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The sustained evidence shows Suffering-Joy producing: (1) **Proven character** — Jas 1:3–4 (the testing of faith through trials → steadfastness → completeness) — Suffering-Joy enables the trials to accomplish their formative work over time; (2) **Resilience across increasing adversity** — Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing in their suffering → continuing to teach daily) — Suffering-Joy produces the sustained agency to continue mission under opposition; (3) **Eschatological orientation** — 1Pe 1:6–9 (present joy in salvation, trials, tested faith → "the outcome of your faith, the salvation of your souls") — sustained Suffering-Joy deepens the eschatological orientation of the inner being; (4) **Freedom from circumstantial dependence** — 2Cor 6:10 (adjacent, confirmed as Suffering-Joy territory: "sorrowful yet always rejoicing") — sustained Suffering-Joy produces a joy that is not contingent on circumstances improving.

---

##### T1.6.2 — What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Security in God (Psa 16:9 — "my whole being rejoices; my flesh also dwells secure"); confidence in God's steadfast love (Psa 13:5; 31:7 — rejoicing grounded in trust in his faithful love); the capacity for volitional joy regardless of circumstance (Hab 3:18); and perpetual orientation toward God as exceeding joy (Psa 43:4 — "God my exceeding joy"). The cumulative portrait across VCG-01 suggests that sustained exultation shapes the person into one whose inner life is constitutionally anchored in the divine reality rather than in fluctuating circumstances.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Sustained joy establishes: (1) A heart that is constitutionally glad in God (Psa 33:21 — "our heart is glad in him, because we trust in his holy name" — the heart's gladness as a stable established state); (2) A worshipping orientation — the feast-joy passages establish Israel's inner posture before God as one of joy rather than dread; (3) A generous, others-oriented inner life — M04-D (sunchairo) and the Pauline joy over communities (Phili 4:1; 1Th 2:20) show sustained joy producing outward attention and care; (4) A hope-sustained endurance — Rom 12:12 ("rejoice in hope, be patient in tribulation") — sustained joy in hope enables patience through tribulation; (5) A light-bearing presence — Act 8:39 (the eunuch "went on his way rejoicing") — sustained joy marks the person's whole deportment in the world.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Accurate moral perception** — sustained engagement with the evaluative faculty forms moral clarity: the person formed by Gladness's evaluative mode sees clearly what is genuinely good and what is not; (2) **Covenantal trust** — sustained gladness in God's promises (M04-O-VCG-04) establishes a trust-orientation that sustains through adversity; Jos 21:45 ("not one word of all the good promises had failed") as the inner foundation of ongoing trust; (3) **Wisdom** — M04-L-VCG-03's persistent preference for wisdom over gold (Pro 8:11; 16:16) establishes a value-hierarchy in the inner life that orients all choices; (4) **Quiet patience** — Lam 3:26 ("it is good to wait quietly for the salvation of the Lord") — sustained recognition that quiet waiting is the fitting inner posture establishes patience as a disposition.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Sustained will alignment** — the person whose Delight is in God progressively finds their desires conformed to his (Psa 37:4); (2) **Law-internalized** — Psa 40:8's "your law is within my heart" as the fruit of delight-in-obedience (M04-M); the inner law-delight produces a person whose will is no longer law-external but law-internal; (3) **Unbroken relationship with God** — Joh 8:29 — Jesus always doing what pleases the Father as the fruit of perfect sustained Delight; (4) **Eschatological orientation** — Job 22:26 (future delight in the Almighty) and Isa 58:14 (delight in the Lord as the promised outcome of Sabbath faithfulness) — sustained Delight establishes forward eschatological orientation; (5) **Worship as natural overflow** — the ki-tov Psalms (already addressed in Char 3, but here the cha.phets/sha.a.shu.im dimension): God's great works studied by those who delight in them (Psa 111:2) — sustained delight produces sustained engagement and eventually worship.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Soul-pleasantness as a stable inner quality** — the person whose inner life is marked by genuine relational and wisdom Pleasure develops a stable inner agreeableness; Pro 3:17's "ways of pleasantness" names the settled orientation of one who walks in wisdom; (2) **Calibrated valuation of material goods** — the M04-K-VCG-03 wisdom-comparatives train the inner being to prefer integrity with modest means over corrupt abundance; sustained engagement with these comparatives forms a person who habitually evaluates what is genuinely more pleasant; (3) **Covenantal worship relationship** — sustained ni.cho.ach worship maintains the divine-human pleasure-relationship that enables covenant life; (4) **Pro 16:24's nourished person** — sustained reception of gracious words produces an inner person sustained in soul-health and body-health simultaneously.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Whole-hearted devotion** — Psa 9:1 ("I will give thanks with my whole heart") — Wonder's sustained presence producing whole-hearted inner orientation toward God; (2) **Lifelong proclamatory orientation** — Psa 71:17 (from youth to old age still proclaiming wondrous deeds) — Wonder as the sustaining thread of a whole life of praise; (3) **Communal and generational transmission** — Psa 78:4 ("we will not hide them from their children, but tell to the coming generation") — sustained Wonder producing a generational inheritance-act; (4) **Contemplative depth** — Psa 119:27 (meditate on wondrous works); 145:5 (meditate on wondrous works) — sustained Wonder deepening into contemplative engagement.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Steadfastness** — Jas 1:4 (the proven character produced by trials endured with joy); (2) **Eschatological confidence** — 1Pe 4:13 (present suffering endured with joy establishes confident expectation of glory); (3) **Freedom from world's assessment** — Mat 5:12 (the persecuted community that rejoices demonstrates it is no longer defined by the world's approval or hostility); (4) **Communal identity** — Act 5:41; Act 16:34 — Suffering-Joy is a communally-shared orientation that strengthens group identity and mission-perseverance.

---

##### T1.6.3 — Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The immediate response is the surge; the sustained effect is the re-orientation of the whole inner being. Psa 16:9 shows the whole-being as the sustained outcome: "my heart is glad, and my whole being rejoices; my flesh also dwells secure" — the immediate gladness has settled into an encompassing security. The difference is one of scope and duration: the immediate response is a directed act; the sustained effect is a constitutional re-orientation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. The immediate response is a surge of gladness in the heart; the sustained effect is the re-orientation of the whole inner life toward joy as a standing posture. The immediate gladness at seeing the ark (1Sa 6:13) is not the same as the established feast-joy of Israel that shapes an entire cultural and liturgical identity (Deu 16:11–15). The immediate joy at Titus's arrival (2Cor 7:13) is not the same as the joy that "goes with him through all his toil" (Ecc 8:15). Sustained joy re-configures the inner being's relationship to life's vicissitudes; immediate joy is the first movement of that re-configuration.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. The immediate response in the good-news register is refreshment and brightening; the sustained effect is the formation of inner orientations and dispositions (moral clarity, covenantal trust, wisdom, patience). The immediate and sustained effects are consistent in kind (both involve recognition of genuine goodness) but differ in duration and constitutional depth. Immediate gladness is a response; sustained gladness is a formation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes significantly. The immediate response is a movement of will or affect toward the object; the sustained effect is transformation of the person: desires restructured (Psa 37:4), the law internalized (Psa 40:8), the inner person sustained through adversity (Psa 119:92), wisdom formed (Psa 1:2). The immediate response is a directional movement; the sustained effect is constitutional change. In the corrupt mode, this distinction is equally stark: the immediate response is lustful attraction (Eze 23:12); the sustained effect is that "their soul delights in their abominations" (Isa 66:3) — the person's deepest inner faculty is now formed around the wrong object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes. The immediate response of Pleasure is a warm inner reception; the sustained effect is formation — wisdom's ways becoming the person's habitual orientation (Pro 3:17), the covenant-worship relationship being sustained (ni.cho.ach), and the inner being nourished over time into health (Pro 16:24). The immediate response is a moment of pleasantness; the sustained effect is a person formed in the capacity to receive and inhabit what is genuinely pleasant.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes significantly. The immediate response is arrest and astonishment (stopped in one's tracks, seized by amazement); the sustained effect is the formation of a life-pattern of proclamation, memory, contemplation, and epistemological humility. The immediate response is a momentary seizure; the sustained effect is a characteristic orientation of the inner person toward the marvellous in God. Psa 71:17's "from youth I still proclaim" shows the sustained effect: decades of sustained Wonder has produced a person whose primary inner-expressive mode is the proclamation of God's marvellous deeds.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes. The immediate response (Spirit-exultation in a crisis moment — Luk 1:47; Act 16:34) is an intense surge; the sustained effect (steadfastness, eschatological confidence, freedom from circumstantial dependence) is a stable orientation of the inner being toward what is transcendently true rather than circumstantially present. The immediate response is the spark; the sustained effect is the formation of an inner life that no longer requires the removal of suffering in order to inhabit joy.

---

#### T1.7 — Conditions of Reception

##### T1.7.1 — What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence identifies several enabling conditions: (1) **trust in God's steadfast love** — Psa 13:5 ("I have trusted in your steadfast love; my heart shall rejoice") makes trust the explicit precondition for the heart's rejoicing; (2) **righteousness and uprightness of heart** — Psa 32:11 commands the righteous and upright in heart to rejoice; Psa 68:3 names "the righteous" as those who "shall be glad; they shall exult before God"; (3) **seeking God** — Psa 40:16 and 70:4 name those who "seek" God as those who rejoice in him; (4) **waiting for God** — Isa 25:9's exultation follows patient waiting ("we have waited for him"); (5) **obedience** — Isa 64:5 identifies "him who joyfully works righteousness" as the one God meets and receives.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence identifies: (1) **Seeking and seeking God** — Psa 40:16; 70:4 ("may all who seek you rejoice"); Psa 85:6 (revival that produces rejoicing in God); (2) **Wholehearted devotion** — 2Ch 15:15 (Judah rejoiced over the oath "for they had sworn with all their heart and had sought him with their whole desire"); 1Ch 29:9 (people rejoiced "because they had given willingly, for with a whole heart they had offered freely"); (3) **Trust** — Psa 33:21 ("our heart is glad in him, because we trust in his holy name"); (4) **Uprightness and righteousness** — Psa 97:11 ("joy for the upright in heart"); Pro 29:6 ("a righteous man sings and rejoices"); (5) **Faith** — Rom 15:13 (joy and peace "in believing"); Act 16:34 (the jailer's household rejoiced "that he had believed in God"); (6) **Comprehension of God's word** — Neh 8:12 (great rejoicing "because they had understood the words that were declared to them").

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Humility** — Deu 9:6 (God correcting Israel's inner sense of merit) reveals that genuine gladness in the good land requires the recognition that it is grace, not merit; pride distorts the evaluative faculty; (2) **Moral alignment** — Psa 73:1 ("God is good to Israel, to those who are pure in heart") — purity of heart is the condition for experiencing God's goodness as directed toward oneself; (3) **Seeking and waiting** — Lam 3:25–26 ("the Lord is good to those who wait for him, to the soul who seeks him… it is good to wait quietly") — patient seeking is the enabling posture for gladness-in-God; (4) **Integrity** — Pro 12:2 ("a good man obtains favor from the Lord") — moral character enables the recognition and reception of divine goodness; (5) **Comprehension** — Gen 40:16 (the baker received Joseph's interpretation as favorable only when he understood it as positive) — accurate understanding is a precondition for gladness's reception.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Wholehearted orientation toward God** — 1Ch 28:9 ("a willing mind" serving with a whole heart); Psa 73:25 ("nothing on earth I desire besides you") — the exclusive orientation is the enabling condition for the deepest Delight; (2) **Deliberate choice** — Isa 56:4 ("who choose the things that please me") — active volitional choosing enables Delight-in-God; (3) **Inward truthfulness** — Psa 51:6 ("you delight in truth in the inward being") — God's delight toward the person presupposes genuine interior honesty; (4) **Fear of God** — Neh 1:11 ("who delight to fear your name") — fearing God is the precondition for the deepest orientation of Delight; (5) **The law as inner possession** — Psa 40:8 ("your law is within my heart") — the law internalized is both precondition and fruit of Delight in God's will; (6) **Obedience** — 1Jo 3:22 ("keep his commandments and do what pleases him") — commanded obedience is both the expression and the enabling condition of God's pleasure.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Wisdom in the heart** — Pro 2:10 ("wisdom will come into your heart, and knowledge will be pleasant to your soul") — the prior dwelling of wisdom enables Pleasure in knowledge; (2) **Covenant faithfulness** — the ni.cho.ach corpus consistently: Lev 26:31 (God will not smell the aromas of the unfaithful) — covenant obedience is the enabling condition for worship-Pleasure; (3) **Purity of speech and thought** — Pro 15:26 (gracious words are pure, contrasted with wicked thoughts) — inner purity enables genuine speech-Pleasure; (4) **Seeking after God** — Psa 27:4 (the one seeking to dwell in God's house and gaze on his beauty) — active seeking is the enabling posture for divine-Pleasure reception; (5) **Inner openness** — Pro 22:18 ("pleasant if you keep them within you") — inward reception of wisdom's words enables their pleasantness to be felt.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Attending and considering** — the most frequently named enabling condition: Job 37:14 ("stop and consider"); Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold") — Wonder requires deliberate attention; (2) **Memory and remembrance** — Psa 77:11; 105:5; 111:4 — the habit of deliberate remembrance of God's acts enables Wonder; (3) **Openness to the incomprehensible** — Job 42:3's posture of recognising one has spoken beyond one's knowledge; Psa 131:1's restraint from overreaching — the epistemological openness that enables genuine Wonder-humility; (4) **Prior consecration** — Jos 3:5 ("consecrate yourselves, for tomorrow the Lord will do wonders") — moral preparation enabling receptive Wonder; (5) **Seeking** — Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes") — asking God to enable the perception of wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Faith in the unseen Christ** — 1Pe 1:8 ("though you do not now see him, you believe in him and rejoice") — faith is the enabling condition for the Spirit-form of Suffering-Joy; (2) **Eschatological orientation** — Mat 5:12 ("your reward is great in heaven"); 1Pe 4:13 ("that you may also rejoice when his glory is revealed") — a forward-oriented inner stance toward eschatological reality enables present Suffering-Joy; (3) **Spirit-filling** — Luk 10:21 ("rejoiced in the Holy Spirit"); 1Th 1:6 (adjacent — "joy of the Holy Spirit") — the Spirit's presence is the enabling condition for the most intense form; (4) **Participation in Christ's suffering** — 1Pe 4:13 ("insofar as you share Christ's sufferings") — genuine participation rather than mere external observation is required.

---

##### T1.7.2 — What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Conditions that block or distort: (1) **unfaithfulness to God** — Hos 9:1 prohibits rejoicing precisely because Israel has "played the whore, forsaking your God"; their inner joy is illegitimate; (2) **idolatrous attachment** — Hos 10:5 shows exultation in an idol produces eventual mourning when the idol fails; (3) **directing exultation at evil** — Pro 2:14 shows those who "rejoice in doing evil" — the characteristic operating in a corrupted form; (4) **extremity of suffering** — Job 3:6–7 shows that overwhelming anguish can make even the capacity for joy seem impossible; though notably Hab 3:18 demonstrates the will can recover exultation even in extreme loss.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

(1) **Unfaithfulness** — Hos 9:1 (Israel commanded not to rejoice because they "played the whore, forsaking your God"); (2) **Wrong object** — Pro 2:14 (those who rejoice in evil); Isa 22:13 (reckless joy in the face of coming judgment, refusing repentance); (3) **Lack of root** — Mat 13:20; Mar 4:16; Luk 8:13 (rocky-ground joy without depth that falls away under testing); (4) **Pride and self-sufficiency** — Amos 6:13 (rejoicing in self-achieved victories without acknowledgment of God); (5) **Malice** — Eze 25:6 (joy rooted in "malice within your soul" produces corrupt joy); (6) **Covenant unfaithfulness** — Deu 28:47 makes failure to serve with joyfulness of heart the very condition that forfeits joy; (7) **Idolatry** — Hos 10:5 (idolatrous priests' joy in the calf collapses when the calf is taken — joy founded on false worship is unstable).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Fear-distorted evaluation** — Num 14:3 (Israel's fear producing the judgment that Egypt was better than Canaan); (2) **Self-reference** — Hezekiah's self-serving reception of Isaiah's word (Isa 39:8) as good only because it means peace in his lifetime; (3) **Idolatrous orientation** — Hos 2:7 (Israel's recognition that "it was better then" comes only after being stripped of idolatry's apparent benefits — the idolatrous orientation had blocked accurate gladness-recognition); (4) **Pride** — the "not good" verdicts in Proverbs consistently target failures of humility, justice, and integrity that distort the evaluative faculty; (5) **Despair** — Jon 4:3, 8 (extreme anguish overwhelming Jonah's ability to evaluate circumstance accurately) — despair blocks reception of genuine gladness even when it is available.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Uncircumcised ears and hardened hearts** — Jer 6:10 ("they take no pleasure in it" — the closed ear as the diagnostic of blocked Delight in God's word); (2) **Self-directed pleasure** — Isa 58:13 (seeking one's own pleasure on the Sabbath — self-will as the blocking condition); (3) **Hollow ritual** — Isa 1:11; Heb 10:6 — external sacrifice without inner transformation blocks God's delight from being engaged; (4) **Misdirected desire** — Eze 23:12 (lust for the Assyrians); Isa 66:3 (delight in abominations) — the faculty is operating but entirely misdirected; (5) **Pride and manipulation** — 1Sa 18:25 (Saul publicly stating his desire while concealing murderous intent) — feigned Delight as the opposite of genuine; (6) **Shrinking back from faith** — Heb 10:38 ("my soul has no pleasure in him") — faith-collapse as the condition that withholds divine delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Covenant unfaithfulness** — Lev 26:31 — the most explicit blocking condition for worship-Pleasure; (2) **Folly** — Pro 9:17 (folly making stolen bread appear pleasant — distorted evaluation of what is genuinely pleasant); Pro 18:2 (fool taking pleasure only in his own opinion — self-referential distortion); Pro 19:10 (luxury unfit for fools — the fool's inner constitution misaligns with genuine Pleasure); (3) **Moral corruption** — Job 20:18 (the wicked getting no enjoyment from profits — moral corruption blocking natural Pleasure reception); (4) **Judgment/curse** — Deu 28:54, 56 (the delicate person's Pleasure capacity destroyed by the covenant curse); Isa 47:1 (Babylon's delicateness stripped away by judgment); (5) **Self-indulgence** — Pro 7:18 (carnal a.las as distorted pleasure) and Ecc 2:8's self-accumulated concubines — when Pleasure is self-accumulated rather than received from genuine goodness, it distorts.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Forgetting** — Neh 9:17; Psa 78:11; 106:7 — the inner act of non-remembering blocks Wonder; (2) **Presumption** — Psa 131:1's warning implies the opposite: the person who occupies themselves with what is too marvellous for them may actually lose the capacity for genuine Wonder by overreaching (treating the incomprehensible as if comprehensible); (3) **Accumulated wisdom without humility** — Isa 29:14 ("the wisdom of their wise men shall perish") — self-sufficient human wisdom closing the person to God's unexpected acts; (4) **Dark wonder** — Rev 17:6–7 (marvelling at the harlot rather than at God) — Wonder misapplied to evil prevents reception of genuine Wonder at the divine.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Overwhelming grief** — M04-F shows that extreme suffering can make even the attempt at cheerfulness impossible (Job 9:27 — he considers attempting it and immediately finds it cannot be sustained); (2) **Shallow grounding** — Joh 5:35 ("willing to rejoice for a while in his light") — agalliao without deep grounding does not endure under pressure; (3) **World-aligned values** — Rev 11:10 (earth-dwellers rejoice over the prophets' deaths) — the person whose inner life is aligned with the world's values will find the world's triumphs over the gospel cause for rejoicing rather than suffering-with-joy; (4) **Absence of eschatological orientation** — Suffering-Joy without eschatological grounding collapses into what M04-F depicts — the hopeless, barely-maintained attempt at brightness before death.

---

##### T1.7.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The VCG-02 passages show the alternative inner state: mourning (Hos 10:5 — priests mourn when the calf departs); joylessness (Job 3:6–7); inverted exultation directed at death (Job 3:22); enemy exultation over the righteous's defeat (Psa 13:4). The person who cannot receive genuine Godward exultation is either in a state of mourning and grief, or has misdirected their exultation-capacity toward wrong objects. The evidence does not show a neutral middle ground — the person is either exulting rightly, exulting wrongly, or emptied of the capacity by extremity.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The VCG-06 corpus provides the evidence: (1) **Mourning and groaning** — Lam 5:15 ("the joy of our hearts has ceased; our dancing has been turned to mourning"); (2) **Sighing** — Isa 24:7 ("all the merry-hearted sigh" when joy is stripped away); (3) **Joylessness as desolation** — Isa 24:11 ("all joy has grown dark; the gladness of the earth is banished") — the inner state is one of inner darkness replacing the brightness of joy; (4) **Shallow inadequacy** — Ecc 2:1–2 (joy pursued and found vain — the Preacher who seeks joy as a project finds it hollow); (5) **Crushing** — Pro 15:13 ("by sorrow of heart the spirit is crushed") — the opposite inner state to the glad heart is a crushed spirit. The person who cannot receive genuine joy is in a state of mourning, sighing, inner darkness, or crushed spiritedness.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Moral blindness** — the fool who finds joy in folly (Pro 15:21 — M04-B, but adjacent) and the one who does not-good are unable to perceive the genuinely good; (2) **Distress** — the Israelites who cannot receive the good land as good remain in fear and distress (Num 14:3); (3) **Hollow festivity** — Isa 22:13's "let us eat and drink, for tomorrow we die" — receiving circumstantial pleasure but not genuine gladness, which requires more than pleasure; (4) **Nostalgia without restoration** — Hos 2:7's "it was better then" — the memory of former gladness without the conditions for its return; (5) **Self-loathing** — Eze 36:31's trajectory from not-good recognition to loathing — the person who encounters the evaluative-gladness faculty in its condemning mode without finding restoration ends in self-directed revulsion.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Alienation from God** — Jer 6:10 (the ear closed to God's word, the heart sealed against its proper object); (2) **Destructive desire** — Jer 42:22 (the people desire to go to Egypt, and their very desire leads to disaster — Delight directing the will toward what destroys); (3) **Moral deformation** — Pro 18:2 (the fool taking pleasure only in his own opinion — Delight contracted onto the self); (4) **Judgment** — Isa 65:12; 66:4 (the people who "chose what I did not delight in" meet judgment); (5) **Spiritual captivation** — Rev 13:3; 17:8 (the world marveling at the beast — the person whose name is not in the book of life, captivated by the wrong magnificent object). The person who encounters but does not receive genuine Delight is not neutral — the Delight faculty continues to operate and attaches itself to whatever object presents itself, however wrong.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Isolation and grief** — 2Sa 1:26 (David's distress at losing Jonathan's pleasant companionship — the absence of pleasantness producing grief); (2) **False pleasure** — Pro 9:17 (stolen bread appearing pleasant — the person receives a simulacrum of Pleasure that leads to death); (3) **Denied enjoyment** — Job 20:18 (the wicked man getting no enjoyment from his profits — blocked from receiving the natural Pleasure of his own labour's fruit); (4) **Hardness and closure** — Jer 6:10's "uncircumcised ear" (adjacent — the ear closed to God's word taking no pleasure) — the inner being sealed against receiving genuine Pleasure; (5) **Restlessness** — Ecc 2:8's self-accumulated pleasures leave the Preacher unsatisfied — when Pleasure is sought rather than received it produces restlessness rather than rest.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Hardened and rebellious** — Neh 9:17 (failed Wonder → stiffened neck → appointing a leader to return to Egypt) — Wonder-failure leading directly to rebellion; (2) **Unbelief** — Psa 78:32 ("despite his wonders, they did not believe") — the person who witnesses wonders but does not receive them as wonders remains in unbelief; (3) **Restless and sin-prone** — Psa 78 generally shows the pattern: Israel witnessed wonder after wonder and still rebelled, showing that Wonder not received is evidentially ineffective for transformation; (4) **Troubled astonishment** — Mar 10:32 (those who followed Jesus were afraid while those who accompanied him were amazed) — partial Wonder reception producing mixed fear rather than full receptive awe.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

M04-F provides the answer: Job 9:27 (grief-saturated, attempting cheerfulness and failing); Psa 39:13 (requesting to smile briefly before death — joy almost entirely beyond reach); Jer 8:18 ("my joy is gone; grief is upon me; my heart is sick within me" — the prophet in the total absence of the characteristic's comfort). These show the person who cannot receive Suffering-Joy in a state of unrelieved grief, heartsickness, and barely-surviving distress. The characteristic's absence is not neutral but marks the full weight of suffering bearing upon the inner person without the Spirit-enabled transcendence.

---

#### T1.8 — Dimension Classification

##### T1.8.1 — What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The primary dimension is **affective** — exultation is first and most fully an affective inner state: the surge of triumph, delight, and gladness directed toward God. This is the dominant pattern across VCG-01's 58 verses: the soul exults, the heart rejoices, the whole being is glad. The affective character is further evidenced by the body's participation (bones — Psa 51:8; flesh — Psa 16:9) and by the sonic expression (re.na.nah, the triumphing cry).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The primary dimension is **affective** — Joy is first and most fully a felt inner state of gladness: the heart is glad (Exo 4:14; Psa 4:7; 16:9; 33:21), the heart rejoices (Psa 13:5; Pro 15:30; Luk 24:41), the whole inner being is filled with joy (Act 13:52; Phili 2:2). The consistently named constitutional seat is the heart as the affective centre of the person, and joy's first movement is always an inner emotional arising rather than an external act.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The primary dimension is **cognitive-evaluative** — Gladness is first and most distinctively an inner act of recognising and assessing what is genuinely good. The M04-L-VCG-02 corpus (45 verses of moral appraisal) is the largest single VCG in the characteristic, and the evaluative function of tov throughout both sub-groups is the defining feature. This is what distinguishes Gladness from the other M04 characteristics: Joy is primarily affective; Exultation is primarily affective-volitional; Gladness has a uniquely prominent cognitive dimension.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The primary dimension is **Emotion-Positive / Relational Disposition in integrated combination**. Delight is not primarily cognitive (like Gladness) or primarily affective-Spirit (like Suffering-Joy) but is the integrated inner-being act of directing pleasurable attention and will toward a treasured object — which simultaneously involves affect (the pleasure) and relational disposition (the orientation toward). The M04-G corpus makes the affective-positive dimension primary; the M04-H volitional corpus makes the volitional dimension prominent; M04-M makes the obedience-orientation prominent. Given the characteristic's breadth, Emotion-Positive (the felt pleasurable quality) is the primary dimension with Relational Disposition (the directedness-toward) as a strong secondary.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The primary dimension is **Emotion-Positive** in the receptive-experiential sense — Pleasure is the felt quality of agreeableness received inwardly from what is genuinely pleasant. Unlike Delight (which has a strong volitional component) or Gladness (which has a strong cognitive-evaluative component), Pleasure is primarily a felt receptive experience — the inner being's pleasant feeling-quality in response to what is agreeable. The ni.cho.ach worship-Pleasure register adds a relational-covenantal dimension that makes the primary dimension more complex: God's inner settled Pleasure at correct worship is the most explicitly inner-being divine emotional response in the Levitical corpus.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The primary dimension is **Cognition** in the perceptive-receptive sense — Wonder specifically engages the cognitive faculty at its limits: (1) VCG-01's "consider," "behold," "tell of," "meditate on," "understand" vocabulary is all cognitively engaged; (2) VCG-02's pa.la in the "too hard/wonderful for you" register is explicitly about cognitive limits; (3) Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me, which I did not know" is cognitively located. Wonder is the inner state at the boundary of cognition — it is specifically the cognitive faculty encountering what it cannot fully process. This makes Wonder the most cognitively-located of the positive M04 characteristics (unlike Suffering-Joy which is Spirit-primary, or Delight which is volitional-primary).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The primary dimension is **affective** in the Spirit-mediated sense: agalliao is first and most fully a felt inner state of exultation produced by the Spirit within the suffering context. However, this affective state is uniquely constituted by volitional and cognitive elements that distinguish it from ordinary affect: (1) Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") requires cognitive reframing; (2) Mat 5:12 ("rejoice and be glad") commands volitional engagement; (3) The Spirit's enabling (Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6) makes it supernaturally-originating affect rather than naturally-arising affect. The primary dimension is best described as **supernaturally-grounded affective-volitional**: affect that is Spirit-produced and involves the will's engaged participation.

---

##### T1.8.2 — What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Psa 16:9 — "my heart is glad, and my whole being rejoices; my flesh also dwells secure" (whole person affected); Psa 63:5 — "my soul will be satisfied as with fat and rich food, and my mouth will praise you with joyful lips" (soul's deep satisfaction producing expressive joy); Isa 61:10 — "I will greatly rejoice in the Lord; my soul shall exult in my God" (soul named explicitly as the exulting agent); Jer 32:41 — God's rejoicing located "with all my heart and all my soul" (full affective-constitutional engagement). The affective dimension is primary across all three VCGs.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Psa 4:7 — "you have put more joy in my heart" (direct affective placement in the heart); Psa 33:21 — "our heart is glad in him" (heart as the seat of gladness); Pro 15:13 — "a glad heart makes a cheerful face, but by sorrow of heart the spirit is crushed" (heart-gladness as constitutional fact with outward expression); Pro 17:22 — "a joyful heart is good medicine" (heart-joy with bodily consequence); Jer 15:16 — "your words became to me a joy and the delight of my heart" (heart explicitly named); Ecc 5:20 — "God keeps him occupied with joy in his heart" (heart-location); Song 3:11 — "the gladness of his heart" (heart-gladness as the king's wedding-day experience).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

M04-L-VCG-02 (45 verses) evidences the cognitive primary: Jethro's deliberate judgment (Exo 18:17 — "what you are doing is not good"); Naomi's weighing of Ruth's options (Rut 2:22 — "it is good… lest in another field you be assaulted"); the Proverbs series (Pro 17:26; 18:5; 20:23; 24:23; 28:21 — "not good" as moral evaluation of specific practices); Job 34:4 — "let us know among ourselves what is good" (communal moral discernment); Mic 6:8 — "he has told you, O man, what is good" (the most programmatic statement of what human goodness is). M04-L-VCG-01's ki-tov declarations also show the cognitive pattern: recognising and declaring divine goodness is a cognitive-doxological act.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Emotion-Positive primary: sha.a.shu.im (Psa 119 series — the law is the psalmist's settled affective delight); a.nog (Psa 37:4 — "delight yourself in the Lord" as affective resting); sunēdomai (Rom 7:22 — "I delight in the law of God" located in the inner being — a felt affective state); Jer 31:20 (Ephraim as God's darling child — the affective warmth of cherishing). Relational Disposition secondary: the directedness-toward in all five sub-groups; Delight without an object is not Delight; every instance names a specific object (law, God, person, wisdom, Sabbath, even idol). The characteristic cannot be described without its relational-directional structure.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Emotion-Positive primary: Pro 2:10 ("pleasant to your soul" — affective inner quality named directly); 2Sa 1:26 ("very pleasant have you been to me" — affective relational quality); Song 1:16; 7:6 (the lover's felt appreciation of the beloved); Psa 133:1 ("how pleasant it is" — affective communal feeling); Gen 8:21 (God's inner calmed response — divine emotional settling); Pro 16:24 (gracious words producing sweetness to the soul — affective nourishment). The consistently affective, receptive, felt quality across all primary instances confirms Emotion-Positive as primary.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Cognitive primary: (1) Job 37:5 ("God thunders wondrously… great things that we cannot comprehend") — cognition's limit named explicitly; (2) Job 42:3 ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — knowledge as the measure; (3) Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law") — perception-request for cognitive opening; (4) Psa 119:27 ("make me understand the way of your precepts, and I will meditate on your wondrous works") — understanding leading to Wonder-meditation; (5) Job 37:14 ("stop and consider the wondrous works of God") — commanded cognitive attention. All these engage the cognitive-perceptive faculty.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Luk 1:47 — Mary's spirit exults in the Spirit-register (spirit-level, affective-intense); 1Pe 1:8 — "inexpressible and filled with glory" — the affective quality is the primary descriptor; Act 16:34 — the jailer's rejoicing is the felt inner state of a person in crisis who has come to faith; Luk 10:21 — Jesus' Spirit-rejoicing is an affective event located in the Holy Spirit. All primary instances name the felt, intense, exultant quality first.

---

##### T1.8.3 — Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: (1) **volitional** — the commanded exultations (Psa 2:11; 32:11; Isa 65:18; Zec 9:9) and Hab 3:18's deliberate choice show a significant volitional dimension; (2) **relational** — exultation is constitutively toward an object (God, his salvation, his people) and is mutual (God exults over his people, his people exult in him); (3) **expressive/performative** — the triumphing cry (re.na.nah), the commanded shout, and the singing are intrinsic to exultation's form. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the primary affective classification but show exultation as a multidimensional characteristic in which affect, will, relation, and expression are integrated.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, significantly: (1) **Volitional** — the commanded nature of feast-joy (Deu 16:11; Lev 23:40) and NT commands ("Rejoice always" — 1Th 5:16; "Count it all joy" — Jas 1:2) show a substantial volitional dimension — joy is a disposition the will can cultivate; (2) **Relational** — M04-D (sunchairo) and the Pauline joy-in-communities show Joy as inherently relational; (3) **Expressive/performative** — the singing, shouting, dancing, and festive music that consistently accompany joy in M04-B show it as constitutively expressive; (4) **Cognitive** — Neh 8:12 (joy arising from comprehension of God's word) and the understanding of divine acts that grounds the feast-joy (Deu 26:11 — "rejoice in all the good that the Lord your God has given") show a cognitive-recognition dimension. The secondary dimensions do not displace the primary affective classification but confirm Joy as a multidimensional characteristic in which affect, will, relation, and expression are integrated.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered.*

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Affective** — M04-O (VCG-01 through VCG-04) is primarily affective — the warm inner response to good news, beneficial states, and covenantal goodness; the circumstantial face of Gladness is affective before it is cognitive; (2) **Moral** — M04-L-VCG-02's moral appraisals make Gladness carry a strong moral-character dimension; (3) **Volitional** — the makarismos instances (M04-O-VCG-04: Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15) involve the state of being-declared-righteous, which has a volitional element (faith); Lam 3:26 ("good to wait quietly") requires volitional discipline. The secondary dimensions do not displace the primary cognitive classification but confirm Gladness as a multi-dimensional characteristic integrating cognitive recognition, affective warmth, and moral orientation.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 3.*

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, multiple: (1) **Volitional** — M04-H's cha.phets/eudokeo corpus is primarily volitional in the sovereign-purposeful and directed-desire registers (Psa 115:3; 135:6; Isa 53:10; Gen 34:19; Psa 40:8); (2) **Moral Character** — M04-M's arestos and tov-in-obedience registers engage the moral character dimension (what is genuinely acceptable and pleasing to God, Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22); (3) **Divine-Human Correspondence** — the shared cha.phets/eudokeo vocabulary between God and humans (T0.3.2) names a dimensional correspondence; (4) **Transformation** — Psa 37:4's desires restructured by Delight in God; the law internalized through Delight (Psa 40:8); Isa 66:3's soul formed in its object by sustained misdirected Delight.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 4.*

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Relational Disposition** — the agreeableness-of-persons register (M04-J) involves relational orientation: Psa 133:1's pleasantness of brotherly unity, 2Sa 1:26's relational warmth; (2) **Moral Character** — the wisdom-comparative register (M04-K-VCG-03) engages moral evaluation of what is genuinely pleasant; Pro 15:16 (little with fear of the Lord better) — the moral character of the person's evaluations shapes their Pleasure; (3) **Vitality/Existence** — Pro 16:24's "health to the body" connects Pleasure to somatic wellbeing; (4) **Divine-Human Correspondence** — the ni.cho.ach relational structure between human worship and divine receptive Pleasure names a correspondence at the worship-interface.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 5.*

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Affective** — the arrested, overwhelmed quality of Wonder (Mar 1:27's thambeō; Rev 17:6's "I marvelled greatly") is affective in character — an inner feeling-state of astonishment; (2) **Emotion-Positive** — VCG-01's wonder-that-produces-praise is a positive affective state; (3) **Agency** — the proclamation-acts that Wonder generates ("tell of his wondrous works") are agentive expressions; (4) **Relational Disposition** — Exo 15:11's "who is like you, O Lord?" places Wonder within the worshiper's relational posture toward God. The secondary dimensions are significant but do not displace the cognitive primary: Wonder is specifically at the cognitive boundary, not primarily an affective surge.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 6.*

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Volitional** — Mat 5:12; Jas 1:2; 1Pe 4:13 (commanded, requiring volitional engagement); (2) **Cognitive** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy" — a cognitive reframing act); Heb 12:2 (Christ's cognitive orientation toward the "joy set before him" enabling the cross-endurance); (3) **Eschatological-cognitive** — the sustained eschatological orientation that sustains present Suffering-Joy. The secondary dimensions are significant but do not displace the primary affective classification.

---

*End of Segment 1 (T0–T1). 36 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 7.*

---

### T2

#### T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

##### T2.1.1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

No verse in M04-A explicitly names the spirit (ruach/pneuma) as the constitutional location of exultation. The spirit-level location is not evidenced in this corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, in specific registers. Luk 1:47 — "my spirit rejoices in God my Savior" (Mary's Magnificat: the agalliao rejoicing is located explicitly in the pneuma/spirit). Luk 10:21 — "he rejoiced in the Holy Spirit" (Jesus' agalliao is located in and produced by the Holy Spirit). Act 13:52 — "the disciples were filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit" (joy and the Holy Spirit co-produced in the same constitutional event). Rom 14:17 — "joy in the Holy Spirit" (joy as a kingdom-constituent specifically in the Spirit). Gal 5:22 — joy as the Spirit's fruit. 1Th 1:6 — "joy of the Holy Spirit" as the accompanying state when the word is received in affliction. Phile 20 — "refresh my heart in Christ" (the Christ-dimension of inner joy). The spirit-level location is evidenced primarily in the NT agalliao and Spirit-fruit passages, and in Mary's Magnificat.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

No verse in the M04-L or M04-O corpus explicitly names the spirit (ruach/pneuma) as the constitutional seat of Gladness. Neh 9:20's "good Spirit" names the Spirit's quality as good but does not locate Gladness in the human spirit. Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

No verse in the M04-G, M04-H, M04-M, M04-N, or M04-P corpus explicitly names the human spirit (ruach/pneuma) as the constitutional seat of Delight. The primary constitutional locations evidenced are the inner being (Rom 7:22), the heart (Psa 40:8; 1:2), the soul (Mat 12:18 — divine), and the inner being as the generative source (Psa 51:6 — "truth in the inward being"). Spirit-level location is not evidenced for the human person's Delight in this corpus.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

No verse in the M04-J or M04-K corpus explicitly names the human spirit (ruach/pneuma) as the constitutional seat of Pleasure. The primary constitutional locations are the soul and the body. Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

No verse in the M04-I corpus explicitly names the human spirit (ruach/pneuma) as the constitutional seat of Wonder. The primary constitutional locations are the eyes/perception, the heart, and the mouth (in proclamation). Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Luk 1:47 — "my spirit rejoices in God my Savior" — the spirit (pneuma) is named as the seat of Mary's agalliao exultation. Luk 10:21 — "he rejoiced in the Holy Spirit" — Jesus' Suffering-Joy (in the context of the disciples' exposure to rejection in mission) is located specifically within the Holy Spirit. These are the clearest spirit-level constitutional locations in the entire M04 cluster. Additionally, the broader agalliao context: 1Th 1:6 (adjacent — "joy of the Holy Spirit" received amid affliction) and Act 13:52 (disciples filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit) confirm the Spirit-level as the primary constitutional home for the most intense Suffering-Joy register.

---

##### T2.1.2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence does not support spirit-level origin for exultation in this corpus. The primary constitutional language names the soul and heart (see T2.2 and T2.3). Spirit-level location is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Partially. The NT Spirit-mediated joy (Act 13:52; 1Th 1:6; Gal 5:22; Rom 14:17) shows that in its most intense and paradoxical forms (joy in affliction, joy under persecution), Joy is produced at the spirit level by the Spirit himself. However, the dominant OT constitutional home is the heart (not the spirit), and the M04-B corpus (281 verses, the largest sub-group) does not name the spirit as the primary location. Joy originates at multiple constitutional levels depending on register: in the heart (primary for the OT communal-festive corpus), in the spirit (primary for the NT Spirit-produced paradoxical joy), and at the whole-being level for its most comprehensive expressions.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

Not evidenced. The primary constitutional language is cognitive-evaluative (the faculty of discernment) and situational-affective (warm inner response). No origin at the spirit level is evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

Not evidenced. The primary constitutional language for Delight's origin is the heart and the inner being — not the spirit. God's Spirit is not named as the producer of Delight in this corpus (contrast with Characteristic 7's Suffering-Joy where the Spirit is the explicit producing agent). Delight appears as a characteristic of the soul and heart that is constitutionally native rather than Spirit-produced.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

Not evidenced. Pleasure in this corpus arises at the soul-body interface (Pro 16:24) and in the soul's receptive response to what is agreeable — not at the spirit level. The characteristic's most distinctive constitutional feature is its explicit body-level engagement (Pro 16:24; Deu 28:54–56; Isa 47:1), which is the opposite of a spirit-level origin.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

Not evidenced. Wonder arises at the cognitive-perceptive boundary — when what is encountered exceeds the mind's categories. This is a soul-level perceptive-cognitive event rather than a Spirit-level impartation. The absent Spirit-level evidence is consistent with Wonder's characteristically creaturely nature: it does not require Spirit-production but is the natural inner response of the finite being encountering the infinite.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, in its primary (agalliao) register. Luk 10:21 makes this explicit for Jesus; Luk 1:47 for Mary. The Spirit as the origin and enabler of the exultant quality of Suffering-Joy is confirmed: 1Th 1:6's "joy of the Holy Spirit" received in affliction names the Spirit as the producing agent. The ba.lag fragile register (M04-F) is not Spirit-located in this way — it is the unaided human attempt at cheerfulness, suggesting the spirit-level location is specific to the Spirit-enabled form and absent from the fragile-attempt form.

---

##### T2.1.3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

Not applicable — spirit-level location is not evidenced in this corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Spirit-level location for Joy reveals that its deepest and most paradox-transcending form — joy amid suffering, inexpressible joy in the unseen Christ (1Pe 1:8) — operates at the deepest constitutional level, below and beyond the affective and cognitive faculties. Mary's "my spirit rejoices" (Luk 1:47) locates this exultation in the innermost self before it reaches the heart and mind. Jesus' rejoicing "in the Holy Spirit" (Luk 10:21) shows that the purest divine-image expression of Joy is Spirit-mediated.
