The spirit-level location explains the characteristic's capacity to transcend adverse circumstances: joy operating at the spirit level is not accessible to the same distortions that affect heart-level and mind-level emotional states.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

Not applicable — spirit-level location is not evidenced. The significance of this silence: unlike Characteristic 7 (Suffering-Joy, where Spirit-mediation is prominent) and some registers of Joy, Gladness does not appear as a Spirit-produced inner state in this corpus. Its depth is evidenced at the evaluative-cognitive and affective levels rather than at the spirit level.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The absence of spirit-level location reveals Delight as characteristically a soul-and-heart-level phenomenon — it is the inner being's own native capacity for pleasurable orientation rather than a Spirit-imparted transcendent state. This distinguishes Delight from Suffering-Joy (which requires Spirit-enabling to transcend circumstances) and from the most intense registers of Joy. Delight arises from within the person's own constitutional inner being as a natural capacity that directs itself toward objects. The question of its disorder is therefore entirely a question of which object the native capacity attaches to — not whether the Spirit is present.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The absence of spirit-level location reveals Pleasure as the most constitutionally embodied positive characteristic in M04. Unlike Suffering-Joy (primarily spirit-level) and Delight (primarily inner-being/soul), Pleasure is the characteristic most directly connected to the body's sensory and material registers. This embodied quality is consistent with the ni.cho.ach aroma's physical-sensory character and the a.nog/ta.a.nug luxury register's explicit bodily orientation.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The absence of spirit-level location reveals Wonder as a naturally-arising creaturely capacity — it does not require special Spirit-production to occur; the finite being naturally experiences Wonder when genuinely encountering what exceeds its comprehension. This distinguishes Wonder from Suffering-Joy (Spirit-produced) and from the highest registers of Joy (Spirit-filled). Wonder is the characteristic most available to unregenerate persons as well as the redeemed — any person who genuinely encounters the extraordinary will experience some form of Wonder. Neh 9:17's failure ("did not consider your wondrous works") is a failure of attention, not a Spirit-absence.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Spirit-level location reveals that Suffering-Joy in its fullest form is not a human psychological achievement but a divinely-produced inner state. This explains the paradox: the person who genuinely exults amid suffering is not stronger-willed or more emotionally resilient than others but is inhabited by the Spirit at the deepest constitutional level. Spirit-level location also explains the characteristic's transcendence of circumstances: what is produced at the spirit level is not accessible to the same distortions that affect heart-level and mind-level inner states, which is why it can coexist with and even arise through suffering that would overwhelm ordinary affective joy.

---

##### T2.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for exultation. All constitutional language in the M04-A corpus points to the soul and heart levels, with bodily extension.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Spirit-level location is evidenced; not silent. It is more extensively evidenced in NT than OT registers.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for Gladness across M04-L and M04-O.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for human Delight across all five sub-groups. Note: Mat 12:18 names God's soul (psychē) as the seat of divine Delight in the Son — this is divine rather than human, and psychē rather than pneuma.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for Pleasure across both sub-groups.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for Wonder across all three VCGs.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Spirit-level location is the most clearly evidenced constitutional location for this characteristic; not silent.

---

#### T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

##### T2.2.1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Psa 35:9 — "my soul will rejoice in the Lord, exulting in his salvation" — names the soul (nephesh) as the active agent of exultation. Isa 61:10 — "my soul shall exult in my God" — confirms the soul as the constitutional locus. Psa 63:5 — "my soul will be satisfied as with fat and rich food, and my mouth will praise you with joyful lips" — shows exultation arising from the soul's deep satisfaction. These three explicit soul-level namings make exultation a confirmed soul-level characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Psa 86:4 — "Gladden the soul of your servant, for to you, O Lord, do I lift up my soul" (soul explicitly named as the seat of gladness to be produced by God). Psa 106:5 — "that I may rejoice in the gladness of your nation" (the aspirational soul-oriented joy of belonging to God's people). Eze 25:6 — "rejoiced with all the malice within your soul" (the soul as the corrupted source of malign joy). The soul appears as a locus of joy in specific passages, but less consistently than the heart.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Partially. Lam 3:25 — "the Lord is good to those who wait for him, to the soul who seeks him" — the soul (nephesh) is named as the seeking agent whose waiting posture enables the experience of God's goodness. Lam 3:26 — "it is good that one should wait quietly" — the benefit is for the person as a whole, with soul implied as the seat of the waiting posture. Ecc 6:3 — "his soul is not satisfied with life's good things" — the soul is the seat of satisfaction/dissatisfaction with the good. These confirm soul-level location in the wellbeing-register of M04-O.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, directly: (1) **Mat 12:18** — "my soul (psychē) is well pleased" — divine Delight located in the soul, establishing soul-level as the constitutional seat; (2) **Isa 66:3** — "their soul (nephesh) delights in their abominations" — soul named as the seat of misdirected corrupt Delight; (3) **Isa 53:10** — "when his soul makes an offering for guilt, he shall see his offspring" — the servant's soul is the constitutional seat of the self-offering that accomplishes God's purpose/delight; (4) **Heb 10:38** — "my soul has no pleasure in him" — soul (psychē) as the seat of divine withheld Delight; (5) **Psa 73:25** — "nothing on earth that I desire besides you" — the soul's exclusive directing of desire; (6) **Psa 94:19** — "your consolations cheer my soul" — the soul receiving delight-as-consolation. Soul-level is the most consistently named constitutional location across both divine and human registers of Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, explicitly: (1) **Pro 2:10** — "knowledge will be pleasant to your soul (nephesh)" — the soul is named as the seat receiving Pleasure in wisdom/knowledge; (2) **Pro 16:24** — "gracious words are like a honeycomb, sweetness to the soul and health to the body" — soul named first as the primary recipient; (3) **Psa 16:11** — "pleasures forevermore" at God's right hand — the pleasures are experienced by the whole person, with the soul as the experiential centre (the Psalm is addressed by the soul to God); (4) **Psa 36:8** — "river of your delights" from which worshippers drink — soul-level receptive drinking image.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Partially and indirectly: (1) **Psa 119:129** — "your testimonies are wonderful; therefore my soul keeps them" — the soul is named as the faculty that responds to Wonder by keeping the testimonies; Wonder in God's word moves the soul to obedience; (2) **Psa 139:14** — "I praise you, for I am fearfully and wonderfully made; wonderful are your works; my soul knows it very well" — the soul explicitly knows the wonderful works; (3) The overall Psalmic proclamatory corpus (VCG-01) is addressed by the whole self, with the soul as the implicit experiential centre. Soul-level location is evidenced through the soul's response to wonder (keeping testimonies; knowing wonders well) rather than as a named seat.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

No verse in the primary agalliao or ba.lag corpus explicitly names the soul (nephesh/psyche) as the constitutional seat of Suffering-Joy. Soul-level location is not directly evidenced in the M04-E-VCG-02 or M04-F corpus.

---

##### T2.2.2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Soul-level location places exultation at the centre of the person's deepest and most individual inner experience. Nephesh (soul) in the OT consistently names the person in their deepest, most essential individuality — the seat of life, appetite, and longing. Exultation arising from the soul means it is not a superficial or peripheral emotional response but a movement of the person's innermost life toward God. Psa 63:5's "soul satisfied as with richest food" reinforces this: the soul's exultation is its deepest satiation, meeting a need as fundamental as hunger.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Soul-level location confirms that Joy reaches into the deepest personal identity of the individual — the soul (nephesh) is the person in their essential individuality and life-force. When the soul is the seat of gladness (Psa 86:4), this means Joy is not a peripheral emotional surface-event but an inner reality engaging the very core of personhood. Eze 25:6's "malice within your soul" as the source of corrupt joy shows that misdirected joy reaches just as deep — the distortion of Joy affects the soul's fundamental orientation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Soul-level location in the Gladness corpus confirms that the soul's orientation (seeking, waiting, being satisfied or dissatisfied) determines whether Gladness is genuinely experienced. Lam 3:25's "the soul who seeks him" as the recipient of God's goodness shows Gladness is not available to any inner posture but specifically to the seeking soul. Ecc 6:3's unsatisfied soul is the inverse: the soul that is not oriented toward genuine goodness cannot receive it.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Soul-level location reveals Delight as the characteristic most deeply rooted in the person's core self — not a surface emotional response but the orientation of the essential person toward a treasured object. Mat 12:18's "my soul is well pleased" places divine Delight at the deepest level of God's inner being; Isa 66:3's "their soul delights in their abominations" shows the depth of corruption when Delight is misdirected — the soul itself has been formed around the wrong object. Soul-level location explains why Delight is so formatively powerful: what the soul orients itself toward becomes the organizing centre of the person's inner life.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Soul-level location confirms that Pleasure is genuinely an inner-being characteristic, not merely a surface sensory reaction. Pro 2:10's "pleasant to your soul" positions the inner person's deepest experiential self as the seat of Pleasure in wisdom — when genuine wisdom enters the heart, the soul experiences a qualitative pleasantness. Pro 16:24's "sweetness to the soul" shows that even speech-Pleasure penetrates to the soul level. The soul receives Pleasure from what is genuinely agreeable — this is the characteristic's primary constitutional function.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Psa 119:129's "my soul keeps them" in response to the testimonies being wonderful reveals that Wonder in God's word produces a soul-level obedience response — the wonderfulness of the testimonies motivates the soul to hold to them. This is analytically distinctive: Wonder is the cognitive-perceptive response, and the soul's keeping is the volitional consequence. Psa 139:14's "my soul knows it very well" places the knowing of Wonder at the soul level — an intimate, deeply personal knowing of God's wondrous works.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

Not evidenced; soul-level constitutional location cannot be commented on from this corpus.

---

##### T2.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Soul-level location is not silent; it is explicitly confirmed at three verses.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced at the referenced passages; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced at the referenced verses; not fully silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Soul-level location is the dominant constitutional evidence; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Soul-level location is explicitly evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced at Psa 119:129 and 139:14; not fully silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

The evidence is silent on soul-level location for Suffering-Joy in the M04-E-VCG-02 and M04-F corpus.

---

#### T2.3 — Heart

##### T2.3.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, explicitly and repeatedly. Psa 13:5 — "my heart shall rejoice in your salvation" (heart named as the site of rejoicing); Psa 16:9 — "my heart is glad, and my whole being rejoices" (heart named first, then the whole being); Psa 32:11 — "all you upright in heart" are commanded to rejoice (the heart's uprightness is the precondition); Isa 66:14 — "your heart shall rejoice" (heart as the organ of the promised future joy); Zec 10:7 — "their hearts shall rejoice in the Lord" (heart explicitly named as the rejoicing seat). God's own exultation in Jer 32:41 is located "with all my heart and all my soul." The heart is the most frequently named constitutional locus for exultation in this corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes — the heart is the most extensively and consistently named constitutional locus for Joy across the entire corpus. Exo 4:14 (Aaron "will be glad in his heart"); Deu 28:47 (joyfulness "of heart" commanded); 1Ki 8:66 / 2Ch 7:10 (joyful and "glad of heart"); Psa 4:7 ("more joy in my heart"); Psa 19:8 ("precepts of the Lord… rejoicing the heart"); Psa 33:21 ("our heart is glad in him"); Psa 97:11 ("joy for the upright in heart"); Psa 105:3 ("hearts of those who seek the Lord rejoice"); Pro 14:10 ("no stranger shares its joy" — the heart's private joy); Pro 14:13 ("even in laughter the heart may ache"); Pro 15:13 ("a glad heart makes a cheerful face"); Pro 17:22 ("a joyful heart is good medicine"); Pro 15:30 ("the light of the eyes rejoices the heart"); Jer 15:16 ("joy and the delight of my heart"); Ecc 5:20 ("God keeps him occupied with joy in his heart"); Song 3:11 ("the gladness of his heart"); Joh 16:22 ("your hearts will rejoice"); Zep 3:14 ("rejoice and exult with all your heart"). The heart is the characteristic's primary constitutional home.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, in specific registers. Ecc 5:20 — "God keeps him occupied with joy in his heart" (sa.s.von — M04-E overlap, but the tov-context: the heart is named as the seat of gladness-in-one's-lot). Jer 15:16 — "your words became to me a joy and the delight of my heart" (sa.s.von — again overlapping M04-E but paradigmatic for Gladness's heart-location). Within the M04-O corpus: Pro 12:25 — "a good word makes him glad" — the gladness produced is in the heart (the heart being weighed down by anxiety is what the good word lifts). Psa 119:111 — "your testimonies are my heritage forever, for they are the joy of my heart" (sa.s.von) — heart-location. In M04-L: the ki-tov declarations produce thanksgiving grounded in the heart's recognition of divine goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, explicitly: (1) **Psa 40:8** — "I delight to do your will, O my God; your law is within my heart" — heart is the seat where God's law resides as the object of Delight, and from which the will to do God's will flows; (2) **Psa 1:2** — "his delight is in the law of the Lord, and on his law he meditates day and night" — the heart as the seat of sustained delight-meditation; (3) **Psa 119:24** — "your testimonies are my delight; they are my counselors" — the testimonies as delight are what counsel the heart; (4) **Psa 112:1** — "the man who greatly delights in his commandments" — the heart-orientation of delight toward God's commands; (5) **Psa 16:3** — "in whom is all my delight" — the heart's pleasure directed toward the community of saints; (6) **1Sa 19:1** — "Jonathan delighted much in David" — the heart's relational delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, indirectly: (1) **Pro 2:10** — "wisdom will come into your heart, and knowledge will be pleasant to your soul" — heart and soul are named in sequence; wisdom enters the heart first, and knowledge becomes pleasant to the soul as a result — the heart is the receiving organ whose state determines whether Pleasure in knowledge follows; (2) **Psa 45:1** — "my heart overflows with a pleasing theme" — the heart as the seat from which the pleasant poetic inspiration wells up; (3) **Gen 8:21** — "the Lord said in his heart" after smelling the pleasing aroma — the divine Pleasure at the offering is located in God's heart (lev); (4) **Pro 15:15** — "the cheerful of heart has a continual feast" — the heart's positive inner state producing a continuous Pleasure-quality to daily life.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 9:1** — "I will give thanks to the Lord with my whole heart; I will recount all of your wonderful deeds" — heart named as the seat of the whole-hearted thanksgiving that Wonder produces; (2) **Gen 8:21** (cross-assigned in M04-K but paradigmatic) — God "said in his heart" after smelling the pleasing aroma — while this is Pleasure territory, the pattern of inner resolve following receptive encounter is analogous; (3) **Psa 131:1** — "my heart is not lifted up; my eyes are not raised too high; I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me" — the heart as the seat of the humble posture that rightly orients toward Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, in one instance. Act 2:26 — "my heart was glad, and my tongue rejoiced" (Peter quoting Psalm 16:9 in the resurrection-promise context — agalliao on the tongue) — the heart is named as the seat of gladness that precedes the tongue's rejoicing. Job 9:27 (M04-F) — "put off my sad face" implicitly involves the heart as the source of the sorrowful countenance, but the term itself (ba.lag) doesn't explicitly name the heart. The heart is evidenced but not the dominant constitutional language — the spirit level is primary for this characteristic.

---

##### T2.3.2 — What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The heart in OT anthropology is the integrating centre of the person — encompassing knowing, willing, feeling, and moral orientation. Heart-location for exultation reveals that this is not a peripheral emotion but an integrated inner state engaging the whole person's central faculty. Psa 32:11's "upright in heart" as the precondition for rejoicing shows exultation is not morally neutral — it is the appropriate inner expression of a heart aligned with God. The heart both originates exultation (Psa 13:5 — "my heart shall rejoice") and sustains it (Psa 89:16 — "exult in your name all the day").

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The heart's integrating role means Joy at the heart level is not a peripheral emotion but an inner state engaging the whole person's central volitional-affective-knowing faculty. Pro 15:13 directly connects heart-gladness to countenance (the outer expression of inner state) and contrasts it with sorrow crushing the spirit — showing the heart as the nexus where Joy or its absence determines the whole person's inner condition. The heart's Joy is the productive source of the person's orientation to the world: Deu 28:47's failure to "serve the Lord with joyfulness and gladness of heart" as the root cause of judgment reveals that the heart's inner posture before God is the most fundamental thing about the covenant person's standing.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Heart-location confirms that Gladness is not purely a cognitive judgment external to the person but an inner-being state that settles in the integrating centre. The heart is where Gladness takes up residence: in Jer 15:16 the word becomes "the delight of my heart" — it is received and held inwardly, not merely assessed externally. Pro 12:25's heart weighed down by anxiety that is relieved by a good word shows the heart as the seat where Gladness's presence or absence is most directly felt.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Heart-location reveals that Delight is the integrating faculty of the heart — it is how the heart orients itself toward its object. Psa 40:8 is paradigmatic: the law within the heart is what the heart delights in, and that delight drives the will to do God's will. The heart does not first decide and then delight; it first delights (law within) and thereby wills rightly. Delight is therefore the heart's orientation-faculty — it is the mechanism by which the heart chooses its object and aligns the will toward it.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Heart-location reveals that Pleasure is heart-mediated: the state of the heart determines the quality of Pleasure received. Pro 2:10's sequence (wisdom enters heart → knowledge pleasant to soul) shows the heart as the gateway: when the heart is rightly constituted by wisdom, the soul receives Pleasure in what is genuinely good. Pro 15:15's "cheerful of heart" confirms the heart as the seat whose positive orientation produces a continuous feast-quality of inner life — the inner disposition of the heart generates the felt pleasantness of daily experience. Gen 8:21 confirms: even divine Pleasure is located in God's heart.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Psa 9:1's "whole heart" in response to Wonder's proclamation shows that genuine Wonder produces whole-hearted engagement — the heart is fully involved in the thanksgiving that Wonder overflows into. Psa 131:1's "my heart is not lifted up" shows that the rightly-ordered heart is the condition for genuine Wonder: the humble heart does not overreach. Heart-location reveals Wonder as requiring heart-humility as an enabling condition and producing heart-wholeness as an effect.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Act 2:26's heart-gladness followed by tongue-rejoicing shows the characteristic moving from the inner constitutional centre (heart) outward to expressive declaration — consistent with the broader inner-to-outer pattern across M04. The heart as the seat of the initial gladness (even in the Peter-quoting-David context) confirms that Suffering-Joy is not purely spirit-level but has a heart-level component in its expressed form.

---

##### T2.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Heart-location is extensively evidenced; no silence to note.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Heart-location is the most extensively evidenced constitutional location in this corpus; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Heart-location is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Heart-location is extensively evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Heart-location is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Heart-location is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Heart-location is evidenced at Act 2:26; not fully silent.

---

#### T2.4 — Mind

##### T2.4.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

No verse in the M04-A corpus explicitly names the mind (leb as rational faculty, dianoia, nous) as the constitutional locus of exultation. The leb-heart is named, but as the integrative affective-volitional centre rather than the rational-cognitive mind specifically.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Partially, as a precondition rather than the seat. Neh 8:12 — "great rejoicing, because they had understood the words that were declared to them" — comprehension (a mind-faculty act) produces joy; the joy is in the heart and expressed in eating and celebration, but the mind's understanding is its direct cause. The Ecclesiastes investigations (Ecc 2:1 — "I said in my heart, come now, I will test you with pleasure") show the mind directing the inner experiment, but the joy itself is located in the heart. No verse explicitly names the mind (as distinct from the heart-as-rational-faculty) as the seat of Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes — more prominently than for any other M04 characteristic. The M04-L-VCG-02 corpus is essentially an exercise of the evaluative-cognitive faculty: weighing, comparing, judging. Exo 18:17 (Jethro's experienced assessment); Rut 2:22 (Naomi's prudential reasoning); Job 34:4 ("let us know among ourselves what is good" — explicitly cognitive discernment); Mic 6:8 ("he has told you, O man, what is good" — knowing is the precondition for doing). The evaluative "better than" comparatives throughout M04-L-VCG-02 and M04-O-VCG-02 are cognitive acts of comparison.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Partially, in the volitional-cognitive dimension: (1) **Job 34:4** — "let us know among ourselves what is good" — though this is in M04-L (Gladness), the adjacent wisdom-comparative corpus in M04-H-VCG-03 (Pro 3:15; 8:11 — "nothing you desire can compare with her" — wisdom as the surpassing object of che.phets) engages the mind's evaluative faculty; (2) **Ecc 12:10** — "the Preacher sought to find words of delight" — the mind's aesthetic-intellectual search for truth expressed in pleasurable form; (3) **1Ch 28:9** — "a willing mind" (cha.phets adj) as the cognitive-volitional inner orientation for serving God; (4) **Psa 111:2** — "great are the works of the Lord, studied by all who delight in them" — Delight engaging the mind toward sustained inquiry. Mind-location is present but secondary to soul and heart.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

No verse in the M04-J or M04-K corpus explicitly names the mind as the constitutional seat of Pleasure. The wisdom-comparative register (M04-K-VCG-03) engages the evaluative faculty which is cognitively located, but the better-than comparatives operate through the heart-soul rather than naming "mind" explicitly. Mind-location is not directly evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes — this is Wonder's primary constitutional location in its cognitive mode: (1) **Job 37:5** ("great things that we cannot comprehend") — mental comprehension as the cognitive faculty that Wonder encounters at its limits; (2) **Job 42:3** ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — knowledge as the cognitive capacity that Wonder exceeds; (3) **Psa 119:27** ("make me understand the way of your precepts, and I will meditate on your wondrous works") — understanding as the prerequisite for meditating on wonders; (4) **Psa 131:1** ("I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me") — the mind deliberately restraining itself from overreach into the incomprehensible; (5) **Isa 29:14** ("the wisdom of their wise men shall perish, and the discernment of their discerning men shall be hidden") — human wisdom and discernment (cognitive faculties) eclipsed by God's wonders.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Partially, through the cognitive-reframing acts: Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") is a cognitive act — the counting/considering is a mental operation; Heb 12:2 ("for the joy that was set before him endured the cross") involves Christ's cognitive orientation toward the eschatological joy as the mental ground for endurance. These are not explicit mind-location statements but show cognitive involvement in sustaining Suffering-Joy.

---

##### T2.4.2 — What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

Not directly evidenced. The cognitive element of exultation (knowing the ground of exultation — God's salvation, reign, presence) is present in the evidence but is the precondition for exultation rather than exultation's constitutional seat.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The mind's role in Joy is as a precondition and director: the person who understands God's acts (Neh 8:12), perceives divine goodness (Psa 97:8 — "Zion hears and is glad"), or comprehends the gospel (Act 13:48 — "the Gentiles heard this, they began rejoicing") has the cognitive reception that enables the heart's joy. The mind provides the true account of what is happening; the heart responds with joy. The two are consistently sequenced: perception/comprehension → heart's gladness → expressed rejoicing.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Mind-location reveals Gladness as uniquely cognitively-constituted among M04 characteristics. The evaluative-gladness faculty is a function of the person's reasoning, discerning, and comparing capacities. This explains why Gladness is less susceptible to direct command than Joy (Phili 4:4) — one cannot simply be commanded to evaluate correctly; one must be formed in the capacity for accurate moral and relational assessment. The cognitive dimension is why the wisdom literature is the primary carrier of M04-L: Proverbs and Ecclesiastes are fundamentally training texts for the evaluative faculty.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Mind involvement in Delight reveals the characteristic as having a wisdom-generating dimension when the object is God's works or truth: Psa 111:2 shows Delight driving study; Ecc 12:10 shows it driving the search for words. Delight in God's law (Psa 1:2 — meditation day and night) engages the mind as the instrument through which the heart's delight sustains itself. Delight does not bypass the mind but channels the mind toward its object — it is the heart-level orientation that directs the mind's engagement.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

Not directly evidenced; the cognitive-evaluative engagement with Pleasure (M04-K-VCG-03) operates through wisdom-formation of the heart and soul rather than through an explicitly named mind. The absence of explicit mind-location confirms Pleasure as primarily affective-receptive rather than cognitively-mediated (unlike Gladness whose primary dimension is cognitive-evaluative).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Mind-location reveals Wonder as the characteristic that specifically arises at the cognitive boundary — it is the response when the mind's comprehension reaches its limit. This makes Wonder unique in M04: it is the only characteristic that is constitutively defined by the cognitive faculty's encounter with what exceeds it. The mind is both the faculty that encounters Wonder (by trying to comprehend what is incomprehensible) and the faculty that is formed by Wonder (into humility and sustained contemplation). Isa 29:14 shows that human wisdom/discernment can actually become an obstacle to Wonder when it becomes presumptuous — the formed mind must be humble to remain genuinely wonder-capable.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The mind's role in Suffering-Joy is specifically in the **eschatological reorientation** that sustains it: by cognitively holding the future joy (reward in heaven, glory to be revealed) as more real than present suffering, the mind enables the spirit's joy to hold. This is the specific cognitive contribution: not reasoning one's way into joy but orienting one's cognitive frame around eschatological truth that grounds the Spirit's work.

---

##### T2.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence is silent on mind-level location for exultation specifically. Mind-level engagement is implicit in the knowing of God's acts (Exo 18:9; Isa 25:9) but the mind is not named as the characteristic's seat.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The mind is evidenced as a precondition of Joy (comprehension enables it) but is not named as its constitutional seat. The primary constitutional seat is the heart.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Mind-location is the most extensively evidenced constitutional location for Gladness; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Mind-involvement is evidenced in the wisdom-study dimension; not fully silent, though secondary.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location for Pleasure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Mind-location is the most prominently evidenced constitutional location for Wonder; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Mind-involvement is evidenced through cognitive reframing (Jas 1:2; Heb 12:2) but not as explicit constitutional seat-naming.

---

#### T2.5 — Other Soul Subsets

##### T2.5.1 — Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: the **whole being** (Psa 16:9 — "my whole being rejoices"; the Hebrew uses the term for "glory" or "my honour/innermost self" as a designation for the whole inner person). This suggests exultation, while arising from the heart and soul, extends to encompass the totality of the person's inner being.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **The whole being / whole inner self** — Psa 16:9 ("my heart is glad, and my whole being rejoices") — Joy extends from the heart to encompass the totality of the inner person; (2) **The mouth and tongue as expressive organs** — Act 2:26 ("my tongue rejoiced") — in this agalliao verse, the tongue is named as the rejoicing organ, showing Joy's primary inner state (heart-gladness) expressing itself through the first inner-to-outer organ of speech; (3) **The bones** — Psa 51:8 ("let the bones that you have broken rejoice") — Joy's restoration is requested at the deepest somatic level.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: **bones** — Pro 15:30 ("good news refreshes the bones") — the deepest somatic structure is the recipient of gladness in the good-news register; the refreshment of good news penetrates to the body's depths. This is the most physicality-affirming instance of Gladness's constitutional location.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **The "inner being"** — Rom 7:22 ("I delight in the law of God, in my inner being") — the most precise and explicit constitutional location for Delight in the NT; sunēdomai locating Delight at the deepest self-level, in contrast to the flesh which operates at a different level; (2) **The will** — the cha.phets/che.phets volitional faculty is constitutionally located in the person's capacity for directed inner resolution; Isa 53:10 ("the will of the Lord") merges delight and volition; (3) **The "secret heart"** — Psa 51:6 ("you teach me wisdom in the secret heart") — the inward/secret part as where God's truth-delight is taught; this is the deepest inner constitutional layer beyond the surface heart.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: **the whole person as receiving subject** — Psa 133:1's "how good and pleasant" is exclaimed over the whole community; Job 36:11's "years in pleasantness" names the whole life-quality; Psa 16:6's "pleasant places" names the whole inheritance-condition; these are not specifically located in heart, mind, or soul individually but name the whole-person experience of Pleasure in one's lot. Additionally: **the perceiving senses** — Psa 27:4's "gaze upon the beauty of the Lord" — the eyes as the perceptive organ; Psa 34:8 (in M04-K — "taste and see that the Lord is good") — the gustatory sense as a perception metaphor.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: **the eyes** — Psa 118:23 ("it is marvellous in our eyes") — the visual perception organ as the specific site of Wonder-reception; Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things") — the eyes as the faculty seeking to receive Wonder; **the mouth** — Psa 9:1 ("I will recount"); Psa 78:4 ("tell to the coming generation") — the mouth as the expressive organ of proclaimed Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: **tongue** — Act 2:26 ("my tongue rejoiced") — the tongue as the expressive organ of inner exultation; **flesh/body** — Act 2:26 ("my flesh also will dwell in hope") — the body as the recipient of the hope that accompanies the rejoicing; **face** — Job 9:27 ("put off my sad face") — the face as the somatic expression of the inner struggle with cheerfulness; Psa 39:13 ("that I may smile again") — the face/countenance as the visible indicator of the barely-attainable brightening.

---

##### T2.5.2 — If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

"My whole being" (Psa 16:9) suggests exultation does not remain confined to a single constitutional sub-level but radiates through the whole inner person. This is consistent with the characteristic's expressive dimension (the surging inner state overflows into voice and body) and its comprehensive scope (the person is not divided in exultation but wholly engaged).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The whole-being location (Psa 16:9) reveals that Joy at its fullest does not stay confined to the heart but radiates through the entire inner person. This is consistent with the characteristic's expressive quality — Joy that truly takes hold of the heart moves through the whole being and out into voice, body, and action. The tongue-rejoicing (Act 2:26) shows Joy constitutively moving toward proclamation as its natural expression channel.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The "bones refreshed" by good news (Pro 15:30) reveals that Gladness in its most intense experiential form reaches the person at their deepest physical level. The bones are the body's inner framework; their refreshment by good news shows Gladness as a holistic inner-being phenomenon — not merely cognitive or affective but reaching to the body's structural level. This is consistent with the somatic imagery of restoration in the broader M04 cluster (Psa 51:8 — bones asked to rejoice).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Rom 7:22's "inner being" (esō anthrōpos) is the most constitutionally significant location for Delight in the entire corpus. It reveals that the deepest layer of the person — below and beneath what the flesh does — genuinely delights in God's law. This creates the Pauline inner conflict: the deepest self (Delight in God's law) and the flesh (doing what the law prohibits) are in opposition. Delight's location at the "inner being" level means it is the constitutional orientation of the regenerate person's deepest self, not merely a surface preference.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The whole-person and sense-perceptive locations reveal Pleasure as the most holistically distributed characteristic in M04 — it registers across the whole person (life-quality, inheritance-condition), through the senses (sight, taste, smell/aroma), in the soul (Pro 2:10), and in the body (Pro 16:24). No other M04 characteristic is as explicitly multi-level in its constitutional distribution.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**Eyes**: Wonder in its VCG-01 register is specifically perceptual — it requires seeing (Psa 118:23 — "marvellous in our eyes") and the petition to see (Psa 119:18 — "open my eyes"). This visual emphasis is unique to Wonder among M04 characteristics. Wonder begins with a perceptive encounter. **Mouth**: Wonder consistently produces proclamation — the mouth as the organ through which inner Wonder overflows into speech. The proclamatory character of Wonder (tell of, sing of, declare, recount) is its most distinctive expressive mode, consistently using the mouth.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The tongue-rejoicing (Act 2:26) shows Suffering-Joy moving from the deepest inner level (spirit/heart) outward to expressive declaration — consistent with agalliao's leaping-expressive root meaning. The face's smile (Psa 39:13; implied in Job 9:27) as the desired visible sign of ba.lag shows the characteristic's outward-expressive quality even in its fragile form: the inner brightening seeks a visible form even when barely attainable.

---

##### T2.5.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Not silent; whole-being location is evidenced at Psa 16:9.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not silent; whole-being and tongue-locations are evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Bones-location evidenced at Pro 15:30; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Inner being and secret heart locations are explicitly evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple locations beyond heart and mind are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Eyes and mouth as Wonder-locations are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Tongue and face/body-level locations are evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T2.6 — Body — Significance

##### T2.6.1 — Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, explicitly. (1) **Bones** — Psa 51:8: "let the bones that you have broken rejoice" — the bones as a felt, bodily image of inner anguish are addressed for rejoicing; this is the most somatic of the exultation sayings, connecting the characteristic's restoration to the body's deepest structural experience. (2) **Flesh** — Psa 16:9: "my flesh also dwells secure" — the body's security is the outward evidence of the inner rejoicing's completeness. (3) **Mouth / lips** — Psa 63:5; 100:2; re.na.nah generally — the mouth and lips as the expressive organs of the triumphing cry. (4) **The sun's course** (Psa 19:5) — the body-in-motion analogy for exultation's vigorous quality.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, multiple: (1) **Bones** — Psa 51:8 ("let the bones that you have broken rejoice") — the bones as the body's deepest structural element asked to participate in restored Joy; (2) **Flesh** — Psa 16:9 ("my flesh also dwells secure") — the body's security as the outer consequence of inner-being Joy; (3) **Tongue** — Act 2:26 ("my tongue rejoiced") — the speech organ as the primary bodily channel of Joy's expression; (4) **Hands and dancing** — 2Sa 6:12 (ark brought "with rejoicing"; David dances before the Lord); Jer 31:13 ("young women rejoice in the dance") — the body's movement as Joy's physical expression; (5) **Face** — Pro 15:13 ("a glad heart makes a cheerful face") — the face as the most visible bodily indicator of inner Joy; (6) **Leaping body** — Luk 1:44 ("the baby in my womb leaped for joy") — the most extreme bodily expression of Joy, occurring in an unborn child; (7) **Womb** — Luk 1:44 as above.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Bones** — Pro 15:30 ("good news refreshes the bones") — the deepest structural body part; (2) **Face** — implicitly through the "smile again" of Psa 39:13 (M04-F corpus but adjacent — in M04-F-VCG-01: "before I depart and am no more, let me smile again" = let me recover a little of the brightness); the face as the outward sign of inner gladness; (3) **The whole body / person** — 1Sa 16:23 ("Saul was refreshed and was well") — the inner-being state of wellbeing extending to the whole person.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **The foot** — Deu 28:56 ("the most tender woman would not venture to set the sole of her foot on the ground because she is so delicate/a.nog") — the foot as the somatic indicator of a.nog's physical register; the cursed loss of delight manifests in the foot touching degraded ground; (2) **The mouth** — Isa 55:2 ("listen diligently to me, and eat what is good, and delight yourselves in rich food" — a.nog) — eating/mouth as the somatic metaphor for Delight's nourishing quality; Isa 66:11 ("nurse and drink deeply with delight from her glorious abundance" — a.nog) — mouth and body engaged in the delight of restoration's abundance; (3) **The knee/hip** — Isa 66:12 (sha.a — being bounced on knees) — the body's most intimate parental care as the image of Delight's quality; (4) **The nose/smell** — ni.cho.ach aroma (M04-M-VCG-01; M04-P-VCG-01) — the soothing aroma reaching God (or idols) through the physical offering — the most unique body-link in the corpus, mediated through smell/aroma.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, multiple: (1) **Nose/smell** — the ni.cho.ach aroma corpus (M04-K-VCG-01) is centred on the olfactory sense: Gen 8:21 ("the Lord smelled the pleasing aroma"); Num 28:2 ("my pleasing aroma") — the nose as the organ through which worship-Pleasure reaches God; (2) **Mouth/tongue** — Pro 16:24 ("gracious words are like a honeycomb, sweetness to the soul") — the honey-simile invokes the gustatory sense; Psa 34:8 ("taste and see that the Lord is good" — cross-assigned) — explicit gustatory-sense invocation; (3) **Eyes** — Psa 27:4 ("to gaze upon the beauty of the Lord") — sight as the medium for divine-beauty Pleasure; (4) **Body overall** — Pro 16:24 ("health to the body") — the body as a whole receiving the healing benefit of gracious-word Pleasure; Deu 28:54, 56 (the delicate person's foot not setting on the ground — somatic delicateness); Isa 47:1 (tender and delicate — somatic luxury).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Eyes** — Psa 118:23; 119:18 — the primary perceptive organ of Wonder; (2) **Mouth** — the proclamatory dimension (tell, declare, sing, recount) — 1Ch 16:9, 24; Psa 9:1; 26:7; 78:4 — the expressive organ; (3) **Hands** — 2Ch 26:15 (Uzziah's machines and his fame spreading because "he was marvellously helped") — the body's productive capacity enabled by wonder-invoking divine assistance; (4) **The whole person prostrating** — Mar 10:32 (the amazed disciples following Jesus toward Jerusalem) implies bodily engagement alongside the inner state.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Tongue** — Act 2:26 ("my tongue rejoiced" — agalliao); (2) **Flesh** — Act 2:26 ("my flesh also will dwell in hope"); (3) **Face/countenance** — Job 9:27 ("put off my sad face"); Psa 39:13 ("that I may smile again").

---

##### T2.6.2 — If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Three functions are evidenced: (1) **Emphasis** — bones as the seat of deepest suffering being asked to rejoice (Psa 51:8) intensifies the characteristic's restoring power: if even the crushed bones can rejoice, the restoration is total; (2) **Indicator** — flesh dwelling secure (Psa 16:9) shows the body as the indicator of the soul's exultation — the person's bodily security is evidence of the inner joy's reality; (3) **Expression** — the mouth and lips are the natural expressive channel through which inner exultation moves outward into the world.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Three functions: (1) **Extension** — the joy that begins in the heart reaches through the whole person and out into the body (Psa 16:9; Pro 15:13) — showing Joy as a characteristic that encompasses the whole human being, not only the inner; (2) **Depth-emphasis** — bones and womb are the body's most hidden and deep levels; joy reaching to the bones (Psa 51:8) and leaping in the womb (Luk 1:44) signals that this inner state penetrates to the deepest physical levels of human existence; (3) **Expression** — tongue, hands, face, and dance are the body's expressive surfaces; their involvement shows Joy as a characteristic that naturally overflows from within outward into visible, audible expression.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Pro 15:30's bones-connection serves an **emphatic** function: it insists that genuine good news does not remain at a surface emotional level but penetrates to the person's physical depths. This is a similar rhetorical strategy to Psa 51:8's "bones that you have broken" — the bones stand for the deepest inner experience. Scripture links Gladness to the bones to convey its thoroughgoing, holistic character: genuine gladness-from-good-news restores the whole person.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) The food/mouth/nursing images (Isa 55:2; 66:11) are **emphatic** — they insist that Delight in God and in his restoration is as physically real and deeply satisfying as nourishing food and the infant's nursing; the body's own experience of satisfaction is the image chosen to convey what soul-level Delight in God is like; (2) The ni.cho.ach aroma link is **mediating** — the physical aroma rises from the altar and reaches God (or in M04-P, the idol), conveying the inner disposition of the worshipper through a physical medium; the external aroma represents the inner orientation of obedient Delight (or its corrupt counterpart); (3) The bounced-on-knees image (Isa 66:12) is **expressive** — it gives somatic form to the quality of carefree, entirely-held, resting Delight in divine peace.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Nose (ni.cho.ach)** — the olfactory link is **mediating**: the physical aroma rises from the altar and reaches God through the olfactory dimension, making the sensory physical act the medium of the worship-Pleasure relationship; the physical smell mediates a spiritual-relational reality (God's reception of the worshiper's offering); (2) **Mouth/honey-sweetness** — Pro 16:24's honey simile is **emphatic**: it insists that genuinely pleasant speech nourishes as concretely and immediately as honey nourishes the body; the bodily taste-image serves to communicate the soul-level impact; (3) **Eyes** — Psa 27:4's "gaze" is **constitutive**: gazing upon God's beauty is the act that receives divine Pleasure; the eyes are not merely metaphorical but are the appropriate organ for encountering beauty; (4) **Body overall** — Pro 16:24's "health to the body" is **integrative**: pleasant speech heals the whole person, demonstrating that genuine Pleasure penetrates from word to soul to body.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Eyes** — the link is **constitutive**: Wonder at God's acts begins with seeing (Psa 118:23 — "it is marvellous in our eyes") and Psa 119:18 asks for opened eyes specifically to behold wonders. The eyes are not merely metaphorical — genuine Wonder requires genuine perceptual encounter. (2) **Mouth** — the link is **expressive**: Wonder consistently overflows through speech into proclamation. The mouth-link reveals that Wonder is constitutively oral-doxological — it characteristically moves from inner astonishment to voiced declaration. The inner state seeks outward expression through the body's speech organ.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) The tongue-link (Act 2:26) is **expressive** — the inner exultation of Suffering-Joy moves outward through the body's speech organ into declaration; (2) The flesh/hope-link (Act 2:26) is **indicative** — the body's hoped-for security is the outward evidence that the inner Suffering-Joy has a bodily dimension and is not merely abstract; (3) The face-smile-link (Job 9:27; Psa 39:13) is **emphatic** — the barely-sought smile is both the goal of ba.lag and the visible evidence of its presence; seeking to smile is seeking the somatically-visible form of inner cheerfulness.

---

##### T2.6.3 — If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced at multiple verses.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Body-part links are extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Body-part link evidenced at Pro 15:30; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple body-part links are evidenced across the corpus; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple body-part links are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Body-part links (eyes, mouth) are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T2.7 — Body — Direction

##### T2.7.1 — Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to the soul, or does it run in both directions?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The primary direction is **inner to outer**: soul exults → mouth praises (Psa 63:5); heart is glad → whole being rejoices → flesh dwells secure (Psa 16:9). The bones-rejoicing (Psa 51:8) is the restoration direction — the inner state of exultation, once restored, reaches through to the body's deepest structural level. There is no clear evidence of the body feeding back into the inner exultation in this corpus — the direction is consistently soul/heart → body/voice.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The primary direction is **inner to outer**: heart gladness → cheerful face (Pro 15:13); heart rejoices → whole being rejoices → flesh dwells secure (Psa 16:9); soul rejoices → tongue rejoices (Act 2:26). The secondary direction — **outer to inner** — appears in the feast-context passages: eating, drinking, and feasting (Deu 16:13–15; 1Ki 8:66; Ecc 9:7) are outer acts prescribed to occasion inner gladness; the bodily act of feasting in God's presence is a means of producing and expressing the inner joy. Wine gladdens the heart (Psa 104:15; Ecc 10:19) — a bodily input producing an inner state. This bidirectionality is notable: Joy is not only inner-to-outer in expression but also cultivated through outer forms that produce inner states.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

**Inner to outer**: the good news received by the inner person (cognitively and affectively) refreshes the bones — the inner gladness moves outward to the body's structural level. There is no evidence of the body initiating gladness in this corpus (unlike some Pleasure instances where sensory input produces inner warmth). The direction is consistently: news/word/circumstance received by the inner person → inner gladness arises → body participates in the refreshment.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Both directions: (1) **Inner to outer** — the primary direction in the affective-receptive register: the soul's delight in God's restoration expresses through the body (nursing, eating, being bounced — Isa 55:2; 66:11–12); the inner orientation produces outward bodily participation; (2) **Outer to inner** — the ni.cho.ach aroma direction: the physical act of offering the correctly-prescribed sacrifice (Lev 1:17; Num 15:13) is the outer act that expresses and reinforces the inner orientation of obedient Delight toward God; the aroma is the outer form of an inner disposition; (3) **Outer as sign of inner loss** — Deu 28:56 — the delicate woman's foot touching the ground is the outward sign of the inner Delight (a.nog) destroyed by judgment; the body signals what the inner being has lost.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Both directions: (1) **Body-to-soul** — the ni.cho.ach aroma rises from the offering (physical) and reaches God's inner being (divine inner response); in the human person: the perception of a pleasant aroma, sight, or taste produces an inner soul response (the olfactory, visual, and gustatory senses feeding inward to the soul); (2) **Soul-to-body** — Pro 16:24's gracious words received by the soul produce "health to the body" — the inner reception of pleasant speech flows outward to bodily health; the soul's Pleasure produces body-benefit; (3) **Body-as-signal** — Deu 28:54, 56 (the delicate body as the sign of Pleasure in pampered ease); the body's condition signals the inner state of Pleasure or its absence.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**External-to-inner-to-outward**: God's marvellous work (external) → perceived by the eyes (perceptive body) → wonder arises in the mind/soul (inner) → proclaimed through the mouth (expressive body). The direction is: external encounter → inner arrest → outward proclamation. This is a three-stage sequence: perception → astonishment → expression.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

**Inner to outer**: spirit/heart exults → tongue rejoices (Act 2:26); inner gladness → face smiles (Psa 39:13). The direction is consistently from the deepest constitutional level (spirit) outward through heart, tongue, and face. There is no evidence in this corpus of bodily state initiating the inner Suffering-Joy.

---

##### T2.7.2 — What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The soul-to-body direction shows exultation as fundamentally an inner-originating characteristic that overflows into the body and voice. The body does not produce the inner state but receives and expresses it. This means exultation cannot be manufactured from the outside — it must originate in the soul/heart's genuine orientation before it reaches the body and voice. The commanded exultations (Psa 32:11; Zec 9:9) work by addressing the will and heart, not by commanding the body.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The bidirectionality reveals that Joy is both a spontaneous inner state that seeks outward expression and a cultivated inner state that can be formed through prescribed outer practices (feasts, singing, dancing, communal eating). This is why Deuteronomy commands the feast-joy — the commanded outer form of rejoicing before God is itself a means of producing and sustaining the inner state. The implication for formation: Joy can be cultivated through embodied communal practices, not only through direct divine encounter or inner resolve. The outer-to-inner direction is the wisdom of the feast commandments.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The inner-to-outer direction confirms that Gladness is an inner-originating state that expresses itself in and through the body, not a bodily state that generates inner gladness. This is significant: the body's refreshment is evidence of inner gladness, not its cause. Genuine gladness must first be received inwardly (cognitively through evaluation, affectively through response) before it reaches the body.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The bidirectional link reveals Delight as fully embodied — it does not remain confined to the inner being but seeks expression through the body and can be reinforced through bodily acts. The ni.cho.ach aroma direction is particularly significant: it shows that the outer form of worship (correctly offered sacrifice) is not indifferent to the inner state but serves as the embodied expression and reinforcement of the inner orientation of Delight. This explains why misdirected ni.cho.ach (M04-P-VCG-01 — Eze 20:28) is so severe: the outer act reinforces and expresses the inner misdirection.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The bidirectional body-link reveals Pleasure as a constitutionally integrative characteristic: it is both received through bodily senses and communicated outward to bodily health. Unlike characteristics that are purely inner-being (no body link) or purely body-triggered (no inner-being consequence), Pleasure is simultaneously sensory-received and soul-expressed, body-triggered and body-healing. This bidirectionality makes Pleasure the most fully embodied positive inner-being characteristic in M04.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The external-to-inner-to-outward direction reveals Wonder as inherently relational in its full expression: it is not self-contained but moves from encounter (external) through inner astonishment to communal proclamation (outward). The person who genuinely wonders cannot simply keep it internal — it moves through the mouth into declaration. This also explains why Wonder's failure (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful") is both an inner failure (not registering) and a communal failure (not declaring to others).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The inner-to-outer direction confirms that Suffering-Joy cannot be manufactured by external performance — the person who forces a smile (attempting ba.lag) without the inner Spirit-work merely performs what is not present. The genuine form requires the inner-being production (Spirit-level) before the tongue and face can genuinely express it. This is the key distinction between genuine Suffering-Joy (agalliao — inner Spirit-produced, expressed outwardly) and mere cheerfulness-performance (attempted ba.lag that may fail).

---

##### T2.7.3 — If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Link is evidenced; see T2.7.1–T2.7.2.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Bidirectional body-characteristic link is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Link is evidenced; see T2.7.1–T2.7.2.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Bidirectional body links are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Bidirectional body links are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Three-stage body links are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Link is evidenced; inner-to-outer direction confirmed.

---

#### T2.8 — Body — Deposit

##### T2.8.1 — Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence does not explicitly address constitutional deposit from sustained exultation. Psa 16:9's "flesh also dwells secure" suggests a bodily outcome of the inner state, but this reads as a present consequence rather than a cumulative deposit. No generational consequence or DNA-level implication is evidenced in this corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Partially evidenced. Pro 17:22 — "a joyful heart is good medicine" — implies that sustained heart-gladness has a medicinal effect on the body, suggesting a positive constitutional consequence. Lam 5:15 — "the joy of our hearts has ceased; our dancing has been turned to mourning" — the sustained absence of joy produces a corresponding physical loss (dancing ended). Isa 24:7 ("all the merry-hearted sigh") shows that sustained joylessness produces a corresponding bodily-inner state of sighing. These suggest that sustained Joy produces a positive bodily-constitutional environment; its sustained absence produces a deflated physical-inner condition. No explicit generational consequence is evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

The evidence does not explicitly address constitutional deposit from sustained Gladness. Pro 15:30's "bones refreshed" is an acute rather than a cumulative effect. No generational consequence or body-deposit language appears in the M04-L or M04-O corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The evidence implies soul-level deposit most strongly: (1) **Isa 66:3 — "their soul delights in their abominations"** — the most direct evidence of a constitutional deposit from sustained misdirected Delight: the soul itself has been formed around the wrong object through sustained engagement with it; (2) **Psa 1:2 — "meditates day and night"** — sustained Delight in God's law drives sustained meditation which deposits wisdom and the disposition of the blessed man (Psa 1:1–3 — "like a tree planted by streams of water"); (3) **Psa 40:8 — "your law is within my heart"** — the internalization of the law in the heart is the constitutional deposit of sustained Delight in God's word. The evidence suggests that sustained Delight forms a deposit at the soul and heart levels, orienting these constitutional layers permanently around the object of Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Implied but not explicitly named: (1) **Pro 16:24's "health to the body"** — sustained reception of gracious-word Pleasure produces an ongoing body-health, suggesting a depositional effect on physical wellbeing; (2) **The curse-inversion** — Deu 28:54, 56 shows that the sustained state of a.nog (pampered ease) leaves a person constitutionally shaped by that ease, so that when it is removed the collapse is catastrophic — the prior sustained Pleasure has formed a constitutional expectation and dependency; (3) **Wisdom-formed Pleasure** (M04-K-VCG-03) — sustained engagement with the wisdom better-than comparatives trains and forms the inner being to habitually evaluate what is genuinely more pleasant — a dispositional deposit.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Implied at the cognitive-dispositional level: (1) **Psa 71:17** ("from my youth you have taught me, and I still proclaim your wondrous deeds") — a lifetime of sustained Wonder has produced a person whose defining inner-expressive orientation is the proclamation of divine wonders; the sustained deposit is a proclamatory vocation; (2) **Psa 131:1**'s posture of not-overreaching implies a formed character of epistemic humility as the deposit of sustained appropriate Wonder; (3) **The generational-transmission pattern** (Psa 78:4 — "we will not hide them from their children") — sustained Wonder produces the disposition to pass on wonder-memory to the next generation; this is a formative cognitive deposit.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

The corpus does not explicitly evidence a constitutional deposit from sustained Suffering-Joy. The formation that Jas 1:3–4 names (steadfastness → completeness) is a soul-dispositional deposit rather than a body-level deposit. No generational consequence or body-deposit language appears.

---

##### T2.8.2 — What evidence supports or contradicts this?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

No supporting evidence for constitutional deposit. The absence does not contradict the possibility but the evidence does not affirm it.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Supporting: Pro 17:22 (joyful heart as good medicine — medicinal metaphor implies body-level impact); Psa 51:8 (restored joy sought for "bones that you have broken" — the body's restoration is bound up with joy's restoration). Qualifying: the evidence describes outcomes and metaphors rather than explicit constitutional-deposit language. The direction is clear (sustained joy → bodily wellbeing; sustained joylessness → bodily-inner decline) but the mechanism is not spelled out.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

No direct evidence for deposit. The pattern of moral formation through sustained evaluative-gladness (the wisdom literature's training of the evaluative faculty) implies a dispositional deposit — the person whose inner life is habitually engaged in accurate moral evaluation becomes a person of formed moral discernment — but the corpus does not name this as a body-level deposit.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Supporting: Isa 66:3's soul-level formation is the clearest evidence; Psa 1's "like a tree planted" is a formation-stability image showing that sustained delight-in-law produces a constitutional stability like a tree's root system. Psa 119's Delight-in-law as the thing that prevents perishing (v.92) — sustained delight has produced a character capable of surviving adversity. No evidence contradicts; the implicit direction is consistently: sustained Delight forms the inner person around its object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Supporting: Pro 16:24 (ongoing health as implied sustained effect); Deu 28:54, 56 (the delicate person's constitution shaped by sustained luxury); Pro 3:17 (wisdom's "ways of pleasantness" as a formed disposition). No direct evidence contradicts.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Supporting: Psa 71:17 (lifelong proclamatory formation); Psa 131:1 (formed epistemic humility); Psa 78:4 (generational transmission disposition). No direct contradicting evidence.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

No direct evidence for body-level deposit. The pattern of Jas 1:3–4 implies dispositional formation (proven character, steadfastness) but describes inner-being formation rather than bodily deposit.

---

##### T2.8.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional deposit from sustained exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not fully silent — medicinal and body-restoration evidence is present — but explicit constitutional-deposit language is absent. The finding is: sustained joy produces positive bodily consequences; its absence produces negative bodily consequences; the explicit deposit mechanism is not described.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional body-level deposit from sustained Gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Constitutional deposit at the soul and heart levels is implied by the evidence; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Constitutional deposit is implied across multiple registers; not fully silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Constitutional deposit at the cognitive-dispositional level is implied; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional body-level deposit from sustained Suffering-Joy.

---

#### T2.9 — Origin and Source

##### T2.9.1 — Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence shows two origin-patterns: (1) **Responsive origin** — exultation arises as a response to what God does: Jethro hears of God's acts and rejoices (Exo 18:9); the psalmist waits for God's salvation and will rejoice in it (Psa 9:14); God's acts of deliverance produce the soul's exultation (Psa 35:9; Isa 25:9). The origin is external (God's acts) received internally. (2) **Volitional origin** — Hab 3:18 ("yet I will rejoice") and the commanded exultations (Psa 32:11; Isa 65:18) show exultation arising from within the person through deliberate will, not waiting for external stimulus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple origins evidenced: (1) **From God** — "you have put more joy in my heart" (Psa 4:7); "the Lord had made them joyful" (Ezr 6:22); "God keeps him occupied with joy in his heart" (Ecc 5:20); "may the God of hope fill you with all joy" (Rom 15:13); Gal 5:22 (Spirit-fruit); — Joy as divinely produced in the inner being; (2) **From the encounter with God's acts** — the spontaneous joy at witnessing divine deliverance or presence (1Sa 6:13; Luk 24:41; Joh 20:20) — originates in the perception of divine reality; (3) **From the will's choice** — Phili 4:4 ("Rejoice always"); Jas 1:2 ("Count it all joy") — Joy initiated by deliberate volitional act of the will directed by God's command; (4) **From community** — M04-D (sunchairo) and Pauline joy over communities (1Th 3:9; Phili 4:1) — Joy produced by and in relational bonds; (5) **Prescribed practice** — feast-commandments (Deu 16:11–15) — Joy cultivated through divinely-ordained communal practices.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple origins: (1) **From God's character** — M04-L-VCG-01 (the ki-tov declarations, Gen 1's "God saw that it was good"): God's own goodness is the source from which the Gladness-quality radiates; (2) **From divine acts** — M04-O-VCG-03 and VCG-04: God's good hand (Ezr 7:9; 8:18; Neh 2:8, 18), covenantal promise-fulfilment (Jos 21:45; Jer 29:10; 33:14) — Gladness originates in the experienced reality of divine action; (3) **From speech** — M04-O-VCG-01: good news, apt words, gracious speech (Pro 12:25; 15:23, 30; Isa 52:7; Zec 1:13) — external speech received by the inner person; (4) **From the person's own evaluative act** — M04-L-VCG-02: the human person's moral discernment producing the recognition of what is good or not-good; Gladness here originates in the person's own correctly-functioning evaluative faculty.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple origins: (1) **From within the person's own inner being** — the native capacity of the soul to orient itself toward objects; Rom 7:22's "inner being" is the place of origin for the person's Delight in God's law — it arises from the deepest constitutive layer of the regenerate person; (2) **From God as object** — when Delight is directed toward God, God himself as the object can be said to originate the Delight (Psa 37:4's "delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart" implies that God as object restructures the origin of desire itself); (3) **From received word** — Jer 31:20 (Ephraim as God's darling child — divine Delight originates in God's relational cherishing); Psa 94:19 (God's consolations originating the soul's cheer/sha.a); (4) **From covenantal relationship** — M04-H-VCG-02's pattern shows divine Delight originating in God's covenantal affection (Deu 30:9; Isa 62:4); (5) **From corrupt formation** — M04-P shows Delight originating in the soul formed around wrong objects through habitual misdirection.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple origins: (1) **From genuine persons, speech, and creation** (M04-J) — the pleasantness of Jonathan (2Sa 1:26), the beloved (Song 1:16; 7:6), wisdom (Pro 2:10; 3:17), and gracious speech (Pro 16:24) originates from the object itself being genuinely pleasant; the inner being receives what is genuinely present in the external reality; (2) **From divine character** — Psa 27:4's no.am as God's own beauty-quality; Psa 36:8's river of delights; the pleasantness originates in God and is received by the worshiper; (3) **From correctly-offered worship** — ni.cho.ach Pleasure originates in the obedient act of sacrifice that evokes God's receptive inner response; (4) **From wisdom's formation** — Pro 2:10 (wisdom coming into the heart enabling Pleasure in knowledge) — wisdom-entry is the originating event enabling Pleasure's reception; (5) **From false sources** — Pro 9:17 (stolen bread as apparent pleasantness) — misdirected Pleasure originates in deceptive appearances.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple origins: (1) **From God's acts** — the dominant origin: Wonder arises in response to God's marvellous works (VCG-01 throughout — Exo 3:20; 15:11; 34:10; Psa corpus); (2) **From encountering the limit of comprehension** — VCG-02's pa.la in the "too hard/wonderful" register: Wonder at what exceeds human cognitive reach originates at the boundary of human understanding (Job 42:3; Jer 32:17, 27); (3) **From perceptive encounter with the extraordinary** — Mar 1:27; 10:24 (thambeō at Jesus' authoritative teaching/advance) — Wonder originates from direct encounter with a person or event that exceeds ordinary categories; (4) **From deliberate remembrance** — Psa 77:11; 105:5; 111:4 — Wonder re-generated through the deliberate inner act of calling to memory God's past wonders; this is the only instance where Wonder is self-originated (through voluntary memory-act).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two clear origin points: (1) **From the Holy Spirit** — Luk 10:21 ("rejoiced in the Holy Spirit"); 1Th 1:6 (adjacent — "joy of the Holy Spirit") — the Spirit is the direct producing agent of agalliao's intensity; (2) **From faith in the unseen Christ** — 1Pe 1:8 ("though you do not now see him, you believe in him and rejoice") — faith as the inner volitional-cognitive act that positions the person to receive Spirit-joy; (3) **From eschatological orientation** — the "joy set before him" (Heb 12:2) and "reward in heaven" (Mat 5:12) as the cognitive-eschatological grounds that produce and sustain the inner orientation; (4) **From deliberate volitional reframing** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") — the will's act of cognitive reframing as origin.

---

##### T2.9.2 — What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Multiple origins: both external-responsive (God's acts received by the soul) and internal-volitional (the will choosing to exult). The two origins are not contradictory — the volitional exultation of Hab 3:18 is grounded in theological knowledge of who God is, making the will's act a response to an already-known divine reality rather than an arbitrary emotion.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple. The evidence across the 15 VCGs of Characteristic 2 shows Joy originating through five distinct pathways (divine production, encounter, will, community, practice). No single origin is exclusive. The different sub-groups evidence different primary origins: M04-B-VCG-01 (feast-commandment joy) is practice-originated; M04-B-VCG-05 (God-directed psalmist joy) is encounter-originated; M04-C-VCG-04 (Spirit-fruit joy) is divinely-produced; M04-D (sunchairo) is community-originated.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple. The four origin pathways (divine character, divine acts, speech, evaluative faculty) each produce Gladness through a different route. This multiplicity is distinctive: Joy has a similar multiplicity but with the Spirit and commanded-will as prominent origins; Gladness's origins cluster around character-recognition, circumstance-response, and evaluative discernment.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple — more so than any other M04 characteristic, reflecting the characteristic's five-sub-group breadth. The origin varies by mode: inner-being constitution (affective Delight), divine sovereign will (God's cha.phets), covenantal relationship (God's pleasure in persons), received word (sha.a cheered by consolation), corrupt formation (M04-P's habituated misdirection).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple — the most varied origin-set in M04, consistent with Pleasure's role as the broadly receptive characteristic: it receives from persons, speech, creation, God's character, and worship-acts.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple — divine acts, cognitive-limit encounters, direct perceptive encounter, and deliberate memory all originate Wonder through different pathways.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Multiple — Spirit, faith, eschatological orientation, and volitional reframing each play a distinct originating role. The Spirit is primary; the others are enabling conditions or means through which the Spirit's origin reaches the person.

---

##### T2.9.3 — Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, with a clear pattern: in the Psalms, exultation predominantly arises responsively from divine acts of salvation and deliverance; in the prophetic corpus (Isa 65:18; Zec 9:9) it is commanded in anticipation of eschatological events; in the wisdom literature (Hab 3:18; Pro 2:14's negative) it is shown as a volitional act chosen in the face of circumstances. The origin moves from responsive through commanded to volitional as the literary context changes — reflecting a progression in the characteristic's expected maturity.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, with clear contextual patterns: Ritual/liturgical contexts (M04-B-VCG-01) → practice-originated; Narrative-rescue contexts (M04-B-VCG-03) → encounter-originated; Psalmist-prayer contexts (M04-B-VCG-05) → encounter and will combined; NT Spirit-and-suffering contexts (M04-C-VCG-04, 05) → Spirit-produced; Relational pastoral contexts (M04-C-VCG-03; M04-D) → community-produced; Wisdom contexts (Ecc, Pro) → divinely-provided or wisdom-cultivated. The multiplicity of origins is itself an important finding: Joy cannot be reduced to a single source but arises through the convergence of divine action, human will, community, and practice.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: doxological contexts (ki-tov Psalms) → originates from recognising divine character; narrative-rescue contexts (M04-O-VCG-03) → originates from experienced deliverance; wisdom contexts (M04-L-VCG-02, 03) → originates from the person's own evaluative act; prophetic contexts (M04-O-VCG-04 — covenantal promises) → originates from trust in divine word.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: law-delight contexts → origin in the inner being's native affective orientation toward its proper object (Rom 7:22); sovereign-will contexts → origin in the divine will (Psa 115:3); relational-pleasure contexts → origin in the relational bond (Jer 31:20; Psa 18:19); corrupt contexts → origin in the soul's habituated misdirection (Isa 66:3); obedience contexts → origin in the will's alignment with what God approves (Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)
