Yes: worship contexts → originates from correctly-offered sacrifice evoking divine response; relational contexts → originates from the genuine pleasantness of persons and bonds; creation contexts → originates from the pleasant qualities of created things and places; wisdom contexts → originates from wisdom entering the heart and enabling Pleasure in knowledge; material contexts → originates from physical ease and luxury.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: worship/historical-memory contexts → originates from deliberate remembrance of God's acts; prophetic-judgment contexts → originates from confronting what God will do that is beyond current comprehension (Isa 29:14 — wonder upon wonder); direct encounter contexts (Mark) → originates from immediate perceptive encounter with Jesus; epistemological-limit contexts → originates at the boundary of human comprehension (Job 42:3; Psa 131:1).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: direct divine encounter contexts (Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21) → Spirit origin; persecution contexts (Mat 5:12; 1Pe 4:13) → eschatological-orientation and volitional-command origin; coming-to-faith contexts (Act 16:34; Joh 8:56) → faith-reception origin; extreme-suffering contexts (M04-F — Job 9:27; Psa 39:13) → attempted-will origin without Spirit-enabling, producing the fragile ba.lag form.

---

#### T2.10 — Constitutional Movement

##### T2.10.1 — Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows a consistent movement from soul/heart → body/voice: Psa 16:9 (heart glad → whole being rejoices → flesh dwells secure); Psa 63:5 (soul satisfied → mouth praises with joyful lips); the re.na.nah pattern throughout (inner state → triumphing cry). Psa 51:8 (bones asked to rejoice) represents the movement from inner exultation reaching to the deepest somatic level.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. The movement is documented in multiple directions: (1) **Spirit → heart → body** — Spirit produces joy (Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6), which is then located in the heart (Psa 4:7; Pro 17:22; Ecc 5:20) and then expressed through the body (face, dance, voice); (2) **Heart → whole being → body** — Psa 16:9 explicitly sequences heart → whole being → flesh; (3) **God → inner being → community** — God produces joy in the heart (Psa 4:7; Ezr 6:22), which then radiates into the community (Neh 12:43 — "the joy of Jerusalem was heard far away"); (4) **Body → heart** (bidirectional) — feast practices produce inner joy (Deu 16:13–15); wine gladdens the heart (Psa 104:15).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. The movement is cognitive recognition → affective warmth → bodily refreshment: (1) The evaluative act (M04-L) is cognitive; (2) The warm inner response (M04-O) is affective; (3) The bones refreshed (Pro 15:30) is somatic. The sequence shows Gladness descending from cognitive recognition through affective warmth to physical refreshment.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in the affective register: inner being/soul → heart (Psa 40:8 — law within the heart as the fruit of soul-level delight orientation); heart → sustained meditation → wisdom (Psa 1:2 — delight in law → meditation day and night → the blessed man's formation); inner state → body (Isa 55:2; 66:11–12 — soul's delight in restoration expressed in bodily images of eating and nursing). In the volitional register: divine cha.phets (inner sovereign pleasure) → immediate action (Psa 115:3 — "he does all that he pleases"; Gen 34:19 — immediate action from delight).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Sensory → soul → body** — Pro 16:24 shows the full movement: gracious words received auditorily → "sweetness to the soul" (soul-level) → "health to the body" (body-level); (2) **Physical offering → inner divine response** — ni.cho.ach: the physical sacrifice rises → God smells (perceptive) → says in his heart (inner resolve); (3) **Divine beauty → inner response → worship** — Psa 27:4: God's beauty (divine) → gazing upon it (perceptive) → dwelling in his house (responsive action).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: Eyes (perceptive body) → mind/inner being (cognitive astonishment) → soul (keeps the testimonies — Psa 119:129) → heart (whole-hearted thanksgiving — Psa 9:1) → mouth (proclaimed Wonder — 1Ch 16:9). The movement is perception-inward-outward in sequence.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes. Spirit → heart → tongue (Act 2:26 — the clearest sequence: heart glad, tongue rejoiced, flesh in hope); Spirit → voice → body (Luk 10:21 — Jesus' spirit-rejoicing immediately becomes vocal prayer; the body of disciples gathered around him participating). Luk 1:47's "my spirit rejoices" also moves outward in the Magnificat's declaration.

---

##### T2.10.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The sequence is consistently: inner locus (soul, heart) → expressive outer (voice, body). There is no evidence of the reverse sequence (body initiating the inner state). The pattern suggests exultation is fully present as an inner-being state before it reaches the body — the body's joy is evidence of, not producer of, the inner state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The dominant sequence is: divine action / Spirit / God's word received → heart glad → whole being rejoices → body expresses → voice proclaims → community participates. This sequence is clearest in the Nehemiah dedication (Neh 12:27–43): appointed singers → gladness accompanies worship → great joy in Jerusalem heard far away. The sequence shows Joy as a radially-expanding characteristic — it begins at the innermost constitutional level (heart or spirit) and expands outward through the whole person into the community and into the world. The reverse sequence (body-to-heart) appears in the feast-commandments as the designed formation pathway: prescribed communal practice produces the inner state.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The sequence for M04-O-VCG-01 (good news) is: speech received → inner evaluation as good → warm inner brightening → bodily refreshment (Pro 15:30). For M04-L-VCG-01 (divine character recognition): perceive God's goodness → declare it in praise → inner stability/gladness established. For M04-O-VCG-03 (wellbeing): God's good hand acts → inner recognition → communal resolve (Neh 2:18). Gladness moves consistently from cognitive-perceptive → affective → outward.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The dominant movement pattern: soul-level orientation toward object → heart engagement → sustained meditation/meditation → wisdom formation → outward action/worship. This is a deep-to-surface movement from the inner being outward through successively more external layers. The volitional sovereign mode shows an immediate inner-to-outer translation (Psa 115:3; Gen 34:19) without the intervening formation stages — volitional Delight moves directly to action because the will is the agency-generating faculty.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The dominant movement pattern is: external pleasant object/act → sensory reception → soul-level Pleasure → body-level health/effect. Pleasure uniquely in M04 moves consistently downward from perception through soul to body — it is the characteristic that most thoroughly integrates sensory, soul, and bodily dimensions in a single movement sequence. Pro 16:24 is the clearest evidence of this three-level sequence.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The movement pattern is: perceptive encounter → cognitive arrest (Wonder arises) → inner-being response (soul keeps, heart thanks) → outward proclamation (mouth declares). This is the full Wonder-sequence, and it is the most consistently complete sequential pattern in M04: every genuine Wonder begins in perceptive encounter and ends in proclaimed declaration. The sequence's completeness reveals Wonder as a fully integrating characteristic — it unites the perceptive, cognitive, affective, and expressive dimensions of the person in a single responsive arc.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Spirit-level → heart-level → tongue/voice → communal participation. The pattern is the deepest-to-shallowest in constitutional terms, moving outward from the spirit to the body and into the community. This is also the fastest-moving of the M04 characteristics' constitutional movements — agalliao's "leaping" root meaning is reflected in the rapid outward movement from deep inner to immediate outer expression.

---

##### T2.10.3 — If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced; see T2.10.1–T2.10.2.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Constitutional movement is extensively evidenced in both directions.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced across the three-level sequence.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced; not silent.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Constitutional movement across three levels is evidenced; not silent.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Constitutional movement across perception → cognition → soul/heart → mouth is evidenced; not silent.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced; not silent.

---

## T3 — Faculty Engagement

---

### T3

#### T3.1 — Perception

##### T3.1.1 — Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. Exultation is consistently triggered by perception — hearing (Exo 18:9 — Jethro heard of God's acts), seeing (Dan 6:23 — the king sees Daniel unharmed; Isa 66:14 — "you shall see, and your heart shall rejoice"), and the inner perception of divine reality (Psa 13:5 — trust in steadfast love as the ground of the heart's rejoicing). The evidence shows exultation engaging primarily inner hearing and inner sight — the capacity to perceive God's acts and character as true and real.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, consistently. The evidence shows Joy arising from perception across all inner senses: (1) **Sight** — "When they saw the star, they rejoiced exceedingly" (Mat 2:10); "when she has found it" (Luk 15:9); "the disciples were glad when they saw the Lord" (Joh 20:20); Psa 97:8 ("Zion hears and is glad"); Isa 66:14 ("you shall see, and your heart shall rejoice"); (2) **Hearing** — Neh 8:12 (joy from understanding what was declared); Psa 34:2 ("let the humble hear and be glad"); "recognizing Peter's voice" (Act 12:14); (3) **Taste** — Ecc 9:7 ("eat your bread with joy") — taste-mediated festive joy; (4) **Spiritual discernment** — Act 11:23 (Barnabas "saw the grace of God, he was glad") — spiritual perception of divine grace producing joy. Perception is the most common immediate trigger for Joy in the corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. Gladness is consistently perception-triggered: Gen 1:4–31 — God "saw" (ra'ah) that it was good — the perceptive act produces the evaluative declaration; Gen 40:16 — the baker "saw that the interpretation was favorable" — visual/perceptive recognition initiating inner brightening; 2Sa 18:27 — David identifies the runner perceptually and judges him "a good man"; Psa 97:11 (M04-B adjacent, but the pattern) — "light is sown for the righteous"; M04-O-VCG-01: hearing good news (Pro 15:30; Isa 52:7) — the auditory perceptive faculty is the trigger.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in several registers: (1) **Hearing** — the primary perceptive trigger for law-delight: Psa 119:16 ("I will delight in your statutes") — statutes heard and received; Jer 6:10 ("the word of the Lord is to them an object of scorn; they take no pleasure in it") — the blocked ear blocking Delight; (2) **Taste/eating** — Isa 55:2 ("eat what is good, and delight yourselves in rich food" — a.nog) — the gustatory metaphor for Delight's perceptive dimension; (3) **Smell** — ni.cho.ach aroma — the olfactory sense as the medium through which correct worship is perceived as pleasing; (4) **Sight** — Rev 13:3; 17:8 (the whole earth marveling at the beast's apparent resurrection) — visual perception triggering the captivation of corrupt Delight; (5) **Inner perception** — Psa 51:6 ("you delight in truth in the inward being") — God's perceptive regard penetrating to the inner being's truthfulness.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes — more explicitly than any other M04 characteristic: (1) **Sight** — Psa 27:4 ("to gaze upon the beauty of the Lord"); (2) **Smell** — Gen 8:21 ("when the Lord smelled the pleasing aroma"); the entire ni.cho.ach corpus is olfactory-mediated; (3) **Taste** — Psa 34:8 ("taste and see that the Lord is good" — cross-assigned to M04-K); (4) **Hearing** — Pro 16:24 (gracious words received auditorily); (5) **Touch** — Deu 28:54, 56 (the delicate woman who would not set her foot on the ground — touch-sensitivity as the somatic marker of pampered Pleasure).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes — more explicitly than any other M04 characteristic in the visual-perceptive mode: (1) **"Marvellous in our eyes"** (Psa 118:23) — sight as the perceptive organ of Wonder; (2) **"Open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things"** (Psa 119:18) — petition for perceptive opening; (3) **"They saw the deeds of the Lord, his wondrous works in the deep"** (Psa 107:24) — Wonder grounded in direct visual perceptive encounter; (4) **"Stop and consider the wondrous works of God"** (Job 37:14) — the imperative to attend perceptively; (5) **"Manoah and his wife were watching"** (Judg 13:19) — wonder-producing encounter witnessed perceptively; (6) **Mar 1:27** (thambeō at teaching heard and seen); **Mar 10:32** (seeing Jesus walk ahead in determination).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, but distinctively. Suffering-Joy is characterised by perception of what is not (yet) visible: 1Pe 1:8 ("though you do not now see him, you believe in him") — the rejoicing arises despite the absence of visible evidence; Joh 8:56 (Abraham "saw" Christ's day through faith-vision, not physical sight) — inner spiritual perception of future reality. Luk 1:44 (adjacent — "the baby in my womb leaped for joy" at the sound of Mary's greeting) — the most physicality-affirming perception-instance: hearing as the trigger of the most bodily form of rejoicing. M04-F: Psa 39:13 ("that I may smile again before I depart") — the perceptive capacity is directed toward the self and its diminishing life; ba.lag is triggered by mortality-perception.

---

##### T3.1.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation deepens perception: Psa 40:16 and 70:4 show that those who "seek" God rejoice in him — the seeking (a perceptive-seeking act) enables exultation, which in turn sustains the seeking. The inverted passages show impairment: exultation directed at idols (Hos 10:5) is accompanied by spiritual blindness (the idol will depart; the joy will become mourning). Rightly-directed exultation appears to sharpen perception of God's reality; misdirected exultation blinds.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens perception in its rightly-directed form: Psa 107:42 ("the upright see it and are glad") — joy at God's acts reinforces the attentiveness to divine action that produced it; Psa 126:3 ("the Lord has done great things for us; we are glad") — the glad perception of divine acts sustains the orientation toward God. Joy impairs perception in its misdirected form: Mat 13:20 (joy without root fails when testing comes — the initial perceptive joy was accurate but too shallow); Act 12:14 (Rhoda's overwhelming joy at Peter's voice means she fails to perceive his actual presence at the gate — joy can momentarily overwhelm practical perception). The rocky-ground passages (Mat 13:20; Luk 8:13) show Joy without depth actually preventing sustained engagement with reality.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens perception in its healthy form: the person who habitually evaluates rightly (M04-L-VCG-02) develops the perceptive capacity to see what is genuinely good or not-good in moral and relational situations. Misdirected Gladness impairs perception: Num 14:3 (fear distorting the perceptive evaluation of the land); Isa 39:8 (Hezekiah's self-referential perception missing the full implication of Isaiah's word). Accurate Gladness both requires and trains accurate perception.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight both deepens and can distort perception: (1) **Deepens**: Psa 111:2 ("great are the works of the Lord, studied by all who delight in them") — Delight in God's works drives sustained perceptive engagement; the person who delights in God's law reads and re-reads with increasing attention (Psa 1:2); (2) **Distorts**: Rev 13:3 (the marveling at the beast) — corrupt Delight produces a captivated perception that cannot see the beast's true nature; Isa 58:2 (delight to seek God without moral reality) — surface perceptive-religious engagement masking the absence of genuine inner Delight; Jer 6:10 (the closed ear taking no pleasure) — blocked Delight correlates with impaired perception.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure deepens perception: the person who genuinely tastes God's goodness (Psa 34:8) perceives him more accurately; Psa 27:4's gaze upon God's beauty is perceptive engagement of the highest kind. Distorted Pleasure impairs perception: Pro 9:17 (stolen bread appearing pleasant — deceived perception evaluating the wrong object as pleasant); the ni.cho.ach withheld (Lev 26:31) implies the covenant-unfaithful person's worship-perception is distorted, offering what cannot reach God.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder deepens perception: Psa 119:18's "open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law" shows that divine opening of perception enables Wonder; Psa 119:27's "make me understand… and I will meditate on your wondrous works" shows that Wonder-capacity grows with understanding. Wonder also depends on perception — its failure (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful") is a failure to perceive or register what has been seen. Wonder-failure is perceptive failure.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy deepens spiritual perception: 1Pe 1:8 (belief in the unseen Christ producing inexpressible joy) shows that Spirit-enabled Suffering-Joy opens the person to perceive realities that ordinary sensory perception cannot access. It does not bypass natural-world perception (the suffering is genuinely perceived and felt) but adds a second perceptive layer — the Spirit-enabled perception of eschatological reality that recontextualises the natural-world suffering.

---

##### T3.1.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is a perceptually-grounded characteristic — it is not emotionally autonomous but arises from and depends upon the accurate perception of who God is and what he has done. Where perception is accurate (God's salvation seen and received), exultation follows. Where perception is distorted (idol-worship, Hos 10:5; spiritual prostitution, Hos 9:1), exultation misfires toward wrong objects.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is a perceptually-grounded characteristic whose depth depends on the depth of perception that grounds it. Surface-level perception → surface-level joy (rocky-ground hearer); accurate, deep perception of divine reality → sustained, transforming joy (Hab 3:18 type; Psa 97:8). The pattern reveals that the quality of a person's inner perception of who God is and what he has done is the single most important determinant of the quality and durability of their Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is perception-dependent in a way that distinguishes it from Joy (which can be commanded even when circumstances are adverse) — Gladness requires the accurate perception of genuine goodness before it can arise. The pattern reveals that forming the perceptive-evaluative faculty is essential to Gladness's health: moral formation that trains perception trains Gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight functions as a perceptive lens: it shapes what the person attends to, dwells in, and is drawn toward. Delight in God's word produces sustained perceptive engagement with Scripture; Delight in the wrong object (beast, idols, abominations) produces captivated perceptive fixation on the wrong thing. The pattern reveals that Delight and perception are mutually shaping: Delight directs the perceptive faculty toward its object, and continued perception reinforces and deepens the Delight. This makes the formation of right Delight a perceptive-shaping act.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is uniquely perception-dependent among M04 characteristics — it arises from sensory encounter with what is genuinely pleasant. The pattern reveals that training perception rightly is essential to genuine Pleasure: the person whose perceptive faculty is attuned to genuine goodness receives genuine Pleasure; the person whose perception is distorted (by folly, false objects, covenant-unfaithfulness) receives counterfeit Pleasure that cannot sustain or nourish.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the characteristic most directly dependent on and productive of genuine perception. It requires the person to genuinely see what is happening (Psa 107:24 — "they saw the deeds of the Lord") and it deepens the person's capacity to see (Psa 119:18 — open my eyes to behold). The pattern reveals perception-training as essential to Wonder-formation: communities that regularly tell of God's wondrous works (VCG-01 proclamatory tradition) are training the perceptive capacity of their members to see God's acts as extraordinary.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is the characteristic most directly associated with faith-perception — the inner-being capacity to perceive what is not yet visible. Its connection with the Spirit (who enables perception of divine realities) and its consistent grounding in eschatological realities (heaven's reward, Christ's glory) confirm it as the characteristic that most fully engages the perceptive faculty in its spiritual-discernment mode rather than its sensory mode.

---

#### T3.2 — Cognition

##### T3.2.1 — Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, as a precondition. Isa 25:9 shows the cognitive recognition ("behold, this is our God; we have waited for him") preceding and grounding the exultation ("let us be glad and rejoice in his salvation"). Exo 18:9 shows Jethro's exultation arising from hearing (cognitive reception) of God's acts. The commanded exultations (Psa 32:11; Isa 65:18) presuppose knowledge of who God is as the ground for the commanded inner state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, as a consistent enabling precondition. Neh 8:12 — joy arising "because they had understood the words declared to them" — the most direct evidence that cognitive comprehension produces Joy. Isa 25:9 — "we have waited for him… behold, this is our God" (recognitive cognition → exultant rejoicing). Act 13:48 — "when the Gentiles heard this, they began rejoicing" — hearing and cognitively receiving the word produces joy. 1Cor 13:6 — love "rejoices with the truth" — the cognitive-evaluative act of recognising truth is the object of Joy. Mat 25:21 ("enter into the joy of your master") — the cognitive understanding of what the master's joy is shapes the servant's aspiration.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes — this is the primary faculty for Gladness, as established at T1.8. The entire M04-L-VCG-02 corpus (45 verses of moral appraisal) is an exercise of the cognitive faculty: weighing conduct against standards of goodness (Exo 18:17; Neh 5:9; Pro 17:26; 18:5; Mic 6:8); comparing relational worth (Rut 4:15; 2Sa 18:3); assessing comparative value of wisdom over wealth (Pro 8:11; 16:16; 16:8). Job 34:4 ("let us know among ourselves what is good") explicitly names cognition as the faculty being exercised.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in the study-and-meditation register: (1) **Psa 1:2** — delight in the law → meditation day and night — Delight producing sustained cognitive engagement; (2) **Psa 111:2** — delight in God's works driving their study; (3) **Psa 119:24** — "your testimonies are my delight; they are my counselors" — Delight in testimonies producing the cognitive guidance that the testimonies provide; (4) **Ecc 12:10** — the Preacher seeking words of delight — cognitive-aesthetic search; (5) **1Ch 28:9** — "a willing mind" (cha.phets adj) — cognitive-volitional orientation; (6) **Pro 8:11** — nothing desired (che.phets) can compare with wisdom — the cognitive act of comparing wisdom against all other desired objects.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially, in the wisdom-comparative register: M04-K-VCG-03 (the better-than comparatives) require cognitive evaluation to assess which option is genuinely more pleasant — Psa 37:16 (little of the righteous better than abundance of wicked); Pro 15:16, 17; 16:32; 17:1 (various integrity-vs-abundance comparatives). This is a cognitive-evaluative engagement, albeit secondary to the primary affective-receptive dimension. Psa 34:8's "taste and see" also involves a cognitive element: the imperative to see (perceive and assess) alongside taste.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes — this is Wonder's primary faculty, as established at T1.8: (1) **"Things we cannot comprehend"** (Job 37:5) — comprehension as the cognitive faculty Wonder presses against; (2) **"Things too wonderful for me, which I did not know"** (Job 42:3) — knowledge as the measure of Wonder; (3) **"Make me understand… I will meditate on your wondrous works"** (Psa 119:27) — understanding enabling meditative engagement with Wonder; (4) **"The wisdom of their wise men shall perish"** (Isa 29:14) — human cognitive accumulation eclipsed by God's wonders; (5) **"Do you know the balancings of the clouds?"** (Job 37:16) — rhetorical challenge to human knowledge producing Wonder-recognition.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, through specific cognitive acts: Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") — counting/reckoning is an arithmetic-like cognitive act; Heb 12:2 ("for the joy that was set before him endured the cross, despising the shame") — Christ's cognitive holding of the eschatological joy as more real than the present shame is a sustained cognitive orientation; Mat 5:12 ("for your reward is great in heaven") gives the cognitive ground for commanded rejoicing — a propositional truth that orients the cognitive frame.

---

##### T3.2.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation does not bypass cognition in this corpus; it builds on it. The pattern is consistently: know God's act → exult in response. There is no instance of exultation preceding or bypassing the knowledge of its grounds. The characteristic deepens rather than impairs cognitive engagement with divine reality — the jubilant exultation of Psa 89:16 ("exult in your name all the day") suggests that sustained exultation sustains the attentiveness to God's character that produced it.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens cognition in its healthy form: Psa 97:8 (joy at God's judgments reinforces the understanding of divine justice); Neh 8:12 (joy following understanding sustains the engagement with God's word). Joy can momentarily disrupt cognitive function in intense encounters: Luk 24:41 ("while they still disbelieved for joy" — joy so overwhelming that it temporarily outpaces belief); Act 12:14 (Rhoda's joy overrides practical reasoning). These disruptions are not presented as failures but as expressions of Joy's intensity exceeding cognitive capacity momentarily.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens cognition: sustained correct evaluation of what is genuinely good trains and sharpens the cognitive-moral faculty (the wisdom literature's training purpose). Misdirected Gladness (Isa 41:7's craftsman; Num 14:3's fear-evaluation) bypasses or distorts cognition — the person reaches a "good" verdict without actually exercising careful moral reasoning. The Psa 119:68 pattern ("you are good and do good; teach me your statutes") explicitly requests continued cognitive formation in divine goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight enables and deepens cognition: Psa 1:2 (sustained meditation driven by Delight); Psa 111:2 (study driven by Delight); Psa 119:24 (testimonies as counselors — Delight in them producing cognitive guidance). In its distorted form Delight can bypass cognition: Pro 18:2 (the fool takes pleasure only in expressing his opinion — self-directed Delight short-circuiting the cognitive engagement with understanding); Rev 13:3 (marveling at the beast — perceptive captivation bypassing cognitive assessment of the beast's true nature).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure in wisdom deepens cognition: Pro 2:10's "knowledge will be pleasant to your soul" — when wisdom is in the heart, the soul's Pleasure in knowledge reinforces the desire to know more; pleasantness in knowledge sustains cognitive engagement. Distorted Pleasure (Pro 9:17 — stolen bread) bypasses honest cognition by making the wrong thing feel pleasant, thereby short-circuiting the evaluation that would recognise its true character.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder simultaneously deepens and disciplines cognition: it deepens by motivating sustained meditation and inquiry into God's acts (Psa 119:27; 145:5); it disciplines by restraining overreach (Psa 131:1 — I do not occupy myself with things too marvellous for me). Wonder-as-epistemological-humility is the most distinctive cognitive-Wonder interaction: the person in genuine Wonder is cognitively active (meditating, considering, studying) but not overconfident (acknowledging the limits of comprehension).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy enables cognition by clarifying value hierarchy: the person who genuinely rejoices amid suffering has cognitively apprehended that eschatological reality is more determinative than present circumstance. This reordering of cognitive priority — the eternal over the temporal — is itself a form of cognitive clarity that Suffering-Joy both requires and reinforces.

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is cognitively grounded but not cognitively produced — knowing provides the ground; the affective-volitional surge of exultation is the response. The characteristic bridges cognition and affect: the mind provides the true object; the soul rises in response.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Cognition and Joy are mutually reinforcing in the normal pattern: comprehension produces Joy; Joy sustains and reinforces the engagement with what is understood. The occasional instances of Joy temporarily exceeding cognitive function (Luk 24:41; Act 12:14) reveal Joy as a characteristic that in its most intense forms temporarily subordinates cognition to affect — the inner being is so flooded with gladness that ordinary reasoning is suspended. This is exceptional rather than normative.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is the most cognitively-constituted characteristic in M04. Its health is directly dependent on the quality of cognition: accurate cognitive evaluation of moral reality produces genuine Gladness; distorted cognition produces distorted Gladness. This makes Gladness uniquely susceptible to formation through instruction — the wisdom literature's training of the evaluative faculty is the primary formative vehicle.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is uniquely positioned as a cognitive-driver: unlike the other M04 characteristics, Delight consistently produces sustained cognitive engagement with its object (study, meditation, inquiry). The pattern reveals that the person's deepest Delight determines what they most consistently think about and explore. Properly directed Delight in God and his word is therefore the most powerful driver of theological and spiritual cognition — it produces a mind that returns repeatedly to its object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure and cognition are indirectly related: Pleasure in wisdom sustains cognitive engagement; Pleasure-seeking without wisdom distorts and bypasses accurate cognition. The relationship is not direct (Pleasure is not a cognitive characteristic) but instrumental: right Pleasure reinforces right knowing; wrong Pleasure corrupts knowing.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the most cognitively-rich M04 characteristic in the perceptive-contemplative mode. Unlike Delight (which is cognitively engaged in wisdom evaluation) or Gladness (which is cognitively evaluative of moral goodness), Wonder's cognitive engagement is specifically at the boundary of comprehension — it is the response when cognition reaches its limit. The pattern reveals Wonder as the characteristic most directly involving the mind in a posture of humble but active engagement with what exceeds it.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy's cognitive engagement is specifically eschatological — its cognitive dimension is the holding of future-reality as present-real. This distinguishes it from Gladness (whose cognitive primary is moral evaluation) and from Joy (whose cognitive ground is comprehension of God's acts). Suffering-Joy's distinctive cognitive mode is eschatological reframing: the present suffering is real but is contextualised by a greater real — the glory to come.

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The dominant pattern of exultation in the Psalms is directed at God's past acts of salvation: Psa 9:14 (exultation anticipated in the future but grounded in God's known character); Psa 31:7 (rejoicing in steadfast love because "you have seen my affliction"); Psa 35:9 (soul's exultation at "his salvation" — the whole history of God's saving acts). The eschatological exultation passages (Isa 65:18–19; Zep 3:17) also engage a remembered pattern — God's past covenant faithfulness is the warrant for future exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Psa 66:6 — "they passed through the river on foot. There did we rejoice in him" — the memory of the Exodus crossing is the ground for present communal rejoicing; the joy is retrospective and memory-anchored. Psa 106:5 — "that I may rejoice in the gladness of your nation" — the psalmist desires to enter into the joy of the nation's memory of God's acts. Psa 137:6 — "if I do not set Jerusalem above my highest joy" — the memory of Jerusalem as the place of joy is the psalmist's highest value. Psa 51:12 — "restore to me the joy of your salvation" — David's memory of pre-sin joy is the reference point for what he asks restored. The M04-E-VCG-01 restoration joy (sa.s.von) is essentially the promised restoration of what was and is remembered: Jer 33:11 (the voice of gladness returning after judgment silenced it) — memory of pre-judgment joy is the criterion of restoration.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. M04-O-VCG-02 (better-than comparatives) frequently engages retrospective memory: Hos 2:7 ("it was better for me then than now") — comparison of present adversity to remembered better past; Jon 4:3, 8 (Jonah's despairing comparison) — past memory of expectations shaping present evaluation. M04-O-VCG-04 (covenantal promise-goodness) engages a different memory: Jos 21:45 ("not one word of all the good promises had failed") — the cumulative memory of God's faithfulness is the ground for present confidence. M04-L-VCG-01's doxological praise formula ("for he is good, for his steadfast love endures forever") is itself a memory-rehearsal — the Psalms' repeated ki-tov declarations sustain communal memory of divine goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **The Psa 119 sha.a pairings** — Psa 119:16 ("I will delight in your statutes; I will not forget your word") — Delight and memory are explicitly paired; the opposite of Delight in God's word is forgetting it; (2) **Jer 31:20** ("as often as I speak against him, I do remember him still") — God's sha.a.shu.im in Ephraim as a darling child sustains memory even through rebuke; divine Delight functions as a memory-anchor for the beloved; (3) **Hos 2:7** (adjacent — the people remembering that "it was better for me then than now" — the memory of former delight driving return); (4) **Psa 37:4** — "he will give you the desires of your heart" — the heart's desires shaped by Delight in God require memory of what God has given as a sustaining reference.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially: (1) **2Sa 1:26** — David's lament for Jonathan recalls the pleasantness of their relationship; memory of pleasantness is what makes grief acute; (2) **Jer 51:34** — Jerusalem's delicacies devoured by Nebuchadnezzar — the memory of former pleasantness intensifies the sense of loss; (3) **Psa 77:11** (in M04-I, not directly Pleasure but adjacent) — the act of remembering pleasant past experiences of God sustains present endurance.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes — memory is Wonder's second most prominent faculty: (1) **"Remember the wondrous works"** (1Ch 16:12; Psa 105:5; 111:4) — deliberate memory-engagement as a core Wonder-practice; (2) **"The wonders of old"** (Psa 77:11) — retrospective memory of past wonders as the inner strategy for sustaining faith through present distress; (3) **"Did not consider your wondrous works"** (Neh 9:17; Psa 106:7) — memory-failure as Wonder-failure; (4) **"He has caused his wondrous works to be remembered"** (Psa 111:4) — God himself ensuring his wonders remain in memory; (5) **"Do not hide them from their children"** (Psa 78:4) — generational memory-transmission as the Wonder-preserving act.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Partially. Joh 8:56 (Abraham's anticipatory joy at Christ's day) involves a prophetic forward-memory — the faith-memory of a promised future. Act 2:26 (Peter quoting Psalm 16 — "my heart was glad, and my tongue rejoiced") is a memory-act — the NT church's appropriation of David's hope as the basis for present confidence. The memory of Christ's suffering and resurrection (1Pe 4:13 — "share Christ's sufferings") grounds present Suffering-Joy in the remembered pattern of Christ's own suffering-to-glory.

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation deepens memory by celebrating what is remembered: the triumphing cry (re.na.nah, Psa 100:2) is a communal re-telling of God's acts. Conversely, the inverted exultation of Hos 10:5 shows that misdirected exultation can displace true memory — the priests' joy in the idol displaced the memory of YHWH's acts.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens memory by celebrating what is remembered: the liturgical feast-joy (M04-B-VCG-01) is constitutively memorial — Deu 16:11 (rejoicing before the Lord "in all that you undertake, in which the Lord your God has blessed you") makes the memory of blessing the ground for present rejoicing. The feast is the regular practice of joy-anchored-in-memory. Conversely, Joy's absence in judgment strips away the memory-sustaining practices: Jer 7:34; 16:9 (silencing of the "voice of mirth and gladness, the voice of the bridegroom and the bride") removes the communal memory-keeping mechanisms that joy sustains.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens memory in its healthy form: the ki-tov liturgical tradition (M04-L-VCG-01) anchors communal memory of God's goodness through repeated declaration; Jos 21:45 consolidates memory of fulfilled promises as the ground of trust. Distorted Gladness distorts memory: Jer 44:17 (the people's false attribution of former wellbeing to idol-worship) shows memory corrupted to serve a wrong conclusion. Accurate Gladness both requires and reinforces accurate memory.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight deepens memory in its healthy form: Psa 119:16's explicit pairing of delight and not-forgetting shows the two as mutually reinforcing — delight sustains memory, and memory returns the person to delight. God's sha.a.shu.im in Ephraim sustains God's own memory of the relationship through rebuke (Jer 31:20). Misdirected Delight can impair memory of genuine goodness: the people who find no pleasure in God's word (Jer 6:10) have effectively suppressed the memory of its truth.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine pleasantness deepens memory: the most pleasant experiences (Jonathan's companionship — 2Sa 1:26; Jerusalem's former delicacies — Jer 51:34) are retained most vividly in memory precisely because they were so pleasant. The ni.cho.ach worship-Pleasure is designed to be repeated (daily, weekly, festal) as a memorial practice — the regularity of worship-Pleasure sustains and reinforces memory of the covenant relationship.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder deeply engages and strengthens memory: the entire VCG-01 proclamatory tradition is a memory-practice — the community that tells of God's wondrous works is simultaneously training and rehearsing its collective memory. God's own act of causing his wonders to be remembered (Psa 111:4) shows Wonder as designed to be memory-embedded. Wonder-failure is consistently named as a memory-failure (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful"; Psa 78:11 — "forgot his works").

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy deepens memory in its redemptive-historical form: the person who rejoices in their sharing of Christ's sufferings (1Pe 4:13) is actively engaging the memory of Christ's own passion as the ground and pattern for their present experience. This is not ordinary biographical memory but the theological memory of salvation-history that grounds present suffering-exultation.

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation functions as a memory-anchoring practice: by exulting in what God has done, the person or community re-engages and reinforces the memory of divine acts. This is most visible in the liturgical context — Psa 100:2's "come into his presence with singing" is a communal memory-and-exultation act.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is a memory-anchoring and memory-sustaining characteristic: the feast practices (M04-B-VCG-01) that produce Joy are simultaneously practices of communal remembrance; to rejoice in what God has done is to remember it; to remember it rightly is to rejoice. Joy sustains the community's engagement with its own narrative of God's acts. The removal of joy under judgment is simultaneously the removal of the community's joy-memory practices — a catastrophic loss of inner-being coherence.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness and accurate memory are mutually reinforcing: the person and community that correctly remember God's goodness (the ki-tov tradition) are the ones who inhabit genuine Gladness. The worship-memory practice of the Psalms (ki-tov as the liturgical anchor) functions as both memory formation and Gladness formation simultaneously.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Psa 119:16's "delight/not forget" pairing is the most analytically significant: it reveals Delight as the memory-anchor for what the person treasures. The soul forgets what it does not delight in; the soul returns to what it does delight in. This makes Delight formation critical for memory formation: training the person's delight toward God's word simultaneously trains their memory to hold what matters most.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure marks what is memorable: what is genuinely pleasant is genuinely held in memory; loss of the pleasant intensifies the memory of it. The repeated ni.cho.ach pattern in Leviticus/Numbers (daily sacrifices as memorial worship-Pleasure) deliberately embeds the covenant-Pleasure relationship in communal memory through bodily practice.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder and memory are inseparably linked in the VCG-01 corpus: Wonder without memory cannot sustain; memory without Wonder becomes mere historical knowledge. The Tell-Remember-Meditate triad (1Ch 16:9, 12; Psa 9:1; 77:11; 105:2, 5; 119:27) shows Wonder as a memory-embedded characteristic whose formation and sustaining requires deliberate memorial practice. This is why the VCG-01 liturgical-proclamatory corpus is so extensive (61 verses) — the entire Psalmic wonder-tradition is a memory-forming practice.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Memory in Suffering-Joy operates primarily as **theological-historical memory** — the memory of Christ's suffering and resurrection that provides the template and ground for present Suffering-Joy. This distinguishes it from Gladness's evaluative-memory (which grounds present assessment in accurate recall of God's character and acts) — Suffering-Joy's memory is specifically christological and eschatological.

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes — exultation is the affective faculty in its most elevated and directed expression. The soul exults (Psa 35:9; Isa 61:10), the heart is glad (Psa 16:9; 13:5), the whole being rejoices (Psa 16:9), the bones are asked to rejoice (Psa 51:8), and the person is "jubilant with joy" (Psa 68:3). The affective faculty is the primary vehicle of exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is the affective faculty in its most fully-engaged participatory expression. The heart's gladness (consistently across both OT and NT), the whole being's rejoicing (Psa 16:9), the Spirit's joy overflowing into the community (Act 13:52; 1Th 1:6), Mary's spirit-rejoicing (Luk 1:47), the inexpressible joy filled with glory (1Pe 1:8) — all are primary affective events. Joy is not primarily cognitive or volitional (though it engages both) but fundamentally affective: a positive, engaged inner feeling directed at its object.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, in the M04-O register. The "good news refreshing the bones" (Pro 15:30), Saul "refreshed and well" (1Sa 16:23), the men of Jabesh "glad when they heard" (1Sa 11:9), the makarismos blessedness (Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15 — a felt inner state of divine-favour happiness), and Lam 3:26's "wait quietly" (a gentle, sustained affective posture) are all affective in character. The M04-L-VCG-01 ki-tov declarations also have an affective dimension — gratitude is a felt inner state.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes — Delight's M04-G register (sha.a.shu.im, sha.a, a.nog) is primarily affective: (1) **sha.a.shu.im** (Psa 119 series) — the multiple-intensity noun for pleasurable cherishing; (2) **sha.a** (Psa 94:19 — "your consolations cheer my soul"; Isa 66:12 — bounced on knees) — affective carefree-pleasure quality; (3) **a.nog** (Psa 37:4 — "delight yourself in the Lord"; Isa 58:14 — "take delight in the Lord"; Isa 66:11 — drink deeply with delight) — luxuriating, resting, pleasurable affect; (4) **sunēdomai** (Rom 7:22 — "I delight in the law of God") — synergistic joy in, the most explicitly affective NT term for Delight in the inner being; (5) **che.med** (Eze 23:12 — lustful desirability) — affective captivation in the corrupt register.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes — this is the primary faculty of Pleasure: (1) **M04-J-VCG-02's relational pleasantness** — 2Sa 1:26 (the affective warmth of Jonathan's companionship); Song 1:16; 7:6 (the lover's affective appreciation of the beloved's beauty); Psa 133:1 (the affective exclamation of communal pleasantness); (2) **Pro 2:10** (knowledge pleasant to the soul — a felt affective quality); (3) **Pro 16:24** (gracious words as sweetness — affective nourishment); (4) **Gen 8:21** (God's inner calmed, settled affective response to the soothing aroma); (5) **Psa 16:11** (pleasures forevermore — the affective quality of God's presence).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, in the arrest-astonishment register: (1) **thambeō** (Mar 1:27; 10:24; 10:32) — the most affectively intense Wonder term: the disciples are seized with astonishment (an inner feeling state of overwhelming surprise); (2) **"I marvelled greatly"** (Rev 17:6) — John's intense inner feeling-response to the vision; (3) **VCG-03's dark astonishment** — Job 10:16 (wonders worked against Job); Gal 1:6 ("I am astonished") — Paul's troubled inner affective state; (4) **"Fearfully and wonderfully made"** (Psa 139:14) — the awe-component of Wonder at one's own creation is affective.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes — Suffering-Joy is primarily affective in its intense form: 1Pe 1:8 ("inexpressible and filled with glory") — the affective quality is named first and most prominently; Act 16:34 (the jailer "rejoiced along with his entire household") — an intense affective event in a crisis context; Luk 1:47 (Mary's spirit exults — an intense affective inner event in a vulnerable context); Luk 10:21 (Jesus' rejoicing in the Holy Spirit — an affective event in the Spirit). M04-F (ba.lag) is also primarily affective — the desired brightening of the inner person's felt condition.

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation deepens and elevates affect by giving it its rightful object and direction. The evidence shows exultation directing the affective faculty toward God in a way that produces wholeness (Psa 16:9's "flesh also dwells secure") and depth (Psa 63:5's "soul satisfied as with fat and rich food"). It does not bypass or impair affect but brings it to its highest function.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens the affective faculty by elevating it and giving it its rightful object: Psa 43:4 ("God my exceeding joy") — the affective capacity of the inner person reaching its highest object; Psa 16:11 ("fullness of joy in your presence") — the maximum affective capacity reached in God's nearness. Pro 17:22 ("joyful heart is good medicine") — Joy in its sustained form heals and strengthens the affective faculty rather than depleting it. The rocky-ground joy (Mat 13:20) shows affect without formation: real but unsustained, depleted by testing rather than deepened through it.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens affect by grounding it in accurate evaluation: the person who genuinely evaluates God as good and receives that as an inner conviction experiences a more stable and deep gladness than one whose affect is merely circumstantially triggered. The "good news refreshing the bones" is a positive affective event; but it is grounded in the cognitive recognition that the news is genuinely good. Gladness does not bypass affect but channels it through cognitive evaluation, making the affective response more reliable and stable.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight deepens affect by giving it a specific worthy object: Psa 37:4 (resting in the Lord produces a quality of affective satisfaction that restructures the heart's desires); Psa 119:92 (Delight in God's law produces affective resilience sustaining the inner person through affliction). Misdirected Delight distorts affect: Eze 23:12 (che.med as lustful captivation — the affective faculty seized by the wrong object); Rev 13:3 (collective marvel as mass affective captivation). Delight shapes the affective faculty's object and therefore the quality and direction of the affective life.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure deepens and sustains positive affect: Pro 15:15's "cheerful of heart has a continual feast" shows positive inner-affect producing a sustained Pleasure-quality to all of daily experience; Pro 16:24's gracious words produce sweetness in the soul — affective nourishment. Distorted Pleasure corrupts affect: Pro 7:18's carnal a.las distorts affect by attaching it to a wrong object; Deu 28:54, 56 shows affect collapsed under judgment.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder deepens positive affect toward God: VCG-01's wonder-at-God's-acts consistently produces thanksgiving, praise, and the joyful affect of wholehearted worship (Psa 9:1 — "whole heart"; 31:21 — "blessed be the Lord"). Dark Wonder (VCG-03) produces negative affect: Job 10:16's wonders-against-Job produce distress; Dan 11:36's astonishing blasphemy produces appalled dread; Gal 1:6's astonishment is troubled dismay. Wonder can deepen either positive or negative affect depending on its object.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy deepens affect by revealing that the inner being's affective capacity is not limited by circumstances — the Spirit can produce genuine joy even when the natural affective response would be grief or fear. 1Pe 1:6 explicitly holds both: "grieved by various trials" (natural affect) alongside "in this you rejoice" (Spirit-produced affect). The characteristic does not bypass natural grief but adds a Spirit-produced layer of affect that coexists with it.

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation represents the affective faculty operating at its designed peak — the soul's and heart's deepest positive inner state directed at its proper object. The evidence suggests the affective faculty was made for this: the soul "satisfied as with fat and rich food" and God named as "my exceeding joy" (Psa 43:4) point to exultation as the affective capacity's fulfilment.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is the affective faculty at its designed peak when rightly directed: the person who rejoices in God has their affect working at its created purpose. The affective faculty was designed to be glad in God; when it is, it is at its fullest and most healthy. The pattern also shows that affect requires depth (root) to sustain Joy: the rocky-ground passages show affect without depth failing; the paradoxical joy under suffering (2Cor 6:10; 1Pe 1:6) shows affect with Spirit-grounding sustaining Joy where shallow affect cannot.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is more cognitively-grounded than the other M04 characteristics' affective expressions: Joy's gladness is more spontaneously affective; Gladness (Characteristic 3) is the version of positive inner-being warmth that is most closely integrated with cognitive evaluation. The pattern reveals Gladness as the characteristic where the intellect most directly shapes and grounds the affective response.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the most affectively-constituted characteristic in M04 alongside Joy — but Delight's distinctive affective quality is resting satisfaction (a.nog) and treasuring-warmth (sha.a.shu.im) rather than Joy's active exultation. The pattern reveals Delight as the characteristic that settles the affective faculty into a specific treasured object, producing stability rather than surge.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is the most affective-receptive of the M04 characteristics: its primary constitutive feature is the felt quality of agreeableness received inwardly. Joy surges upward; Suffering-Joy paradoxically transcends; Delight rests in a specific object; Pleasure is the ambient felt-pleasantness of what is genuinely agreeable — the most immediate, least mediated affective experience of genuine goodness in M04.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder's affective dimension is secondary to its cognitive dimension but is real: the arrested quality of Wonder is felt as well as known. The pattern reveals that Wonder is the characteristic where cognitive encounter and affective arrest are most closely integrated — the mind cannot comprehend, and the affect registers the incomprehension as astonishment. The two dimensions (cognitive limit + affective arrest) are constitutive of genuine Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy reveals that the affective faculty has a Spirit-accessible depth below its naturally-triggered surface. The suffering genuinely affects the natural affective registers (grief, fear, heartsickness — M04-F); but the Spirit can produce genuine exultation at a level below or beyond those surface registers. This dual-layer quality of affect — natural grief and Spirit-joy coexisting — is the characteristic's most distinctive affective feature.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, partially. The triumphing cry (re.na.nah) and the association with singing (Psa 100:2; Isa 49:13; Zep 3:17 — God exulting with singing) suggest that exultation naturally generates creative expression — song, poetry, and vocal art. The Psalms themselves are creative acts that arise from and give shape to exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. The consistent association of Joy with music, poetry, and song is the primary creative evidence: 1Ch 15:16 (David appointing Levites to raise "sounds of joy" with instruments — organised creative music in service of Joy); Psa 30:11 (mourning turned to dancing — the creative-bodily form of joy); Jer 31:13 ("young women rejoice in the dance; young men and old shall be merry") — dance as Joy's creative-bodily expression; Neh 12:27 (gladness expressed through singing, cymbals, harps, lyres at the dedication); Isa 55:12 ("you shall go out in joy… the mountains and the hills before you shall break forth into singing, and all the trees of the field shall clap their hands") — creation's Joy expressed in personified creative response. The Psalms themselves are creative products of joy-oriented engagement with God.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Partially. The M04-L-VCG-01 ki-tov declarations produce and are embedded in the Psalms — creative works generated from the inner recognition of divine goodness. Isa 52:7 (the good-news herald) is a creative-prophetic image (the beauty of the messenger's feet). The doxological praise tradition that grows from the ki-tov recognition involves creative expression (song, poetry, communal liturgy). However, creativity is not the dominant faculty of Gladness in this corpus — it is secondary to the cognitive and affective.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Pro 8:30–31** — Wisdom as God's daily delight, "rejoicing before him always, rejoicing in his inhabited world and delighting in the children of man" — Wisdom's creative delight in the world and in humanity; this is the most creatively-charged delight in the corpus; the creation itself is the object of Wisdom's sha.a.shu.im; (2) **Ecc 12:10** — "the Preacher sought to find words of delight" — creative-literary work driven by the desire to find language that carries genuine pleasure; (3) **Psa 119's Delight in God's law as poetic corpus** — the entire Psa 119 sha.a.shu.im series is itself a creative work generated from Delight in the law; Delight in God's word produces the creativity of the psalmist's literary meditation.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 45:1** — "my heart overflows with a pleasing theme; I address my verses to the king; my tongue is like the pen of a ready scribe" — the pleasantness of the creative-poetic impulse arising from the heart; Pleasure in the subject-matter (the king's beauty and virtue) generates creative expression; (2) **Pro 16:24's gracious words** — the crafting of genuinely pleasant speech is a creative act; the one who produces words that are "like a honeycomb" engages the creative faculty in service of Pleasure; (3) **Pro 3:17** (wisdom's ways as pleasantness) — wisdom's creative work produces a life-path characterised by pleasantness.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **The Psalmic proclamatory tradition** — the entire VCG-01 wonder-proclamation corpus represents creative acts: songs, psalms, and hymns generated from Wonder at God's acts (Exo 15:11's Song of the Sea is a primary creative-Wonder text; Psa 98:1 — "sing a new song" because "he has done marvellous things"); (2) **Psa 40:5** ("yet they are more than can be told") — Wonder's exceeding quality motivating the attempt at ever-new creative expression; (3) **2Ch 2:9** (the temple as "great and wonderful") — the creative work of the temple as wonder-architecture; (4) **Isa 9:6** ("Wonderful Counselor") — the prophetic creative act of naming the coming child's wonder-quality.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, in specific forms. Luk 1:47's Mary's exultation immediately moves into the Magnificat — a creative poetic-prophetic work generated from the agalliao state. Act 2:26 (Peter's appropriation of Psalm 16 in a Spirit-exultation context) shows the creative-interpretive act of applying past creative work (David's Psalm) to a new Spirit-context. M04-F's ba.lag-seeking also has a creative dimension: Job 9:27's deliberate attempt at cheerfulness ("I will put off my sad face, and be of good cheer") is a self-directed creative act of inner-state engineering.

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation enables and generates creative expression — it is the affective-volitional pressure that produces song and poetry. The Psalms in this corpus are themselves evidence of this: exultation pressed into creative literary form (Psa 21:1; 32:11; 89:16; 149:2).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy enables and generates creative expression: 1Ch 15:16 shows David's Joy producing organised creative music-making as its institutional form; the Psalms of this corpus are creative literary works produced from the inner experience of Joy-in-God. Joy does not bypass creativity but pressures it toward expression — the inner gladness seeks a form adequate to itself.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness enables creativity in its doxological expression: recognising divine goodness naturally produces the impulse toward praise-expression (the ki-tov formula moving into singing). Gladness does not bypass creativity but gives it its content and occasion.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight enables creativity specifically by directing it toward its proper object: Wisdom's sha.a.shu.im in creation (Pro 8:30–31) produces the creative work of the inhabited world as an object of Delight; the Preacher's search for words of delight (Ecc 12:10) produces the literary creativity of Ecclesiastes. Delight in God's word produces the psalm's creative-poetic meditation. Misdirected Delight (M04-P) does not produce creative works evidenced in the corpus — it produces destructive captivation instead.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure in a worthy subject (Psa 45:1 — the king's beauty) enables creative expression: the heart overflows, the tongue becomes agile. Pleasure functions as the creative motivating force when the object is genuinely pleasant — the pleasantness of what is experienced generates the impulse to express it in beautiful form.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder enables and generates creativity: the inexhaustibility of God's wonders (Psa 40:5 — "more than can be told") motivates continued creative expression in new attempts to capture what cannot be fully told. The "new song" (Psa 98:1; 96:1) — the creative response to each new wonder — shows Wonder as the generative source of fresh creative expression. Wonder cannot be adequately expressed in existing forms, so it generates new ones.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy generates a specific form of creativity: the Spirit-produced exultation in adversity naturally seeks expression through prophetic poetry (the Magnificat; the tradition of lament-moving-into-praise in the Psalms). The creative act is both the expression of the inner state and the means of its consolidation.

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is a generative characteristic — it produces creative expression as a natural overflow. The triumphing cry becomes the song; the inner surge becomes the poem.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is a generative characteristic: its inner pressure naturally seeks and produces creative forms — song, poetry, dance, communal festivity. The feast-commandments (Deu 16:11–15) are in part the institutional recognition that Joy requires a creative-communal form to sustain and express itself. The pattern suggests Joy and creativity are mutually reinforcing: Joy presses toward creative expression; creative expression sustains and deepens Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness generates a particular form of creativity — the doxological and declarative. The creative expression that Gladness produces is primarily the expression of recognised goodness: testimony, praise declaration, and the written wisdom that codifies evaluative learning (Proverbs, Ecclesiastes as creative-literary crystallisations of the evaluative-gladness faculty).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is a creative-generative characteristic: Pro 8:30–31's Wisdom delighting in the children of man frames Delight as constitutive of the creative act — God and Wisdom delight in creating and in what they have created. Human creativity that arises from Delight in God's word and wisdom participates in this creative-delight pattern. The pattern reveals Delight as the inner source from which authentic creativity flows.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is creativity-generating in its relational and beauty-appreciating register: when the inner person is genuinely pleased by what it perceives, creative expression follows naturally. Psa 45:1 is the clearest evidence — a heart overflowing with pleasing matter cannot but speak it. The pattern reveals Pleasure as one of the generative roots of creative expression in Scripture.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is creatively generative specifically because its object (God's incomprehensible acts) can never be fully expressed — the inexhaustibility of the wonder-object perpetually motivates new creative attempts. The Psalmic tradition's breadth and variety (61 verses across many different psalms all proclaiming God's wondrous works) is itself the evidence of this creative generativity: each poet's encounter with divine wonders produces a new creative expression.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy generates prophetic-creative expression as a natural overflow — the exultation that transcends circumstances presses toward poetry and praise. This is consistent with the agalliao root's leaping-outward quality: what arises in the deepest inner being seeks the most expressive outer form.

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, significantly. The commanded exultations (Psa 2:11; 32:11; Isa 65:18; 66:10; Zec 9:9) presuppose that the will can direct the inner state. Hab 3:18 ("yet I will rejoice") is the clearest evidence of volitional exultation — a deliberate choice to exult in God regardless of circumstances. Psa 118:24 ("let us rejoice and be glad in it") is a communal volitional act.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, substantially. The commanded nature of Joy across both OT and NT is the primary evidence: Deu 16:11 ("you shall rejoice"); Lev 23:40 ("you shall rejoice before the Lord"); Phili 4:4 ("rejoice in the Lord always"); 1Th 5:16 ("rejoice always"); Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy… when you meet trials"). These are volitional commands — they presuppose that the will can initiate, sustain, and direct the inner state of rejoicing. Luk 10:20 (Jesus redirecting rejoicing from wrong object to right object) and Jas 1:2 (counting trials as joy by a cognitive-volitional act) are the clearest examples of will directly shaping Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, in several registers: (1) **Jeremiah's submission** (Jer 26:14 — M04-H-VCG-03 overlap, one verse in M04-L-VCG's cross-assign) — volitional deference to what seems good to the other; (2) **Lam 3:26** — "it is good to wait quietly" — the waiting is a volitional choice; (3) **The makarismos passages** (M04-O-VCG-04) — blessedness is received through faith, which is itself a volitional act; (4) **The wisdom-comparative evaluations** (M04-L-VCG-03) — choosing wisdom over gold (Pro 16:16) is a volitional act informed by the evaluative faculty.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes — this is the dominant mode of M04-H's 184-verse corpus. The cha.phets/che.phets volitional register spans: (1) **Divine sovereign will** — Psa 115:3; 135:6; Isa 44:28; 46:10; 53:10; 55:11 — God's cha.phets as the operative principle of all divine action; (2) **Human directed desire and choice** — Gen 34:19 (Shechem's delight → immediate action); Psa 40:8 ("I delight to do your will") — the will oriented toward God's will by Delight; (3) **The diplomatic-preference idiom** (M04-H-VCG-03's 105 verses) — "as it seems good to you" throughout the historical books — volitional deference framed through the Delight vocabulary; (4) **Love's own timing** — Song 2:7; 3:5; 8:4 ("not stir up or awaken love until it pleases") — Delight attributed to Love itself as its inner volitional readiness.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially and indirectly: (1) **The worship-Pleasure mode** (ni.cho.ach) requires volitional obedience — the pleasing aroma arises from correctly and deliberately offered sacrifice; the worshiper must choose to offer what is prescribed; Lev 26:31's withholding of divine Pleasure from the unfaithful implies the faithful person's volitional offering is the enabling condition; (2) **Psa 27:4** ("one thing have I asked… that will I seek after") — seeking to gaze upon God's beauty is a volitional act; (3) **The wisdom-comparative register** (M04-K-VCG-03) — the better-than comparatives require the will to choose modest integrity over corrupt abundance.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Partially: (1) **Deliberate memory-act** — "remember the wondrous works" (1Ch 16:12; Psa 105:5) — the act of deliberate remembrance is volitional; Wonder's sustaining requires the will's choice to return to and rehearse God's acts; (2) **Proclamatory act** — "tell of all his wondrous works" (1Ch 16:9) — the act of telling/proclaiming is volitional; (3) **Restraint act** — Psa 131:1 ("I do not occupy myself with things too marvellous for me") — the volitional act of restraining oneself from overreach; (4) **Consecration** — Jos 3:5 ("consecrate yourselves") — the volitional moral preparation for receiving wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, significantly. Mat 5:12 and Luk 6:23 ("rejoice in that day and leap for joy") — direct commands addressed to the will; Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") — the most explicit volitional-cognitive act in the corpus; 1Pe 4:13 ("rejoice insofar as you share Christ's sufferings") — the command presupposes volitional engagement; Job 9:27 ("I will forget my complaint, I will put off my sad face, and be of good cheer") — Job considers the volitional act of redirecting his inner state (though he then realises he cannot sustain it — M04-F).

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation both requires and strengthens volition. The commands require the will to engage; Hab 3:18 shows the will overriding adverse circumstances to choose exultation. The sustained orientation of Psa 89:16 ("all the day") shows a will that has been trained to maintain exultation as a standing posture.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy enables and strengthens volition by providing the inner motivation for action: 2Cor 8:2 (abundance of joy in poverty overflowing into generosity — Joy produces volitional giving); Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength") — Joy enables the will's perseverance; Act 5:41 (apostles "rejoicing that they were counted worthy to suffer" — joy enabling volitional endurance under persecution). Joy does not bypass volition but works through it, providing the inner incentive for difficult volitional acts.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness enables volition by providing the cognitive-evaluative framework within which good choices are made: the person who accurately evaluates what is genuinely good (M04-L-VCG-02) has the inner clarity needed for right volitional choices. Gladness does not bypass volition but informs it. The Proverbs evaluative corpus is essentially a guide to informed volition — knowing what is good (evaluative Gladness) enables choosing what is good (volition).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the primary shaper of volition in M04: (1) **Enables** — Psa 40:8 (Delight to do God's will enables willing obedience); Gen 34:19 (Delight driving immediate action — will energised by desire); (2) **Deepens** — God's sovereign cha.phets cannot be diverted or overridden (Psa 115:3; Isa 46:10) — perfect Delight produces perfect volitional consistency; the will shaped by Delight in God's law becomes a will that naturally chooses what it loves (Psa 1:2; 40:8); (3) **Distorts** — misdirected Delight drives the will toward wrong objects (Isa 65:12; 2Th 2:12 — the will shaped by pleasure in unrighteousness); desire without knowledge (Pro 19:2) shows Delight as a volitional driver that can produce disaster when unguided by wisdom.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure in wisdom and right worship enables volition by providing clear grounds for choosing what is genuinely good: Pro 16:24's gracious-word Pleasure enables the will to prefer gentle speech; the wisdom-comparative Pleasure enables the will to choose integrity over material abundance. Distorted Pleasure (Pro 7:18's a.las; Pro 9:17's stolen bread) bypasses and corrupts volition by making wrong choices feel pleasant.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder-at-God enables volition by motivating action: Psa 119:129 ("your testimonies are wonderful; therefore my soul keeps them") — Wonder in God's word motivating the volitional act of keeping the testimonies; the wonderfulness of God's commands is what motivates obedience. Wonder-failure (Neh 9:17) leads to volitional rebellion — the absence of wonder removes the motivational ground for obedience.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy both requires and strengthens volition: the commands require the will to engage; the Spirit's enabling empowers the will to sustain what it cannot produce alone (Job's failed volitional attempt at ba.lag vs. the Spirit-enabled agalliao). Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing → continuing to teach) shows Suffering-Joy enabling sustained volitional ministry despite ongoing opposition.

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is not purely spontaneous but involves the will as a significant constituent — particularly in adverse circumstances and in cultivated sustained orientation. The volitional dimension distinguishes exultation from passive emotional states and makes it susceptible to formation and practice.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy and volition have a constitutive relationship in both directions: the will can cultivate and direct Joy (commanded joy); Joy in turn enables and motivates the will (joy produces strength, generosity, endurance). This bidirectional relationship is what makes Joy a formation characteristic — it is both a goal of volitional formation and a resource for further volitional formation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness and volition are related in the pattern of cognition-informs-choice: Gladness's cognitive face (accurate evaluation of the good) is the prerequisite for good volitional choices. The pattern reveals Gladness as the inner faculty that prepares the will — it is not the same as the will but it precedes and enables its right operation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the most volitionally-constituted characteristic in M04, distinctly more so than Gladness (primarily cognitive), Suffering-Joy (primarily Spirit-produced), or Joy (primarily affective). The cha.phets/che.phets vocabulary's pervasive use for both divine sovereign will and human desire confirms that Delight and volition are structurally intertwined: Delight is what the will is when fully engaged with its proper or improper object. The pattern reveals that the deepest volitional structure of a person is their Delight — what they are directed toward with their deepest pleasure.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Unlike Delight (where volition is constitutive) and Joy (where volition is involved through command), Pleasure engages volition instrumentally: right Pleasure supports right willing; wrong Pleasure corrupts and bypasses right willing. Pleasure is primarily receptive rather than volitional — but the quality of what is received as pleasant directly shapes and can corrupt volitional direction.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Psa 119:129's "wonderful… therefore my soul keeps them" is the most analytically significant volition-Wonder connection: Wonder in the testimonies motivates obedience. Wonder provides the motivational ground for volition: the person who is genuinely arrested by the wonderfulness of God's commands has a deep motivational reason to keep them beyond mere duty.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is the characteristic most explicitly requiring volitional engagement in M04: the commands are the most insistent (Jas 1:2's "count it ALL joy"; Mat 5:12's doubled command "rejoice AND be glad"). This volitional insistence confirms that the natural response to suffering is not joy and the will must be actively engaged by command. The Spirit enables what the will is commanded to do.

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. Exultation is expressed through agency — the shout of praise (Psa 32:11), the coming before God in singing (Psa 100:2), the approaching the altar (Psa 43:4). The person who exults acts: they come, they sing, they shout, they proclaim. The inner state moves the person into concrete action.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Joy consistently produces and motivates action: Act 8:39 (the eunuch "went on his way rejoicing" — joy motivating continued journey); 2Cor 8:2 (joy overflowing into generous giving — agency produced by joy); Isa 55:12 ("you shall go out in joy" — joy as the mode of redemptive departure); Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing → continuing to teach in Jesus' name — joy motivating ongoing apostolic agency); Mat 13:44 ("in his joy he goes and sells all that he has" — joy as the inner motivator of radical action); Jer 31:13 (young women rejoice in the dance — joy producing movement and active festivity).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. Neh 2:18 — the people's resolve to build ("let us rise up and build") was stirred by hearing of God's good hand — Gladness-recognition producing agency; 1Sa 11:9 — the men of Jabesh glad at the news of coming deliverance → implicit enabling of their sustained resolve; Lam 3:27 — "it is good for a man that he bear the yoke in his youth" — the gladness of formative discipline enables the agentive capacity of the mature person.
