The wisdom-evaluative corpus (M04-L-VCG-02, 03) produces agency through clarified moral vision: knowing what is genuinely good enables acting accordingly.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, extensively: (1) **Sovereign divine agency** — M04-H-VCG-01: God's cha.phets/eudokeo produces immediate, unrestricted action (Psa 115:3; 135:6; Isa 55:11; 44:28 — Cyrus fulfilling God's purpose); divine Delight is the most agentively-direct characteristic in the entire programme — God's pleasure immediately produces action; (2) **Human urgent action** — Gen 34:19 (Shechem's delight → "did not delay to do the thing") — the most dramatic human agency-from-Delight example; (3) **Diplomatic agency** — the M04-H-VCG-03 "as it seems good to you" formula throughout the historical books frames Delight as the standard by which agency is authorised and directed; (4) **Obedience-agency** — Joh 8:29 (Jesus always doing what pleases the Father — continuous agentive faithfulness produced by Delight-in-the-Father); 1Jo 3:22 (doing what pleases God → receiving prayer answers — agency motivated by and productive of Delight).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, indirectly: (1) **Worship agency** — the ni.cho.ach corpus requires the worshiper to act (offer the sacrifice, wash the entrails, burn the fat) — agency in right worship produces the Pleasure-quality of the aroma; (2) **Psa 27:4's seeking** — "one thing have I asked… that will I seek" — the seeking act is agentive; (3) **Pro 15:26's gracious speech** — speaking pleasant words is an agentive act that extends Pleasure to others; (4) **Neh 9:17 negative** (in M04-I but adjacent) — Israel's failure to act in response to God's wonders shows agency failure as blocking the right Pleasure-response.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Proclamatory agency** — "declare his glory among the nations, his marvellous works" (1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3) — active going-out to declare; (2) **Generational-transmission agency** — "we will not hide them from their children, but tell to the coming generation" (Psa 78:4) — active intergenerational teaching; (3) **Jos 3:5** — Israel's active consecration in anticipation of God's wonders; (4) **Mar 1:27** — the crowd's immediately acting to question among themselves following the wonder-seizure; (5) **2Ch 26:15** — Uzziah being "marvellously helped" enabling his productive agency (making machines, defending the city).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes. Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing that they were counted worthy to suffer for Jesus' name → continuing to teach — Suffering-Joy producing continued agentive mission); Act 16:34 (the jailer coming to faith in crisis → communal agentive response of bringing Paul and Silas into the house, setting food before them, entire household rejoicing — agency around the crisis); Luk 10:21 (Jesus' Spirit-rejoicing is immediately followed by the declaration to the Father and instruction to the disciples — the rejoicing generates continued agentive proclamation).

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation enables and motivates agency: Isa 64:5 names "him who joyfully works righteousness" — exultation in God produces active righteous conduct. Hab 3:18 shows the exulting prophet in a posture of perseverance. Exultation does not impair agency.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy enables and motivates agency: the consistent pattern is that the inner state of gladness produces outward action (singing, going, giving, dancing, proclaiming). There is no evidence of Joy impairing agency except in the comic instance of Act 12:14 (Rhoda's joy briefly overriding practical action of opening the gate — quickly resolved). The general pattern is joy → enabled, motivated action.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness enables agency: Neh 2:18 is the clearest evidence — the gladness of knowing God's good hand is upon the work is what enables the community's collective agentive resolve. The covenantal-promise Gladness (M04-O-VCG-04) particularly enables sustained agency: knowing God's good promises as reliable (Jos 21:45) provides the inner confidence that enables continued faithful action.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the primary agentive driver in M04: it enables and energises agency directly (Gen 34:19; Joh 8:29), and in its sovereign divine form it is the sole operative principle of all action (Psa 115:3). Misdirected Delight impairs agency by directing it toward destructive ends: Jer 42:22 (desire for Egypt leading to disaster in Egypt — the will energised by Delight drives the person toward their destruction); Isa 65:12 (choosing what God did not delight in → sword — agency in destructive direction).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure in right objects enables agency toward those objects: Psa 27:4's longing for God's beauty motivates the agentive seeking of his presence; Pro 24:25's delight at rebuking the wicked motivates moral courageous agency. In its distorted form (Pro 7:18; Pro 9:17), wrong Pleasure motivates agency toward destructive ends.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder in God enables agency through the missionary-proclamatory impulse: the person who has genuinely encountered divine wonders is driven to declare them (1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3). The generational-transmission imperative (Psa 78:4) shows Wonder as agentively demanding — it cannot be held privately. Uzziah's being marvellously helped (2Ch 26:15) shows divine wonder-power enabling productive human agency.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy enables agency by detaching the will from circumstantial-dependent motivation: the apostle who rejoices in suffering is not waiting for circumstances to improve before acting; the Spirit-joy frees the will to act in the present regardless of external conditions. This is the most agentively-liberating characteristic in M04: it produces the capacity to act when circumstances most strongly suggest stopping.

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is an agentive characteristic — it issues in action. The inner surge overflows into the shout, the song, the righteous work, the approach to God's presence. This is consistent with the kinetic root meaning of gil (spinning, leaping movement).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is agentively generative: persons in the full experience of Joy characteristically act from it — they go, they give, they sing, they proclaim, they persist. This makes Joy a reliable formation resource for agency: communities whose inner life is characterized by Joy will be communities that act, serve, and persist.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness functions as a moral-clarity and confidence-generating characteristic that enables agency: the person and community that accurately assess God's goodness and their own moral situation are those who can act from a stable, informed inner base. Gladness does not generate the impulse to action in the same way Joy does (Joy's energy propels action); rather, Gladness provides the stable cognitive-affective foundation from which reliable action proceeds.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the most agentively-powerful characteristic in M04: it directly energises the will and produces action without requiring intermediate steps. This is why the misdirection of Delight is so dangerous (M04-P, M04-H-VCG-04) — the same agency-generating power that in the righteous person drives obedience and mission drives the unrighteous person toward destruction with equal energy. Delight does not produce tentative or half-hearted action; Gen 34:19's "did not delay" and God's "he does all that he pleases" are at the same ends of the spectrum — both show Delight as immediately and fully agentive.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is not primarily an agentive characteristic but it motivates agency toward its object: what is experienced as pleasant draws the person toward it. The ni.cho.ach corpus's link between obedient sacrificial action and divine Pleasure shows the most direct Pleasure-agency relationship: right worship-action produces the Pleasure-quality of the aroma; the action and the Pleasure are inseparable.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the characteristic most agentively directed toward proclamation and teaching: the primary action it generates is not service or justice (Delight's obedience modes) but declaration — going out to tell, proclaim, sing, and pass on. Wonder's agency is inherently communicative and missional.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is agentively generative precisely because it removes the circumstantial dependency of motivation. Where Joy (Characteristic 2) produces agency through the energy of gladness in what is good, Suffering-Joy produces agency through the freedom from requiring the presence of the good before acting. This is the characteristic's most distinctive contribution to the inner being's agency.

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The evidence repeatedly shows that exultation requires and exercises moral evaluation — distinguishing its legitimate from its illegitimate forms. Pro 24:17 prohibits exultation over an enemy's fall; Pro 2:14 marks exultation in evil as a sign of moral corruption; Hos 9:1 prohibits Israel's exultation on moral grounds; Psa 13:4 frames enemy exultation over the righteous as a feared moral wrong. The person's moral evaluation of the appropriate objects of exultation is itself a moral act.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, bidirectionally. (1) **Moral evaluation enabling Joy** — 1Cor 13:6 ("rejoices with the truth") — love's Joy is morally constrained by the capacity to evaluate what is truly good; Psa 97:8 (joy at God's "judgments" — moral appreciation of divine justice produces joy); Job 31:25, 29 (Job denies having rejoiced in wealth or at enemy's ruin — negating morally problematic joy forms); (2) **Joy enabling moral evaluation** — Psa 58:10 ("the righteous will rejoice when he sees the vengeance") — the righteous person's joy at justice being done reflects and reinforces moral evaluation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes — this is Gladness's most distinctive faculty engagement across the entire M04 cluster. M04-L-VCG-02 (45 verses) is almost entirely the moral evaluation faculty in operation: the systematic "is this good? is this not-good?" exercise of the Proverbs corpus; the comparative "better than" assessments; the "what is good?" investigations of Ecclesiastes; Mic 6:8's definitional statement of what human goodness is; Job 34:4's communal moral discernment process. Gladness in its evaluative-cognitive face IS the moral evaluation faculty as an inner-being characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in M04-G and M04-M: (1) **M04-G's law-delight** — Psa 119's Delight in God's statutes, testimonies, commandments is simultaneously moral engagement: the psalmist who delights in the law is engaging the moral evaluation faculty through pleasurable orientation; Psa 40:8 ("I delight to do your will, O my God") — delight as moral alignment; (2) **M04-M-VCG-02** — the series of "doing what is good and right in God's sight" texts (Deu 6:18; 12:28; 1Sa 15:22; Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22) — all engage moral evaluation as the faculty that identifies what is pleasing to God; (3) **M04-H-VCG-02** — God's moral preferences revealed: what God delights in (steadfast love, justice, righteousness — Jer 9:24; Mic 7:18; Hos 6:6) is a moral declaration; (4) **M04-H-VCG-04** — the corrupt-Delight instances (Isa 65:12; 66:3; 2Th 2:12) engage moral evaluation by negation — pleasure in what God condemns reveals the moral inversion.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, primarily in M04-K-VCG-03: (1) **Psa 37:16** (little of righteous better than abundance of wicked — moral-comparative evaluation); (2) **Pro 15:16** (little with fear of Lord better than great treasure with trouble — moral priority); (3) **Pro 15:17** (dinner of herbs with love better than feast with hatred — moral-relational evaluation); (4) **Pro 16:32** (slow to anger better than mighty — inner character better than external power — shared anchor with anger registry); (5) **Pro 19:22** (steadfast love most desirable — moral evaluation of character-quality over material goods). M04-K-VCG-03 is essentially the moral evaluation faculty applied to material Pleasure — the wisdom literature training the evaluative faculty to prefer what is genuinely more pleasant.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Partially: (1) **Psa 118:23** ("this is the Lord's doing; it is marvellous in our eyes") — the evaluative act of recognising God as the agent of the marvellous is a form of moral-theological evaluation; (2) **Gal 1:6** — Paul's astonished moral evaluation of the Galatians' theological defection; his thauma is simultaneously a moral judgment that something wrong has happened; (3) **Rev 17:7** — the angel's "why do you marvel?" to John implies that some marvelling requires moral-evaluative redirection — not everything that produces Wonder deserves it; (4) **Psa 9:1** ("wonderful deeds" in the context of God's just judgment on the wicked — Psa 9:4–6) — Wonder at God's just judgments involves moral evaluation.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Partially. 1Cor 13:6 (love "does not rejoice at wrongdoing, but rejoices with the truth" — adjacent to M04-D but the "rejoices with the truth" in the sunchairo corpus is a moral-evaluative rejoicing about what is genuinely right). Jas 1:2's "trials of various kinds" presupposes the moral evaluation that trials are genuinely adverse and the counter-intuitive reframing that they are also genuinely beneficial (v.3–4). The moral evaluation faculty is engaged but not primary — the characteristic's defining feature is not its moral evaluation of suffering but its transcendence of circumstances through Spirit-enabled joy.

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Rightly-directed exultation deepens moral evaluation — Psa 97:8 shows the daughters of Judah rejoicing specifically because of God's "judgments," making moral appreciation of divine justice the ground of their joy. Misdirected exultation (Pro 2:14; Hos 9:1; 10:5) is associated with moral blindness and corruption. The characteristic both requires and reinforces moral discernment.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Rightly-directed Joy deepens moral evaluation: the person who rejoices in God's judgments (Psa 97:8) is thereby reinforcing their appreciation of divine justice. Misdirected Joy corrupts and bypasses moral evaluation: Pro 2:14 (those who "rejoice in doing evil") show Joy bypassing moral evaluation entirely; Eze 25:6 ("malice within your soul" as source of corrupt joy) shows Joy rooted in moral corruption producing perverse evaluation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens moral evaluation: the person whose inner life is settled in the recognition of what is genuinely good (M04-L-VCG-01 — divine character goodness as the standard) has the reference point from which all other moral evaluation proceeds. Distorted Gladness bypasses moral evaluation: Isa 41:7's craftsman saying "it is good" over an idol is a short-circuit of genuine moral evaluation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight deepens moral evaluation when rightly directed: the person who delights in God's law meditates on its moral content continuously (Psa 1:2); the person who delights in doing God's will has an inward moral compass (Psa 40:8; Joh 8:29). Misdirected Delight impairs and bypasses moral evaluation: Isa 66:3 (soul delighting in abominations — the moral evaluation faculty overridden by the force of misdirected pleasure); 2Th 2:12 (pleasure in unrighteousness — those condemned had their moral evaluation replaced by an anti-moral Delight); Pro 18:2 (fool taking pleasure only in his own opinion — moral evaluation bypassed by self-referential delight).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Right Pleasure in wisdom enables and deepens moral evaluation: Pro 2:10's wisdom-in-heart producing Pleasure in knowledge enables the whole evaluative apparatus of wisdom including moral judgment. Wrong Pleasure bypasses moral evaluation: Pro 9:17's stolen-bread Pleasure makes the forbidden appear genuinely pleasant, preventing accurate moral evaluation of the act.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder at God's justice (Psa 9) deepens moral evaluation: recognising God's acts as marvellous includes recognising that he acts with justice, which deepens the appreciation of moral reality. Rev 17:7's redirected wonder shows that Wonder can be applied inappropriately (marvelling at evil) — the angel's "why do you marvel?" is a moral-evaluative correction to misapplied Wonder. Genuine Wonder at the right object deepens moral evaluation; misapplied Wonder bypasses it.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy does not bypass moral evaluation of suffering — 1Pe 1:6 acknowledges the grief as genuine and the trials as actually grievous; Jas 1:2 does not say trials are good (evaluating them as the good) but says to count them AS joy because of what they produce. The moral faculty is not bypassed but the characteristic operates at a different level — not evaluation of the suffering's goodness but transcendence of the evaluation through Spirit-grounding.

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is morally-loaded in its object: it is not morally neutral. The evidence shows that what a person exults in reveals and reinforces their moral orientation. Exultation in God's judgments (Psa 97:8) deepens moral formation; exultation in evil degrades it.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is morally directional: the object of Joy is the most significant moral indicator. Rejoicing in God's judgments, in the truth, in righteousness → moral evaluation deepened; rejoicing in evil, in enemy's ruin, in idols → moral evaluation bypassed or corrupted. The characteristic's moral quality is therefore entirely determined by what it is directed at.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is the most morally-constituted characteristic in M04. Its evaluative face (M04-L) is functionally identical with the moral evaluation faculty in operation — Gladness and moral evaluation are co-constitutive in this corpus. This is the most analytically distinctive feature of Characteristic 3 within the M04 cluster.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The relationship between Delight and moral evaluation is the most diagnostically significant in M04: the direction of a person's Delight reveals the state of their moral evaluation faculty. What a person delights in is what they judge to be good; if the Delight is misdirected, the moral evaluation faculty has been captured by the wrong object. This is Jer 9:24's theological logic reversed: the person who does not delight in what God delights in (steadfast love, justice, righteousness) has substituted their own standard for God's.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure and moral evaluation are related through the wisdom-formation link: the person whose Pleasure is calibrated by wisdom evaluates moral choices more accurately; the person whose Pleasure is distorted by folly evaluates moral choices inaccurately. The wisdom better-than corpus (M04-K-VCG-03) is the explicit training programme for calibrating Pleasure to moral reality.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder and moral evaluation are connected through the right identification of what is genuinely marvellous: the person who wonders at the right things (God's extraordinary justice, mercy, and power) has a rightly calibrated moral-evaluative faculty; the person who wonders at the wrong things (the beast's apparent resurrection — Rev 13:3; the harlot's power — Rev 17:6) has a distorted one.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy operates above and alongside moral evaluation rather than through it. The suffering is accurately evaluated as suffering; the characteristic does not require misrepresenting the suffering as actually good (which would be the evaluative route). Instead, the Spirit produces a genuine joy that coexists with accurate recognition of suffering's real cost.

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Partially. Psa 51:8 ("let the bones that you have broken rejoice") is the most direct conscience-connection: the broken bones are the bodily image of a conscience-struck person (Psa 51 is David's penitential psalm); the asked-for restoration of exultation in the broken bones presupposes that conscience has done its work (conviction, confession) and exultation is the state that follows restoration. The characteristic engages conscience in the sequence: conviction → confession → restored exultation, not in the exultation itself.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, in a specific sequence. Psa 51:8, 12 — David's loss of joy is the direct consequence of his sin, and his restoration of joy is sought after genuine repentance (Psa 51:17 — the broken and contrite heart). The sequence is: conscience convicts → joy is lost (Psa 51:8) → repentance → restoration of joy (Psa 51:12). Ecc 8:15's commendation of joy "for God has already approved what you do" implies that conscience clearance is a precondition for genuine, untroubled joy. Pro 29:6 ("a righteous man sings and rejoices") implies that the righteous man's freedom from the snare of sin enables joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. Eze 36:31 — "your deeds that were not good, and you will loathe yourselves" — the evaluative faculty turned inward in conviction: the recognition that one's own past deeds were not-good produces self-loathing; this is the moral conscience engaging through the Gladness-evaluation faculty. Pro 20:23 — "false scales are not good" — the moral conscience is engaged through the evaluative standard. 1Sa 26:16 — "this thing you have done is not good" — conscience speaks through the not-good verdict.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Partially: (1) **M04-H-VCG-04's negated Delight** as divine condemnation — Heb 10:38 ("my soul has no pleasure in him") is the divine-conscience-equivalent: God's withholding of delight functions as his verdict on the person who shrinks back; (2) **1Cor 10:5** ("with most of them God was not pleased, for they were overthrown in the wilderness") — God's displeasure as the conscience-verdict of history; (3) **Job 6:10** (sa.lad in M04-G-VCG-01 — "I would even exult in pain unsparing, for I have not denied the words of the Holy One") — Job's clear conscience expressed as a form of inner exultation even in pain; fidelity to God's word sustains the inner person against conscience-guilt; (4) **Psa 51:6** ("you delight in truth in the inward being") — God's delight in inner truth is the positive conscience-standard; where it is met, Delight follows; where it is absent, God's delight is withheld.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially: (1) **Pro 15:26** — "thoughts of the wicked are an abomination to the Lord, but gracious words are pure" — the contrast between wicked thoughts (conscience-bad) and gracious words (conscience-pure) shows that Pleasure in speech is conscience-indexed; genuinely pleasant speech is also morally pure; (2) **Ni.cho.ach withheld** (Lev 26:31) — God's non-reception of the unfaithful's aromas implies the conscience of the worshiper should recognise that their worship has failed the covenant standard; the absent ni.cho.ach is an implicit conscience-signal; (3) **Job 20:18** (the wicked gets no enjoyment) — the blocked Pleasure of the wicked is itself a conscience-indicator: natural Pleasure is denied as a consequence of moral failure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

The M04-I corpus does not directly evidence Wonder engaging the conscience (the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction). Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me" comes after Job's confrontation with God in the whirlwind; the conscience may have been engaged prior to Wonder in that sequence, but Wonder itself is the response to the incomprehensible divine display rather than the conscience's direct engagement.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

The M04-E-VCG-02 and M04-F corpus does not show Suffering-Joy engaging the conscience (the acute witness of sin, guilt, and conviction) directly. Act 16:34 (the jailer came to faith after apparent conviction — the surrounding narrative implies prior conscience-work, but the verse itself focuses on the rejoicing that follows). The characteristic's relationship with conscience is indirect and not evidenced in the primary corpus.

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation follows conscience's work rather than engaging or bypassing it. The inverted exultation of Hos 10:5 and Pro 2:14 suggests that misdirected exultation is associated with a dulled or bypassed conscience — those who exult in evil are not engaging their conscience. Rightly-directed exultation follows and completes conscience's work.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Genuine Joy follows conscience's work rather than bypassing it: Psa 51 shows conscience doing its full work (conviction, acknowledgement of sin) before Joy is restored. The misdirected-Joy passages (Pro 2:14; Eze 25:6) show joy that has bypassed conscience — these are the corrupted forms. Genuine Joy, in the evidence, consistently comes after or alongside a clear conscience; it does not precede or bypass it.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness's evaluative face deepens conscience: the person who accurately evaluates conduct against the standard of genuine goodness is exercising the same faculty as the conscience. Eze 36:31's self-loathing shows conscience operating through the evaluative-gladness faculty in its most convicting register. Distorted Gladness can bypass conscience: the craftsman who declares his idol-work "good" (Isa 41:7) without genuine moral evaluation has circumvented the conscience.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight in God's word deepens conscience: the person whose Delight is in God's testimonies has an active, engaged moral sense aligned with divine standards. Delight in abominations (Isa 66:3) bypasses and suppresses conscience: the soul that delights in what God condemns has effectively silenced the conscience through the force of misdirected Delight. The most serious form of conscience-impairment in the corpus is 2Th 2:12's "pleasure in unrighteousness" — Delight so deeply misdirected that the conscience's witness is drowned.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure in what is morally good enables conscience: the person who finds gracious words genuinely pleasant (Pro 15:26) has a conscience aligned with what is morally pure. Distorted Pleasure bypasses conscience: the seductress's a.las (Pro 7:18) makes the conscience-violating act feel pleasant, and the stolen bread's apparent pleasantness (Pro 9:17) bypasses the conscience's recognition of wrongdoing.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

Not directly evidenced. Adjacent: the VCG-03 dark Wonder (astonishment at evil — Gal 1:6's troubled astonishment at doctrinal defection) operates alongside conscience in moral judgment, but Wonder itself is the astonishment response rather than the conscience's accusation. Not evidenced.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

Not directly evidenced. Silent on conscience engagement in this corpus.

---

##### T3.9.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is the characteristic that comes after conscience — not the one that engages it in its convicting work. The sequence of Psa 51 is paradigmatic: broken → convicted → restored → exultation. Conscience clears the ground; exultation is the inner state that occupies the cleared ground.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The sequence conscience → (if needed: repentance) → joy is a consistent pattern where Joy is healthy. Joy that bypasses conscience is corrupted Joy. Joy that follows conscience's convicting and cleansing work is genuine. The Psa 51 pattern (broken → convicted → restored in joy) is the paradigmatic formation sequence for Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The moral evaluation faculty (M04-L) and the conscience are closely allied in Gladness's evidence: both involve comparing reality against a standard of genuine goodness, and the correct operation of one requires and reinforces the correct operation of the other. Gladness is the characteristic most closely integrated with conscience in M04.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Conscience and Delight are mutually determinative: a healthy conscience enables authentic Delight in what is genuinely good; Delight in what is genuinely good reinforces and deepens conscience. Misdirected Delight is the mechanism by which conscience is suppressed — the pleasure taken in the wrong object generates its own justification, progressively silencing the inner witness. This is the pathway of Isa 66:3 and 2Th 2:12: sustained wrong Delight forms a soul in which conscience has been replaced by anti-conscience.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The relationship between Pleasure and conscience is diagnostic: when genuine pleasantness and moral goodness align (Pro 15:26 — gracious words are both pleasant and pure; Pro 16:24 — pleasant words are health-giving), the conscience and the Pleasure faculty are in agreement. When they diverge (Pro 9:17 — stolen bread feels pleasant but is morally wrong), the Pleasure faculty has been captured by the wrong object against the conscience's proper witness.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

The silence on conscience engagement confirms Wonder as primarily a cognitive-perceptive and doxological characteristic rather than a conscience-involving one. Wonder operates at the boundary of comprehension and in the space of proclamation, not primarily in the space of moral self-accusation.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

The silence suggests Suffering-Joy operates after conscience's work rather than engaging it — consistent with the broader M04 pattern (Joy follows conscience's convicting work; Suffering-Joy follows faith-reception). The characteristic presupposes the conscience has done its work of conviction and the person has come to faith; it is what follows, not what accompanies, the conscience's work.

---

#### T3.10 — Conscientiousness

##### T3.10.1 — Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, in its sustained and commanded forms. Psa 89:16 ("exult in your name all the day") requires the integrated response of moral awareness, will, and action that constitutes conscientiousness. Isa 64:5 shows "him who joyfully works righteousness" — conscientiousness and exultation joined in a single portrait of the person whose moral awareness, will, and action are unified in glad righteous activity.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Deu 28:47 — failure to serve with "joyfulness and gladness of heart" as the root of covenant judgment — directly links conscientiousness (integrated moral-volitional responsive service) to Joy. The person who is conscientious in covenant service does so joyfully; the absence of joyfulness in service is itself a form of unfaithfulness. Isa 64:5 ("you meet him who joyfully works righteousness") joins Joy and righteous action as a unified inner-being posture. 1Ch 29:17 ("offering freely and joyously to you") joins conscientiousness (upright heart, freewill offering) with Joy as the appropriate inner spirit of morally-conscious giving.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. Mic 6:8 ("he has told you, O man, what is good… do justice, love kindness, walk humbly") integrates moral awareness (knowing what is good), volition (doing, loving, walking), and action — the full definition of conscientiousness. The Proverbs corpus (M04-L-VCG-02) consistently connects evaluative recognition of what is good with the call to live accordingly: Pro 2:20 ("walk in the way of the good") — the good recognised becomes the good lived. The covenantal-prompt "so that it may be well with you" (Deu 19:13; M04-O-VCG-03) links just action (conscientiousness) with experienced wellbeing (gladness).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, primarily through M04-M and M04-H-VCG-02: (1) **Joh 8:29** ("I always do the things that are pleasing to him") — the most perfect integration of Delight and conscientiousness in the corpus: Jesus' continuous Delight-in-the-Father's-pleasure produces continuous conscientious action; the inner orientation (Delight) and the outward consistency of action (conscientiousness) are indistinguishable; (2) **1Jo 3:22** ("do what pleases him") — obedient Delight producing conscientious commandment-keeping; (3) **Psa 40:8** ("I delight to do your will") — Delight making conscientiousness natural and willing rather than reluctant; (4) **1Sa 15:22** ("to obey is better than sacrifice") — the conscientious inner orientation toward obedience as the form God's Delight takes.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, in the ni.cho.ach worship register: (1) **Lev 1:9; 2:2; 3:5** (and throughout M04-K-VCG-01) — each offering must be carefully prepared (washed, properly arranged, fully burned) before producing the pleasing aroma; conscientiousness in ritual detail is what produces the worship-Pleasure; (2) **Num 28:2** — "you shall be careful to offer to me at its appointed time" — conscientiousness in timing is explicitly commanded as the condition for pleasing-aroma worship; (3) **Joh 8:29** (cross-assigned in M04-M, but paradigmatic) — "I always do the things that are pleasing" — continuous conscientious action as the form Pleasure-in-obedience takes.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, indirectly: (1) **Psa 119:129** — "your testimonies are wonderful; therefore my soul keeps them" — the wonderfulness of the testimonies producing conscientious law-keeping; (2) **Jos 3:5** — "consecrate yourselves, for tomorrow the Lord will do wonders" — the conscientious moral preparation as the condition for receiving Wonder; (3) **Num 28:2** (adjacent — careful offering of pleasing aroma) — conscientious worship-practice producing the worship-Pleasure relationship; the implied parallel: Wonder at God's acts motivating conscientious covenant-faithfulness.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes. Act 5:41 (apostles rejoicing → continuing to teach daily in the temple and from house to house — the rejoicing in suffering produces and sustains conscientious mission-faithfulness); 1Pe 4:13's "insofar as you share Christ's sufferings" implies the conscientious engagement with Christ's mission that occasions the sharing of his suffering; Jas 1:2–4 (count trials as joy → steadfastness → complete works) shows Suffering-Joy producing the integrated-responsive-action-pattern that is conscientiousness.

---

##### T3.10.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Rightly-directed exultation deepens conscientiousness: the person who exults in God's righteousness and judgments (Psa 97:8) is reinforcing the integrated moral-volitional responsiveness that is conscientiousness. Misdirected exultation (Pro 2:14) is the portrait of conscientiousness collapsed.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens conscientiousness by motivating and sustaining it: the Deuteronomic feast-joy (Deu 16:11–15) produces the inner condition of gladness that makes covenant service an act of delight rather than duty. Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength") — the inner joy produced by hearing God's word enables conscientious engagement with the Law's demands. Joyless service (Deu 28:47) produces covenant unfaithfulness — conscientiousness without joy is structural unfaithfulness in the evidence.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens conscientiousness through the Mic 6:8 pattern: knowing what is good (evaluative Gladness) enables and motivates doing what is good (conscientiousness). The "so that it may be well with you" conditional in Deu 19:13 and similar texts shows that conscientiousness in right action produces the gladness-of-wellbeing, confirming the mutual reinforcement of Gladness and conscientiousness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight enables and deepens conscientiousness: Joh 8:29 shows Delight producing unbroken conscientiousness — always doing what pleases the Father; 1Jo 3:22's structure (obedience → pleasing God → prayer answered) shows conscientiousness reinforced by Delight's relational framing (pleasing someone I delight in is the highest motivation for consistent action). In its distorted form, misdirected Delight bypasses conscientiousness: Isa 58:13 (seeking one's own pleasure on the Sabbath — self-Delight displacing the conscientious Sabbath-orientation).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure in right worship enables and sustains conscientiousness in worship practice: the worship community that experiences the ongoing pleasure-relationship with God through ni.cho.ach sacrifice is motivated to maintain its conscientious practice. The delight of receiving God's favour through correctly-offered sacrifice (Eze 20:41 — "as a pleasing aroma I will accept you") provides the motivation for sustained conscientious worship.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder enables conscientiousness by providing motivational grounding: Psa 119:129's "wonderful… therefore my soul keeps them" is the clearest evidence — the wonderfulness of God's word provides the deep motivational why for conscientious obedience. Conversely, Wonder-absence (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful of the wonders") directly produced covenant-unfaithfulness — the absence of Wonder removed the motivational ground for conscientious covenant-keeping.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy deepens and enables conscientiousness specifically under opposition: the apostles who could rejoice in being counted worthy to suffer (Act 5:41) are the ones who continued teaching despite the opposition. Conscientiousness without Suffering-Joy would collapse under sustained persecution; Suffering-Joy provides the inner resource that sustains conscientious action when circumstances make it costly.

---

##### T3.10.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation and conscientiousness reinforce each other when properly ordered: the person whose whole life is conscientiously directed toward God (Isa 64:5) is the one who exults; the person who exults rightly reinforces their conscientious orientation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy and conscientiousness are constitutively linked: the conscientious covenant person is joyful in their service; the joyful person is motivated toward conscientious action. The removal of Joy produces joyless service; joyless service produces covenant failure. This is the moral-formation logic of Deu 28:47 — the deepest root of covenant unfaithfulness is not external disobedience but the inner loss of joyfulness in God's service.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness and conscientiousness form an integrated moral-inner cycle: accurate recognition of what is good (Gladness) → conscientious living toward the good → experienced wellbeing as Gladness's fruit → reinforcing the recognition that this is genuinely the good life. The Deuteronomic conditional structure ("do this good thing, so that it may be well with you") is the explicit biblical articulation of this cycle.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Joh 8:29 is the most analytically significant data point: it names the perfected integration of Delight and conscientiousness. "Always doing what pleases the Father" — the always is the conscientiousness; "what pleases the Father" is the Delight object. The pattern reveals that where Delight is perfectly directed (toward God's pleasure), conscientiousness is perfectly consistent. This is the inner logic of M04-M as a register of Delight: Delight-as-obedience-orientation is exactly the integration of Delight and conscientiousness that Jesus perfectly embodied and that 1Jo 3:22 prescribes for believers.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The ni.cho.ach corpus is the most explicit evidence in M04 for Pleasure as a motivator of conscientiousness: the worshiper who knows that carefully-offered sacrifice produces the pleasing aroma (God's receptive Pleasure) is motivated to sustained careful practice. Pleasure in the worship-relationship produces conscientiousness in worship-action.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the motivational ground for conscientiousness: the person who is genuinely arrested by the wonderfulness of God's commands, acts, and character has the deepest possible motivation for conscientious obedience. Psa 119:129's structure (Wonder → keeping) is analytically precise: Wonder precedes and produces conscientiousness as its natural fruit.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is the characteristic that enables conscientiousness to hold under pressure. It is therefore the critical inner-being resource for mission-faithfulness under persecution — the specific inner capacity that prevents the gap between moral awareness (I should continue) and action (I do continue) from being opened by suffering's pressure.

---

#### T3.11 — Relational Capacity

##### T3.11.1 — Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, strongly and in both directions. Human-to-God: exultation is consistently a relational act directed toward God — "exult in your name" (Psa 89:16), "rejoice in the Lord" (Psa 32:11), "God my exceeding joy" (Psa 43:4). God-to-human: God exults over his people (Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41; Isa 62:5; 65:19) — the relational direction is mutual. Human-to-human: Pro 23:24–25 (father's exultation over a righteous son), Isa 66:10 (exulting with Jerusalem among those who love her), VCG-03 (parental and creation-participatory exultation).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, extensively — Joy is one of the most relationally-constituted characteristics in M04. (1) **God-to-human relational Joy** — God's Joy over his people (Luk 15:7; Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41); (2) **Human-to-God relational Joy** — "rejoice in the Lord" (Psa 32:11; Phili 4:4); (3) **Human-to-human relational Joy** — M04-B-VCG-04 is entirely relational (parental joy over children; spousal joy; friendship joy; communal joy); M04-D is constitutively relational (sunchairo — co-rejoicing); the Pauline joy over specific communities (1Th 2:19–20; 3Jo 4; Phili 4:1) names persons as the content of joy; (4) **Creation-to-creator relational Joy** — the cosmic rejoicing passages (Psa 96:11; 97:1; Isa 49:13) call all creation to rejoice before its Creator.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, substantially. M04-L-VCG-02 contains significant relational evaluations: Rut 4:15 (Ruth's love declared better than seven sons — relational worth appraised superlatively); 1Sa 25:3 (Abigail's inner quality of wisdom contrasted with Nabal's harshness); 1Sa 25:15 (David's men's relational goodness toward Nabal's servants); the good man who "leaves an inheritance" (Pro 13:22 — relational generativity); "better is open rebuke than hidden love" (Pro 27:5 — relational honesty assessed as the genuinely better good). M04-O-VCG-03's wellbeing-gladness is often relationally produced: Saul's recovery through David's music (1Sa 16:23); Jonathan's testimony of David's deeds (1Sa 19:4).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, pervasively: (1) **God's relational Delight in persons** (M04-H-VCG-02) — Psa 18:19 (delighted in → rescued); Num 14:8 (delights in us → brings us to the land); 1Ki 10:9 (delighted in Solomon → set on the throne); Isa 62:4 (delights in Zion → renames her); Jer 31:20 (Ephraim as darling child — sha.a.shu.im persisting through rebuke); Eze 18:23; 33:11 (no pleasure in wicked person's death — relational orientation toward life); Mic 7:18 (delights in steadfast love — relational Delight as the deepest expression of God's character); (2) **Human relational Delight** — 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan delighting much in David — deep personal affection overriding familial loyalty); Psa 16:3 (all my delight in the saints); 1Th 2:8 (Paul's affectionate desire for the Thessalonians producing self-giving); (3) **Parental Delight** (M04-N) — Mic 1:16 (children of your delight — ta.a.nug as parental tender attachment); (4) **Corrupt relational Delight** (M04-N-VCG-02, M04-P-VCG-02) — Rev 13:3; 17:8 (marveling at the beast) and Eze 23:12 (lustful captivation) — the relational capacity corrupted.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, extensively — M04-J is almost entirely relational: (1) **2Sa 1:26** — Jonathan's pleasantness to David as the deepest relational warmth in the corpus; (2) **Psa 133:1** — brotherly unity as pleasant — communal relational pleasantness; (3) **Song 1:16; 7:6** — the beloved's pleasantness as received aesthetic-relational Pleasure; (4) **Pro 16:24** — gracious words as pleasant — the relational speech-act as Pleasure medium; (5) **Pro 3:17** — wisdom's ways as pleasantness — wisdom's relational character; (6) **Zec 11:7, 10** — the No'am staff as the covenant-favour relationship personified; (7) **Psa 27:4** — the pleasantness of dwelling in God's house as the relational intimacy-quality.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, in multiple dimensions: (1) **Communal proclamation** — the VCG-01 corpus is overwhelmingly communal: "we will not hide them from their children" (Psa 78:4); "declare his glory among the nations" (1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3); "let the heavens praise your wonders, O Lord" (Psa 89:5) — Wonder is proclaimed in community, not held privately; (2) **Intergenerational relationship** — Psa 78:4's generational transmission is a relational act; (3) **Witness-relationship** — Exo 34:10 ("all the people among whom you are shall see the work of the Lord") — Wonder creates a witness-relationship with observers; (4) **2Sa 1:26** (Jonathan's love as "extraordinary" — pa.la) — Wonder as a quality of deep human relational experience (the extraordinary love that exceeded normal categories is named by the Wonder-term).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes. Act 16:34 — the jailer's agalliao encompasses his entire household; the coming-to-faith joy is constitutively communal and relational; Luk 15:6, 9 (adjacent — sunchairo in M04-D, but the pattern is clear) — Suffering-Joy moves into communal celebration; Act 5:41 (apostles — a communal sharing of the suffering-joy experience); 1Pe 4:13 (the "we" implied in sharing Christ's sufferings is communal participation).

---

##### T3.11.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation deepens relational capacity: the person who exults in God is most fully alive to the relationship's reality. God's exulting over his people (Zep 3:17) deepens the relational bond — the image of God exulting over Zion with loud singing is a portrait of the fullest divine-human relational delight. The co-exultation of Isa 66:10 (all who love Jerusalem invited to exult with her) shows the characteristic generating relational solidarity.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy deepens relational capacity: M04-D (sunchairo) shows Joy as constitutively completing the relational bond — the co-rejoicing body is the rightly-ordered body; 1Jo 1:4 ("that our joy may be complete" through shared fellowship) and 2Jo 12 ("our joy may be complete" through face-to-face meeting) show Joy as the inner experience that reaches its fullness in genuine relational communion. The Pauline joy-in-communities shows that the relational bonds Paul has with specific people are the substance of his deepest Joy — persons are named as his joy (Phili 4:1; 1Th 2:20). Joy without genuine relational capacity (isolated, self-directed) is not fully evidenced as Joy in this corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness deepens relational capacity by enabling accurate relational evaluation: the person who can assess relational worth accurately (Rut 4:15; Pro 27:5) has the inner clarity to form and sustain genuine relationships. Gladness's wellbeing register (M04-O-VCG-03) is often relationally produced — good music, good testimony, good deeds — showing that gladness-as-wellbeing flows through relational channels.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight deepens genuine relational capacity: 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan's Delight in David enabling him to protect David against his father's command); Jer 31:20 (God's Delight in Ephraim sustaining the relationship through rebuke — Delight as the relational bond that persists through discipline); 1Th 2:8 (Paul's affectionate desire for the Thessalonians producing self-sharing — Delight as the relational motor for self-giving). Corrupt Delight (M04-P; M04-N-VCG-02) distorts relational capacity into captivation, lust, or predation (Eze 23:12; Rev 13:3) — the relational faculty seized by the wrong object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Genuine Pleasure deepens relational capacity: 2Sa 1:26's Jonathan-David pleasantness is the relational depth evidenced by David's grief at the loss; the pleasantness of the relationship was constitutive of its depth. Pro 16:24's gracious-word Pleasure actively sustains relationships through speech. Distorted Pleasure impairs relational capacity: Pro 9:17's stolen-bread Pleasure exploits and degrades relationships; Jer 51:34's Nebuchadnezzar consuming Jerusalem's delicacies is destructive of the relational context.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder deepens relational capacity in two registers: (1) **Community-formation** — shared Wonder creates community; the people who together remember and proclaim God's marvellous works are bound by that shared wonder-memory (Psa 78:4); (2) **Depth of relational experience** — 2Sa 1:26's use of pa.la for Jonathan's extraordinary love shows Wonder as the capacity to recognise and be astonished by genuine extraordinary depth in human relationships.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy deepens relational capacity by creating a community formed around shared participation in Christ's suffering and anticipated glory (1Pe 4:13; Act 5:41). The communal experience of Suffering-Joy — rejoicing together despite or through shared adversity — creates bonds of peculiar depth and solidarity.

---

##### T3.11.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is constitutively relational — it cannot occur in the absence of an object, and its proper object is God in the divine-human relation. The mutuality of exultation (God exults over his people; his people exult in him) makes this characteristic the affective evidence of the covenant relationship at its fullest.

---

## T4 — Relational Interface

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is constitutively relational — it reaches its fullness in and through genuine relational bonds. The M04-D sunchairo evidence is the most concentrated expression of this: co-rejoicing is a distinct inner-being phenomenon because Joy is structurally incomplete without being shared. The pattern reveals that Joy has a relational telos: present partial joy moves toward communal and divine-relational fullness (Joh 15:11; 16:24; 1Jo 1:4; Rev 19:7).

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). 36 (Seg 1) + 64 (Seg 2) = 100 of 189 prompts answered.*

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness and relational capacity are mutually reinforcing in the relational-evaluation sub-register: the person who evaluates relational worth accurately inhabits genuine Gladness in their relationships (Ruth's love is genuinely better; open rebuke is genuinely the better good). And the person formed in genuine Gladness becomes more capable of authentic relational evaluation and engagement.

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). Cumulative: 36 + 64 = 100 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 3.*

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the relational characteristic most closely tied to the motivational structure of relationships: what a person delights in determines who they protect (Jonathan and David), who they cherish (God and Ephraim), who they give themselves to (Paul and the Thessalonians), and who they become dangerously attached to (beast-captivation). The pattern reveals Delight as the relational-motivational engine — it is the inner disposition that drives relational action, making it the most powerful and most dangerous relational capacity in M04.

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). Cumulative: 36 + 64 = 100 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 4.*

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is the characteristic most directly generated through and sustained by relational bonds in M04. M04-J's entire corpus is relational pleasantness — the quality of what is agreeable between persons. The pattern reveals that the deepest human Pleasure in this corpus is relational (Jonathan-David; the beloved; brotherly unity) rather than material or sensory — relational pleasantness is the characteristic's most profound register.

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). Cumulative: 36 + 64 = 100 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 5.*

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is inherently communal in its primary register: the VCG-01 proclamatory tradition is a community-sustaining practice. The pattern reveals that Wonder cannot remain private — its natural expression is communal declaration. This makes Wonder the most communally-directed characteristic in M04: its characteristic expressive mode is not personal prayer (like Delight) or individual formation (like Gladness through wisdom) but communal proclamation across generational boundaries.

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). Cumulative: 36 + 64 = 100 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 6.*

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is constitutively communal in its primary NT register: the agalliao passages consistently show it shared, celebrated, and expressed in community. The characteristic deepens relational bonds precisely because it is a sharing of the paradox — the community that has genuinely rejoiced together through suffering has a bond that shared prosperity cannot produce.

---

*End of Segment 2 (T2–T3). Cumulative: 36 + 64 = 100 of 189 prompts answered for Characteristic 7.*

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, explicitly and repeatedly. God exults over his people with gladness and loud singing (Zep 3:17 — su.s and gil_verb); rejoices in doing Israel good with all his heart and soul (Jer 32:41 — su.s); will rejoice over restored Zion as a bridegroom over a bride (Isa 62:5 — su.s); will rejoice in Jerusalem and be glad in his people (Isa 65:19 — gil_verb and su.s); takes delight in prospering the restored (Deu 30:9 — su.s). The God-to-human direction is one of the most strongly evidenced directions in the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, extensively and across multiple registers: (1) **God produces joy in the heart** — Psa 4:7 ("you have put more joy in my heart"); Ezr 6:22 ("the Lord had made them joyful"); Ecc 5:20 ("God keeps him occupied with joy in his heart"); 2Ch 20:27 ("the Lord had made them rejoice over their enemies"); (2) **God gives joy as a gift** — Ecc 2:26 ("God has given wisdom and knowledge and joy" to the one who pleases him); Psa 126:3 ("the Lord has done great things for us; we are glad"); (3) **God fills with joy** — Rom 15:13 ("may the God of hope fill you with all joy and peace in believing"); Act 13:52 ("filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit"); (4) **God's own joy over his people** — Luk 15:7, 10 (joy in heaven and before the angels over the repentant sinner); Zep 3:17 (God rejoicing over his people with gladness); Jer 32:41 (God rejoicing over Israel in doing good); (5) **Jesus' joy given to disciples** — Joh 15:11 ("my joy may be in you"); Joh 17:13 ("that they may have my joy fulfilled in themselves"); Mat 25:21, 23 ("enter into the joy of your master").

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, extensively and at the most fundamental level. (1) **M04-L-VCG-01 — divine character goodness**: God is the originating subject of the evaluative-goodness faculty — Gen 1:4–31 (God sees and declares good); Gen 2:18 (God identifies the not-good and remedies it); Psa 25:8 ("good and upright is the Lord"); Psa 86:5 ("you are good and forgiving"); Psa 100:5; 106:1; 107:1; 118:1, 29; 135:3; 136:1 (the ki-tov formulas — God's goodness declared as the ground for praise); Nah 1:7 ("The Lord is good, a stronghold in the day of trouble"); Lam 3:25 ("The Lord is good to those who wait for him"); Psa 145:9 ("The Lord is good to all"); (2) **M04-O-VCG-04 — covenantal promise and good hand**: God's good hand enabling Ezra's journey (Ezr 7:9; 8:18); God's good hand enabling Nehemiah's petition (Neh 2:8); God's good hand as the testimony motivating communal action (Neh 2:18); God's good promises fulfilled (Jos 21:45; Jer 29:10; 33:14; Num 10:29); (3) **M04-O-VCG-03 — God producing wellbeing**: Ezr 6:22 ("the Lord had made them joyful"); 2Ch 20:27 ("the Lord had made them rejoice" — adjacent); Psa 112:5 ("it is well with the man who deals generously" — God's moral order producing wellbeing for the righteous).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes — God's Delight directed toward the human person is the most extensively documented God-to-human inner-being movement in M04. Six modes: (1) **Rescue and exaltation from Delight** — Psa 18:19 / 2Sa 22:20 ("he rescued me, because he delighted in me"); Psa 37:23 ("the steps of a man are established by the Lord, when he delights in his way"); 1Ki 10:9; 2Ch 9:8 ("delighted in you and set you on the throne"); Num 14:8 ("if the Lord delights in us, he will bring us into this land"); (2) **Relational naming from Delight** — Isa 62:4 ("you shall be called My Delight Is in Her, for the Lord delights in you, and your land shall be married") — God's Delight toward Zion producing a new covenantal identity; (3) **Parental cherishing** — Jer 31:20 ("Ephraim my darling child" — sha.a.shu.im persisting through rebuke, God's heart yearning) — God-to-human Delight as the most tender relational form; (4) **Restoration from Delight** — Deu 30:9 ("the Lord will again take delight in prospering you") — divine Delight as the engine of national restoration; (5) **Wisdom as God's delight** — Pro 8:30–31 — God's daily sha.a.shu.im in Wisdom, and through Wisdom in the children of man — the creative-relational Delight that constitutes the human-divine relationship from the beginning; (6) **Trinitarian Delight** — Mat 3:17; 12:18; 17:5; Mar 1:11; Luk 3:22; Col 1:19; 2Pe 1:17 — the Father's eudokeo directed toward the Son, which is the archetype of all divine-to-human Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, in three primary God-to-human registers: (1) **God's pleasant character extended toward the community** — Psa 90:17 ("let the favor/pleasantness [no.am] of the Lord our God be upon us") — divine pleasantness as a character-quality that God extends toward his people; (2) **Divine beauty received by the worshiper** — Psa 27:4 ("to gaze upon the beauty [no.am] of the Lord") — God's own beauty as the object that the worshiper receives as Pleasure; God extends his beauty toward the seeking person; (3) **Divine river of delights** — Psa 36:8 ("you give them drink from the river of your delights [ed.nah]") — God lavishly supplying delight from his own inexhaustible source toward those who feast in his house; (4) **Eschatological acceptance as pleasing aroma** — Eze 20:41 ("as a pleasing aroma I will accept you") — God extending his receptive Pleasure toward restored Israel as a future-oriented covenantal gift; (5) **Pleasures forevermore** — Psa 16:11 ("at your right hand are pleasures forevermore") — God as the permanent source of pleasure in his own presence.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, in two primary God-to-human directions: (1) **God performing wonders toward Israel** — the dominant VCG-01 pattern throughout: God's marvellous deeds are the divine acts directed toward the human community that produce Wonder as the response; Exo 3:20 (wonders done in Egypt); Exo 34:10 (marvels "before all your people"); Psa 31:21 ("he has wondrously shown his steadfast love to me when I was in a besieged city") — divine wonders extended as saving acts toward the person in distress; Joe 2:26 ("the Lord your God, who has dealt wondrously with you") — wonder-acts as the mode of divine engagement with the covenant community; (2) **God opening the eyes to behold wonders** — Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law") — the petition implies God extends the capacity for Wonder as a gift; the ability to perceive the wondrous in Scripture is itself a God-to-human act.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, in two registers: (1) **Spirit-produced agalliao** — the Holy Spirit is the primary agent producing Suffering-Joy in the human person: Luk 10:21 (Jesus' agalliao is "in the Holy Spirit"); 1Th 1:6 (adjacent — "joy of the Holy Spirit" received amid affliction); Act 13:52 (adjacent — "filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit"). The Spirit is God-toward-the-human-person in the constitutional dimension; (2) **Eschatological promise as the ground** — the "joy set before him" (Heb 12:2), "your reward is great in heaven" (Mat 5:12), and "when his glory is revealed" (1Pe 4:13) are God's word-of-promise operating as the cognitive-eschatological ground that the Spirit works through to produce Suffering-Joy. God-toward-the-human-person operates through both Spirit and word.

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

God's exultation toward his people is consistently **covenantal and responsive**: (1) **Covenantal** — Jer 32:41's context is the new covenant; Deu 30:9's is the restoration covenant after return; Isa 62:5's is the eschatological marriage of YHWH and Zion; (2) **Responsive** — God's exultation is directed at a restored people (Deu 30:9 — "as he took delight in your fathers"; Zep 3:17 — he who will save, in your midst); (3) **Conditional by the people's covenant posture** — Deu 28:63 shows the same su.s applied to God's delight in ruin when Israel is unfaithful, confirming the covenantal conditionality. God's exultation over his people is not unconditional but arises from the fulfilment of covenant relationship.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple bases evidenced: (1) **Covenantal faithfulness** — the feast-commandment joy (Deu 16:11–15) is joy given in the context of covenant obedience and God's blessing; Deu 28:47 makes its withdrawal contingent on covenant failure; (2) **Repentance** — Luk 15:7, 10 (God's joy over the repentant sinner — Joy given in response to turning); Psa 51:12 (restoration of joy requested after confession); (3) **Pleasing God** — Ecc 2:26 (God gives joy "to the one who pleases him"); (4) **Grace in Christ** — the NT Spirit-mediated joy (Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6; Rom 14:17) is given through the Spirit as a gift, not earned; Joh 15:11 (Christ's joy given as part of abiding relationship with him); (5) **Eschatological promise** — M04-E (sa.s.von) shows God promising joy as the eschatological reversal of sorrow, grounded in his covenant commitment to restore.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple bases: (1) **Unconditional character-goodness** — God's intrinsic goodness (M04-L-VCG-01) is not conditioned on human response; it is the permanent quality of his nature ("his steadfast love endures forever" — ki-tov formulas); (2) **Covenantal faithfulness** — M04-O-VCG-04: God's good promises are fulfilled to the covenant community (Jos 21:45); his good hand enables those who are faithful to his call (Ezr 7:9; Neh 2:8); (3) **Moral responsiveness** — Psa 73:1 ("God is good to Israel, to those who are pure in heart") — moral purity is the precondition for experiencing God's goodness as directed toward oneself; Psa 112:5 ("it is well with the man who deals generously") — justice and generosity are conditions for the wellbeing Gladness; (4) **Grace in redemption** — Gen 2:18 (God identifies the not-good and provides the remedy — grace without merit); Deu 9:6 ("not because of your righteousness" — the good land given by grace).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple bases, none purely meritocratic: (1) **Grace in election** — Deu 30:9 ("as he took delight in your fathers") — the delight in the fathers is prior to any merit; Jer 31:20's Ephraim-cherishing persists through rebuke — grace, not merit; (2) **Moral faithfulness** — Psa 37:23 ("when he delights in his way") — the person's way is what God delights in, making faithfulness a condition of received divine pleasure; Psa 51:6 ("you delight in truth in the inward being") — inward truthfulness as the condition; (3) **Covenantal relationship** — Isa 62:4 (God's Delight in Zion as the covenantal reversal of desolation); (4) **Christ's perfect pleasing** — Mat 3:17; 12:18 — the basis of God's ultimate eudokeo toward the Son is the Son's perfect correspondence to the Father; this becomes the basis for God's delight in all who are in Christ; (5) **Repentance** — Eze 18:23 ("I have no pleasure in the death of the wicked, but that the wicked turn from his way and live") — God's Delight toward the sinner is specifically conditioned on turn-and-live; his Delight toward life is the basis of the command to repent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple bases: (1) **Covenantal faithfulness** — the ni.cho.ach corpus: God's receptive Pleasure at worship depends on covenant-obedient offering (Lev 26:31 — withheld from unfaithful); the basis is obedient worship; (2) **Seeking his presence** — Psa 27:4 (one who asks and seeks after God receives the Pleasure of his beauty); (3) **Grace and character** — Psa 36:8 (the river of delights is lavishly given to those in God's house — gracious supply); Psa 90:17 (divine pleasantness asked to rest upon the community — grace); (4) **Restoration** — Eze 20:41 (God will accept the restored Israel as a pleasing aroma after scattering — restoration as the basis of resumed Pleasure).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple bases: (1) **Covenantal faithfulness** — Exo 34:10 ("before all your people I will do marvels… it is an awesome thing that I will do with you") — covenantal relationship as the basis; (2) **Steadfast love** — Psa 31:21 ("wondrously shown his steadfast love") — hesed as the inner motivation of God's wonder-acts; Psa 107:8, 15, 21, 31 (wondrous works to the children of man, grounds for thanking steadfast love) — steadfast love and wondrous works are paired; (3) **Purpose and sovereign plan** — Isa 25:1 ("plans formed of old, faithful and sure") — God's wonder-acts executed according to long-planned purpose; (4) **Restoration** — Eze 20:41 (God acting wondrously at the regathering — adjacent); Mic 7:15; Joel 2:26 — restoration as the basis of renewed wonder-acts.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Gospel relationship** — Act 16:34 (the jailer's Suffering-Joy arises immediately upon coming to faith in God — the basis is the new faith-relationship); (2) **Participation in Christ's suffering** — 1Pe 4:13 ("insofar as you share Christ's sufferings") — the basis is active participation in Christ's mission-suffering, not merely suffering in general; (3) **Covenant faithfulness and call** — Mat 5:12's context (persecution for righteousness' sake) and Luk 6:23's context (rejection for the Son of Man's sake) — the basis is faithful alignment with Christ under persecution; (4) **Faith in the unseen** — 1Pe 1:8 ("you believe in him and rejoice") — faith is both the basis and the enabling condition.

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

God's exultation over his people reveals his disposition as one of genuine relational delight — not merely governance or provision but a surging inner joy directed at his people. Jer 32:41's "with all my heart and all my soul" is the strongest constitutional language applied to God's inner disposition in the entire corpus: it locates his rejoicing at the deepest level of his inner being. Zep 3:17's pairing of exultation with love that quiets — "he will quiet you by his love; he will exult over you with loud singing" — shows exultation as the expression of God's deepest relational tenderness alongside his triumphant joy. God delights in his people.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

God's Joy-giving reveals: (1) **Relational investment** — Luk 15:7, 10 (heaven's joy over one repentant sinner — God's investment in individual persons' restoration produces his own inner joy); (2) **Fatherly desire for human flourishing** — Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength" — God intends his people to be strong through joy); Rom 15:13 ("may the God of hope fill you with all joy") — God desires abundance of joy for his people; (3) **Delight in covenant relationship** — Jer 32:41 ("I will rejoice in doing them good… with all my heart and all my soul") — God's Joy in doing good to his people is not reluctant duty but whole-hearted delight; (4) **Eschatological commitment** — the restoration-Joy passages (Isa 35:10; 51:11; Jer 31:13; Zec 8:19) reveal God's purpose to give everlasting Joy as the final state of his people.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

God's extension of Gladness as his character-goodness reveals: (1) **Constancy** — "his steadfast love endures forever" (ki-tov formula repeated) — God's goodness is not fluctuating but permanent and reliable; (2) **Generosity** — Psa 145:9 ("good to all, mercy over all he has made") — divine goodness extends universally, not selectively; (3) **Protective care** — Nah 1:7 ("a stronghold in the day of trouble") — God's goodness translates into refuge and protection; (4) **Covenantal fidelity** — Jos 21:45 ("not one word had failed") — divine goodness is demonstrated in complete promise-fulfilment; (5) **Instructive character** — Psa 25:8 ("good and upright… therefore he instructs sinners in the way") — divine goodness manifests as patient instruction toward the good path.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

God's extension of Delight reveals: (1) **Tender relational attachment** — Jer 31:20 (sha.a.shu.im persisting through rebuke; "my heart yearns for him") — God's Delight includes visceral yearning for the person; (2) **Purposeful favor** — 1Ki 10:9 (delighted in Solomon → set on the throne) — God's Delight is not merely affective but purposively active, producing exaltation; (3) **Life-orientation** — Eze 18:23; 33:11 ("no pleasure in the death of anyone… so turn, and live") — God's deepest Delight is oriented toward human life and restoration, not judgment; (4) **Faithful constancy** — Deu 30:9 ("as he took delight in your fathers") — divine Delight is not a new mood but a continuation of original covenantal pleasure; (5) **Unconditional grounding** — even where Delight is conditioned on the person's faithfulness (Psa 37:23), the ground is God's own prior Delight that makes faithfulness possible (Psa 37:4 — delight in the Lord produces the desires God gives).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Lavish generosity** — Psa 36:8's river of delights shows God as extravagant in his pleasantness-supply; (2) **Covenant faithfulness** — the ni.cho.ach corpus shows divine Pleasure as reliable and consistent toward those who worship rightly; (3) **Personal beauty** — Psa 27:4's no.am as God's own quality shows his disposition as inherently beautiful and agreeable — he is not merely useful but genuinely pleasant to encounter; (4) **Restorative orientation** — Eze 20:41's future-oriented acceptance shows God's disposition toward restored relationship as the ultimate goal; (5) **Eternal supply** — Psa 16:11's "forevermore" shows God's Pleasure-giving as permanently available, not exhausted.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Redemptive orientation** — the overwhelming weight of VCG-01 shows God's wonder-acts as redemptive: Exodus, conquest, healing, rescue at sea, restoration; his disposition is toward his people's salvation through extraordinary means; (2) **Exclusivity** — Psa 72:18; 86:10 ("who alone does wondrous things") — God's disposition to be the exclusive worker of genuine wonders reveals his jealousy for his own incomparable status; (3) **Exceeding generosity** — Psa 40:5 ("your wondrous deeds and your thoughts toward us; none can compare with you! They are more than can be told") — wonder-acts multiplied without limit; (4) **Pedagogical intent** — Exo 34:10 ("all the people among whom you are shall see the work of the Lord, for it is an awesome thing") — God extends wonders with the explicit purpose of being witnessed and acknowledged.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

God's extension of Suffering-Joy through the Spirit reveals: (1) **His presence with the suffering person** — the Spirit's production of agalliao within the suffering context means God is not absent in suffering but intensely present; (2) **His eschatological commitment** — the "reward in heaven" and "glory to be revealed" show God's disposition to honour the suffering of faithful witnesses with ultimate eschatological vindication; (3) **His desire for the inner life to transcend circumstances** — the Spirit's production of joy within suffering shows God's aim for the human inner being to be constituted by divine reality rather than circumstantial reality; (4) **His fatherly delight** — Luk 10:21's Jesus rejoicing in the Father's gracious will shows that Suffering-Joy at its most intense is the shared inner life between Father and Son that the Spirit also makes available to the human person.

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Not silent; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not silent; God-to-human Joy is among the most extensively evidenced directions in this corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Not silent; God-to-human Gladness is the dominant register of M04-L-VCG-01 and a major register of M04-O-VCG-04.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Not silent; God's Delight directed toward the human person is the most documented God-to-human inner-being characteristic in the M04 cluster.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Not silent; God-to-human Pleasure is documented across five registers.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Not silent; God's wonder-acts toward the human person are the dominant pattern of the entire VCG-01 corpus.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Not silent; God-to-human operation through the Spirit is the primary form of Suffering-Joy's most intense register.

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes — this is the dominant direction in the corpus. The vast majority of VCG-01's 58 verses show human exultation directed toward God: "my soul will rejoice in the Lord" (Psa 35:9); "I will greatly rejoice in the Lord; my soul shall exult in my God" (Isa 61:10); "yet I will rejoice in the Lord" (Hab 3:18); "exult in your name all the day" (Psa 89:16); "to God my exceeding joy" (Psa 43:4). The human-to-God direction is the primary mode of this characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes — this is the dominant direction in M04-B-VCG-05 (90 verses of God-directed psalmist and prophetic gladness) and throughout M04-C. The human-to-God direction includes: direct "rejoice in the Lord" commands (Psa 32:11; 97:12; Phili 4:4; 3:1); rejoicing in God's salvation as the psalmist's oriented movement (Psa 9:2; 14:7; 35:9; 53:6; 63:11; Isa 25:9; 61:10); the feast-joy before God at his sanctuary (Deu 12:7, 18; 16:11–15 — the spatial movement of Israel to the chosen place and the inner movement toward God); praise, thanksgiving, and prayer accompanying joy (Psa 100:2; Jer 33:11; Phili 4:4–6).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. (1) **Doxological movement** — the ki-tov praise declarations (Psa 100:5; 106:1 — "give thanks to the Lord, for he is good") are the human person's movement toward God in recognition of his goodness; the formula frames thanksgiving and praise as the inner movement prompted by Gladness-recognition; (2) **Seeking** — Lam 3:25–26 ("the Lord is good to those who wait for him, to the soul who seeks him") — seeking God is the human movement that positions the person to experience his goodness; (3) **Gratitude** — Ezr 3:11 ("for he is good, for his steadfast love endures forever toward Israel" — responsive praise at the temple foundation); Deu 8:10 ("you shall bless the Lord your God for the good land") — receiving the good land occasions the movement of blessing toward God; (4) **Trust** — the entire M04-O-VCG-04 register shows the human person trusting in God's good promises as a movement of the inner being toward him.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in M04-G and M04-H's upward registers: (1) **Affective upward movement** — Psa 37:4 ("delight yourself in the Lord") — commanded upward orientation of the inner being toward God as its object; Isa 58:14 ("you shall take delight in the Lord") — Delight as the human person's movement toward God; Job 22:26 (future delight in the Almighty); Job 27:10 (the hypocrite who will not delight in the Almighty — exposing the expected upward movement as absent); (2) **Delight in God's word as movement toward God** — Psa 119 series (delight in statutes, testimonies, commandments, law — all as God's self-expression); Rom 7:22 ("I delight in the law of God, in my inner being") — the innermost self moving toward God through his word; (3) **Obedience-Delight** (M04-M) — Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22 — the soul's movement toward what pleases God as the sustaining orientation of the inner person's upward relationship; (4) **Seeking God's presence as Delight** — Psa 73:28 ("it is good to be near God") — the human person's inner experience of divine nearness as the supreme good, motivating continued movement toward it; (5) **Neh 1:11** — "who delight to fear your name" — the soul's reverential Delight in God's name as the form of upward movement.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)
