Yes: (1) **Psa 27:4** — "one thing have I asked of the Lord, that will I seek after: that I may dwell in the house of the Lord… to gaze upon the beauty of the Lord" — the entire movement of the seeking person toward God is motivated by and culminates in Pleasure (gazing upon divine beauty); (2) **The ni.cho.ach worship acts** (M04-K-VCG-01) — the worshiper's act of offering correctly-prepared sacrifice is a movement toward God that produces the pleasing-aroma Pleasure relationship; human-to-God Pleasure operates through worship action; (3) **Psa 147:1** — "for it is good to sing praises to our God; for it is pleasant and a song of praise is fitting" — the pleasantness of praise as the experience of human worship-movement toward God; (4) **Psa 135:3** — "praise the Lord… for it is pleasant!" — pleasantness of worship as the felt quality of the human movement toward God in praise.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Wonder producing worship-movement** — the proclamatory corpus is consistently doxological: "sing to him, sing praises to him; tell of all his wondrous works" (1Ch 16:9) — Wonder moves the person toward God in praise; "I will give thanks to the Lord with my whole heart; I will recount all of your wonderful deeds" (Psa 9:1) — Wonder producing wholehearted Godward movement; (2) **Seeking to behold** — Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law") — Wonder-seeking in the law as movement toward God through his word; (3) **Contemplative movement** — Psa 119:27 ("make me understand the way of your precepts, and I will meditate on your wondrous works"); Psa 145:5 ("on your wondrous works, I will meditate") — sustained contemplative movement toward God through Wonder-meditation; (4) **Job's return** — Job 42:3 ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — Job's Wonder-humility as the restored posture of a person returned to right relationship with God.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Worship and prayer** — Luk 10:21 (Jesus' agalliao immediately moves into addressed prayer: "I thank you, Father") — Suffering-Joy is the inner state that generates worshipful movement toward the Father; Luk 1:47 (Mary's spirit exults "in God my Savior" — the exultation is directed toward God as its object); Act 2:26 (tongue rejoicing → "my flesh also will dwell in hope" — the movement toward trust in God); (2) **Continued faithful mission** — Act 5:41 (apostles' rejoicing → continued teaching — the movement toward God through faithful mission-action); (3) **Joyful endurance** — Heb 12:2 (Christ's joy-grounded endurance of the cross — the cross as the climactic movement toward the Father's purpose).

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Trust (Psa 13:5); uprightness of heart (Psa 32:11); seeking God (Psa 40:16; 70:4); waiting for God (Isa 25:9); love of God's salvation (Psa 40:16; 70:4); righteous living (Psa 68:3; 97:8). The characteristic's inner posture is not passive — it requires active orientation toward God through trust, seeking, and righteous alignment.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Inner postures that enable Joy toward God: (1) **Seeking** — Psa 40:16; 70:4 ("may all who seek you rejoice and be glad in you"); Psa 85:6 (revival → rejoicing "in you"); (2) **Trust** — Psa 33:21 ("our heart is glad in him, because we trust in his holy name"); (3) **Uprightness and righteousness** — Psa 32:11 ("rejoice, O righteous"); Psa 97:11 ("joy for the upright in heart"); (4) **Wholehearted devotion** — 2Ch 15:15 ("sworn with all their heart and had sought him with their whole desire"); (5) **Obedience** — 1Jo 3:22 paired with Gal 5:22 — the obedient life produces Spirit-joy; (6) **Faith in Christ** — Rom 15:13 ("joy and peace in believing"); Act 16:34 (joy because of faith in God).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The inner postures that enable human-to-God Gladness: (1) **Purity of heart** — Psa 73:1 ("those who are pure in heart" experience God's goodness toward them); (2) **Seeking and waiting** — Lam 3:25–26 (the soul who seeks, who waits quietly); (3) **Gratitude** — Deu 8:10 (eating and blessing God for the good land — gratitude as the posture); (4) **Trust in God's promise** — M04-O-VCG-04's covenantal gladness requires the inner act of trusting that God's good word will be fulfilled; (5) **Humility** — Deu 9:6 (receiving the good land as grace, not merit — the humble posture).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Wholeness / non-divided will** — Psa 37:4's "delight yourself in the Lord" presupposes an undivided orientation; Psa 73:25's exclusive desire ("nothing on earth I desire besides you") is the fullest form; (2) **Choosing what God chooses** — Isa 56:4 ("who choose the things that please me") — active volitional alignment; (3) **Fearing God** — Neh 1:11 ("delight to fear your name") — reverence as the inner posture that sustains Delight-in-God; (4) **Inward truthfulness** — Psa 51:6 ("you delight in truth in the inward being") — authentic interior honesty as the enabling condition for receiving God's Delight; (5) **Sabbath faithfulness** — Isa 58:13 (honoring the Sabbath → "you shall take delight in the Lord" — Isa 58:14) — Sabbath as the practised form of upward Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Single-minded seeking** — Psa 27:4 ("one thing have I asked") — the one thing focused on God's beauty enables receiving his Pleasure; (2) **Covenant obedience** — the ni.cho.ach corpus: correct, prescribed worship is the enabling posture; (3) **Faithfulness** — Job 36:11 ("if they listen and serve him, they complete their years in pleasantness") — listening and serving as the inner posture that enables Pleasure to be the quality of one's years; (4) **Willingness to praise** — Psa 147:1; 135:3 — the posture of genuine praise enabling the felt pleasantness of worship.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Attending and considering** — Job 37:14 ("stop and consider the wondrous works of God") — deliberate attention as the prerequisite; (2) **Wholehearted engagement** — Psa 9:1 ("with my whole heart") — half-hearted Wonder-movement toward God is insufficient; (3) **Humility and non-overreach** — Psa 131:1 ("my heart is not lifted up… I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me") — the humble not-overreaching posture as enabling genuine Wonder; (4) **Prior consecration** — Jos 3:5 ("consecrate yourselves, for tomorrow the Lord will do wonders") — moral preparedness enabling receptive Wonder; (5) **Memory-engagement** — Psa 77:11 (deliberate memory of the Lord's wonders as the inner strategy for Wonder-movement toward God through distress).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Faith in the unseen** — 1Pe 1:8 ("though you do not now see him, you believe") — faith as the inner posture that opens toward God and enables Suffering-Joy; (2) **Eschatological orientation** — the cognitive holding of future glory as the ground for present exultation; (3) **Identification with Christ** — 1Pe 4:13 (sharing Christ's sufferings as the posture that produces Suffering-Joy in the movement toward him); (4) **Humility before the Father's will** — Luk 10:21's "yes, Father, for such was your gracious will" — receptive humility toward divine sovereignty as the posture that enables the Spirit's rejoicing.

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

It reveals that exultation is the highest and most concentrated expression of the person's covenantal relationship with God — the inner being's fullest response to who God is. Psa 43:4's "God my exceeding joy" makes God himself the content of the exultation, not merely its object: the person does not rejoice at what God does but in God as the very source and substance of their deepest joy.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy directed toward God is the inner-being evidence of a right-ordered covenant relationship. Psa 43:4 ("God my exceeding joy") makes God himself the content of the person's deepest joy — the most complete expression of a relationship in which God is genuinely the person's supreme good. Deu 28:47's verdict that failing to serve "with joyfulness and gladness of heart" constitutes covenant unfaithfulness reveals that the quality of inner joy before God is the diagnostic of the covenant relationship's inner health. Joy toward God is not one response among many but the criterion of genuine relationship.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The human-to-God direction of Gladness is primarily doxological and trustful: it moves toward God in recognition of his character-goodness (the ki-tov praise) and in confident reliance on his promises (covenantal Gladness). This reveals a relationship structured around recognition and trust: the human person who genuinely gladdens in God's goodness has grasped something true about God's character that grounds a deep and stable relational posture.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Human Delight toward God reveals: (1) **The relationship's truest form** — Psa 73:25 ("nothing on earth I desire besides you") names the state of the person whose relationship with God is properly oriented — exclusivity of desire toward God; (2) **That God's law is loved, not merely obeyed** — Psa 1:2; 40:8; 119 series show the relationship characterized by pleasurable orientation toward God's word, not merely dutiful compliance; (3) **The sustainability of the relationship under adversity** — Psa 119:92 (Delight sustaining through affliction) shows that human Delight in God is what enables the relationship to hold under pressure; (4) **The convergence of will** — Psa 40:8 ("I delight to do your will") — human Delight toward God produces convergence of the human will with divine will; this is the deepest form of the relationship.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals: (1) **Relationship centred on beauty and pleasantness** — Psa 27:4 frames the entire relationship with God as oriented toward gazing on his beauty; the relationship is not merely duty but pleasure-in-God; (2) **Worship as a pleasure-exchange** — the ni.cho.ach structure shows worship as a genuine bidirectional pleasure relationship: the human offers rightly → divine Pleasure is evoked → the relationship is maintained pleasantly; (3) **The pleasantness of praise** — Psa 147:1; 135:3 show that the human person's movement toward God in praise is itself a pleasurable inner experience — worship is not merely correct but genuinely pleasant to those who engage it.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals: (1) **A relationship defined by asymmetric greatness** — the person who genuinely wonders at God has correctly perceived the infinite qualitative difference between themselves and God; Wonder is the relational posture of the creature acknowledging the Creator's incomprehensible superiority; (2) **A relationship sustained by memory** — Psa 77:11's deliberate return to God through remembered wonders shows the relationship maintained through deliberate memorial practice rather than continuous fresh experience; (3) **A relationship that produces proclamation** — the human-toward-God movement in Wonder does not stay private but moves through the mouth into communal declaration (1Ch 16:9, 24); (4) **A relationship of epistemological humility** — Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me, which I did not know" positions the restored relationship with God as marked by humble acknowledgment of the limits of one's own understanding.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The human-to-God direction of Suffering-Joy reveals that the deepest and most paradox-transcending form of closeness to God occurs through suffering rather than despite it: 1Pe 4:13 (sharing Christ's sufferings as the path to sharing his glory); Heb 12:2 (the cross as the path to the exaltation); Act 5:41 (being counted worthy to suffer for the name as the form of relationship-affirmation). The person who exults in suffering toward God has grasped a deeper truth about the divine-human relationship than the person who only exults when circumstances are good.

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Not silent; it is the primary direction.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not silent; human-to-God Joy is extensively evidenced as the characteristic's primary direction.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Not silent; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Human-to-God Delight is extensively documented; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Human-to-God Pleasure is evidenced through seeking, worship, and praise; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Human-to-God Wonder is extensively evidenced through the entire VCG-01 proclamatory tradition; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Human-to-God direction is evidenced throughout the agalliao corpus; not silent.

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, partially. VCG-03 (relational and natural gladness) contains Pro 23:24–25 (father's exultation over a righteous son; mother called to rejoice at her child's goodness). Isa 9:3 shows the people glad "as when they divide the spoil" — communal exultation that involves persons sharing in a collective triumph. Song 1:4 shows relational exultation directed toward the beloved king. Isa 66:10 calls "all who love Jerusalem" to rejoice with her.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, extensively. (1) **M04-B-VCG-04** — parental joy over wise children (Pro 10:1; 15:20; 23:24–25; 29:3; 29:6); Deu 24:5 (husband making wife glad — a legal provision for Joy directed toward a spouse); (2) **M04-D** — sunchairo throughout: the shepherd calling neighbours to co-rejoice (Luk 15:6, 9); co-rejoicing in the body (1Cor 12:26); Paul rejoicing with the Philippians (Phili 2:17–18); (3) **Pauline relational joy** (M04-C-VCG-03) — Paul's pastoral joy over communities (1Th 3:9; Phili 4:1; 1Th 2:19–20; 3Jo 3–4; Phili 2:2); (4) **News-bearing joy** — Luk 1:14 (Zechariah's joy to be shared with many at John's birth); Act 15:3 (Barnabas and Paul bringing great joy to the brothers through news of Gentile conversions); (5) **Act 2:46** — the community receiving food with glad and generous hearts, expressing outward-directed joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. (1) **Good words and news** — M04-O-VCG-01: Pro 12:25 ("a good word makes him glad") — the apt word extended by one person toward another; Pro 15:23 ("to make an apt answer is a joy to a man") — the speaker extends Gladness through speech; Isa 52:7's good-news herald brings Gladness to Zion; 2Sa 18:27's "good man comes with good news" — character and news combined in relational extension; (2) **Relational loyalty and goodness** — 1Sa 25:15 ("the men were very good to us") — David's men extending practical goodness to Nabal's servants; 1Sa 19:4 (Jonathan testifying of David's good deeds to Saul — relational advocacy); 1Sa 24:19 (Saul acknowledging David's relational goodness); (3) **Testimony of God's good hand** — Neh 2:18 (Nehemiah sharing the testimony of God's good hand, which motivates the community's resolve).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Interpersonal relational Delight** — 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan delighting much in David — extending protective affection despite paternal command); 1Sa 18:22 (Saul's claimed delight in David — extended relationally, though falsely); (2) **Paul's affectionate Delight** — 1Th 2:8 ("affectionately desirous of you, we were ready to share with you not only the gospel but also our own selves") — relational Delight extended as self-giving; (3) **Parental Delight in children** — Mic 1:16 (ta.a.nug — children of your delight); Jer 31:20 (God's sha.a.shu.im in Ephraim as parental model); (4) **Neighbour-relational Delight** — Pro 27:10 (the reliable nearby neighbour as better — relational pleasantness extended through proximity and care); (5) **Diplomatic relational Delight** — the M04-H-VCG-03 "do as it pleases you" formula: one person extending the authority of their Delight to another, a form of relational generosity.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Speech-Pleasure extended** — Pro 16:24 (gracious words extended toward another, producing sweetness in their soul and health in their body); Pro 15:26 (gracious words pure — extended as morally wholesome Pleasure); Psa 45:1 (the psalmist's pleasing theme extended toward the king in praise-poetry); (2) **Relational pleasantness** — Psa 133:1's brotherly unity — each person in the community extending pleasantness to the others through harmonious living; (3) **Tactile pleasantness extended** — 2Sa 1:24 (Saul clothing the daughters of Israel luxuriously in scarlet — extending material Pleasure outward); (4) **Song of Songs** — Song 1:16; 7:6 — mutual pleasantness extended between the lovers; each appreciates and extends the pleasure of the other's presence.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Generational transmission** — Psa 78:4 ("we will not hide them from their children, but tell to the coming generation the glorious deeds of the Lord… and the wonders that he has done") — the act of extending Wonder to the next generation by telling them of God's wondrous deeds; (2) **Nations-directed proclamation** — 1Ch 16:24 ("declare his glory among the nations, his marvellous works among all the peoples"); Psa 96:3 — extending Wonder outward toward peoples who have not yet encountered it; (3) **2Sa 1:26** (pa.la — Jonathan's love as "extraordinary") — the experience of extraordinary depth in relationship that one person extends to another; David receiving the wonder-quality of Jonathan's love; (4) **Communal worship** — Psa 89:5 ("let the heavens praise your wonders, O Lord") — the heavenly assembly's communal Wonder-extension.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: Act 16:34 (the jailer's rejoicing encompasses his entire household — the characteristic radiates from the newly-believing person into the communal relational network); Act 5:41 (the apostles rejoicing together — the characteristic is shared among the community, extending from each to the others in the shared experience); Luk 1:44 (the baby in Elizabeth's womb leaping for joy at Mary's greeting — Suffering-Joy radiating across the relational encounter of two pregnant women in vulnerable circumstances); Luk 15:6, 9 (M04-D adjacent — the shepherd/woman calling neighbours to co-rejoice, but the Spirit-joy quality of the lost-found is adjacent to this characteristic's intensity).

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence identifies: righteous character in the one toward whom exultation is directed (Pro 23:24 — "the father of the righteous will greatly rejoice"; the son's righteousness is the condition for the father's joy); love of the other (Song 1:4; Isa 66:10 — "all who love her"). Exultation directed toward another person appears to require genuine relational attachment and recognition of real worth in the other.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

(1) **Love for the other** — 1Cor 13:6 (love's joy rejoices with the truth; it is other-directed); 3Jo 4 ("no greater joy than to hear that my children are walking in the truth" — joy rooted in love for the other's flourishing); (2) **Genuine relational investment** — Phile 7 ("I have derived much joy and comfort from your love, my brother, because the hearts of the saints have been refreshed through you") — the other's active love toward others produces joy in the observer; (3) **Generosity** — 2Cor 8:2 (the Macedonians' joy in poverty overflowing into generous giving — a joy that produces outward extension); (4) **Recognition of goodness in the other** — 2Cor 7:4 (joy overflowing in Paul's affliction because of the Corinthians' response); (5) **Solidarity in suffering** — Phili 2:17–18 (Paul and Philippians co-rejoicing across shared sacrifice).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Moral integrity** — the good deeds that occasion relational Gladness (1Sa 25:15; 19:4) require prior inner goodness in the one who gives; (2) **Discernment** — Pro 15:23 ("apt answer") — the ability to say the right thing at the right time requires the evaluative-gladness faculty operating accurately; (3) **Truthfulness** — Pro 27:5 ("better is open rebuke than hidden love") — genuine extension of Gladness sometimes requires honest confrontation rather than comfortable flattery; (4) **Trust-witness** — Neh 2:18 (Nehemiah's testimony of God's good hand) — having personally experienced divine goodness enables genuine witness that extends Gladness to others.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Prior Delight in God** — Jer 31:20 as the divine model: God's Delight in Ephraim flows from his own character of steadfast love; the human extension of genuine Delight in others is analogously enabled by prior right orientation of the will; (2) **Genuine affection** — 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan's "much delight" — the intensity of personal affection as the prerequisite for protective action); 1Th 2:8 (Paul's affectionate desire as the enabling condition for self-sharing); (3) **Honesty** — contrast with 1Sa 18:22 (Saul's false claimed Delight) — the genuine extension requires that the inner disposition actually exists; (4) **Relational stability** — Pro 27:10 (the nearby neighbour's value proven through crisis) — consistent presence as the form of relational Delight's extension.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Inner pleasantness of character** — the person who extends genuine pleasant speech (Pro 16:24) must have an inward purity (Pro 15:26 — "gracious words are pure") — the inner state of purity enables the extension of genuine Pleasure; (2) **Genuine appreciation of the other** — Song 1:16; 7:6 — the lover's genuine delight in the beloved's beauty enables the pleasantness to be authentically extended; (3) **Harmonious inner orientation** — Psa 133:1's brotherly unity requires each person to be inwardly harmoniously oriented toward the community; (4) **Wisdom** — Pro 3:17's wisdom-pleasantness — the wise person's life naturally extends pleasantness to those around them.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Prior personal Wonder** — the person who has genuinely experienced Wonder at God's acts can extend it to others; Psa 71:17's "from my youth you have taught me, and I still proclaim your wondrous deeds" shows sustained personal Wonder as the basis for sustained proclamatory extension; (2) **Generational faithfulness** — Psa 78:4's "we will not hide them from their children" implies an active decision not to interrupt the chain of Wonder-extension; (3) **Worship-community membership** — the Tell-Remember-Meditate tradition presupposes a worshipping community that sustains and transmits Wonder as a communal practice; (4) **Knowledge of God's acts** — 1Ch 16:12 ("remember the wondrous works") — knowing the wonders is the precondition for declaring them.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Genuine Spirit-produced agalliao in the giver** — the jailer's extension to his household requires that the joy is real in him first; (2) **Shared faith context** — Act 5:41 (the apostles' shared joy in persecution is enabled by their shared faith-commitment); (3) **Love for those to whom it extends** — Act 16:34's household-encompassing joy requires relational investment; Luk 1:44's joy across Elizabeth and Mary requires the bond of kinship and shared vocation.

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence does not directly address this. The implication of VCG-03 is that the parent who exults in their righteous child has themselves cultivated the capacity for exultation — the father's joy at righteousness suggests he values righteousness, which requires his own moral formation. But the evidence does not make this explicit.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence implies: (1) **First received God's Joy** — the feast-joy (M04-B-VCG-01) must first be produced by divine blessing before it can overflow into communal sharing; Jer 32:41 (God's Joy over Israel precedes and enables Israel's Joy); (2) **Rightly-oriented inner life** — 1Cor 13:6 (love as the precondition of rightly-directed Joy extension — the person who rejoices with the truth must first love the truth); (3) **Spirit-filled** — Act 13:52 (filled with joy and the Holy Spirit — the Spirit's filling enables the joy that then radiates); (4) **Wholehearted** — 2Ch 15:15 (wholehearted seeking as the precondition for the joy that then unites the community). The person cannot genuinely give Joy toward others without first having received it in right relationship with God.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The evidence implies: (1) **Moral formation** — the person who gives good evaluative judgment (Jethro in Exo 18:17; Naomi in Rut 2:22) must have the formed evaluative faculty; (2) **Experience of God's goodness** — Nehemiah's testimony (Neh 2:18) presupposes his own experience of God's good hand; (3) **Character goodness** — 1Sa 25:3 (Abigail's discernment enabling her relational goodness) — inner character is the prerequisite for extended relational Gladness; (4) **Wisdom** — the wisdom-comparative evaluations (M04-L-VCG-03) presuppose a formed wisdom that can correctly value wisdom above gold.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The evidence implies: (1) **Genuine Delight in God first** — Psa 37:4 (delight in the Lord producing aligned desires) — the person rightly ordered toward God can extend genuine relational Delight; (2) **Known parental/divine cherishing** — Jer 31:20 (God's cherishing as the model for the human parental Delight in children); the one who has been genuinely delighted in (by God, by a parent) has the inner pattern from which to give Delight genuinely to others; (3) **Law internalized** — Psa 40:8 (law within the heart) — the person formed by law-Delight has the moral orientation enabling them to rightly identify and extend Delight appropriately.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Wisdom dwelling in the heart** — Pro 2:10's "wisdom will come into your heart" enables the Pleasure in knowledge that can then be extended to others in wise speech (Pro 16:24); (2) **Prior experience of divine Pleasure** — Psa 27:4's one who gazes on God's beauty has received the deepest Pleasure and can then extend pleasantness in praise (Psa 45:1's overflow); (3) **Genuine appreciation of beauty** — the lover in Song of Songs who genuinely experiences the beloved as pleasant (Song 7:6) can extend genuine appreciative Pleasure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **A genuine encounter with divine Wonder** — Psa 107:24 ("they saw the deeds of the Lord, his wondrous works in the deep") — direct perceptive encounter with divine wonders; (2) **Formed memory** — 1Ch 16:12; Psa 77:11; 105:5 — the Wonder-tradition must be internalised in memory before it can be extended to others; (3) **Epistemological humility** — Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me" — the person who has recognised the limits of their own knowledge can genuinely give Wonder without distorting it with false comprehension; (4) **Consecrated inner life** — Jos 3:5 — the morally prepared person can both receive and extend Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The evidence implies: (1) **Prior Spirit-filling** — the agalliao form requires being filled with or led by the Spirit; (2) **Prior coming-to-faith** — Act 16:34's jailer can only extend the joy to his household after he himself has believed; (3) **Prior experience of the suffering-paradox** — the apostles (Act 5:41) can extend the characteristic because they have themselves navigated the paradox of suffering-in-mission. One cannot genuinely give what one has not genuinely received.

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The giving direction is partially evidenced (VCG-03, Song 1:4, Isa 66:10) but not elaborated. The primary giving direction in the corpus is God-to-human rather than human-to-human.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not silent; human-to-human Joy extension is extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Giving direction is evidenced through multiple channels (good words, good deeds, good testimony); not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Giving direction is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Giving direction is evidenced through speech, communal harmony, and relational appreciation; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Giving direction through generational transmission and missional proclamation is the defining characteristic of VCG-01's corpus; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Giving direction is evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

In the divine-to-human direction: the people receive God's exultation over them (Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41), and the effect of knowing God exults over them appears to generate responsive exultation in them. Deu 30:9's promise that God will "again take delight in prospering you" implies the people's experience of being the object of divine delight. In the human-to-human direction: Pro 23:24–25 implies the righteous son's awareness of his parents' joy; Isa 66:10 implies Jerusalem receiving the solidarity-exultation of those who love her.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. (1) **Received from news** — Luk 1:14 (Zechariah will have joy; many will rejoice at John's birth); Act 15:3 (great joy brought to the brothers); Act 15:31 (rejoicing at the encouraging letter); (2) **Received from community** — Phile 20 ("refresh my heart in Christ") — Paul receiving joy from Philemon's response; 2Cor 7:13 (Paul's joy increased by hearing of Titus's refreshment); 1Th 3:9 (Paul's overflowing joy at the Thessalonians' faithfulness); (3) **Received from a person's return** — Act 12:14 (Rhoda's joy at Peter's voice); Phili 2:28 (Philippians' joy at seeing Epaphroditus); 2Ti 1:4 (Paul longing to be filled with joy at seeing Timothy).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. (1) **Received through good news** — Pro 12:25 (the weighed-down heart receives gladness from a good word); Pro 15:30 (bones refreshed by good news received); Isa 39:8 (Hezekiah receiving Isaiah's word as good); Gen 40:16 (baker receiving Joseph's interpretation as favorable); 2Sa 18:27 (David's expectant reception of the runner's good news); (2) **Received through testimony** — Neh 2:18 (the people's inner resolve stirred by receiving Nehemiah's testimony of God's good hand); (3) **Received as inner wellbeing through God's acts** — 1Sa 16:23 (Saul receiving inner refreshment through David's music); 1Sa 11:9 (men of Jabesh receiving the good news of deliverance); (4) **Received as declared blessedness** — makarismos (Rom 4:6, 9 — blessedness declared over Abraham and received by faith).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Received divine Delight** — the dominant instance: Psa 18:19 (rescue received because God delighted in David); 1Ki 10:9 (throne received because God delighted in Solomon); Isa 62:4 (new name and covenantal restoration received from God's Delight); (2) **Received human relational Delight** — 1Sa 18:22 (David told the king delights in you — whether genuine or false); 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan's Delight received by David as protection); 1Th 2:8 (the Thessalonians receiving Paul's self-giving from his relational Delight); (3) **Received consolation-Delight** — Psa 94:19 (soul cheered by God's consolations — sha.a received into the overwhelmed inner being); (4) **Received parental Delight** — Mic 1:16's children as "children of your delight" implicitly receive the parent's tender attachment; (5) **Received obedience-pleasing** — 1Jo 3:22 (prayers answered as the received consequence of pleasing God through obedience).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Received relational pleasantness** — 2Sa 1:26 (David receiving Jonathan's pleasantness; the quality of Jonathan's companionship was a Pleasure received by David's inner being); Song 1:16; 7:6 (the lover receiving the beloved's pleasantness); (2) **Received speech-Pleasure** — Pro 16:24 (gracious words received by the soul — an inner being receiving pleasant speech from another); Pro 2:10's "pleasant to your soul" implies a received quality; (3) **Received material pleasantness** — 2Sa 1:24 (daughters of Israel receiving the luxury of Saul's scarlet and gold); Jer 51:34 (Jerusalem's delicacies received — and then consumed by the enemy); (4) **Received communal Pleasure** — Psa 133:1 (each brother receiving the pleasantness of the unified community).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Received from the worshipping community** — the entire VCG-01 Tell-Remember tradition is a received-tradition: "we will tell to the coming generation" (Psa 78:4) — the coming generation receives Wonder through being told; "he has caused his wondrous works to be remembered" (Psa 111:4) — God ensures the Wonder is receivable; (2) **Received from God directly** — Psa 119:18's "open my eyes, that I may behold" — Wonder received as a God-given perceptive capacity; (3) **2Sa 1:26** — David receiving Jonathan's extraordinary love; (4) **Mar 1:27** — the crowd receiving the wonder-shock of Jesus' authoritative exorcism; **Mar 10:24** — disciples receiving amazement from Jesus' teaching.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: Act 16:34 (the jailer's household receives the characteristic from the jailer's faith-joy — they all rejoice together); Luk 1:44 (Elizabeth's baby leaps for joy at receiving the Spirit-gladness transmitted through Mary's greeting — the most physicality-affirming reception in the corpus); the communities addressed in Mat 5:12 and 1Pe 4:13 receive the characteristic through apostolic command that channels the Spirit's work. Joh 8:56 (Abraham's agalliao at Christ's day coming) — reception through prophetic-faith perception of a future reality.

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Receptivity to God's exultation over the person is enabled by covenant faithfulness and openness to relational reality; Deu 28:63 shows that covenant-breaking forfeits the experience of being delighted in. Exultation cannot be received by a person who has placed themselves outside the covenant relation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Enabling conditions: (1) **Love for the giver** — the joy at a beloved person's return (Peter, Epaphroditus, Timothy) requires relational investment; (2) **Shared values** — 2Jo 4 (the elder rejoices greatly to find children walking in truth — shared commitment to truth enables the joy); (3) **Relational openness** — 2Co 7:13 (Titus's spirit refreshed → Paul's joy increased — the openness of the relational bond enables the transmission). Blocking conditions: (1) **Broken relationship** — 2Cor 2:3 (Paul's expected joy at the Corinthians' reception of him is prevented by their unresolved conflict); (2) **Wrong object** — joy received from a person toward wrong ends (Haman's friends encouraging him toward Mordecai's destruction — Est 5:14) is morally corrupt reception.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Enabling: humility, accuracy of evaluation, openness to hearing (the baker's openness in Gen 40:16; the men of Jabesh's readiness in 1Sa 11:9). Blocking: fear (Num 14:3 — Israel unable to receive the good land as good because fear distorted their evaluation); self-reference (Hezekiah's partial reception in Isa 39:8); despair (Jon 4:3, 8 — extreme anguish blocking any gladness-reception); idolatrous orientation (Jer 44:17 — false attribution blocking accurate receipt of God's genuine goodness).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Enabling: inward truthfulness (Psa 51:6); faithfulness in the way (Psa 37:23); faith and fearing God (Neh 1:11); turning from evil (Eze 18:23; 33:11 — repentance as the condition for receiving the Delight of God's orientation toward life). Blocking: hardened ears (Jer 6:10 — the person who takes no pleasure in God's word cannot receive divine Delight in their hearing); hollow ritual (Isa 1:11; Heb 10:6–8 — the person whose inner orientation is external-ritual-only does not engage God's delight; it remains withheld); shrinking back (Heb 10:38 — faith-collapse blocking divine pleasure); corrupt Delight (Isa 66:3; 2Th 2:12 — the soul formed around wrong objects cannot receive God's genuine Delight, which requires inward truthfulness).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Enabling: wisdom in the heart (Pro 2:10); seeking God's presence (Psa 27:4); openness to gracious speech (Pro 22:18 — "pleasant if you keep them within you"); receptivity within right relationships. Blocking: covenant unfaithfulness (Lev 26:31 — God will not smell the pleasing aromas); folly (Pro 19:10 — luxury unfit for fools); moral corruption (Job 20:18 — wicked getting no enjoyment from profits); judgment/curse (Deu 28:54, 56 — pleasure capacity destroyed).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Enabling: attending and considering (Job 37:14); opening the eyes (Psa 119:18 — petition for divine enabling); consecration (Jos 3:5); wholehearted engagement (Psa 9:1). Blocking: forgetting (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful"; Psa 78:11 — "forgot his works"); not considering (Psa 106:7 — "did not consider your wondrous works"); self-sufficient wisdom (Isa 29:14 — wisdom-accumulation that stops perceiving God's acts as extraordinary); dark wonder misapplied (Rev 17:7 — angel correcting John's misapplied marvelling).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Enabling: faith (1Pe 1:8); Spirit-openness (Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6); shared participation in suffering-mission (1Pe 4:13). Blocking: Joh 5:35 (the crowds' willingness to rejoice for a while in John's light — the agalliao was real but shallow; blocking came from lack of depth in the faith-commitment); M04-F's ba.lag pattern (extreme grief overwhelming the capacity to receive even the fragile comfort).

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence does not directly address this. No passage shows a person encountering God's exultation over them and remaining unmoved or hardened. The evidence is silent on failed reception of divine exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence implies a state of relational closure or moral obstruction. Haman's inability to receive genuine joy even from his wife's counsel (Est 5:9–14 — his gladness is immediately destroyed by Mordecai's presence) shows that his inner orientation toward pride and honour-rivalry prevents reception of stable joy from any relational source. The broader inverted-joy corpus (Eze 25:6; Lam 5:15) shows communities unable to receive joy because their inner orientation is toward malice or desolation.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Distress and distorted evaluation: Num 14:3 (fear and complaint); Jon 4:3, 8 (despair declaring death preferable); Ecc 6:3 (soul not satisfied with life's good things — the person unable to receive the good that is actually present remains in a state of inner dissatisfaction). The common thread is the inner faculty that cannot accurately perceive genuine goodness when it is offered.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

M04-H-VCG-04 provides the primary evidence: (1) **Closed and alienated** — Jer 6:10 (uncircumcised ear, closed to God's word — the person sealed against receiving God's Delight through his word); (2) **Under judgment** — Isa 65:12 (choosing what God did not delight in → sword); Heb 10:38 (God's soul has no pleasure → the person under divine non-pleasure); (3) **Spiritually empty** — the person who "delights to seek God" (Isa 58:2) but without moral reality is performing religious desire without genuine inner Delight reception — the divine pleasure remains unengaged; (4) **Deceived** — Rev 13:3; 17:8 (the world marveling at the beast — receiving a counterfeit Delight object while remaining sealed against the genuine).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Unfit reception** — Pro 19:10 (the fool experiencing luxury as unfitting — the inner being constitutionally misaligned with the Pleasure it encounters); (2) **Blocked enjoyment** — Job 20:18 (the wicked man prevented from enjoying his profits — encountering material Pleasure but unable to receive it as genuine enjoyment); (3) **False reception** — Pro 9:17 (stolen bread appearing pleasant — the person receives what feels pleasant but is not genuinely so; the inner being is deceived); (4) **Grief at loss** — 2Sa 1:26 (David's distress upon losing Jonathan's pleasantness — the memory of received Pleasure intensifying the grief of its loss).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Hard-hearted and rebellious** — Neh 9:17 (wonder-failure → stiffened neck → rebellion); Psa 78:32 ("despite his wonders, they did not believe") — unbelief despite encountering the marvellous; (2) **Spiritually forgetful** — Psa 78:11; 106:7 — forgetting rather than denial; the inner being simply does not register the Wonder; (3) **Unchanged** — Psa 78:32 (sinned still despite wonders) — the wonder was present but produced no inner transformation because it was not genuinely received; (4) **Open to misapplication** — Rev 17:6, 7 — John marvels greatly at the harlot, which the angel immediately corrects; the person whose Wonder-capacity is not rightly anchored to God's acts alone can receive wrong objects.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

M04-F provides the primary evidence: Job 9:27 (the considered attempt at ba.lag immediately collapsing under the weight of suffering — the person is in a state of grief so severe that even the attempt at inner brightening fails); Jer 8:18 ("my joy is gone; grief is upon me; my heart is sick within me") — total absence of the characteristic, leaving the person in heartsickness. Joh 5:35 (the crowds who cannot receive the deeper agalliao of persevering faith remain with a transient surface-rejoicing that cannot hold under pressure — they encounter and partially receive but not in its full paradox-sustaining form).

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Receiving is partially evidenced (divine-to-human receiving implied in Zep 3:17; Deu 30:9); failed reception is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Receiving direction is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Receiving direction is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Receiving direction is the dominant narrative in M04-H-VCG-02; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Receiving direction is the dominant register of M04-J; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Receiving direction is evidenced through community-reception and individual perceptive encounter; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Receiving direction is evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. Exultation within the covenant community is the dominant pattern — the Psalms' exultation is always within the context of Israel's covenant relationship with YHWH. The one exception that crosses relational distance is Exo 18:9 (Jethro, a Midianite priest, rejoices at hearing of God's acts for Israel) — a non-Israelite exulting in YHWH's saving acts for another's people. This suggests exultation can occur across covenantal distance when the object (God's character and acts) transcends covenantal membership.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Joy within existing bonds is more readily transmitted and completed: the sunchairo passages (M04-D) presuppose existing relational bonds in the community (shepherd's neighbours, body members, Paul and Philippians); 2Jo 12 explicitly argues that the joy of existing fellowship reaches its completeness only in face-to-face meeting — relational distance limits Joy's completeness. Across relational distance: Act 15:3 (Barnabas and Paul bringing joy across geographical distance through news) — Joy can cross relational distance through news-bearing but with less immediate impact. The Johannine emphasis on face-to-face completion (2Jo 12; 3Jo 14) suggests that Joy's fullest relational form requires proximity.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The good-news and good-word register (M04-O-VCG-01) can operate across relational distance — Pro 25:25 ("like cold water to a thirsty soul, so is good news from a far country") explicitly affirms that Gladness through good news reaches across geographical distance. The covenantal Gladness (M04-O-VCG-04 — God's promises) is inherently non-proximate — it involves trusting a word not yet fulfilled. The relational-evaluative Gladness (M04-L-VCG-02 — Ruth's love, David's men's goodness) requires existing relational bonds to be evident and assessed.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The relational-delight instances (M04-N; M04-H-VCG-02) are predominantly within existing bonds: Jer 31:20 (God's Delight in Ephraim — the covenantal parent-child bond); 1Sa 19:1 (Jonathan and David — existing friendship bond); Mic 1:16 (parental bond); 1Th 2:8 (Paul and the Thessalonians — apostolic-community bond). The diplomatic-preference idiom (M04-H-VCG-03) operates across hierarchical and political relationships where existing bonds of authority structure the Delight-reference. Psa 73:25 and Psa 37:4's Delight in God operate within the covenantal bond. The evidence suggests Delight is primarily bond-internal: it is sustained and expressed within existing relational contexts rather than extending primarily across relational distance.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

M04-J's relational pleasantness is primarily bond-internal: Psa 133:1 (brothers dwelling together), 2Sa 1:26 (the deep friendship of David and Jonathan), Song 1:16; 7:6 (the beloved relationship). The speech-Pleasure (Pro 16:24) can operate across relational distance but is most effective within bonds of mutual respect. The ni.cho.ach worship-Pleasure operates within the covenantal relationship. The cross-boundary instance: Num 15:14 ("if a stranger is sojourning with you… and he wishes to offer a food offering, with a pleasing aroma to the Lord, he shall do as you do") — the worship-Pleasure relationship is extended to include resident foreigners who observe the same ritual conditions.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder operates across both: (1) **Within the covenant community** — the primary VCG-01 context is Israel's internal worship and memory tradition (the Psalms, Chronicles); (2) **Across national boundaries** — 1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3 ("declare his glory among the nations, his marvellous works among all the peoples") — Wonder extends missionally outward to all peoples; Exo 34:10 ("all the people among whom you are shall see the work of the Lord") — the witness of Wonder is explicitly intended for surrounding nations; (3) **2Ch 26:15** — Uzziah's fame spreading "far" because he was marvellously helped — wonder-acts creating a reputation that extends across geographical distance.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Act 16:34's household-encompassing joy shows the characteristic radiating most immediately through existing relational bonds (family). Luk 1:44 (Spirit-joy communicated across the intimate encounter of kinswomen) confirms existing-bond primacy. Mat 5:12 and 1Pe 4:13 address communities of faith under persecution — existing bonds of shared faith. No evidence of Suffering-Joy operating specifically across relational distance or strangers in this corpus.

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

It crosses covenantal boundaries in at least one clear instance (Jethro, Exo 18:9) and in the cosmic-rejoicing passages (Psa 96:11; 97:1 — the whole earth and its coastlands called to rejoice). The eschatological passages (Isa 66:10 calling "all who love Jerusalem") also suggest a scope broader than ethnic Israel. Exultation is covenantally grounded but not covenantally restricted in its ultimate scope.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy crosses covenantal boundaries: Luk 2:10 — "good news of great joy that will be for all the people" — the gospel joy is for all peoples; Act 13:48 (Gentiles rejoicing at the word of eternal life — covenantal outsiders receiving gospel Joy); Psa 67:4 ("let the nations be glad and sing for joy") — all nations called to Joy; the cosmic-rejoicing passages (Psa 96:11; 97:1) call all creation to Joy. The Deuteronomic feast-joy includes sojourners and the vulnerable (Deu 16:11, 14) — crossing social and ethnic boundaries within Israel. Joy is covenantally grounded but universally offered in its eschatological fullness.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness crosses covenantal boundaries: Exo 18:17 (Jethro, a Midianite, exercising accurate evaluative-gladness toward Moses); Rut 2:22 (Naomi assessing Ruth's best course — a Moabite within Israel's covenant community); 2Sa 18:27 (Achish's moral assessment of David's blamelessness — a Philistine king exercising the evaluative-gladness faculty). The evaluative-gladness faculty is not covenantally restricted; it is a human-image-bearing capacity that operates wherever persons make moral assessments. The doxological and covenantal registers are more specifically covenant-shaped.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight crosses covenantal boundaries in specific instances: (1) **M04-H-VCG-03's diplomatic idiom** — non-Israelite kings (Abimelech — Gen 20:15; Achish — 1Sa 29:6) and non-covenant contexts (the Esther/Nehemiah court of Persia) use the Delight-vocabulary for practical preference — the capacity for directed inner pleasure is pan-human; (2) **1Th 2:8** (Paul's Delight in Gentile believers) — crosses the Jew-Gentile boundary through the new covenant; (3) **Rom 15:26–27** (Macedonia and Achaia's Delight in contributing to Jerusalem's poor) — cross-ethnic new-covenant Delight. The corrupt register (M04-P) crosses any boundary — Eze 23:12's lustful Delight in Assyrians crosses national and covenant lines destructively.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The worship-Pleasure (ni.cho.ach) is explicitly bounded by covenant: Lev 26:31 (withheld from the unfaithful); Eze 20:41 (restored after regathering). However, Num 15:14 shows the worship-Pleasure accessible to any who follow the prescribed form, crossing ethnic boundaries. The relational-Pleasure register (M04-J) is not covenant-restricted — the pleasantness of wisdom's ways (Pro 3:17), gracious speech (Pro 16:24), and communal harmony (Psa 133:1) are available wherever wisdom is practiced and genuine agreeableness exists.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

No — Wonder crosses covenantal boundaries in the missional proclamation register. Psa 107:24's seafarers who saw God's wondrous works in the deep are not necessarily Israelites — the sea-rescue wonders in Psa 107 are available to all who encounter divine rescue. Exo 34:10's "all the people among whom you are" explicitly includes non-Israelites as witnesses. The marvellous works in VCG-02's "is anything too hard for the Lord?" (Gen 18:14; Jer 32:17, 27) are directed at universal divine capability, not covenantal restriction.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The agalliao corpus is primarily new-covenant: the characteristic in its Spirit-enabled form operates within the covenant community of faith (the persecuted disciples, the apostles, the Petrine communities). Act 16:34 (the Philippian jailer — a Roman, not an Israelite) shows the characteristic crossing covenantal-ethnic boundaries: Suffering-Joy is given through faith regardless of covenant background. Joh 8:56 (Abraham's anticipatory agalliao) is OT-covenant-located but anticipates Christ's day — making it typologically covenant-crossing.

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The scope is ultimately universal — cosmic rejoicing (Psa 96:11; 97:1; 1Ch 16:31; Isa 49:13) calls the whole created order to exult. But the primary and most specified locus is within the covenant community (Israel, Zion, the righteous). The characteristic moves from the individual soul (Psa 35:9), through the community (Psa 32:11; 48:11; Zec 9:9), to the cosmos (Psa 97:1), and finally to God himself (Zep 3:17; Jer 32:41) — a concentric relational scope.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy has the widest relational scope of any characteristic in M04: from the individual heart (Psa 4:7), through the household (Deu 12:7 — "you and your households"), the community (Neh 12:43), the nation (Est 8:17 — "gladness and joy among the Jews"), all peoples (Luk 2:10), and all creation (Psa 96:11; Isa 55:12 — mountains and trees), to God himself (Zep 3:17; Luk 15:7). The characteristic has a concentrically-expanding relational scope that reaches its fullness in the eschatological wedding of the Lamb (Rev 19:7).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness has a broad but ordered relational scope: (1) **Universal** — Psa 145:9 ("good to all") — divine goodness extends universally; (2) **Covenantal primary** — the ki-tov traditions, the good-hand narratives, and the promise-fulfilment texts are Israel-centred; (3) **Personal and relational** — the good-word and relational-evaluation registers operate at the individual and communal level; (4) **Cross-boundary** — the evaluative faculty operates wherever persons make moral assessments (Jethro, Ruth, Achish). The scope is ordered from divine goodness (universal) → covenantal community → individual relational → cross-boundary.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight's scope is: (1) **Primary**: the most intimate bonds — parental, covenantal, friendship; (2) **Hierarchical**: the diplomatic-preference idiom throughout historical books shows Delight structuring all hierarchical relationships (king-subject, captor-captive, general-army); (3) **Universal at the base level**: the human capacity for directed inner pleasure is evidenced across all human relationships; (4) **Eschatologically inclusive**: Isa 62:4 and Mal 3:12 show the scope expanding to encompass the whole restored community as the object of divine Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Scope: (1) **Most intimate bonds** (primary) — David-Jonathan, Song lovers, brotherly unity; (2) **Community** — Psa 133:1's communal pleasantness; (3) **Covenantal-inclusive** — Num 15:14's extension to resident foreigners; (4) **Eschatological** — Psa 16:11 and Eze 20:41's future-oriented Pleasure extending to all the restored community.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder has the widest relational scope of any M04 characteristic: (1) Within Israel (primary); (2) Extending to surrounding nations through witness (Exo 34:10; 1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3); (3) To all peoples universally (Psa 107's sea-narrative); (4) To the heavenly assembly (Psa 89:5 — "let the heavens praise your wonders"); (5) Eschatologically — Isa 29:14's "wonder upon wonder" reaching all who encounter God's final acts. Wonder's scope is universal and trans-generational.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy's relational scope is: (1) **Primary**: the Spirit-filled faith community (the persecuted disciples, apostles, NT epistolary communities); (2) **Cross-ethnic through faith**: Act 16:34; (3) **Household-encompassing**: Act 16:34's household (the primary social unit); (4) **Anticipatory-historical**: Joh 8:56 (Abraham's faith-joy reaching across millennia). The scope is primarily eschatologically-determined rather than ethnically-bounded: whoever shares in Christ's suffering and faith-orientation participates.

---

##### T4.5.4 — If the evidence is silent on relational boundaries, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Not silent; relational scope is evidenced across multiple registers.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Relational scope is among the most thoroughly evidenced features of this characteristic; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Relational scope is evidenced across all levels; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Relational scope is evidenced at multiple levels; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Relational scope is evidenced from intimate bonds through community to covenantal inclusion; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Relational scope from covenant community to universal proclamation is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Relational scope is evidenced as primarily faith-community but not ethnically-restricted; not silent.

---

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence does not name angelic beings as participants in exultation in this corpus. The cosmic rejoicing passages (Psa 96:11; 97:1; 1Ch 16:31) include the heavens and earth but do not specify angelic beings. The inverted passages (Pro 2:14; Hos 10:5; Hos 9:1) show the characteristic distorted by idolatrous and demonic influence (idols as the displaced objects of exultation) but do not name spiritual adversaries directly.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. (1) **Heavenly/angelic Joy** — Luk 15:7 ("joy in heaven over one sinner who repents"); Luk 15:10 ("joy before the angels of God") — Joy is an active reality in the heavenly realm, responsive to human repentance; (2) **The Holy Spirit as Joy-agent** — Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6; Rom 14:17; Act 13:52 — the Spirit is the agent of Joy in the NT's Spirit-mediated register; Luk 10:21 (Jesus rejoices "in the Holy Spirit") — the Spirit is the medium of Christ's own Joy; (3) **Eschatological angelic context** — Jude 24 ("with great joy" before God's presence — at the final presentation); Rev 4:9; 7:12 (heavenly creatures giving thanks — the joy-adjacent thanksgiving of heavenly worship).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

The evidence does not show Gladness operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings in the M04-L or M04-O corpus. Neh 9:20's "good Spirit to instruct them" attributes goodness to the divine Spirit but does not show the Spirit as an agent of Gladness transmission in the M04 sense. No angelic or adversarial interface is evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **The beast-captivation** (M04-N-VCG-02; Rev 13:3; 17:8) — the most explicit spiritual-beings interface in the corpus: the beast (an adversarial spiritual power) is the object of the whole earth's marveling-Delight; the characteristic of Delight is here shown as the instrument through which an adversarial spiritual power captivates the unredeemed; (2) **Idol-worship Delight** (M04-P-VCG-01; Eze 6:13; 16:19; 20:28) — Israel's ni.cho.ach directed toward idols; the pleasing-aroma of worship diverted from YHWH to spiritual powers with demonic associations (the "gods" of the nations); (3) **Wisdom's delight** (Pro 8:30–31) — Personified Wisdom (widely read in Jewish tradition as a created being or divine attribute personified) as the object of divine Delight before creation.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

The M04-J and M04-K corpus does not explicitly show Pleasure operating in relation to angelic beings. The ni.cho.ach aroma reaches God and is received by him; angels are not named as participants. The Psa 36:8 "river of delights" and Psa 16:11 "pleasures forevermore" are in God's presence, but the angelic dimension is not named.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Heavenly assembly** — Psa 89:5 ("let the heavens praise your wonders, O Lord, your faithfulness in the assembly of the holy ones") — Wonder is the appropriate response of the holy ones (angelic beings) to God's extraordinary works; (2) **Dark Wonder at adversarial powers** — Dan 8:24 ("fearful destruction"); Dan 11:36 (astonishing blasphemy) — the adversarial king whose acts produce dark wonder; (3) **Unclean spirits** — Mar 1:27 (thambeō arising from the exorcism of an unclean spirit — the crowd's Wonder at Jesus' authority over spiritual powers); (4) **The angel questioning Wonder** — Rev 17:7 (the angel addressing John's marvelling at the harlot) — an angelic being redirecting misapplied human Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **The Holy Spirit as producer** — Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6; Act 13:52 — the Spirit is the primary agent of Suffering-Joy's most intense form; the characteristic is directly Spirit-mediated; (2) **Angelic context** — Luk 1:44 (the baby leaping at Mary's Spirit-anointed greeting — the Spirit who has overshadowed Mary transmits through the incarnation-announcement context); Mat 5:12's "reward in heaven" implies the angelic-heavenly realm as the context within which the reward awaits.

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, implicitly. The idolatrous-exultation passages (Hos 10:5; Hos 9:1; Pro 2:14) show the characteristic's capacity for misdirection toward idol-worship — which in the OT theological framework involves demonic distortion (the idols as false alternatives to YHWH). The characteristic is a site of adversarial interference in the sense that exultation directed toward false objects displaces and corrupts the proper Godward orientation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, implicitly. The VCG-06 (inverted/corrupt/absent joy) corpus shows the systematic adversarial displacement of Joy: Hos 9:1 (Israel's joy corrupted by spiritual prostitution); Hos 2:11 (God putting an end to all Israel's mirth as judgment — which the adversarial system of idolatry precipitated); the misdirected-joy passages (Pro 2:14 — rejoicing in evil; Eze 25:6 — joy rooted in malice) show Joy's capacity being redirected toward evil through adversarial distortion. The enemy's attempt to produce joy over the righteous's downfall (Psa 13:4; 35:15, 19, 24, 26) is an adversarial deployment of Joy's oppositional form against God's people.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Implicitly. The distorted-evaluative instances (Isa 41:7's idol-making; Num 14:3's fear-evaluation; Jer 44:17's false attribution) show the evaluative-gladness faculty being corrupted — which could be framed as adversarial interference, but the evidence does not name spiritual adversaries explicitly. The corpus does not directly evidence adversarial targeting of Gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes — most directly through the beast-captivation. Rev 13:3 and 17:8 show the adversarial power exploiting the human capacity for Delight-captivation: the beast's apparent resurrection produces a collective marveling that draws the whole earth into following. The adversary's strategy is not to destroy Delight but to redirect it toward a counterfeit object (the beast) that produces the same captivated-following response that genuine Delight in God would produce toward God. M04-P's ni.cho.ach directed toward idols shows the same strategy at the cultic level: the worship-Delight faculty is redirected toward spiritual powers opposed to YHWH.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Implicitly, in the corrupt registers: (1) **Pro 9:17** (stolen bread appearing pleasant — the seductress Folly exploiting the Pleasure faculty through deceptive appearance); (2) **Pro 7:18** (the seductress inviting a.las as carnal Pleasure — adversarial exploitation of the sensory-Pleasure capacity); (3) **The misdirected ni.cho.ach** (M04-P-VCG-01 — Eze 20:28 in the M04-P corpus) — the worship-Pleasure faculty redirected toward idols. The adversary's strategy for Pleasure is to make wrong things appear genuinely pleasant (the deception of folly) and to redirect the worship-Pleasure faculty toward wrong objects.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, significantly in VCG-03: (1) **Dan 11:36's astonishing blasphemy** — the adversarial king speaking "astonishing things against the God of gods" — using the wonder-vocabulary to describe audacious rebellion against God; the adversary generates a counter-wonder of presumptuous blasphemy; (2) **Rev 17:6–7** — John's marvelling at the harlot (an adversarial power) is immediately questioned by the angel; the adversary's power and mystery can captivate the Wonder-faculty, drawing it toward wrong objects (this overlaps with the beast-captivation in the Delight analysis — Rev 13:3; 17:8 — both Delight and Wonder are exploited by the same adversarial strategy); (3) **Lam 1:9** (pe.le — "her fall is terrible") — the adversarial destruction of Jerusalem producing dark Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, explicitly. The contexts that produce Suffering-Joy (persecution in Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23; trials in 1Pe 1:6; Jas 1:2; apostolic suffering in Act 5:41) are all contexts of adversarial activity — the opposition to the gospel that occasions the suffering is adversarially-driven in the NT theological framework. Suffering-Joy is the inner-being response to adversarial attack that refuses to let the adversary's activity define the inner state. The characteristic is therefore the specific inner-being weapon against adversarial discouragement: adversaries can produce suffering but cannot prevent the Spirit from producing joy within it.

---

##### T4.6.3 — Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence does not show angelic ministry in the mediation or strengthening of exultation in this corpus. Silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Partially evidenced. Luk 2:10 — the angel announces "good news of great joy" to the shepherds; the angelic announcement is the vehicle through which the gospel Joy is first communicated to humanity. Luk 1:14 — the angel (Gabriel) announces the Joy that Zechariah will have. These are the clearest instances of angelic mediation of Joy's announcement.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

Not evidenced in this corpus. Silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

Not evidenced in this corpus. The voice at baptism/transfiguration (Mat 3:17; 17:5) declaring divine Delight operates through divine speech, not angelic mediation. The ni.cho.ach aroma operates through the cultic-ritual mechanism, not angels. Angelic mediation of Delight is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

Not evidenced in this corpus. Silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes, in the Rev 17:7 instance: the angel mediates a corrective response to John's Wonder — "why do you marvel? I will tell you the mystery" — the angel redirects and explicates John's Wonder, offering interpretive mediation of what was initially an overwhelming and disorienting inner response. The angel does not destroy John's Wonder but channels it toward proper understanding.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

Not directly evidenced in this corpus. The Spirit is the mediating agent; angels are not named as mediators of Suffering-Joy in the M04-E-VCG-02 or M04-F evidence.

---

##### T4.6.4 — If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

The evidence is silent on angelic mediation of exultation. Adversarial misdirection is implicitly evidenced in the idol-worship passages.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Not silent; heavenly Joy, Spirit-mediation, and angelic announcement of Joy are all evidenced.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

The evidence is silent on angelic mediation and adversarial activity targeting Gladness in the M04-L and M04-O corpus.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Beast-captivation and idol-worship are evidenced; angelic mediation is not; the adversarial exploitation of Delight (through the beast) is the most significant spiritual-beings finding in this corpus.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Adversarial exploitation of Pleasure is evidenced (Pro 9:17; 7:18); angelic mediation is not evidenced.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Adversarial exploitation and angelic mediation of Wonder are both evidenced; not silent.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Spirit-mediation is central; adversarial activity as the context is evidenced; angelic mediation is not evidenced.

---

## T5 — Formation and Transformation

---

### T5

#### T5.1 — Nature of Transformation

##### T5.1.1 — Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation to their condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. Psa 16:9's "flesh also dwells secure" shows the inner exultation producing a transformed bodily state — security and ease replacing anxiety. Psa 51:8's hoped-for restoration of rejoicing in "bones that you have broken" would represent a transformation from brokenness to restored vitality. Hab 3:18's "yet I will rejoice" in total material loss represents a transformation of inner condition despite unchanged external circumstances — the exultation produces an altered relationship to the circumstances rather than altered circumstances.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Primary evidence: (1) **Mourning to dancing** — Psa 30:11 ("you have turned for me my mourning into dancing; you have clothed me with gladness") — the person's inner-being state is fundamentally transformed by God through Joy; (2) **Sorrow to Joy** — Joh 16:20 ("your sorrow will turn into joy"); Jer 31:13 ("I will turn their mourning into joy") — a categorical inner-being reversal; (3) **Anxiety displaced** — Phili 4:4–7 (commanded Joy in the Lord produces the peace that surpasses understanding — Joy transforms the anxious inner state into peace); (4) **Poverty-to-generosity** — 2Cor 8:2 (joy in extreme poverty overflowing into generosity — the characteristic transforms the self-protective posture of poverty into outward-directed giving); (5) **Fear to peace** — Luk 2:10 (the angel's announcement of Joy accompanies "fear not" — Joy displaces fear).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Good news transforming inner state** — Pro 12:25 (anxiety → gladness through good word); Pro 15:30 (weariness/desire → refreshment through good news); 1Sa 16:23 (Saul: torment → refreshed and well through music); (2) **Testimony transforming communal inner state** — Neh 2:18 (discouragement → resolve through hearing God's good hand); (3) **Divine declaration transforming status** — makarismos (Rom 4:6, 9 — the divine declaration of blessedness transforms the inner status of the one to whom God counts righteousness); (4) **Moral evaluation convicting and transforming** — Eze 36:31 (recognition of "not good" deeds → self-loathing → the beginning of restored conscience).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, in multiple registers: (1) **Will aligned through Delight** — Psa 37:4 ("delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart") — the will's desires are transformed by Delight in God; (2) **Law internalized** — Psa 40:8 ("your law is within my heart") — the law's location changes from external to internal through Delight; (3) **Covenantal identity transformed** — Isa 62:4 (Zion renamed "My Delight Is in Her" — her identity transformed by being the object of divine Delight); (4) **Soul formed around object** — Isa 66:3 (soul delighting in abominations — the person's deepest self formed around the wrong object through sustained misdirected Delight); (5) **Adversity-surviving resilience** — Psa 119:92 (Delight in the law sustaining through affliction — the inner person transformed into one capable of enduring without perishing).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Pro 16:24** — gracious-word Pleasure producing "sweetness to the soul and health to the body" — a holistic transformative healing effect on the whole person; (2) **Gen 8:21** — God's inner Pleasure at Noah's offering producing a divine resolve ("I will never again curse the ground") — the soothing aroma transforms God's stated disposition toward the fallen world; (3) **Psa 27:4** — sustained dwelling in God's house and gazing on his beauty produces transformation toward that beauty; (4) **Job 36:11** — listening and serving God producing "years in pleasantness" — transformation of life-quality through the obedient posture; (5) **Deu 28:54, 56** — the reverse: loss of Pleasure under the curse transforms the character of daily life and inner experience.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Job's restoration** — Job 42:3 ("things too wonderful for me, which I did not know") — Wonder at God's incomprehensibility produces Job's restored inner posture; the divine whirlwind-encounter producing Wonder-humility is the hinge of Job's transformation from complaint to restored relationship; (2) **Psa 119:129** — "your testimonies are wonderful; therefore my soul keeps them" — Wonder in God's law producing obedient keeping; (3) **Mar 1:27** — the crowd's transformation from the routine synagogue assembly into a questioning, astonished community encountering something utterly new; (4) **The anti-type — Neh 9:17** — wonder-failure producing the transformation from covenant people into rebels; the failure to wonder precedes and enables the moral transformation toward rebellion.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, significantly: (1) **Character formation through trials** — Jas 1:2–4 (counting trials as joy → the testing of faith → steadfastness → completeness and wholeness) — Suffering-Joy is the enabling inner posture that allows trials to accomplish their full formative work; (2) **Freedom from circumstantial-dependence** — 2Cor 6:10 (adjacent — "sorrowful, yet always rejoicing") — the person formed by Suffering-Joy is transformed from one whose inner state mirrors external conditions to one whose inner life is constitutionally Spirit-anchored; (3) **Eschatological deepening** — 1Pe 4:13 ("that you may also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed") — present Suffering-Joy transforms the inner person toward the eschatological state of unqualified joy; (4) **Crisis-to-faith** — Act 16:34 (the jailer's crisis of the earthquake → coming to faith → rejoicing) — the most dramatic transformation instance in the corpus.

---

##### T5.1.2 — Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence shows both. Reversible: the VCG-02 passages (Deu 28:63; Joe 1:16; Isa 16:10; Jer 48:33) show exultation stripped away by judgment — the transformation it produced is reversed when the covenant relationship is broken. Irreversible in eschatological projection: Isa 65:18 commands "be glad and rejoice forever in that which I create" — suggesting the eschatological exultation is permanent, not liable to reversal.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Both registers are evidenced: (1) **Reversible** — Psa 51:8, 12 (David's joy lost and requiring restoration — transformation reversed by sin); Haman's gladness instantly reversed by Mordecai's presence (Est 5:9–14); the rocky-ground joy (Mat 13:20) reversed by testing; the merry-hearted who sigh when the vine fails (Isa 24:7) — circumstantially-grounded joy is reversible; (2) **Irreversible in eschatological form** — Joh 16:22 ("no one will take your joy from you"); Isa 51:11; 35:10 ("everlasting joy" upon the ransomed); Joh 15:11 (fullness of joy as the goal of abiding in Christ); Rev 19:7 (the Lamb's marriage — Joy consummated permanently). Present joy is reversible; eschatological joy is not.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Varies by register: (1) **Reversible** — Jon 4:6 (Jonah's gladness in the plant reversed when the plant withers — circumstantially-grounded gladness is reversible); 1Sa 11:9's relief could be reversed by new threats; (2) **Durable** — the ki-tov recognition of divine goodness tends toward durable inner reorientation (the Psalms' sustained praise tradition); (3) **Irreversible in eschatological form** — makarismos (Rom 4:6 — the declared blessedness is a permanent status change before God); Jos 21:45 (not one word has failed — the completeness of fulfilment is irrevocable).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Varies: (1) **Reversible** — Deu 30:9 ("the Lord will again take delight in prospering you") — divine Delight restored after it had been withheld; Eze 18:23; 33:11 (the wicked turning → God's Delight toward life restored) — the divine-Delight relationship is restorable through repentance; (2) **Durable formation** — Psa 1's "tree planted by streams" (from Delight-in-law) images a stable constitutional formation; Psa 119:92's survival of affliction shows durable inner transformation through law-Delight; (3) **Eschatologically permanent** — Isa 62:4 (renamed identity — "My Delight Is in Her") — the eschatological transformation appears permanent; Mal 3:12 ("you will be a land of delight") — the restored state is declared as the permanent eschatological condition; (4) **Corrupt formation** — Isa 66:3's soul-delighting-in-abominations is shown as a deeply entrenched state; whether reversible only through divine intervention is implicit.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Varies: (1) **The ni.cho.ach relationship** — reversible in both directions: Lev 26:31 (God stops receiving aromas — reversible by repentance); Eze 20:41 (God will again accept as pleasing aroma — restoration restoring the Pleasure relationship); (2) **The luxury-curse transformation** (Deu 28:54, 56) — presented as severe but reversible through covenant restoration; (3) **Pro 16:24's health to the body** — implies an ongoing sustaining effect rather than a permanent irreversible change; (4) **Eschatological Pleasure** (Psa 16:11) — "forevermore" implies permanent and irreversible eschatological transformation.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Varies: (1) **Reversible** — Neh 9:17's transformation from wonder to rebellion is reversed by God's mercy (the same verse: "but you are a God ready to forgive, gracious and merciful"); Mic 7:15's "as in the days when you came out of Egypt, I will show them marvellous things" shows wonder-based transformation restorable; (2) **Durable** — Psa 71:17's lifelong proclamatory orientation formed by sustained Wonder; (3) **Eschatologically permanent** — Isa 29:14's "wonder upon wonder" pointing toward transformations that the wise cannot reverse; Dan 12:6's end-time wonders producing the permanent transition to the final age.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Varies: (1) **Reversible in the fragile form** — M04-F's ba.lag is explicitly temporary and reversible; Job 9:27's attempted cheerfulness fails; Psa 39:13's desired smile is momentary before departure; (2) **Irreversible in the eschatological form** — "no one will take your joy from you" (Joh 16:22 — adjacent) applies to the eschatological form; the "glory to be revealed" (1Pe 4:13) is a permanent eschatological state; (3) **Formation-durable** — the steadfastness produced by Jas 1:3–4 is the durable inner-being deposit of sustained Suffering-Joy; once the person has been formed through trials-in-joy, the proven character is a lasting possession.

---

##### T5.1.3 — If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly.
