**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Transformation is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Transformation is evidenced across multiple clusters; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Transformation is evidenced across multiple registers; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Transformation evidence is pervasive across all five sub-groups; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Transformation evidence is present across multiple registers; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Transformation evidence is present in multiple registers; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Transformation is extensively evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T5.2 — Sequence of Inner States

##### T5.2.1 — Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, in several clusters: (1) **Affliction → waiting → exultation** — Isa 25:9 (patient waiting for God → "we have waited for him" → exultation in his salvation); Psa 9:14 (distress → anticipated exultation in God's salvation); (2) **Covenant faithfulness → God's delight → prospering → exultation** — Deu 30:9 (return to God → God's delight in prospering → the people's flourishing); (3) **Trust → heart's exultation** — Psa 13:5 (trust in steadfast love → "my heart shall rejoice"); (4) **Brokenness → restoration → bone-exultation** — Psa 51:8 (penitential brokenness → hoped-for restoration of rejoicing in the bones).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, multiple sequences: (1) **Mourning → Joy** — Jer 31:13; Isa 61:3; Psa 30:11 — sorrow as the prior state that Joy replaces; (2) **Waiting → Joy** — Isa 25:9 ("we have waited for him… let us be glad and rejoice in his salvation") — patient waiting as the prior state that divine action resolves into Joy; Psa 51:8, 12 (brokenness → restoration → Joy); (3) **Affliction → Joy** — 2Cor 8:2; 1Pe 1:6; 1Th 1:6 — suffering as the context through which Spirit-Joy operates; (4) **Comprehension → Joy** — Neh 8:12 (understanding → great rejoicing); (5) **Faith → Joy** — Rom 15:13 ("joy and peace in believing"); Act 16:34 (believed → rejoiced). The dominant sequence across the corpus is: prior condition of lack, loss, or longing → divine action or gospel reception → Joy arising.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Anxiety → good word → gladness** — Pro 12:25 (anxiety weighing → good word → inner brightening); (2) **Torment → music → wellbeing** — 1Sa 16:23 (harmful spirit → David's lyre → Saul refreshed and well); (3) **Mourning → divine act → gladness** — Jer 31:13 (mourning → God turns → joy); Isa 61:3 (ashes → oil of gladness given by God); (4) **Discouragement → testimony → resolve** — Neh 2:18 (community state unclear → Nehemiah testifies of God's good hand → resolve to build); (5) **Seeking → God's goodness received** — Lam 3:25 (waiting and seeking → Lord's goodness experienced).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 37:4 sequence**: delight yourself in the Lord → he will give you the desires of your heart; (2) **Psa 40:8 sequence**: law within the heart → I delight to do your will — the inner law produces Delight-in-obedience; (3) **Isa 58:13–14 sequence**: call the Sabbath a delight → honor it → you shall take delight in the Lord → God exalts; (4) **M04-H-VCG-02 rescue sequence**: God delights in the person → rescue/exaltation follows (Psa 18:19; 37:23; Num 14:8); (5) **Psa 119:92 sequence**: law as delight (prior) → affliction (present) → the law-delight sustains through affliction (outcome); (6) **Corrupt sequence**: wrong Delight chosen → soul formed around wrong object → soul delights in abominations (Isa 66:3) — progressive entrenchment.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Pro 2:9–10 sequence**: wisdom enters heart → knowledge pleasant to soul → good path understood; (2) **Pro 16:24 sequence**: gracious words heard → sweetness to the soul → health to the body; (3) **Gen 8:21 sequence**: Noah offers → Lord smells → Lord says in his heart → divine resolve formed; (4) **Psa 27:4 sequence**: ask/seek → dwell in God's house → gaze on his beauty → inquiry in his temple; (5) **Job 36:11 sequence**: listen and serve God → complete days in prosperity → years in pleasantness.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Exo 34:10 sequence**: God announces marvels → all the people see the work of the Lord → it is an awesome thing; (2) **Psa 9:1 sequence**: wonder at wonderful deeds → wholehearted thanks → recounting/proclamation; (3) **Psa 119:129 sequence**: testimonies are wonderful → therefore the soul keeps them; (4) **Job 42:3 sequence**: encountered the incomprehensible → spoke beyond knowledge → now recognises things too wonderful for me → restored humility; (5) **Neh 9:17 sequence**: wonders performed → not mindful → stiffened neck → appointed leader to return to Egypt — a reverse sequence showing wonder-failure producing the sequence toward rebellion.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, clearly: (1) **Jas 1:2–4 sequence**: meeting trials → counting them as joy → testing of faith → steadfastness → completeness; (2) **1Pe 1:6–9 sequence**: rejoicing in salvation → grieved by trials → tested faith like gold → praise/glory/honour at the revelation of Jesus Christ; (3) **1Pe 4:13 sequence**: sharing Christ's sufferings (present) → rejoice insofar (present Suffering-Joy) → rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed (future unqualified joy); (4) **M04-F sequence**: extreme suffering → desired comfort (ba.lag) → barely attained or not attained → departure (Job 10:20; Psa 39:13 — the sequence ends without resolution in the fragile register).

---

##### T5.2.2 — What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The sequences reveal that exultation is consistently a terminus — it is the inner state that arrives after the prior sequence (affliction, waiting, trust, brokenness, seeking) has been traversed. It is rarely the starting point but the culmination: what the waiting was for, what the trust produces, what the brokenness moves toward. This positions exultation as the characteristic that marks completed movement rather than initiating movement.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The sequences reveal Joy as a characteristic that is often arrived at rather than simply present: it is the inner-being destination of waiting, seeking, mourning, and faith. This positions Joy as eschatologically-structured even in its present occurrences — each present instance of Joy is a partial arrival at what is fully available only in the eschatological fullness. The sequence also reveals that Joy is not manufactured but received: the prior condition (mourning, waiting, suffering) is not removed by human effort but reversed by divine action, and Joy is the inner-being sign that the reversal has taken place.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The sequences reveal Gladness as characteristically a terminus — it is the inner state that arrives after a prior condition of lack or distress has been addressed. Unlike Joy (which can be commanded directly), Gladness in this corpus tends to arise in response to something genuinely and accurately received. The sequence is consistently: prior condition (anxiety, torment, mourning, discouragement, seeking) → genuinely good input received or recognised → Gladness arising as the inner response.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Two distinct sequence-patterns: (1) **Upward formation** — Delight in God/law → transformed desires → obedience → rescue/exaltation/blessing. This is the characteristic's primary formative trajectory; (2) **Downward entrenchment** — wrong Delight chosen → soul formed around wrong object → deepening corruption (Isa 66:3). The sequences reveal Delight as a formative characteristic more than any other in M04: the direction of Delight determines the direction of the person's entire formation arc.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The dominant sequences reveal Pleasure as the fruit or outcome of a prior enabling condition: wisdom enters, then Pleasure follows (Pro 2:10); gracious words are received, then Pleasure flows (Pro 16:24); Noah obediently offers, then God's Pleasure responds (Gen 8:21). Pleasure is consistently the experiential fruit of something prior — right worship, wisdom, seeking, obedient service. It is received rather than generated.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Two opposing sequences: (1) **Upward arc** — divine wonder-act → perceptive encounter → Wonder arises → proclamation, obedience, humility, praise; (2) **Downward arc** — divine wonder-act → failure to perceive/remember → Wonder-absence → hardness → rebellion. The sequences reveal Wonder as the critical hinge characteristic: when genuine Wonder arises from encounter with God's extraordinary acts, it produces the upward arc; when it fails to arise (not-attending, not-remembering), the downward arc follows. No other M04 characteristic has such a clearly documented downward arc through its absence.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two distinct sequence-patterns: (1) **The Spirit-enabled sequence** (agalliao): present suffering → Spirit-produced Suffering-Joy → formation (proven character, steadfastness) → eschatological fullness (glory at revelation). This is a progressive, upward sequence in which the suffering is the necessary context of the formation. (2) **The fragile sequence** (ba.lag): extreme suffering → attempted cheer → failure to sustain → departure. This is a downward sequence that ends without resolution — the OT type that requires the NT's Spirit-enablement to transform. The two sequences together reveal that Suffering-Joy has a resolution in the Spirit that the human person unaided cannot achieve.

---

##### T5.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Sequence is evidenced across multiple clusters.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple sequences are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Sequences are evidenced across multiple clusters; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Sequences are evidenced in multiple sub-groups; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Sequences are evidenced across multiple clusters; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Both upward and downward sequences are extensively documented; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Sequences are clearly evidenced in both registers; not silent.

---

#### T5.3 — Mechanism of Change

##### T5.3.1 — What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformation, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Two mechanisms: (1) **Encounter** — the direct encounter with God's saving act produces immediate exultation (Exo 18:9; Dan 6:23; Isa 25:9); (2) **Volitional cultivation** — Hab 3:18 and the commanded exultations show exultation cultivated by deliberate volitional choice and repeated practice (Psa 89:16 — "all the day" suggests habitual practice). The mechanism differs by context: extraordinary encounters produce spontaneous exultation; ordinary life requires cultivated volitional exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple mechanisms: (1) **Encounter with divine reality** — Exo 4:14 (Aaron's heart gladness at seeing Moses); Joh 20:20 (disciples glad when they saw the Lord) — direct perceptual encounter with God's saving reality produces Joy which transforms the inner state; (2) **Word comprehension** — Neh 8:12 (understanding → Joy → transformed community engagement); Act 13:48 (hearing the word → rejoicing → believing); (3) **Prescribed practice** — the feast-commandments (Deu 16:11–15) — communal embodied practice cultivates the inner state; (4) **Spirit impartation** — Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6; Act 13:52 — the Spirit directly produces Joy as fruit; (5) **Volitional direction** — Phili 4:4 (commanded Joy redirects the will which in turn re-orients the inner state).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Three primary mechanisms: (1) **Word/news reception** — the primary mechanism in M04-O-VCG-01 (Pro 12:25; 15:30; Isa 52:7): a word or news accurately received produces inner brightening; (2) **Evaluative formation** — the primary mechanism in M04-L-VCG-02: sustained practice of accurate moral evaluation, trained through wisdom literature and experience, forms the evaluative faculty and the gladness that recognition of the good produces; (3) **Divine declaration / good hand** — M04-O-VCG-04: God's promise or providential action, recognised and received with trust, produces gladness; the mechanism is reception of divine word and act.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Four mechanisms: (1) **Sustained orientation** — the primary mechanism of M04-G: Delight in God's law drives continuous meditation (Psa 1:2) which progressively forms the person around its object; (2) **Divine responsive action** — M04-H-VCG-02: God's Delight toward the person produces immediate divine action (rescue, exaltation, restoration); the mechanism is divine favor producing divine act; (3) **Volitional direction** — the cha.phets mechanism: Delight energising the will toward its object produces immediate and sustained action (Gen 34:19; Joh 8:29); (4) **Naming/identity-declaration** — Isa 62:4 (God's Delight producing the new name) — the mechanism of declarative identity change through divine Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Three primary mechanisms: (1) **Nourishment** — Pro 16:24's honey-simile: pleasant speech nourishes the soul and heals the body; the mechanism is saturation and sustenance; (2) **Soothing** — the ni.cho.ach mechanism: the pleasing aroma soothes and settles; the mechanism is calming of agitation into settled receptive state; (3) **Drawn beauty** — Psa 27:4's gazing upon God's beauty: the mechanism is aesthetic encounter drawing the person toward what is beautiful, producing the transformation of attraction and orientation.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Three mechanisms: (1) **Cognitive humbling** — the encounter with what exceeds comprehension (Job 37:5; 42:3; Psa 131:1) humbles the inner being into right creaturely posture; the mechanism is intellectual arrest; (2) **Memory-embedding** — God causing his wondrous works to be remembered (Psa 111:4); the mechanism of repeated memorial practice embedding wonder-recognition in the person's cognitive and affective formation; (3) **Proclamatory overflow** — wonder-at-God's-acts producing the impulse to declare them (1Ch 16:9, 24; Psa 9:1); the mechanism is the inner state overflowing into communal speech and action.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Three distinct mechanisms: (1) **Spirit-impartation** — the primary mechanism for agalliao: the Holy Spirit directly produces the exultation (Luk 10:21; 1Th 1:6); (2) **Volitional-cognitive reframing** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") and Heb 12:2 (Christ's orientation toward "the joy set before him") — the deliberate cognitive-volitional holding of eschatological reality as more determinative than present suffering; (3) **Trial-formation** — Jas 1:3–4 (the trial itself, when met with Suffering-Joy, is the mechanism of character formation through testing → steadfastness → completeness). The three mechanisms are not alternatives but collaborative: the Spirit enables the volitional reframing which enables the trial to do its formative work.

---

##### T5.3.2 — Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes — the Psalms' commanded and habitual exultation (Psa 89:16; 32:11; 118:24) represents the formation mechanism; the narrative encounters (Exo 18:9; Dan 6:23) represent the encounter mechanism. The prophetic passages (Hab 3:18; Zec 9:9) blend both: the command grounds itself in what God has already done and is doing.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. Crisis contexts → encounter-mechanism (Exo 4:14; Joh 20:20; Act 12:14); ordinary-life formation → practice-mechanism (feast-commandments); persecution contexts → Spirit-mechanism (1Th 1:6; 2Cor 8:2); pastoral contexts → word-comprehension mechanism (Neh 8:12; Act 13:48); sustained-life formation → volitional-discipline mechanism (Phili 4:4; 1Th 5:16). Each mechanism is appropriate to its context; no single mechanism is universal.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: crisis contexts → good news mechanism (acute refreshment); wisdom-formation contexts → evaluative training mechanism (gradual formation); doxological contexts → divine declaration mechanism (recognition of God's character producing praise-gladness); covenantal-trust contexts → promise-reception mechanism (trusting the good word as reliable).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: law-delight → sustained orientation mechanism (gradual formation through meditation); God's Delight toward the person → divine action mechanism (immediate); human volitional Delight → will-energising mechanism (immediate action from desire); corrupt Delight → habituation mechanism (gradual formation in wrong direction). The divine action mechanism operates immediately and without requiring the formation stages; the human formation mechanism requires sustained practice.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: worship contexts → soothing mechanism (ni.cho.ach — calming); speech contexts → nourishing mechanism (Pro 16:24 — honey-sustenance); seeking-God contexts → beauty-attraction mechanism (Psa 27:4 — drawn toward the beautiful); wisdom contexts → wisdom-formation mechanism (Pro 2:10 — wisdom entering the heart enabling Pleasure in knowledge).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: VCG-01 contexts → memory-embedding and proclamatory-overflow mechanisms (the liturgical-worship context); VCG-02 contexts → cognitive-humbling mechanism (the epistemological-limit context); VCG-03 dark Wonder contexts → disturbing-arrest mechanism (the troubled-astonishment and dread of VCG-03).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: direct-encounter contexts (Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21; Act 16:34) → Spirit-impartation mechanism; persecution/suffering contexts addressed by apostolic letter (Jas 1:2; 1Pe 1:6; 4:13; Mat 5:12) → volitional-cognitive reframing with Spirit-enabling; extreme adversity without explicit Spirit-context (M04-F — Job 9:27; Psa 39:13) → attempted-will mechanism without Spirit-impartation, producing the fragile form.

---

##### T5.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Mechanism is evidenced in both encounter and formation registers.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple mechanisms evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple mechanisms evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple mechanisms evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Three distinct mechanisms evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Multiple mechanisms clearly evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T5.4 — Suffering and Affliction

##### T5.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or a context for it?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, significantly. Psa 31:7 — "I will rejoice and be glad in your steadfast love, because you have seen my affliction" — makes affliction the context for the exultation. Psa 51:8 — "the bones that you have broken" — presupposes penitential suffering as the context from which exultation is sought. Hab 3:18 — "yet I will rejoice" after naming total material loss (fig tree not blossoming, no fruit, no flock, no herd) — is the clearest suffering-and-exultation passage in the corpus. Job 3:6–7; 3:22 show the suffering so extreme that exultation is denied or inverted.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, prominently — this is one of the most distinctive features of Joy in Characteristic 2. (1) **Joy in affliction as a commanded stance** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy when you meet trials"); Mat 5:12 (commanded to "rejoice and be glad" under persecution); Luk 6:23 ("Rejoice in that day and leap for joy" under rejection); (2) **Joy coexisting with suffering** — 2Cor 6:10 ("sorrowful, yet always rejoicing"); Col 1:24 (rejoicing in sufferings for the church); Phili 2:17 (Paul glad and rejoicing even facing death); (3) **Joy in affliction through the Spirit** — 1Th 1:6 ("much affliction, with the joy of the Holy Spirit"); 2Cor 8:2 (abundance of joy in severe affliction); (4) **Eschatological ground of Joy in suffering** — 1Pe 1:6 (rejoicing despite grief from trials, grounded in the salvation being revealed); 1Pe 4:13 (rejoicing insofar as sharing Christ's sufferings, toward future Glory); Heb 12:2 (Joy set before Christ as the eschatological ground for enduring the cross).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, but as a response to or relief from suffering rather than as a product of it: (1) **Gladness as relief from affliction** — 1Sa 16:23 (Saul's gladness from Saul's restoration — the harmful spirit's departure is the affliction relieved); (2) **Gladness under adversity as a chosen posture** — Lam 3:26–27 ("it is good to wait quietly… good for a man to bear the yoke in his youth") — the evaluative faculty naming the formative benefit of suffering as genuinely good; (3) **Gladness contrasted with suffering** — Jon 4:3, 8 (extreme suffering producing despair-evaluation rather than gladness — showing gladness's fragility under extreme affliction); (4) **Gladness as the reversal of sorrow** — M04-O-VCG-03 (gladness expected as the fruit of God's restorative acts, standing against prior suffering).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Delight as affliction-sustainer** — Psa 119:92 ("if your law had not been my delight, I would have perished in my affliction") — the most direct statement; Psa 119:143 ("trouble and anguish have found me out, but your commandments are my delight") — Delight standing as a direct counterweight to trouble; Psa 119:77 ("let your mercy come to me, that I may live; for your law is my delight") — Delight sustaining the desire for life under pressure; (2) **Delight in God enabling suffering** — Job 6:10 (sa.lad — "I would even exult in pain unsparing, for I have not denied the words of the Holy One") — fidelity-Delight enabling the endurance of unsparing pain; (3) **Delight destroyed by judgment-suffering** — Deu 28:56 (the delicate woman's a.nog destroyed by siege-desperation); Jer 16:9 ("I will silence the voice of gladness and joy") — Delight's absence naming the fullness of judgment.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes, primarily as contrast and consolation: (1) **Pro 15:15** — "all the days of the afflicted are evil, but the cheerful of heart has a continual feast" — the contrast positions Pleasure as the inner state that transcends circumstantial adversity; (2) **Psa 16:6** — "lines have fallen for me in pleasant places" — the psalmist's reception of pleasant inheritance in the context of a psalm expressing trust through difficulty; (3) **Job 36:11** — obedient service producing years of pleasantness in contrast to the adversity of the unobedient; (4) **Deu 28:54, 56** — the curse destroying Pleasure under siege-adversity — the most direct evidence of affliction eliminating Pleasure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 31:21** — "blessed be the Lord, for he has wondrously shown his steadfast love to me when I was in a besieged city" — Wonder at divine rescue arising precisely from the context of extreme suffering; (2) **Psa 77:11** — "I will remember the deeds of the Lord; yes, I will remember your wonders of old" — deliberate memory of past wonders as the inner strategy for sustaining faith through present distress; (3) **Job 10:16** (VCG-03) — wonders worked against Job in his suffering — dark Wonder at divine power directed against him; (4) **Lam 1:9** — Jerusalem's terrible fall (pe.le) as the dark wonder of judgment experienced in suffering; (5) **Deu 28:59** — "extraordinary afflictions" (pa.la) as the dark wonder of covenantal judgment.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes — suffering is the defining context of this characteristic; the relationship to suffering is constitutive rather than incidental: (1) **Joy within suffering** — 1Pe 1:6 ("though now for a little while, if necessary, you have been grieved by various trials"); (2) **Joy through suffering** — 1Pe 4:13 ("rejoice insofar as you share Christ's sufferings"); (3) **Joy commanded under persecution** — Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23; (4) **Joy enabling endurance of suffering** — Heb 12:2 (the joy set before Christ enabling endurance of the cross); (5) **Sought comfort in extreme suffering** — M04-F-VCG-01 (ba.lag/mav.li.git — Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13; Jer 8:18 — all contexts of overwhelming adversity).

---

##### T5.4.2 — Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence shows suffering primarily **testing** and **revealing** exultation: Hab 3:18 reveals the depth of practiced exultation by showing it surviving total material loss. Psa 31:7 shows that the person in affliction whose trust holds is the one who can rejoice. The severity of suffering in Job 3 shows that exultation can be overwhelmed to the point of inversion (Job 3:22 — rejoicing at the grave) — revealing the characteristic's limits under extreme distress. Suffering does not appear to produce exultation directly in this corpus; it tests and refines what is already there.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The evidence shows all four: (1) **Suffering tests Joy** — the rocky-ground passages (Mat 13:20; Luk 8:13) show that suffering reveals whether Joy has root; (2) **Suffering reveals Joy's depth** — 2Cor 8:2 (joy in poverty and affliction is more revelatory than joy in prosperity — it demonstrates Spirit-grounding); 1Pe 1:6–8 (joy amid trials makes the faith's genuineness apparent); (3) **Suffering deepens Joy** — Col 1:24 (Paul's rejoicing in sufferings deepens his participation in Christ's work); Phili 2:17 (facing possible death deepens rather than diminishes Joy); (4) **In its NT paradoxical form, suffering produces Joy** — Jas 1:2 ("count it all joy") frames the trial itself as the occasion for a higher Joy than comfortable circumstances produce; M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao in suffering) is the concentrated evidence for this producing-function.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Suffering primarily **tests and reveals** Gladness in this corpus: Jon 4:3, 8 (extreme suffering revealing the limits of Jonah's evaluative gladness); Lam 3:26–27 (suffering reveals that the patient, evaluative posture — naming suffering as formatively good — is the appropriate inner response). Lam 3:26's "it is good to wait quietly for the salvation of the Lord" shows suffering **producing** a deeper gladness when the evaluative faculty correctly assesses the formative benefit of endurance. Unlike Characteristic 7 (Suffering-Joy), Gladness does not arise paradoxically from suffering but from accurate evaluation of suffering's formative meaning.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Suffering **tests and reveals** Delight in this corpus: Psa 119:92 reveals that the person's prior Delight in God's law was the thing that sustained them — the suffering doesn't produce the Delight but reveals whether it was genuinely present. Psa 119:143 shows Delight standing firm against trouble — the test of affliction exposing whether the Delight is genuine or superficial. Job 6:10 shows suffering **deepening** the awareness of Delight's value: the pain reveals that fidelity to God's words is what enables even pain to be endured. Suffering does not produce Delight in this corpus in the same sense that it produces Suffering-Joy (Characteristic 7); instead it tests and reveals Delight already present.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Suffering primarily **tests and reveals** whether Pleasure is genuine: Pro 15:15 reveals that the cheerful-of-heart person maintains a feast-quality even in adversity, showing genuine inner Pleasure independent of circumstance. Deu 28:54, 56 shows suffering **destroying** Pleasure that was dependent on comfort — the siege reveals the fragility of luxury-Pleasure. The characteristic contrast: inner Pleasure (M04-J's relational and wisdom variety) survives adversity better than material Pleasure (M04-K-VCG-02's luxury register). Suffering does not produce Pleasure in this corpus in the way Suffering-Joy arises through suffering.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Suffering both **tests Wonder** (does the person return to remembered wonders in distress — Psa 77:11?) and **produces Wonder** at God's extraordinary rescue acts (Psa 31:21 — Wonder arising precisely from the besieged-city context). Suffering also produces **dark Wonder** (Job 10:16; Lam 1:9 — the incomprehensibility of extreme suffering itself producing astonished dread). The most analytically significant: Psa 77:11 shows Wonder as the inner resource the Psalmist deliberately returns to under suffering — deliberate memory of past wonders is the therapeutic inner-strategy for navigating present distress.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

All four: (1) **Produces** — Jas 1:2's "count it all joy when you meet trials" — the trial is the occasion for the commanded Suffering-Joy; 1Pe 4:13's "insofar as you share Christ's sufferings" — sharing suffering is what produces the present form of this joy; (2) **Tests** — 1Pe 1:6–7 (trials testing faith as gold is tested by fire — the testing reveals whether the Suffering-Joy has genuine Spirit-grounding or is merely performed); (3) **Reveals** — M04-F's ba.lag sequences reveal the limits of unaided human cheerfulness under extreme suffering — the suffering reveals the characteristic's dependence on Spirit-enabling; (4) **Deepens** — Jas 1:3–4 (steadfastness produced by tested faith → completeness) — sustained Suffering-Joy through trials deepens the proven character.

---

##### T5.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy's relationship to suffering is among the most extensively evidenced features of Characteristic 2; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced, primarily in the Lamentations texts and Jon 4; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced primarily in the Psa 119 affliction-Delight series; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced through contrast and curse-context; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced across rescue-wonder (VCG-01), dark wonder (VCG-03), and suffering-as-judgment contexts; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The relationship to suffering is constitutive of this characteristic; not silent.

---

#### T5.5 — Formation and Sanctification

##### T5.5.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the person over time toward greater likeness?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The commanded exultations (Psa 2:11; 32:11; Isa 65:18) and the sustained orientation of Psa 89:16 ("all the day") presuppose formation — exultation as a cultivated, habituated inner posture over time. The sequence from Psa 51:8 (broken bones) to the asked-for restoration suggests a character-formation arc from guilt through penitence to restored exultation. Isa 64:5's "him who joyfully works righteousness" is a portrait of a person formed into a joyful-righteous character — not a momentary state but a stable character-expression.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. (1) **Feast-commandments as formation practice** — the Deuteronomic feast-joy is not a single event but a recurring commanded annual practice designed to form Israel's inner life across generations; the repeated festivals produce the habituated inner posture of Joy before God; (2) **Pauline formation toward Joy** — Phili 1:25 (Paul remains for the Philippians' "progress and joy in the faith" — Joy and spiritual progress are linked in the formation arc); 2Co 1:24 (Paul "works with you for your joy" — joy is a goal of ongoing apostolic formation); (3) **Joy enabling endurance that produces character** — Rom 12:12 ("rejoice in hope, be patient in tribulation") — Joy in hope as the enabling posture for the patient endurance that produces character; (4) **Commanded Joy as formative discipline** — Phili 4:4 ("Rejoice always") — a standing command whose repeated observance forms the inner life over time.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes. M04-L-VCG-02 (45 verses of Proverbs and wisdom moral appraisal) is inherently a formation text: the repeated "better than," "not good," and "good man" pronouncements are the training curriculum of the evaluative-gladness faculty across a lifetime. Pro 2:20 ("walk in the way of the good") — the formed habit of walking the good way is the long-arc outcome. Lam 3:27 ("it is good for a man that he bear the yoke in his youth") — the youthful formation of endurance produces the gladness of mature, stable character. The ki-tov liturgical tradition (M04-L-VCG-01) forms the community's doxological orientation through repeated rehearsal across generations.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes — Delight is the most explicitly formative characteristic in M04: (1) **Psa 1:2** — delight in the law → meditation day and night → "like a tree planted by streams of water, yielding its fruit in its season, its leaf does not wither" — the most complete formation image in the corpus; (2) **Psa 37:4** — delight in the Lord → restructured desires → blessing; (3) **Psa 40:8** — "your law is within my heart" as the fully-formed state where Delight has so internalized the law that obedience becomes natural willing; (4) **Isa 66:3** — sustained misdirected Delight producing a soul formed around abominations — the negative formation arc confirming that Delight is the primary formative force in both directions.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Pro 3:17** ("her ways are ways of pleasantness, and all her paths are peace") — wisdom's pleasantness-quality is the characteristic of a whole life formed by wisdom; (2) **Pro 2:10** ("wisdom will come into your heart, and knowledge will be pleasant to your soul") — the long-arc formation of wisdom in the heart produces Pleasure in knowledge as the ongoing experiential quality; (3) **M04-K-VCG-03 wisdom-comparatives** — the sustained engagement with wisdom's better-than comparatives forms a person whose Pleasure is calibrated to prefer genuine goodness over material abundance; (4) **The ni.cho.ach worship practice** — twice-daily, weekly, festal; the sustained practice of worship-Pleasure forms the community's covenantal identity over time.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 71:17** — "from my youth you have taught me, and I still proclaim your wondrous deeds" — the fullest formation-arc evidence in the corpus: Wonder formed from youth producing a lifetime of proclamatory vocation; (2) **Psa 78:4** — "we will not hide them from their children, but tell to the coming generation" — the intergenerational formation arc: Wonder transmitted through communal telling forming each generation; (3) **Psa 131:1** — the formed epistemological humility of the person who has learned not to overreach; a character quality formed by sustained Wonder; (4) **Job's arc** — Job 42:3's humble Wonder following the whirlwind as the resolution of a life-arc through suffering and complaint toward restored relationship.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes — Jas 1:2–4 is the most explicit formation text in the entire M04 cluster: "count it all joy... knowing that the testing of your faith produces steadfastness. And let steadfastness have its full effect, that you may be perfect and complete, lacking in nothing." Suffering-Joy is the inner posture that enables the trial to accomplish the long-arc formation work: steadfastness → completeness → lacking nothing. This is the most theologically-developed formation sequence in M04.

---

##### T5.5.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is both a product and a sustaining force in character formation: it is produced by right orientation toward God (trust, seeking, righteousness), and it in turn sustains that orientation by anchoring the person's inner life in the divine reality. The person who habitually exults in God (Psa 89:16) is being formed through that habit into one whose inner life is constitutionally Godward.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy occupies two roles in the formation arc: (1) **A goal of formation** — spiritual progress, apostolic work, and community health aim at Joy as their inner-being telos; (2) **An enabling condition of formation** — Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength") shows Joy enabling the further formation work; 2Cor 8:2 (joy producing generosity) shows Joy enabling the next formative act. Joy is both destination and fuel of the formation arc — it is what formation produces and what makes further formation possible.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness plays two roles in the formation arc: (1) **Formative goal** — the evaluative faculty is what formation is developing; the person formed by wisdom becomes one who accurately sees what is genuinely good and inhabits the gladness that recognition produces; (2) **Formative means** — the practice of evaluating rightly (M04-L-VCG-02's wisdom training) and declaring God's goodness (M04-L-VCG-01's ki-tov liturgical tradition) are themselves formative practices that shape the inner person over time.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight is the primary driver of the long-arc formation in M04: it determines the direction of formation (toward God or away from him) and provides the sustaining energy that enables formation to continue through adversity (Psa 119:92; Job 6:10). Psa 1:2's "meditates day and night" driven by Delight is the most complete description of formation-through-Delight: the characteristic sustains the sustained practice that produces the formed character. The two formation arcs (upward through right Delight; downward through misdirected Delight) confirm that Delight is the most powerfully formative inner-being characteristic in M04.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure plays a sustaining and reinforcing role in formation: wisdom-formation produces Pleasure in knowledge which reinforces continued wisdom-seeking (Pro 2:10); the pleasantness of wisdom's ways (Pro 3:17) makes the wisdom-path genuinely attractive and sustainable. Pleasure is the experiential quality that makes the formation path pleasant to walk — it is both a fruit of formation and a sustainer of it.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder is the formative thread of a life directed toward God in proclamation and praise: Psa 71:17's "from my youth… I still proclaim" shows Wonder as the characteristic that, when established early and sustained deliberately, becomes the defining inner-expressive orientation of a whole life. Psa 78's generational-transmission passage shows Wonder as the content of character formation passed between generations — not as a single experience but as a sustained practice of telling and remembering. Wonder's role in formation is as the doxological spine of the covenant life.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy occupies a unique role: it is the enabling posture that allows suffering to do its formative work rather than merely damaging the person. Without Suffering-Joy, trials produce bitterness, despair, or collapse (M04-F's trajectory); with Suffering-Joy, trials produce steadfastness and completeness (Jas 1:3–4). The characteristic is therefore the necessary inner condition that converts suffering from a destructive force into a formative one.

---

##### T5.5.3 — If the evidence is silent on formation and sanctification, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Formation is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Formation evidence is extensively present; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Formation evidence is extensively present in the wisdom corpus; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Formation evidence is the most extensive in M04 for this characteristic; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Formation evidence is present across wisdom and worship registers; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Formation evidence is extensive (Psa 71:17; 78:4; 131:1; Job 42:3); not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Formation is the most strongly evidenced dimension of this characteristic (Jas 1:2–4); not silent.

---

#### T5.6 — Eschatological Trajectory

##### T5.6.1 — Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is oriented?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, strongly. The eschatological concentration of exultation passages is one of the most notable features of the corpus: Isa 65:18 (forever exultation in God's new creation); Isa 65:19 (God's own exultation in the new Jerusalem); Isa 66:10 (all who love Jerusalem exulting in her restoration); Jer 32:41 (God's new-covenant exultation over Israel); Zep 3:17 (God exulting with loud singing over his people in the final restoration); Zec 9:9 (Zion exulting at her king's coming). The eschatological fullness of exultation is both the human exultation at God's final acts and God's own exultation over his fully restored people.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, this is one of the most prominent features of Characteristic 2. (1) **Fullness of Joy as eschatological goal** — Joh 15:11 ("your joy may be full"); Joh 16:24 ("that your joy may be full" through asking in Jesus' name); 1Jo 1:4; 2Jo 12 (joy made complete through communion); (2) **Everlasting Joy** — Isa 35:10; 51:11 ("everlasting joy shall be upon their heads"); Isa 61:7 ("everlasting joy"); (3) **Irremovable Joy** — Joh 16:22 ("no one will take your joy from you"); (4) **Eschatological event Joy** — Rev 19:7 (commanded corporate Joy at the Lamb's marriage); Mat 25:21, 23 (entering the master's Joy as final reward); Jude 24 (presented before God's glory "with great joy"); (5) **OT restoration Joy** — M04-E-VCG-01 throughout — the entire sa.s.von corpus is eschatologically oriented.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Partially — less strongly than Joy (Characteristic 2). The covenantal-promise register (M04-O-VCG-04: Jer 29:10; 33:14; Jos 21:45) shows Gladness anchored in promise-fulfilment, which has an eschatological dimension. The ki-tov declarations ("for his steadfast love endures forever") orient Gladness toward the eternal character of God's goodness. Lam 3:25–26 (waiting for the salvation of the Lord) has an eschatological orientation. The makarismos passages (Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15) point to the blessedness declared in Christ as an eschatological state already received. However, compared to Joy's extensive "everlasting joy" and "fullness of joy" vocabulary, Gladness's eschatological orientation is present but less concentrated.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, significantly: (1) **Isa 62:4** — "you shall be called My Delight Is in Her" — God's Delight in Zion as eschatological name and identity; (2) **Mal 3:12** — "you will be a land of delight" — the restored community as a delight-characterized eschatological state; (3) **Isa 58:14** — "then you shall take delight in the Lord, and I will make you ride on the heights of the earth" — Sabbath faithfulness leading to eschatological Delight-in-God and divine exaltation; (4) **Job 22:26** — "then you will delight yourself in the Almighty" — the restored person's future Delight in the Almighty; (5) **Isa 11:8** — sha.a in the messianic age (nursing child playing over cobra's hole) — the carefree Delight of the eschatological peace when fear is removed; (6) **Luk 12:32** — "it is your Father's good pleasure to give you the kingdom" — the eschatological gift driven by divine eudokeo.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 16:11** — "at your right hand are pleasures forevermore" — the most explicit eschatological Pleasure statement in the corpus: pleasures in God's permanent presence; (2) **Eze 20:41** — future divine acceptance as pleasing aroma — eschatological restoration of the worship-Pleasure relationship; (3) **Psa 36:8** — "river of your delights" as the eschatological supply in God's house (anticipating the river of life — Rev 22:1); (4) **Zec 8:19** — former fasts becoming cheerful feasts — the eschatological transformation of communal mourning into Pleasure; (5) **Job 36:11** — years of pleasantness as the outcome of faithful service — anticipating the fullness of pleasantness in the age of complete justice.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Isa 29:14** ("I will again do wonderful things with this people, with wonder upon wonder") — the escalating wonder of God's future acts as an eschatological promise; (2) **Mic 7:15** ("as in the days when you came out of Egypt, I will show them marvellous things") — new-Exodus wonders as eschatological fullness; (3) **Isa 9:6** ("his name shall be called Wonderful Counselor") — the coming child's wonder-name as the eschatological fullness of all divine wonder-acts; (4) **Dan 12:6** ("how long till the end of these wonders?") — apocalyptic wonders as transitional to the final age; (5) **Isa 25:1** ("wonderful things, plans formed of old, faithful and sure") — God's ancient purposes being revealed in wonder as the eschatological disclosure.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, this is constitutive of the characteristic's structure: (1) **Reward in heaven** — Mat 5:12 ("your reward is great in heaven"); (2) **Glory at revelation** — 1Pe 4:13 ("that you may also rejoice and be glad when his glory is revealed"); (3) **Inexpressible and glorious** — 1Pe 1:8 ("joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory") — the present joy already participates in the eschatological quality of glory; (4) **Christ's joy fully realised** — Heb 12:2 (the joy set before Christ → now seated at the right hand) — the eschatological resolution of his suffering-joy is the pattern and promise for the believer's; (5) **Lamb's marriage** — Rev 19:7 (agalliao in the eschatological wedding celebration — the final and unqualified form of the joy that present Suffering-Joy anticipates).

---

##### T5.6.2 — What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Present exultation in God's salvation (Psa 35:9; Isa 61:10; Hab 3:18) anticipates: (1) the completion of all partial deliverances in a final, total rescue; (2) the mutual exultation of God and his people ("your God will exult over you" — Zep 3:17; "I will rejoice in Jerusalem" — Isa 65:19) at the fullest expression of the covenant; (3) the extension of exultation to the whole created order (Psa 96:11; 97:1; Isa 49:13) in cosmic celebration of God's reign. Present exultation is a first-fruits of an eschatological harvest.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Present Joy is consistently characterised as partial and anticipatory: Joh 16:22 (sorrow now, hearts will rejoice when Jesus is seen again — present sorrow is the birth-pangs of future Joy); Psa 51:12 (restore to me Joy — present lack as the pointer to promised fullness); 1Pe 1:6–8 (rejoicing in salvation being revealed — present partial experience of an inheritance fully coming). The present experience of Joy functions as a first-fruits: genuine, real, but not yet at its promised maximum. The NT's emphasis on Joy's fullness (pleron — full, filled, complete) throughout the Johannine corpus confirms this: present joy is real but moves toward completion.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Present Gladness anticipates: (1) the complete vindication of the evaluative faculty — when creation's "very good" (Gen 1:31) is fully restored; (2) the complete fulfilment of all God's good promises (the trajectory of Jos 21:45 applied eschatologically); (3) the blessedness of the fully declared-righteous before God (the makarismos trajectory). Present Gladness in God's character-goodness (ki-tov) is a present experience of what will be the permanent, uninterrupted inner state of those who know him.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Present Delight in God's law (Psa 119; Psa 1) anticipates the eschatological state where law is fully internalized (Jer 31:33 — new covenant writing on the heart) and obedience is no longer law-external but perfectly law-internal (Psa 40:8 fulfilled completely). Present Delight in the Lord (Psa 37:4; Isa 58:14) anticipates the eschatological state of Job 22:26 where Delight in the Almighty is uninterrupted and fully satisfying. Present divine Delight in the person (Psa 18:19; Isa 62:4) anticipates the eschatological community named "My Delight Is in Her" — where God's Delight toward his people is the permanent, publicly declared, eternally sustaining reality.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Present Pleasure in God's beauty (Psa 27:4 — gazing in the temple) anticipates the fullness of Psa 16:11's "pleasures forevermore" when God's presence is unmediated and permanent. The present ni.cho.ach worship-Pleasure relationship anticipates Eze 20:41's final acceptance. Present wisdom-Pleasure (Pro 2:10; 3:17) anticipates a future in which the whole person and community inhabit wisdom's pleasantness completely. The river of delights (Psa 36:8) anticipates the eschatological river of life.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Present Wonder at God's acts in history (VCG-01) anticipates the eschatological fullness of Isa 29:14's "wonder upon wonder" when God's acts will so completely exceed human comprehension that even the wise will be rendered speechless. Present Wonder at the Wonderful Counselor (Isa 9:6) anticipates the fullness of encounter with him whose character is inherently wonder-inducing. Present epistemological humility (Job 42:3; Psa 131:1) anticipates the eschatological state of perfect knowing before the fully-revealed God (1Cor 13:12 — "then I shall know fully, even as I have been fully known" — not in corpus but anticipated by the Wonder-humility posture).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Present Suffering-Joy anticipates: (1) the full replacement of suffering by unqualified joy (1Pe 4:13 — "rejoice and be glad" at revelation, without the "insofar as suffering" qualification); (2) the full revelation of the glory that present joy is already filled with (1Pe 1:8's "filled with glory" → fully manifest at the revelation); (3) the communal eschatological celebration of the Lamb's marriage (Rev 19:7) — the final convergence of all suffering-joy into an unqualified corporate rejoicing. Present Suffering-Joy is partial, coexisting with grief (1Pe 1:6); future fullness is unqualified, permanent, and communal.

---

##### T5.6.3 — If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is one of the most strongly evidenced features of this characteristic; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is extensively evidenced; it is one of Joy's defining features in this corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Eschatological orientation is present but less concentrated than in Joy; not fully silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is evidenced across multiple sub-groups; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is clearly evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is clearly evidenced through multiple prophetic texts; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is constitutive of this characteristic's structure; not silent.

---

#### T5.7 — Deposit Consequence

##### T5.7.1 — Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that deposit produce over time?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

T2.8 found no constitutional deposit evidenced. T5.7 is therefore closed.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

T2.8 identified partial evidence for bodily consequence (Pro 17:22 — joyful heart as good medicine; sustained joy produces positive bodily conditions) but not an explicit constitutional deposit. The developmental consequence of sustained Joy based on the evidence is: increased inner resilience (Neh 8:10); increased generosity (2Cor 8:2); sustained orientation toward God as the ground of all experience; and body-level wellbeing (Pro 17:22 — medicinal effect).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

T2.8 found the evidence silent on constitutional body-level deposit. T5.7 notes: the dispositional deposit of sustained evaluative-gladness is the formed moral discernment capacity — the habituation of the evaluative faculty toward accurate recognition of genuine goodness. This is a soul-level rather than body-level deposit. No body-level deposit is evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

T2.8 found soul-level and heart-level deposit from sustained Delight: (1) **The formation consequence of law-Delight** — Psa 1:2's "tree planted by streams of water" is the deposit-consequence: the person formed by sustained law-Delight develops a productive, stable, fruitful character — "yielding its fruit in its season" — showing that the deposit is not merely a private inner change but a publicly visible character fruitfulness; (2) **The internalized law** — Psa 40:8 ("your law is within my heart") — the developmental consequence of sustained Delight in God's commands is that the law moves from external requirement to internal orientation; this is the most direct evidence of the formation deposit's consequence; (3) **Corruption consequence** — Isa 66:3's soul formed around abominations — the developmental consequence of sustained misdirected Delight is the soul's entrenched orientation toward the wrong object, which eventually determines all moral evaluation (seeing evil as good — Mal 2:17).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

T2.8 found implied soul-level and body-level deposit from sustained Pleasure: (1) **Body-health deposit** — Pro 16:24's "health to the body" from gracious-word Pleasure suggests a somatic deposit of sustained receptive Pleasure: the person who habitually receives genuinely pleasant speech develops a healthier physical constitution; (2) **Wisdom-disposition deposit** — Pro 2:10's "wisdom in the heart" enabling Pleasure in knowledge: sustained engagement with wisdom-Pleasure produces a person formed in the wisdom-disposition that makes knowledge permanently pleasant; (3) **Luxury-formation deposit** — Deu 28:54, 56: the person constitutionally formed by sustained luxury-Pleasure (a.nog) has a fragile constitution that collapses catastrophically when the luxury is removed; the sustained Pleasure deposit has made them unable to function without it.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

T2.8 found cognitive-dispositional deposit from sustained Wonder: (1) **Proclamatory vocation as deposit** — Psa 71:17's lifelong proclamation as the developmental consequence of Wonder formed from youth; the sustained Wonder-deposit produces a person whose primary life-vocation is the declaration of divine marvels; (2) **Epistemological humility as deposit** — Psa 131:1's formed character of not-overreaching; sustained Wonder-humility produces a stable intellectual character; (3) **Generational transmission disposition** — Psa 78:4's "we will not hide them from their children" as the deposit of sustained communal Wonder — the formed community's disposition to pass Wonder on.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

T2.8 found no body-level constitutional deposit. T5.7 notes: the soul-level dispositional deposit of sustained Suffering-Joy is the proven character and steadfastness named in Jas 1:3–4 — the person formed through trials-in-Suffering-Joy becomes one who is "perfect and complete, lacking in nothing." This is the most specific formation-consequence language in M04.

---

##### T5.7.2 — Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

No generational consequence is evidenced for exultation in this corpus. T5.7 closed.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The feast-commandments (Deu 16:11 including "your son and your daughter") and the promise of Joy to "your children" (Jer 31:13 — "young women rejoice in the dance; young men and the old shall be merry") suggest a generational dimension to Joy's formation: the feast practices are explicitly designed to form the inner lives of the next generation. Neh 12:43 (women and children also rejoicing at the wall dedication) shows communal Joy actively forming children through participation. No explicit genetic-deposit language is present.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The ki-tov liturgical tradition (M04-L-VCG-01) is explicitly intergenerational — Psa 100:5 ("his faithfulness to all generations"); Psa 136:1 (the great hallel, designed for communal and generational rehearsal). The wisdom literature (M04-L-VCG-02, 03) is generationally-intended formation: the father passing to the son (Pro 2:20; 4:2; 8:11–19). Pro 13:22 ("a good man leaves an inheritance to his children's children") shows the multigenerational consequence of the good man's character. Gladness's formative tradition is therefore inherently generational.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Deu 30:9** — "as he took delight in your fathers" — God's Delight toward Israel is presented as generationally continuous, persisting from the fathers to the restoration generation; (2) **Deu 12:28** — "that it may go well with you and with your children after you forever, when you do what is good and right in the sight of the Lord" — the obedience-Delight orientation produces multigenerational wellbeing; (3) **Pro 8:30–31** — Wisdom's sha.a.shu.im in the children of man is directed at humanity across all generations — the creative-relational Delight that is constitutive of the human condition generationally; (4) **Mic 1:16** — "children of your delight" — parental Delight is generationally productive of children who are themselves the objects and recipients of that Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially: (1) **The ni.cho.ach worship tradition** — the daily, weekly, and annual pattern transmits the worship-Pleasure relationship intergenerationally through Israel's cultic practice; the Levitical system is generationally transmitted; (2) **Pro 13:22** (cross-registered in Gladness but adjacent) — a good man's inheritance to grandchildren; the person formed in wisdom-Pleasure passes the formation to the next generation. No direct generational deposit language for Pleasure specifically.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes — the most explicitly documented generational consequence of any M04 characteristic: Psa 78:4 ("we will not hide them from their children, but tell to the coming generation the glorious deeds of the Lord… and the wonders that he has done") — the deliberate, active, non-hiding transmission of Wonder to the next generation is the covenant community's formative act. Wonder is the one M04 characteristic whose generational transmission is most explicitly commanded and documented.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

No generational consequence is explicitly evidenced in this corpus. The formation is individual and communal, not generational in the biological sense.

---

##### T5.7.3 — If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

T2.8 found no constitutional deposit. T5.7 closed accordingly.

---

T2.8 found partial evidence for bodily consequence but not explicit deposit language. T5.7 notes: sustained Joy's developmental consequence is inner resilience, generosity, and bodily wellbeing; generational formation is evidenced through prescribed communal practices that include children. T5.7 closed.
