### T6

#### T6.1 — Co-occurrence

##### T6.1.1 — Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The most frequent co-occurring characteristics within M04 in this corpus: (1) **Gladness** (sim.chah, sa.me.ach) — Psa 14:7 ("let Jacob rejoice [gil], let Israel be glad [sa.me.ach]"); Psa 35:9 pairs rejoice (gil_verb) with a soul exulting; Psa 45:15 ("joy and gladness"); Psa 48:11 ("be glad... rejoice"); Isa 35:1 (glad and rejoice); Isa 65:18 (be glad and rejoice); Isa 66:10 — gladness is the most consistent co-occurring inner state with exultation. (2) **Praise and worship** — the exultation passages consistently move into praise (Psa 9:14; 63:5; 100:2; Isa 49:13). (3) **Trust** — Psa 13:5 explicitly pairs trust with rejoicing as precondition and state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Primary co-occurring characteristics: (1) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — the most frequent co-occurrence across the entire corpus; sa.mach and sim.chah appear together (Deu 28:47; Est 8:16–17; Psa 45:15; Isa 35:10; 51:11; Jer 7:34; 33:11; Zep 3:17); chairo and chara appear with agalliasis (Luk 1:14); the phrases "joy and gladness" are formulaic throughout M04-B and M04-E; (2) **Exultation** (Characteristic 1) — gil_verb and sa.mach appear together (Psa 14:7; 32:11; 53:6; Isa 35:1–2; 49:13; 65:18–19; 66:10; Joe 2:21–23); (3) **Wonder** (Characteristic 6) — agalliao and thauma appear in the same passages (Luk 24:41; Mat 28:8 — fear and great joy at the resurrection; the disciples' disbelief from joy); (4) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — sha.a.shu.im and sim.chah in Psalms; eucharistia alongside chairo (M04-C-VCG-06 within this characteristic); (5) **Peace** — not a joy-cluster characteristic but consistently co-occurring in the NT (Rom 14:17; 15:13; Phili 4:4–7).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The dominant co-occurrence patterns: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — the formulaic "joy and gladness" pairing runs throughout both sub-groups: Isa 35:10; 51:3, 11 (sa.s.von — gladness and joy paired in restoration); Jer 31:13; 33:9, 11 (sa.s.von — gladness and joy paired in return from exile); Zec 8:19 (sa.s.von — seasons of joy and gladness); Est 8:16–17 (sa.s.von — gladness and joy among the Jews). Within M04-O: Isa 52:7 (good news bringing peace and happiness — adjacent to Joy's proclaimed content). This co-occurrence is the most analytically significant in the corpus; (2) **Praise and thanksgiving** — M04-L-VCG-01: the ki-tov declarations consistently move into praise; Ezr 3:11; Neh 12:43; the liturgical tradition linking recognition of divine goodness to doxological expression; (3) **Peace** — Isa 52:7 (good news of peace alongside good news of happiness); Mic 6:8 (walking humbly as the third of Gladness's constitutive trio, adjacent to peace/shalom).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Primary co-occurrences: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Jer 7:34; 16:9 ("I will silence the voice of mirth and the voice of gladness, the voice of the bridegroom and the voice of the bride") — the formula pairs gladness/joy with Delight-register celebrations; the removal of Delight and Joy together as judgment; (2) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — the overlap is most prominent in M04-G's tov-comparative register (Psa 73:28; 84:10; 118:8–9 — all in M04-G-VCG-02) where Delight in God's nearness/refuge and Gladness's evaluative-goodness overlap substantially; (3) **Praise and worship** — doxological texts in M04-H-VCG-01 (the "whatever the Lord pleases he does" declarations producing worship) and M04-G (Delight in God's law motivating praise); (4) **Love** — Jer 31:20 ("my heart yearns for him") pairing sha.a.shu.im with parental love vocabulary; 1Th 2:8's affectionate desire (eudokeo) alongside relational self-giving; (5) **Obedience/faithfulness** — M04-M's entire register pairs Delight with obedience (arestos, Joh 8:29; 1Jo 3:22).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primary co-occurrences: (1) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — Psa 133:1 uses both tov (good) and na.im (pleasant) in the same breath: "how good and pleasant it is when brothers dwell in unity"; Zec 8:19 (sa.s.von, sa.me.ach, and tov-cheerful feast together); (2) **Delight** (Characteristic 4) — the no.am/sha.a overlap at the wisdom register: Pro 3:17 (wisdom's ways as pleasantness) is adjacent to Pro 8:30–31's sha.a.shu.im; the luxury register (ed.nah, ta.a.nug) overlaps with Delight's a.nog; Song 7:6 appears in both M04-J-VCG-02 and Delight; (3) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — the festal contexts: Zec 8:19 pairs joy, gladness, and cheerful feasts; (4) **Peace/Shalom** — Pro 3:17 pairs wisdom's pleasantness with "all her paths are peace" — Pleasure and Peace are the twin experiential qualities of wisdom's way.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primary co-occurrences: (1) **Joy/Thanks/Praise** — the VCG-01 proclamatory corpus consistently pairs Wonder with thanks and praise: Psa 9:1 ("I will give thanks… I will recount all your wonderful deeds"); Psa 107:8, 15, 21, 31 (thanks to the Lord for steadfast love and wondrous works — paired refrain); 1Ch 16:9, 12 (sing, sing praises, tell of wondrous works, remember); (2) **Gladness** — Psa 40:5 (wondrous deeds and thoughts, none can compare — the whole heart of Gladness-and-Wonder together in the response to multiplied divine gifts); (3) **Memory/Faithful remembrance** — While not a named M04 characteristic, memory as a faculty is paired with Wonder throughout VCG-01 (Tell-Remember-Meditate triad); (4) **Fear/Awe** — Exo 34:10 ("for it is an awesome thing that I will do with you"); Psa 89:5 (wonder alongside faithfulness of the holy ones); Mar 10:32 (amazed + afraid) — Wonder and fear are closely paired but distinct.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The co-occurrence patterns within the agalliao corpus: (1) **Joy** (Characteristic 2) — Mat 5:12 ("rejoice AND be glad") pairs the commanded agalliao with chairo/chara; 1Pe 1:8 (agalliao) appears alongside chara (the verse carries both the noun and the verb); Rev 19:7 (agalliao alongside chairo); the characteristics are most consistently co-occurring at the intensity-register; (2) **Gladness** (Characteristic 3) — in the M04-E-VCG-01 sa.s.von restoration corpus (which overlaps both Characteristics 2 and 3): Isa 35:10; 51:11 ("everlasting joy... gladness and joy") — the restoration gladness register is the adjacent context of the suffering-reversal; (3) **Peace** — 1Pe 1:6–8's context of tested-faith joy is consistently adjacent to peace/hope in the Petrine framework; (4) **M04-F's fragile cheerfulness** — ba.lag's relationship to the absence of comfort (mav.li.git — Jer 8:18) positions it adjacent to the grief/lament characteristics.

---

##### T6.1.2 — What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Gladness and exultation are regularly paired in the evidence as a natural inner-state cluster — they appear to co-occur so frequently that they may constitute a characteristic pair. Exultation appears to be the more intense, more directional member of the pair; gladness the more diffuse and sustained. The pattern suggests they are related but distinct inner states that naturally accompany each other in worship and celebration contexts.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals that Joy does not operate in isolation but as part of a cluster of positive inner-being states that mutually reinforce each other. Gladness and Joy are the closest and most frequently co-occurring pair — confirming the characteristic-map analysis that they are distinct but adjacent inner-being states. The formula "joy and gladness" throughout the prophetic and historical books is a literary and theological convention reflecting their natural paired experience. The Exultation-Joy pairing (gil + sa.mach) confirms that at the highest moments of divine encounter, Joy rises toward Exultation. The Wonder co-occurrence at the resurrection appearances shows that Joy and Wonder arise simultaneously at the most extraordinary divine events.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The Joy/Gladness co-occurrence confirms the boundary established in the characteristic map and in Characteristic 2's Phase 9: the two characteristics are distinct but naturally adjacent inner states that arise together in the same circumstances. Joy is the active-participatory face; Gladness is the warm-settled cognitive face; they co-occur because genuine encounter with divine goodness produces both the active rejoicing (Joy) and the settled recognition (Gladness) simultaneously. The Praise co-occurrence confirms Gladness as a fundamentally doxological characteristic at its divine-recognition level — recognising God as good naturally overflows into praise-declaration.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Three analytically significant co-occurrence patterns: (1) **Joy-Delight co-occurrence** (Jer 7:34 etc.) confirms adjacency while also confirming distinction — they are silenced together because they are distinct but related forms of positive inner orientation; (2) **Delight-Obedience integration** (M04-M) shows the most distinctive Delight co-occurrence not found in other M04 characteristics: Delight and obedience are constitutively linked in this corpus; pleasing God through commandment-keeping is the form Delight takes in the obedience register; (3) **Delight-Love adjacency** (Jer 31:20; 1Th 2:8) reveals Delight as the pleasurable dimension of Love — they co-occur because Love-without-Delight is obligation without pleasure, and Delight-without-Love lacks the relational commitment that gives Delight its relational grounding.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The tov-na.im pairing of Psa 133:1 ("how good and pleasant") confirms Pleasure as the experiential-felt quality that accompanies and completes Gladness's evaluative-cognitive goodness: Gladness says "this is genuinely good"; Pleasure says "and it feels agreeable." The Pleasure-Peace pairing (Pro 3:17) confirms Pleasure as the inner experiential quality of wisdom's path — wisdom's good is experienced as both pleasant (inner felt quality) and peaceful (inner settled state). The co-occurrence reveals Pleasure as consistently the felt-experiential dimension of what other characteristics evaluate or choose.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The consistent pairing of Wonder with thanks and praise (Psa 9:1; 107:8, 15, 21, 31) confirms Wonder as the motivational source of doxological praise — not merely an inner feeling but the characteristic that drives the praise-response. The pairing of Wonder and fear (Exo 34:10; Mar 10:32) confirms their adjacency while preserving their distinction: fear is the threat-response to encountered power; Wonder is specifically the astonishment-response to what exceeds categories. The Tell-Remember-Meditate triad's consistent co-occurrence with Wonder confirms memory and proclamation as Wonder's defining co-practices.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy co-occurs most consistently with Joy (Characteristic 2) — confirming the analytical judgment that they are related but distinct: Suffering-Joy is Joy in its most paradox-sustaining, Spirit-enabled form operating in the specific context of suffering. The co-occurrence reveals they are on a continuum rather than entirely separate. M04-F's adjacent absence-of-comfort (mav.li.git) shows the characteristic negatively defined: what Suffering-Joy is not is the state of grief-without-comfort that replaces it when the Spirit's enabling is absent.

---

##### T6.1.3 — If no significant co-occurrence patterns emerge, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Co-occurrence with gladness is the dominant pattern; it is consistently evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Co-occurrence with Gladness is the dominant and most analytically significant pattern; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Co-occurrence with Joy is the dominant pattern; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are extensive and analytically significant; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Co-occurrence with Gladness and Peace is the most analytically significant; evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder-praise and Wonder-fear pairings are analytically significant; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Co-occurrence with Joy (Characteristic 2) is the dominant pattern; evidenced.

---

#### T6.2 — Sequential Relationships

##### T6.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation consistently **follows** trust and waiting (Psa 13:5; Isa 25:9; Hab 3:18) and **precedes** praise-declaration (Psa 63:5 — soul exults → mouth praises; Psa 32:11 — be glad and rejoice → shout for joy; Psa 100:2 — serve with gladness → come with singing). The sequence is: trust/seeking → exultation → praise/declaration.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy consistently **follows** a prior inner state and **produces** a subsequent one: (1) **Joy follows** — trust (Psa 33:21); waiting (Isa 25:9); mourning (Jer 31:13; Psa 30:11); comprehension (Neh 8:12); faith (Rom 15:13); encounter with God's acts (Joh 20:20); (2) **Joy produces** — strength (Neh 8:10); generosity (2Cor 8:2); praise and thanksgiving (Psa 100:2; Act 13:48); peace (Phili 4:7 — joy alongside prayer → peace); proclamation (Psa 96:11; Act 8:39); (3) **Joy accompanies** — Gladness (throughout, as a paired state); Peace (Rom 14:17; 15:13; Phili 4:7).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness follows prior conditions and precedes subsequent ones: (1) **Gladness follows** — mourning (Jer 31:13 — "I will turn their mourning into joy"; Isa 61:3 — oil of gladness instead of mourning); suffering/adversity (Lam 3:26 — the gladness of patient waiting comes after endured difficulty); seeking and waiting (Lam 3:25 — the soul who seeks discovers God's goodness); (2) **Gladness precedes** — action and resolve (Neh 2:18 — gladness in God's good hand → communal resolve to build); praise and thanksgiving (the ki-tov formula: gladness-recognition → "give thanks to the Lord"); (3) **Gladness accompanies** — Joy (throughout the paired-formula evidence); trust (M04-O-VCG-04 — gladness in God's good promises accompanies and sustains trust).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Delight precedes** — action (Gen 34:19 — Delight → did not delay); rescue (Psa 18:19 — God delights → rescues); trust (Psa 37:4–5 — delight in the Lord → commit your way); Delight consistently precedes motivated action; (2) **Delight follows** — obedience (Isa 58:13–14 — Sabbath honored → delight in the Lord follows); inward truthfulness (Psa 51:6 — truth in inward being → God delights); correct worship (M04-M — arestos as the quality of obedient-Delight following right action); (3) **Delight accompanies** — sustained Delight accompanies meditation continuously (Psa 1:2 — delight AND meditates as the paired sustained practices).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Pleasure follows** — wisdom (Pro 2:10 — wisdom enters heart → Pleasure in knowledge); obedience (Job 36:11 — listen and serve → years in pleasantness); seeking God (Psa 27:4 — seek and dwell → gaze upon beauty); correct worship (ni.cho.ach corpus — obedient offering → pleasing aroma); (2) **Pleasure accompanies** — Gladness (Psa 133:1 — good and pleasant together); Peace (Pro 3:17 — pleasantness and peace as paired wisdom-qualities); (3) **Pleasure precedes** — health and bodily wellbeing (Pro 16:24 — Pleasure in gracious words → body health); praise and creative expression (Psa 45:1 — pleasing theme → overflowing heart → tongue ready to speak).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Wonder precedes** — proclamation (1Ch 16:9 — wondrous works → tell of them); praise (Psa 9:1 — wonderful deeds → recount with whole heart); obedience (Psa 119:129 — testimonies are wonderful → therefore the soul keeps them); (2) **Wonder follows** — seeing God's acts (Psa 107:24 — saw the deeds of the Lord → wondrous works in the deep); encountering the incomprehensible (Job 37:5 — great things we cannot comprehend → wonder); (3) **Wonder accompanies** — steadfast love (Psa 31:21 — wondrously shown steadfast love; Psa 107:8 — wondrous works alongside steadfast love).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Suffering-Joy follows** — faith-reception (Act 16:34 — comes to faith → rejoices); Spirit-filling (Luk 10:21 — Spirit-rejoicing follows the disciples' return from mission); (2) **Suffering-Joy precedes** — proven character/steadfastness (Jas 1:2–4 — Suffering-Joy precedes the produced steadfastness); eschatological fullness (1Pe 4:13 — present Suffering-Joy precedes the full unqualified joy at glory's revelation); (3) **Suffering-Joy accompanies** — grief (1Pe 1:6 — "grieved by various trials" alongside "in this you rejoice"); suffering (1Pe 4:13 — "insofar as you share Christ's sufferings").

---

##### T6.2.2 — What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Exultation is the mediating inner state between the posture (trust, waiting, seeking) and the expression (praise, declaration, triumphing cry). It is not the first inner state in the sequence nor the last, but the inner-state pivot that transforms the posture into expression.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy is the inner-being pivot between orientation (trust, waiting, seeking) and expression (praise, proclamation, generosity). It is the inner state that converts the posture of the seeking person into the outpouring of the celebrating person. This confirms Joy as the characteristic that mediates between inner-being formation and outward engagement — the inner posture of trust or waiting that is maintained becomes Joy when God acts or is encountered, and Joy then generates the expressions that sustain and build the community.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Gladness is a mediating inner state: it typically follows a prior evaluation or recognition (of divine goodness, of genuinely good news, of restored circumstances) and produces a subsequent orientation (praise, resolve, trust). This is consistent with its cognitive-evaluative primary dimension: evaluation produces Gladness, and Gladness produces action/praise. The sequence is: accurate perception → evaluative recognition → Gladness arising → praise/resolve/action following.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight occupies a mediating and motivating position in the sequence: it follows certain enabling conditions (obedience, inward truth, covenantal relationship) and immediately precedes motivated action (rescue, mission, sustained study). Unlike Joy (which tends to follow divine action) and Suffering-Joy (which follows Spirit-impartation), Delight is positioned both after its enabling conditions and before the action it produces. This bidirectional position confirms Delight as the inner-being engine of the formation arc: it is both the fruit of right orientation and the driver of further formation.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Pleasure is primarily a consequential characteristic — it follows right orientation (wisdom, obedience, worship, seeking) and precedes further expression (health, praise, creativity). Unlike Delight (which both precedes and generates directly) and Joy (which can be commanded), Pleasure arrives as the felt quality of right relationship with God, wisdom, and persons. The sequence reveals Pleasure as characteristically the pleasant texture of a well-ordered inner and relational life.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder occupies the mediating position between perceptive encounter (seeing God's acts) and proclamatory response (declaring them). It is the inner hinge between the divine act and the human doxological response. Unlike Delight (which is self-sustaining in its orientation) and Gladness (which settles inwardly), Wonder is constitutively relational-directional — it moves from the object (God's marvellous act) through the inner being (arrested astonishment) outward to communal proclamation. The sequence is always: encounter → Wonder → proclamation.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Suffering-Joy is positioned between faith/Spirit-reception (which precedes it) and eschatological fullness (which follows it). It is the characteristic that marks the in-between period — the "little while" of 1Pe 1:6 ("though now for a little while you have been grieved") — the transitional state between present suffering-faith and future glory. This eschatological positioning is the most distinctive feature of its sequential relationship: no other M04 characteristic is so explicitly framed as a transitional state between present suffering and future glory.

---

##### T6.2.3 — If no sequential pattern is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Sequential pattern is clearly evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Sequential patterns are among the most clearly evidenced features of this characteristic; not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Sequential patterns are clearly evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Sequential patterns are clearly evidenced in multiple sub-groups; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Sequential patterns are clearly evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Sequential patterns (encounter → Wonder → proclamation) are clearly and consistently evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Sequential patterns are clearly evidenced; not silent.

---

#### T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships

##### T6.3.1 — Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: **praise and declaration** — Psa 63:5 (soul exults → mouth praises with joyful lips); Psa 100:2 (serve with gladness → come before God with singing); re.na.nah throughout (inner exultation → triumphing cry). Exultation appears to produce the expressive-declarative characteristic as its natural output. **Security** — Psa 16:9 (heart glad, whole being rejoices → flesh dwells secure): exultation produces a grounded bodily security. **Sustained orientation toward God** — Psa 89:16 ("all the day") suggests exultation, when habitual, produces and maintains the Godward orientation of the whole inner life.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Strength** — Neh 8:10 ("the joy of the Lord is your strength") — Joy produces inner resilience; (2) **Generosity** — 2Cor 8:2 (abundance of Joy overflowing in generous giving — Joy produces the giving capacity); (3) **Praise and worship** — Joy consistently moves into praise (Psa 100:2; Act 13:48; 1Ch 15:16); (4) **Peace** — Phili 4:7 (commanded Joy → prayer → peace of God); (5) **Co-rejoicing (Characteristic 4 adjacent)** — the Pauline relational Joy (M04-C-VCG-03) produces the sunchairo dimension of co-rejoicing (M04-D); (6) **Endurance** — Col 1:11 (Joy enabling all endurance and patience with Joy); (7) **Health** — Pro 17:22 (joyful heart produces medicinal inner health).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Praise and thanksgiving** — the ki-tov formula (M04-L-VCG-01) consistently shows Gladness in divine goodness producing praise; Ezr 3:11 (gladness in God's goodness → "all the people shouted with a great shout when they praised the Lord"); (2) **Communal resolve and agency** — Neh 2:18 (gladness in God's good hand → "let us rise up and build"); (3) **Strength** — by implication from the closely adjacent Neh 8:10 pattern (the joy of the Lord is strength — the gladness of receiving divine goodness produces inner resilience); (4) **Trust** — the covenantal-promise Gladness (M04-O-VCG-04) produces and sustains trust as its natural fruit.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Wisdom** — Psa 1:2 (delight → meditation → the blessed person formed in wisdom); Psa 111:2 (delight in God's works driving study — wisdom as the fruit of Delight-in-God); (2) **Obedience** — Psa 40:8 (Delight to do God's will — Delight producing willing obedience as its natural overflow); Joh 8:29 (always doing what pleases the Father — continuous obedience from Delight-in-the-Father); (3) **Praise** — M04-G's Delight in God's law overflows into the doxological tradition (Psa 111:2 — great works studied → praise flows); (4) **Generosity** — 1Th 2:8 (affectionate Delight in the Thessalonians → ready to share self and gospel — Delight producing self-giving); Rom 15:26–27 (pleased/eudokeo → contributing generously); (5) **Resilience** — Psa 119:92 (law-Delight producing survival through affliction — resilience as Delight's product under pressure).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Body health** — Pro 16:24 (gracious-word Pleasure producing health to the body); (2) **Creative expression** — Psa 45:1 (a pleasing theme overflowing into praise-poetry — Pleasure producing creativity); (3) **Sustained engagement** — Pro 2:10's Pleasure in knowledge reinforces continued wisdom-seeking; (4) **Praise and worship** — Psa 147:1; 135:3 (the pleasantness of praise producing continued worship); (5) **Divine resolve** — Gen 8:21 (God's Pleasure at the pleasing aroma producing his resolve never again to curse the ground — the most direct Pleasure → action sequence in the corpus).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Praise and thanksgiving** — Psa 9:1; 107:8 etc. — Wonder producing wholehearted praise as its dominant output; (2) **Obedience/faithfulness** — Psa 119:129 ("therefore my soul keeps them") — Wonder producing obedient keeping; (3) **Epistemological humility** — Job 42:3; Psa 131:1 — Wonder producing the formed character of not-overreaching; (4) **Generational faithfulness** — Psa 78:4 — Wonder producing the community's disposition to transmit to the next generation; (5) **Mission impulse** — 1Ch 16:24; Psa 96:3 — Wonder producing the drive to declare among the nations.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Steadfastness** — Jas 1:3–4 (suffering counted as joy → tested faith → steadfastness); (2) **Completeness** — Jas 1:4 ("that you may be perfect and complete, lacking in nothing"); (3) **Sustained agency** — Act 5:41 (rejoicing in suffering → continued apostolic teaching); (4) **Praise and worship** — Luk 10:21 (Spirit-rejoicing → worship-prayer to the Father); Luk 1:47 (spirit exulting → the Magnificat — creative worship). Suffering-Joy produces the characteristics of perseverance, completeness, and continued worshipful-agentive engagement with God's mission.

---

##### T6.3.2 — Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: **trust** (Psa 13:5 — trust in steadfast love → heart rejoices); **seeking God** (Psa 40:16; 70:4 — seeking → rejoicing in him); **hope/waiting** (Isa 25:9 — waiting for God → exultation in his salvation); **righteousness and uprightness** (Psa 68:3; 97:8 — the righteous shall exult; daughters of Judah rejoice because of God's judgments). Exultation is produced by these pre-existing inner orientations when they encounter divine reality.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Trust** (Psa 33:21); (2) **Seeking God** (Psa 40:16; 70:4); (3) **Righteousness / uprightness** (Psa 97:11; Pro 29:6); (4) **Obedience / love for God** — Ecc 2:26 (God gives Joy to the one who pleases him); (5) **Faith in Christ** — Rom 15:13; Act 16:34; (6) **The Spirit** — Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6; (7) **God's word comprehended** — Neh 8:12; Act 13:48.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **Trust** — Psa 73:1 (God is good to the pure in heart — Gladness is the experiential fruit of trusting purity before God); Lam 3:25 (the seeking soul discovers God's goodness — trust/seeking produces the experience of Gladness); (2) **Wisdom** — M04-L-VCG-03 (Pro 8:11; 16:16; 16:8 — wisdom recognising its own surpassing worth is produced through the wisdom formation that precedes it); (3) **Good news reception** — M04-O-VCG-01 (the good word produces gladness in the receiving inner person); (4) **Divine acts** — M04-O-VCG-03 (God's providential acts of rescue and provision produce experienced wellbeing-gladness in those who receive them).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **Fear of God** — Neh 1:11 ("delight to fear your name") — reverence as the inner orientation producing Delight-in-God; (2) **Obedience** — Isa 58:13–14 (Sabbath honoring → "you shall take delight in the Lord") — obedience producing Delight as its fruit; M04-M-VCG-02's pattern throughout shows the good/right done in God's sight producing the good/pleasant state; (3) **Trust** — Psa 37:4's sequence implies that trust enables the disposition of Delight in the Lord; (4) **Wisdom** — Pro 8:11 (wisdom recognized as surpassing all desires — wisdom recognized producing Delight in wisdom); (5) **Divine rescue and exaltation** — the experience of divine rescue (Psa 18:19; Jer 31:20) produces the capacity for deeper Delight in God who delights in the person.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Wisdom** — Pro 2:10; 3:17 (wisdom producing Pleasure in knowledge and pleasantness of ways); (2) **Obedience** — Job 36:11; ni.cho.ach corpus (obedient worship producing pleasing aroma); (3) **Fear of the Lord** — Job 36:11 (listening and serving → Pleasure); Pro 15:16 (fear of Lord better than treasure — the inner quality of fear-of-God orientation correlating with genuine Pleasure); (4) **Gracious speech** — Pro 16:24 (pleasant words → Pleasure received in soul and body); (5) **Relational harmony** — Psa 133:1 (brotherly unity → pleasantness experienced communally).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Encounter with God's acts** — the primary producer; (2) **Deliberate remembrance** — Psa 77:11 (deliberate act of remembering God's wonders re-producing Wonder); (3) **Understanding** — Psa 119:27 ("make me understand… and I will meditate on your wondrous works") — understanding producing capacity for Wonder-meditation; (4) **Consecration** — Jos 3:5 — moral preparation enabling receptive Wonder; (5) **Prayer/seeking** — Psa 119:18 ("open my eyes") — petition producing the God-given capacity for Wonder-perception.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **Faith** — 1Pe 1:8 ("you believe in him and rejoice"); Act 16:34 (belief → rejoicing); (2) **Hope** — the eschatological orientation that grounds present Suffering-Joy is itself a form of hope; (3) **Love for the unseen Christ** — 1Pe 1:8 ("though you have not seen him, you love him... you believe in him and rejoice") — love and faith together produce the agalliao; (4) **The Spirit's gift** — Gal 5:22 (adjacent — Spirit-fruit including joy) — the Spirit's presence is the constitutive producing agent.

---

##### T6.3.3 — Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The evidence suggests exultation is a constituent element of **worship** in the OT framework — the Psalmic and prophetic commanded exultations (Psa 2:11; 32:11; 100:2; Isa 65:18) show exultation as integral to what worship is. Worship is not complete without exultation. Conversely, **gladness** (M04 Characteristic 3) appears to be partially constituted by exultation in the highest registers — the gladness that co-occurs with exultation (Psa 14:7; 48:11; Isa 65:18) may include the exultation as its most elevated expression.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

(1) **Joy is a constituent element of worship** — the feast-commandments make Joy intrinsic to worship; the "serve the Lord with gladness" command (Psa 100:2) makes Joy constitutive of the service-relationship; (2) **Joy is a constituent of the kingdom of God** — Rom 14:17 ("righteousness and peace and joy in the Holy Spirit") names Joy as one of three kingdom-constituents; (3) **Thanksgiving (eucharistia, M04-C-VCG-06) is partly constituted by Joy** — the gratitude register within this characteristic shares Joy's affective character; (4) **Suffering-Joy (Characteristic 7) is partly constituted by Joy** — the paradoxical suffering-Joy register (agalliao in M04-E-VCG-02) is Joy operating in the specific context of suffering, not a fully distinct phenomenon.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Gladness is a constituent of worship** — the ki-tov tradition makes accurate evaluation of divine goodness intrinsic to worship; recognising God as good is the cognitive foundation of doxological worship; (2) **The evaluative-gladness faculty is partly constitutive of wisdom** — M04-L-VCG-03 (wisdom's surpassing worth is recognised through the comparative-evaluative faculty of Gladness); (3) **Gladness-as-wellbeing (M04-O-VCG-03) is partly constituted by Delight** (Characteristic 4) — "it is well with him" (Psa 112:5; 128:2) and Delight's satisfaction in what is genuinely good overlap; the boundary is that Gladness is more cognitively-settled and less object-focused than Delight.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Delight constitutes Love's pleasurable dimension** — Jer 31:20 (sha.a.shu.im alongside "my heart yearns for him"); 1Th 2:8 (affectionate Delight as the pleasurable face of Paul's love for the Thessalonians); Delight is the affective-pleasurable constituent within the broader experience of Love; (2) **Delight constitutes worship's motivational core** — M04-G's Delight in God's word is constitutive of genuine worship; Delight is what makes worship pleasurable and sustained rather than dutiful and intermittent; (3) **Obedience constitutes Delight's obedience-face** — M04-M shows obedience-orientation as a constitutive element of Delight (the soul directed toward what pleases God is the obedience-form of Delight); (4) **Delight is partly constituted by will** — the cha.phets vocabulary makes volitional direction a constitutive element of Delight; Delight without the volitional direction (the will engaged) is merely passive pleasure.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Pleasure is the experiential face of Gladness** — Psa 133:1 (tov + na.im = Gladness's evaluative-cognitive quality + Pleasure's felt-experiential quality); Pleasure is the felt dimension of what Gladness evaluates; (2) **Pleasure is the sensory-experiential face of Delight** — the a.nog/ta.a.nug/ed.nah vocabulary serves both Delight (specific object-focused treasuring) and Pleasure (ambient sensory ease); M04-K-VCG-02 constitutes a Pleasure dimension partly shared with Delight's luxury register; (3) **Ni.cho.ach-Pleasure constitutes the receptive face of the worship-relationship** — the ni.cho.ach is the experiential-Pleasure dimension of the covenantal worship relationship, which includes also obedience, faith, and covenant faithfulness as its constituent elements.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Wonder is a constituent of worship** — the VCG-01 proclamatory corpus shows Wonder as constitutive of genuine biblical worship; worship without Wonder is not the characteristic whole-hearted response Scripture describes; (2) **Wonder partially constitutes epistemological humility** — Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me" contributes to the humility that is constituted by recognising one's cognitive limits before God; (3) **Fear/awe partially constitutes Wonder's VCG-03 register** — dark Wonder is partly constituted by awe-as-dread, though Wonder is the broader term that includes positive astonishment as well.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Suffering-Joy partly constitutes Hope** — the characteristic's eschatological orientation is the affective-experiential face of the theological virtue of hope; (2) **Joy (Characteristic 2) partly constitutes Suffering-Joy** — the agalliao term is shared; Suffering-Joy is Joy in its most paradox-sustaining form; Joy provides the genus of which Suffering-Joy is a specific species; (3) **The Spirit's joy (Gal 5:22) constitutes Suffering-Joy** — the Spirit-fruit of joy is the constitutive Spirit-level element that makes agalliao in suffering possible.

---

##### T6.3.4 — If no causal or constitutive relationship is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Multiple causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced.

---

#### T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing

##### T6.4.1 — Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. **gil_verb / gil** (H1523 / H1524A) appears in M04-A (exultation) and also in the Gladness sub-groups (M04-B uses sim.chah but the terms co-occur in the same verses). **su.s** (H7797) is shared with M04-H (volitional delight: Deu 30:9 assigned to M04-H-VCG-02 — God's relational delight toward persons — using su.s; the same term appears in M04-A as exultation). **re.na.nah** appears across multiple M04 sub-groups. The sharing is significant: the same Hebrew root can function as volitional delight (M04-H), gladness (M04-B), and exultation (M04-A) depending on context.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, extensively: (1) **sa.mach / sim.chah** — shared with M04-E (sa.s.von is a distinct root but co-occurs with sa.mach throughout the corpus); (2) **gil_verb / gil** (H1523/H1524A) — shared with Characteristic 1 (Exultation; both use this root; M04-A-VCG-01 and M04-B-VCG-05 overlap heavily in the same Psalms); (3) **chairo / chara** — shared with M04-E (agalliao appears alongside chairo in 1Pe 1:6–8; Mat 5:12); (4) **ma.s.vo.s** — used for both communal Joy (M04-B) and the Exultation register of Isa 60:15 (M04-A adjacent); (5) **tov** — several tov verses appear in M04-B (Psa 92:1; 147:1; Jer 33:11; Est 5:9) — crossing the Joy / Gladness / Evaluative boundary; (6) **eucharistia** — shared between M04-C-VCG-06 (Thanksgiving within Joy) and M04-M (Pleasing as Obedience, Delight characteristic).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes, extensively: (1) **tov** (H2896A) — the dominant Gladness term, shared with multiple other characteristics. Tov appears in M04-B (Pro 15:13; Pro 17:22 — both M04-B instances of the glad heart/joyful heart: "a glad heart makes a cheerful face" — M04-B-VCG-04, using sa.me.ach for the person but tov implicit in the gladness-wellbeing context). Tov also appears in adjacent clusters (M04-H — Delight in the volitional sense "as seems good and right to you" — Jer 26:14, M04-H-VCG-03 cross-assignment); (2) **sa.s.von** — shared with M04-E (Characteristic 7's overlap sub-group). The M04-E-VCG-01 sa.s.von corpus (gladness as restoration-reverse-of-sorrow) sits under both Gladness's experiential register and Characteristic 7's suffering-reversal register; (3) **makarismos** (G3108) — shared with the blessedness vocabulary in other NT registers.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, extensively: (1) **tov** (H2896A) — shared with Gladness (Characteristic 3) extensively; M04-G-VCG-02 and M04-H-VCG-03 carry tov in forms that also appear in Characteristic 3's M04-L and M04-O sub-groups; (2) **sha.a.shu.im / sha.a** — partially shared with the M04-E corpus (sa.s.von is distinct but sha.a appears in Isa 66:12 which is also adjacent to Characteristic 2's restoration register); (3) **eudokeo** (G2106) — shared with Characteristic 2 (Joy) where it appears in the NT blessing/pleasure registers; (4) **cha.phets / che.phets** — appear across M04 and also in adjacent clusters; (5) **arestos** (G0701) — uniquely in M04-M-VCG-02 within M04; (6) **ni.cho.ach** — shared between M04-M-VCG-01 (correct worship) and M04-P-VCG-01 (misdirected worship) — the same term serving both the obedience and corrupt registers of Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **ni.cho.ach** (H5207) — shared with M04-M (obedience-orientation: Lev 1:17; Num 15:13) and M04-P (corrupted worship: Eze 6:13; 16:19; 20:28) — the same soothing-aroma term serves righteous worship (M04-K-VCG-01), obedience-pleasing (M04-M), and its corrupt counterpart (M04-P); (2) **ta.a.nug** (H8588) — shared with M04-N (Mic 1:16 — parental Delight in children); (3) **a.nog** (H6026) — shared with M04-G (Delight in God: Psa 37:4, 11; Isa 58:14) and M04-K-VCG-02 (luxury register); (4) **tov** (H2896A) — M04-K-VCG-03's better-than comparatives use tov, shared extensively with Gladness (Characteristic 3) and other registries; (5) **ed.nah** (H5730B) — Psa 36:8 and 2Sa 1:24 are the primary instances; (6) **na.im/na.em/no.am** — uniquely concentrated in M04-J within M04.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **pa.la** (H6381) — the dominant Wonder term appears in M04-I but also in M04-K cross-assigned verse (Mar 10:24 thambeō in Pleasure) and in 2Sa 1:26 (cross-assigned to M04-I-VCG-02 from the Pleasure register); (2) **thambeō** (G2284) — appears in Mar 10:24 (in M04-K-VCG-01 for Pleasure) and Mar 1:27; 10:32 (in M04-I-VCG-01 for Wonder) — the same Greek term serving both Pleasure (amazement at Jesus' teaching) and Wonder (amazement at Jesus' exorcism/advance); (3) **thaumazō** (G2296) — appears in M04-I-VCG-03 (Rev 17:6, 7) and M04-N-VCG-02 (Rev 13:3; 17:8 — beast-captivation Wonder in Delight); (4) **thauma** (G2295) — appears in Rev 17:6 (Wonder, VCG-03) and 2Cor 11:14 (negated Wonder); (5) **pa.la** appears in 2Sa 1:26 (extraordinary love — assigned to M04-I-VCG-02) which also appears in M04-J-VCG-02 for Pleasure.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **agalliao** (G0021) — shared with Joy (Characteristic 2): Joh 8:56 (Abraham's agalliao); Act 16:34 (jailer's agalliao — both appear in Joy's evidence and here); 1Pe 1:8 (agalliao alongside chara — the terms appear together in Joy's corpus and here); Heb 1:9 (oil of gladness — agalliasis alongside Psa 45:7's sa.s.von, shared between Joy's eschatological register and this characteristic); (2) **ba.lag** (H1082) — not shared with other M04 characteristics — unique to M04-F-VCG-01 in this cluster; (3) **mav.li.git** (H4010) — unique to M04-F-VCG-01 (Jer 8:18).

---

##### T6.4.2 — Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes. The su.s root is shared across M04-A (exultation in God's salvation) and M04-H (God's delight in prospering — Deu 30:9, previously assigned to M04-H-VCG-02 in Step 5). This root-level sharing suggests that exultation and volitional delight are closely related inner-being states at the lexical level — they share the same affective intensity and directedness, differing primarily in the constitutional faculty engaged (affective-responsive vs. volitional-directed).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes. The sa.mach root (H8055) and its nominal form sim.chah (H8057) are the dominant shared root, generating sa.mach (verb), sim.chah (noun), and sa.me.ach (adjective) — all three grammatical forms used across M04-B. This root also appears in M04-E's sa.s.von (related root; distinct but semantically adjacent). The chairo root generates chairo (verb) and chara (noun) — the two dominant NT Joy forms — and sunchairo (M04-D), and is related to the agalliao register of M04-E.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: **tov** is the most widely-distributed root in the Hebrew inner-being vocabulary — it generates the noun/adjective (H2896A, used here), appears in multiple other registries (goodness, uprightness), and forms the root for related terms. The pervasive use of tov across M04-L (evaluative), M04-O (circumstantial), and adjacent characteristics confirms that Gladness shares its primary root with the widest possible range of inner-being goodness-related states.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **tov root** — shared with Gladness (Characteristic 3) at the root level — both characteristics draw on H2896A tov, making Delight and Gladness root-level kin; the tov root in M04-G-VCG-02 (experiential Delight in God) and in Characteristic 3's M04-O (circumstantial Gladness) shows the same root serving two distinct but adjacent characteristics; (2) **cha.phets root** — H2654A, H2655, H2656 share the same root across verbal, adjectival, and nominal forms; the root's internal family structure (verb, noun, adjective) confirms Delight as a multi-modal characteristic; (3) **sha.a root** — sha.a (H8173B) and sha.a.shu.im (H8191) share the same root, the plural-of-intensity form intensifying the basic verbal meaning.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **na.em root** (na.im H5273A, na.em H5276, no.am H5278, na.a.man H5282) — the na.em root generates four distinct vocabulary forms all serving Pleasure's relational-pleasantness register; the root-family is essentially dedicated to Pleasure within M04; (2) **ni.cho.ach root** — related to the nuach root (to rest, give rest); the soothing-aroma quality is semantically connected to the concept of rest and settling; (3) **a.nog root** — generates a.nog (H6026, verb) and ta.a.nug (H8588, noun) and a.nag (H6029), shared across M04-K and M04-G.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **pa.la/pe.le/miph.la.ah** — the pa.la root generates the verbal (H6381), nominal (H6382), and construct-nominal (H4652) forms; all three appear in M04-I; the root's internal family is dedicated to the Wonder register; (2) **thauma root** — thauma (G2295), thaumazō (G2296), thambeō (G2284) — three distinct Greek wonder-terms sharing the thauma root; all three serve the Wonder/astonishment register in the NT, distributed across M04-I and cross-assigned verses.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: **agalliao** shares the agan+hallesthai root with agalliasis (the noun form appearing in Luk 1:44; Heb 1:9; Jude 24) — these generate the same root across both Characteristic 2's evidence (particularly in M04-C-VCG-04 — Heb 1:9) and Characteristic 7's evidence (M04-E-VCG-02). The shared root confirms the Joy/Suffering-Joy relationship as a root-level lexical kinship, not merely a semantic proximity.

---

##### T6.4.3 — What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The shared vocabulary (su.s, gil) across exultation, gladness, and volitional delight confirms that these characteristics are not sharply bounded in the Hebrew inner-being vocabulary — they form a cluster of related inner states sharing the same high-intensity positive register. The distinctions between them (Exultation's surging directedness, Gladness's warm diffuseness, Volitional Delight's will-faculty engagement) are real but operate within a shared semantic field.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The extensive vocabulary sharing between Joy (Characteristic 2), Gladness (Characteristic 3), and Exultation (Characteristic 1) confirms that these three characteristics form a semantic cluster: they are distinct inner-being states that share the same Hebrew and Greek lexical family because they are cognate experiences. Joy and Gladness are so lexically close (sa.mach / sim.chah appear in the same passages, often in synonymous parallelism) that the distinction between them is primarily phenomenological (active-participatory vs. warm-diffuse) rather than lexical. This has implications for Phase 9 findings: the Joy/Gladness boundary should be expected to appear as an important analytical question in Session D synthesis.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Tov's pervasive presence across moral, relational, and circumstantial registers confirms that Gladness (as the evaluative-cognitive recognition of genuine goodness) is the broadest-scope positive inner characteristic in M04 — it is the characteristic most directly connected to the concept of goodness itself, which is why its primary term (tov) ranges across the widest semantic field of any M04 term. The vocabulary sharing with Joy (sa.mach/sim.chah frequently appear alongside tov in the same passages) confirms the Joy/Gladness adjacency already established.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The tov-root sharing between Delight (M04-G-VCG-02) and Gladness (Characteristic 3) is the most conceptually significant: both characteristics claim portions of the tov corpus, which means they are using the same primary Hebrew term to name different inner-being states. The difference is that Gladness uses tov in its evaluative-cognitive and circumstantial registers, while Delight uses tov in its experiential-orientation registers (Psa 73:28 — "it is good to be near God"; Psa 118:8–9 — taking refuge in the Lord as better). The conceptual relationship revealed: Delight and Gladness are the two closest characteristics in M04, sharing a root and a lexical corpus while remaining analytically distinct through their different primary dimensions (Delight's affective-volitional vs. Gladness's cognitive-evaluative).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The ni.cho.ach sharing across M04-K-VCG-01 (Pleasure), M04-M (obedience-orientation), and M04-P (corrupt worship) confirms that the same worship-pleasure mechanism is operative across three different moral contexts — what differs is the object and the inner orientation, not the mechanism itself. The a.nog sharing across Pleasure (M04-K) and Delight (M04-G) confirms the closest vocabulary relationship between these two characteristics. The tov sharing across Pleasure (M04-K-VCG-03) and Gladness (Characteristic 3) confirms the root-level kinship identified in the Gladness analysis.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The thaumazō sharing between Wonder (M04-I-VCG-03 — Rev 17:6, 7) and Delight's beast-captivation (M04-N-VCG-02 — Rev 13:3; 17:8) is analytically significant: both Rev 13:3 and Rev 17:6–7 describe the same human response (marvelling) to the same adversarial powers; but one instance (thaumazō in Rev 13:3; 17:8) is classified under Delight (captivation-delight) and the other (Rev 17:6 — John's marvelling) is classified under Wonder (dark astonishment at evil). This confirms that the same vocabulary term can serve distinct inner-being characteristics depending on its object and the nature of the inner engagement.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The shared agalliao/agalliasis root between Characteristic 2 (Joy) and Characteristic 7 (Suffering-Joy) confirms that these are the most closely related characteristics in M04 — they are not merely adjacent but share the same lexical family at its most intense register. The difference is contextual rather than lexical: the same term (agalliao) names Joy's most intense form in favourable circumstances and Suffering-Joy's primary form in adverse circumstances. The context of suffering is the distinguishing marker of Characteristic 7, not a distinct vocabulary.

---

##### T6.4.4 — If no significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Extensive vocabulary sharing is evidenced; the shared vocabulary is one of the defining analytical challenges for this cluster.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Extensive vocabulary sharing confirmed; not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Extensive root-level vocabulary sharing confirmed, especially with Gladness (Characteristic 3); not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Extensive vocabulary sharing confirmed, especially with Delight (a.nog) and Gladness (tov); not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Vocabulary sharing with Delight (thaumazō) and Pleasure (thambeō; 2Sa 1:26 pa.la) is evidenced; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing with Characteristic 2 (Joy) is confirmed at the root level; not silent.

---

#### T6.5 — Distinctions

##### T6.5.1 — Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

**Gladness** (M04 Characteristic 3) is the closest adjacent characteristic — both are positive inner states, both use overlapping vocabulary (gil_verb; su.s appears in both), both are Godward in their primary orientation. The distinction: Exultation is characterised by **surging intensity, directedness, and triumph** — it rises toward its object; Gladness is characterised by **warmth, brightness, and settled positivity** — it pervades the inner being without the surge. Psa 14:7 — "let Jacob rejoice (gil), let Israel be glad (sa.me.ach)" — places them in synonymous parallel, suggesting they are experienced together, but the different terms signal different qualities of the same positive inner territory.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**Gladness** (Characteristic 3) is the closest adjacent characteristic. The distinction has been established across Phase 9: (1) **Activity vs. warmth** — Joy is active and participatory (rejoices *in* something, engaged, directional); Gladness is warm, diffuse, and settled (the heart is glad, the inner condition is bright); (2) **Independence from circumstance** — Joy can transcend and persist through adverse circumstances (Hab 3:18; 2Cor 6:10; 1Pe 1:6); Gladness is more characteristically responsive to circumstances assessed as good (M04-O; M04-L); (3) **Communal structure** — Joy has a constitutively communal dimension (feast-joy; sunchairo); Gladness is more characteristically individual or circumstantially responsive; (4) **Object-specificity** — Joy consistently names its object ("rejoice in the Lord," "rejoice at his birth"); Gladness is more characteristically a condition without always specifying an object.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

**Joy** (Characteristic 2) is the closest adjacent characteristic. The distinction has been progressively established across both Phase 9 runs: (1) **Activity vs. settled warmth** — Joy is active, participatory, and engaged (rejoices *in* something, commanded to constant orientation); Gladness is settled, warm, and diffuse (the inner condition of one who has assessed that things are genuinely good); (2) **Independence from circumstance** — Joy can transcend adverse circumstances (Phili 4:4 "always"; Hab 3:18); Gladness in its circumstantial face (M04-O) is more characteristically responsive to assessed-good circumstances — Jon 4:3, 8 (circumstances reversed → Gladness collapses); (3) **Primary faculty** — Joy's primary dimension is affective; Gladness's primary dimension is cognitive-evaluative; (4) **Command-susceptibility** — Joy is more directly commandable (Phili 4:4; 1Th 5:16; the Deuteronomic feast-commands); Gladness's evaluative face is less directly commandable — one must be formed in the capacity for accurate evaluation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

**Gladness** (Characteristic 3) is the closest adjacent characteristic, sharing the tov vocabulary and overlapping in certain registers (Psa 73:28; 84:10; 118:8–9 appear in both clusters' evidence). The precise distinctions: (1) **Object-focus vs. diffuseness** — Delight is always delight *in* a specific object (law, God, person, wisdom, idol); Gladness is diffuse warmth, an inner state of being-glad that is not necessarily anchored to a single treasured object; (2) **Affective-volitional vs. cognitive-evaluative** — Delight's primary dimension is affective-volitional (the pleasurable orienting of affect and will toward the object); Gladness's primary dimension is cognitive-evaluative (the assessment that something is genuinely good); (3) **Resting vs. assessing** — Delight rests in its object; Gladness assesses that things are good; (4) **Breadth** — Delight has 247 verses across 5 sub-groups; Gladness has 133 verses across 2 sub-groups; Delight is the broader characteristic, encompassing a corrupt register (M04-P) that Gladness does not have as a primary concern.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

**Delight** (Characteristic 4) is the closest adjacent characteristic. Precise distinctions: (1) **Object-focus vs. ambient** — Delight focuses on a specific treasured object (sha.a.shu.im, cha.phets directed toward God, law, persons); Pleasure is the more ambient quality of agreeableness received from what surrounds the person without necessarily focusing on a single treasured object; (2) **Volitional vs. receptive** — Delight has a strong volitional component (cha.phets/eudokeo); Pleasure is more purely receptive (na.im/ni.cho.ach); (3) **Constitutional depth** — Delight operates primarily at the inner being/soul level (Rom 7:22; Mat 12:18); Pleasure operates across a wider constitutional range including explicit body-level (Pro 16:24; Deu 28:54, 56); (4) **Shared vocabulary** — a.nog appears in both, marking the overlap zone: Psa 37:4's a.nog in Delight (directed toward God as specific object) vs. Deu 28:54's a.nog in Pleasure (ambient luxury-ease) — the same root, different directional structure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**Exultation** (Characteristic 1) is the closest adjacent in terms of the response to God's extraordinary acts. Precise distinctions: (1) **Arrested vs. surging** — Wonder stills the inner being; Exultation surges upward; (2) **Receptive-perceptive vs. active-emotive** — Wonder is the response to what is seen/encountered; Exultation is the active upward thrust of the inner being; (3) **Cognitive boundary vs. emotive peak** — Wonder arises at the limit of comprehension; Exultation arises at the peak of received salvation/victory; (4) **Proclamatory vs. participatory** — Wonder's characteristic expression is telling/declaring; Exultation's characteristic expression is jubilation and shouting; (5) **Not requiring Spirit** — Wonder is available to the natural person encountering the extraordinary; Exultation in its highest register may require Spirit-production.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

**Joy** (Characteristic 2) is the closest — confirmed by the shared agalliao vocabulary, the co-occurrence patterns, and the sequential relationship. The precise distinction: (1) **Context** — Joy (Characteristic 2) rejoices in what is genuinely celebratable and good; Suffering-Joy rejoices specifically in the context of what is genuinely adverse and painful; (2) **Mechanism** — Joy can arise through multiple mechanisms (word comprehension, divine encounter, volitional cultivation, feast practice); Suffering-Joy's primary mechanism is Spirit-impartation and eschatological grounding; (3) **Constitutive role of suffering** — for Suffering-Joy, the suffering is not merely the context but the constitutive occasion of the characteristic: "insofar as you share Christ's sufferings" (1Pe 4:13) — the sharing of suffering is the condition and form of the joy; (4) **Eschatological concentration** — Suffering-Joy has a higher eschatological concentration than Joy; every instance of its primary (agalliao) evidence is grounded in eschatological reality.

---

##### T6.5.2 — Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The boundary is most visible in Hab 3:18 ("yet I will rejoice in the Lord") and Psa 13:5 ("my heart shall rejoice in your salvation"). These are exultation — deliberate, surging, directed acts — in the face of adversity. Gladness (M04-O, M04-L) does not operate this way: it is the warm inner response to circumstances assessed as good. Exultation can survive the removal of all good circumstances (Hab 3:18); Gladness is characteristically responsive to present-good circumstances. This is the sharpest boundary.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The "joy and gladness" formulaic pairing (Est 8:16; Isa 35:10; 51:11; Jer 7:34; 33:11; Zep 3:17) is where the boundary is most porous. The pairing suggests co-occurrence rather than identity — both states arise together, confirming they are distinct but adjacent. The boundary is clearest at the extremes: Hab 3:18's volitional Joy under total material loss is not Gladness (Gladness would not characteristically persist under such conditions); conversely, Lam 3:26's "it is good that one should wait quietly for the salvation of the Lord" is Gladness (settled warm inner brightness under adversity) rather than active Joy.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The formulaic "joy and gladness" pairing is the boundary zone. The boundary is clearest at the extremes: (1) Hab 3:18 — volitional joy despite total material loss — this is Joy, not Gladness (Gladness's circumstantial face would not persist under such conditions); (2) Lam 3:26 — "it is good to wait quietly for the salvation of the Lord" — this is Gladness (the evaluative recognition that quiet waiting is the appropriate and genuinely beneficial inner posture) rather than Joy (which would be the active exulting in what is coming). (3) The ki-tov praise declarations (M04-L-VCG-01) — these are primarily Gladness (cognitive recognition of divine goodness producing praise) rather than Joy (though they produce Joy as a co-occurrence).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The tov-comparative verses (Psa 73:28 — "it is good to be near God"; Psa 118:8–9 — "better to take refuge in the Lord") are the boundary zone. The boundary: these verses are assigned to M04-G-VCG-02 (Delight sub-group) rather than M04-L/O (Gladness sub-groups) because their inner-being content is specifically the experiential orientation of the soul toward God as refuge and nearness — object-focused Delight — rather than the evaluative recognition that God's character is good (Gladness). Psa 73:28's "it is good to be near God" is the soul's resting orientation toward God (Delight) rather than the cognitive appraisal that divine nearness is morally superior (Gladness), though both elements are present. The boundary is thin but real.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The a.nog overlap is the boundary zone: (1) a.nog in M04-G (Psa 37:4 — "delight yourself in the Lord") is Delight because it is specifically directed toward God as the treasured object with the reflexive hitpael; (2) a.nog in M04-K-VCG-02 (Deu 28:54, 56 — the pampered person's comfort) is Pleasure because it names a general quality of physical ease rather than directed orientation toward a specific object; (3) ta.a.nug appears in M04-N-VCG-01 (Mic 1:16 — parental Delight in children) as directed attachment and in M04-K-VCG-02 (Pro 19:10; Ecc 2:8; Mic 2:9) as ambient sensory luxury — the same term serving both directed-Delight and ambient-Pleasure contexts.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The Song of the Sea (Exo 15) is the boundary zone: Exo 15:11 ("who is like you… doing wonders?") appears in M04-I-VCG-01 (Wonder) — the question form and the pe.le term mark it as Wonder-language; but Exo 15's larger context is exultation-language (the whole poem is a song of triumph). The boundary: Exo 15:11 is Wonder because it specifically names God's incomparability through the wonder-vocabulary and the rhetorical question of non-comparability; the surrounding song is Exultation. The wonder-verse is the perceptive-cognitive hinge within the larger exultation-song.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The boundary is the role of suffering: where agalliao appears in contexts of blessing, faith-reception, or divine encounter without adversity as the constitutive occasion (Joh 8:56 — Abraham's anticipatory joy; Act 16:34 — coming-to-faith joy), it belongs to Characteristic 2 or sits in the boundary zone. Where agalliao appears with suffering as the constitutive context and occasion (1Pe 1:6 — grieved by trials yet rejoicing; 1Pe 4:13 — insofar as sharing Christ's sufferings; Mat 5:12 — persecuted yet commanded to rejoice; M04-F's ba.lag — attempted cheer under extreme adversity), it belongs to Characteristic 7. The 1Pe 1:6–8 passage is the most complex boundary case — it holds both the eschatological-Joy dimension and the suffering-paradox dimension simultaneously.

---

##### T6.5.3 — Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Primarily **degree and direction**. The constitutional level (soul and heart) is shared. The direction for both is primarily Godward. The difference is in degree (intensity: exultation is the more surging, triumphant state; gladness is warmer and more diffuse) and in the relationship to circumstances (exultation can transcend adverse circumstances; gladness is more responsive to them).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Primarily **kind and degree**, with some difference in constitutional level. Kind: Joy is active/participatory; Gladness is warm/diffuse — these are different kinds of inner-being state, not merely different intensities of the same state. Degree: Joy is consistently more intense than Gladness in the evidence (the feast-joy is exuberant; Gladness can be quiet). Constitutional level: both are primarily heart-located; Joy additionally appears at spirit level (Luk 1:47; Gal 5:22) more consistently than Gladness.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Primarily **kind** (different types of inner-being state: cognitive-evaluative warmth vs. active participatory engagement) with secondary **degree** differences (Joy is typically more intense) and minor **constitutional level** differences (Joy has stronger spirit-level evidence through the NT; Gladness has stronger cognitive-faculty evidence). The direction is similar (both primarily Godward in their healthy forms). Kind is the primary distinction.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Primarily **kind** — they are different types of inner-being state: object-focused resting-satisfaction (Delight) vs. diffuse cognitive warmth (Gladness). Secondary **constitutional level** difference: Delight's primary constitutional home is the soul and the inner being (Mat 12:18; Rom 7:22); Gladness's is the cognitive-evaluative faculty and heart. The direction is similar (both have God as their proper primary object); the degree varies (Delight can be more intense in the sha.a.shu.im register, Gladness more stable in the ki-tov register).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primarily **direction and kind**: (1) Direction — Delight is directed toward a specific treasured object; Pleasure is received from what is genuinely agreeable; (2) Kind — Delight is fundamentally volitional-affective (the will and affect oriented toward the object); Pleasure is fundamentally receptive-experiential (the inner being receiving pleasantness); (3) Constitutional level — secondary difference: Delight's primary constitutional evidence is the soul and inner being; Pleasure's is more explicitly bodily and sensory.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primarily **kind**: they are different types of inner response to God's extraordinary acts — one arrested-cognitive (Wonder) and one active-emotive-upward (Exultation). Secondary **direction**: Wonder is directed perceptively toward the wondrous object; Exultation is directed actively upward in response. Not merely a difference of degree (stronger Joy) but a qualitatively different inner state.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Primarily **kind and context**: (1) Kind — the paradoxical structure (joy through/in suffering rather than joy in what is good) marks a different type of inner-being state; (2) Context — the constitutive role of suffering is the defining contextual marker; (3) Constitutional level — Suffering-Joy has a stronger spirit-level evidence (Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21) than Joy's general corpus, though Joy also has spirit-level registers (1Th 1:6). The direction is similar (both Godward); the degree is similar in the agalliao register (both intense).

---

##### T6.5.4 — If no significant distinction work is required, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Distinction work is required and evidenced particularly for the Exultation / Gladness boundary.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Joy/Gladness distinction is one of the most analytically significant findings of Phase 9 for M04; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Joy/Gladness distinction is the primary analytical task for this characteristic in Phase 9; extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Delight/Gladness distinction is the most significant boundary-work for this characteristic in Phase 9; evidenced above.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Delight/Pleasure distinction is the most significant boundary-work for Characteristic 5; evidenced above.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Wonder/Exultation distinction is the most significant boundary-work for this characteristic; evidenced above.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Joy/Suffering-Joy distinction is the most significant boundary-work for this characteristic; extensively evidenced.

---

#### T6.6 — Shared Verse Anchors

##### T6.6.1 — Does any verse in this characteristic's evidence base also function as a primary anchor in another characteristic's study?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: **Deu 30:9** (su.s) was assigned to M04-H-VCG-02 (God's relational delight toward persons — Volitional Delight characteristic) in Step 5. The same verse appears in the M04-A corpus here as an exultation instance. This shared verse reveals that Deu 30:9 carries evidence for both Exultation and Volitional Delight — the su.s term in that verse spans both characteristics. Similarly, **Psa 119:14 and 119:162** (su.s — rejoice in God's testimonies/word) were assigned to M04-A-VCG-01 but are directly adjacent to M04-G's delight-in-God's-word characteristic; these verses may function as anchors at the Exultation/Delight boundary.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, multiple shared anchors: (1) **Psa 35:9** — assigned to M04-A (Exultation, VCG-01) and also appears in M04-B-VCG-05 (Gil_verb) — shared between Exultation and Joy; (2) **Psa 16:9** — appears in M04-A corpus (Exultation) and in M04-B-VCG-05 (sa.mach) — shared; (3) **Isa 65:18** — uses both ma.s.vo.s (M04-B-VCG-05) and gi.lah (M04-E-VCG-01) — shared between sub-groups; (4) **1Pe 1:8** — appears in both M04-C-VCG-05 (chara) and M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao) — shared across the Joy/Suffering-Joy boundary; (5) **Mat 5:12** — appears in M04-C-VCG-05 (chairo) and M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao) — shared; (6) **Rev 19:7** — appears in M04-C-VCG-04 (chairo) and M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao) — shared.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple shared anchors: (1) **Psa 63:3** ("your steadfast love is better than life") — M04-L-VCG-01 (Gladness) and Characteristic 1 (Exultation) — the same verse names God's steadfast love as the supreme good while also belonging to the exultation corpus; (2) **Isa 52:7** (M04-O-VCG-01) — shared with the Joy corpus; (3) **Gen 1:31** ("very good") — M04-L-VCG-01 anchor, but also the creation-foundation verse that grounds multiple other characteristics' understanding of created design; (4) **Mic 6:8** (M04-L-VCG-02) — the programme's OBS-027 identifies six other registries sharing this anchor; it is one of the most cross-characteristic anchors in the entire programme; (5) **Eze 36:31** (M04-L-VCG-02) — shared anchor with Registry 97 and multiple other registries per SP-006.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple shared anchors: (1) **Psa 51:6** ("you delight in truth in the inward being, and you teach me wisdom in the secret heart") — primary anchor for Delight (God's delight in interior truth as the ground of transformation); also a primary anchor for Characteristic 2's inner-transformation registers; (2) **Psa 40:8** ("I delight to do your will; your law is within my heart") — shared with Hebrews 10:7's christological application; (3) **1Sa 15:22** ("to obey is better than sacrifice") — appears in both M04-H-VCG-02 (Delight, God's pleasure in obedience) and M04-M-VCG-02 (obedience-orientation sub-group); (4) **Jer 9:24** — "I delight in steadfast love, justice, and righteousness" — shared with multiple programme registries; (5) **Isa 53:10** — "it was the will of the Lord to crush him" — primary christological anchor shared with multiple programme registries; (6) **Mat 3:17; 12:18; 17:5** — the eudokeo baptism/transfiguration verses are shared with every cluster discussing the Father-Son relationship.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple shared anchors: (1) **Psa 37:16** (better is the little of the righteous) — shared anchor between M04-K-VCG-03 (Pleasure) and M04-L-VCG-03 in Gladness (wisdom-comparative); (2) **Pro 15:15–17** (cheerful heart/better-than comparatives) — shared across Gladness (comparative evaluations) and Pleasure (experiential quality); (3) **1Sa 15:22** ("to obey is better than sacrifice") — shared between M04-M (Delight-obedience) and M04-K-VCG-03 adjacent (better-than framework); (4) **Psa 34:8** ("taste and see" — cross-assigned to M04-K in this corpus) — widely shared across multiple registries; (5) **Song 7:6** — shared between M04-J (Pleasure's relational register) and M04-N's parental Delight; (6) **Zec 8:19** — shared between M04-B (feast-joy) and M04-K (cheerful-feast Pleasure).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple shared anchors: (1) **Psa 118:23** ("this is the Lord's doing; it is marvellous in our eyes") — primary Wonder anchor; also the christological anchor of Mat 21:42 (rejected stone); shared across Wonder, Exultation, and the programme's Christology; (2) **Isa 9:6** ("Wonderful Counselor") — shared between Wonder and every study addressing the incarnate Christ's identity; (3) **2Sa 1:26** (pa.la for Jonathan's extraordinary love) — shared between Wonder (VCG-02) and Pleasure (M04-J-VCG-02 for the relational-pleasantness of Jonathan); (4) **Exo 15:11** (doing wonders, Exo 15 Song of the Sea) — shared between Wonder (VCG-01) and Exultation (Characteristic 1); (5) **Deu 28:59** (extraordinary afflictions — pa.la in judgment) — shared between Wonder (dark register) and Gladness's structural-opposite section.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Multiple shared anchors: (1) **1Pe 1:8** — carries evidence for both Characteristic 2 (Joy — chara) and Characteristic 7 (Suffering-Joy — agalliao) simultaneously; (2) **Mat 5:12** — carries both M04-C-VCG-05 (chairo) and M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao) — shared between Characteristics 2 and 7; (3) **Rev 19:7** — carries both M04-C-VCG-04 (chairo) and M04-E-VCG-02 (agalliao) — shared; (4) **Joh 8:56** — agalliao in a non-suffering context, making it sit in the boundary between Characteristics 2 and 7; (5) **Psa 45:7** (sa.s.von — M04-E-VCG-01) → applied christologically in Heb 1:9 — shared anchor between Characteristic 7's restoration register and Characteristic 1 (Exultation's royal-anointing dimension).

---

##### T6.6.2 — What does the shared anchor reveal about the relationship between the two characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The shared anchors confirm the porous boundary between Exultation and Volitional Delight (both using su.s in the God-to-human relational register) and between Exultation and Delight-in-God's-word (Psa 119:14; 119:162 — the exulting-in-testimonies verses that could equally evidence M04-G). These shared anchors are evidence of the inter-characteristic relationships that Phase 9 should flag for Session D synthesis.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The most analytically significant shared anchors are those at the Joy/Suffering-Joy boundary (1Pe 1:8; Mat 5:12; Rev 19:7) — the same verses carry evidence for both Characteristic 2 and Characteristic 7, confirming that the split of M04-E across two characteristics is a genuine analytical judgment call and not an artificial division. The Joy/Exultation shared anchors (Psa 35:9; 16:9; Isa 65:18) confirm the porous boundary between those two characteristics at the high end of Joy's intensity.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Mic 6:8's shared anchoring across six registries reveals that Gladness in its evaluative face (what is good = doing justice, loving kindness, walking humbly) is constitutively intersected with multiple other inner-being characteristics — each of the three named elements of the good (justice, kindness, humility) belongs to other registries. This confirms the observation from T0.3.1: Gladness's evaluative-cognitive face is the integrating faculty across multiple inner-being characteristics, not a single isolated state. Gen 1:31's shared anchoring confirms Gladness as the characteristic most directly tied to the ontological foundation of Scripture's goodness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Psa 40:8's shared anchoring (Delight and NT christological application in Heb 10:7) reveals Delight as a characteristic directly fulfilled in Christ — his law-within-the-heart Delight in doing the Father's will is the human image of divine-inner-being Delight in its perfect form. Isa 53:10's shared anchoring reveals Delight as the inner divine disposition that motivates the most costly redemptive act in Scripture — God's will/cha.phets to crush the servant is the theologically deepest instance of divine Delight in the corpus. Jer 9:24's shared anchoring confirms Delight as the characteristic most directly revealing God's moral preferences — what God delights in (steadfast love, justice, righteousness) is the core curriculum of moral character formation.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Psa 37:16's shared anchoring between Pleasure and Gladness confirms the tov-root kinship: the same better-than evaluation serves both as Gladness (evaluative-cognitive recognition of what is genuinely good) and Pleasure (the wisdom-calibrated preference for what is genuinely more pleasant). Song 7:6's shared anchoring between Pleasure (relational pleasantness) and Delight (directed attachment toward the beloved) confirms the overlap zone between these two adjacent characteristics precisely in the Song of Songs, where beauty perceived as pleasant and beauty treasured as a specific beloved object converge in a single verse.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Psa 118:23's shared anchoring (Wonder + Christology) is the most analytically significant: the verse's "marvellous in our eyes" locates the Christ-event as the supreme instance of Wonder — the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone is literally described with the Wonder vocabulary, making Wonder the inner state of those who rightly perceive the christological event. 2Sa 1:26's shared anchoring (Wonder + Pleasure) confirms the overlap zone between the two characteristics: the same pa.la term serves both the incomprehensibility register (Jonathan's love exceeding ordinary categories — Wonder) and the relational-pleasantness register (2Sa 1:26 in M04-J for Pleasure).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The shared anchors at 1Pe 1:8; Mat 5:12; Rev 19:7 confirm what the carry-forward analysis established: the suffering-paradox register and the eschatological-Joy register are genuinely interpenetrating at the verse level — some verses carry evidence for both Characteristics 2 and 7 simultaneously. This is not a problem to be resolved but an analytically significant finding: the two characteristics are most closely related precisely at the point of intense, eschatologically-grounded rejoicing, and several verses evidence both.

---

##### T6.6.3 — If no shared verse anchors are identified, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Shared anchors identified at Deu 30:9 and Psa 119:14; 119:162.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple shared anchors identified at the Joy/Exultation and Joy/Suffering-Joy boundaries.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple shared anchors confirmed, Mic 6:8 being the most cross-characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Multiple high-significance shared anchors confirmed; not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Multiple shared anchors confirmed; not silent.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Multiple shared anchors confirmed; not silent.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Multiple shared anchors confirmed at the Joy/Suffering-Joy boundary.
