#### T6.7 — Dimensional Sharing

##### T6.7.1 — How many of this characteristic's confirmed analytical dimensions are shared with another characteristic in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (G)

Dimensional sharing data across all 7 M04 characteristics is not yet available — Phase 9 is running sequentially, and Characteristics 2–7 have not yet been analysed. A complete dimensional-sharing assessment requires all characteristics to be processed.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (G)

Dimensional sharing data across all 7 M04 characteristics is not yet available — Phase 9 is running sequentially. From the evidence available: Joy shares the affective dimension with Exultation and Gladness; the volitional dimension with Delight (M04-H — volitional pleasure); the relational dimension with Shared Gladness (M04-D, which is partly within this characteristic). Full dimensional-sharing assessment requires Characteristics 3–7 to be processed.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (G)

Dimensional sharing data across all 7 M04 characteristics is not yet available — Characteristics 4–7 have not been processed. From evidence available: the cognitive-evaluative dimension is shared with Wisdom (M15) and likely with other cognitively-constituted characteristics across the programme; the affective-warmth dimension is shared with Joy (Characteristic 2) and Delight (Characteristic 4); the moral-evaluation dimension is shared with multiple ethics-related characteristics. Full dimensional-sharing assessment requires remaining characteristics to be processed.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (G)

Dimensional sharing data across all 7 M04 characteristics is not yet complete. From available evidence: Delight's affective-positive dimension is shared with Joy and Gladness; the volitional dimension is shared with characteristics that carry strong will-engagement; the relational-disposition dimension is shared with Love and Faithfulness registers in adjacent clusters; the moral-character dimension (M04-M) is shared with uprightness and obedience characteristics. Full assessment requires remaining characteristics to be processed.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet available (Characteristics 4–7 partial at this stage). From available evidence: the Emotion-Positive dimension is shared with Joy, Gladness, and Delight; the Relational-Disposition dimension is shared with Delight and Love characteristics; the Vitality/Existence dimension (body-health) is shared with characteristics that carry somatic wellbeing evidence. What is relatively unique to Pleasure is its explicit body-level constitutional evidence (Pro 16:24; Deu 28:54, 56) and the ni.cho.ach worship-interface structure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet complete. From available evidence: Wonder's primary Cognition dimension is partially shared with characteristics that engage the mind (Gladness's cognitive-evaluative dimension; Delight's cognitive-wisdom register); Wonder's secondary Emotion-Positive dimension is shared with Joy, Gladness, Delight, and Pleasure; Wonder's Relational-Disposition dimension (communal proclamation) is shared with characteristics that have strong communal expression.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (G)

Dimensional sharing data across all 7 M04 characteristics is not yet complete — Characteristics 4–6 have not been processed. From available evidence: the affective-Spirit dimension is shared with the Spirit-mediated registers of Joy (Characteristic 2); the volitional dimension is shared with Joy's commanded registers; the eschatological dimension is shared with Joy's eschatological registers. What is unique to Characteristic 7 is the constitutive role of suffering as the occasion of the joy.

---

##### T6.7.2 — What does the pattern of dimensional sharing reveal about the relationship between this characteristic and those it shares dimensions with?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (G)

Not yet determinable. Data needed: Phase 9 findings for Characteristics 2–7.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (G)

Not yet fully determinable. The partial evidence suggests Joy shares more dimensions with more characteristics than any other characteristic in M04 — a finding consistent with Joy being the cluster's central characteristic and the one most semantically entangled with adjacent states.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (G)

Not yet fully determinable. The partial evidence suggests Gladness shares its cognitive-evaluative dimension with the programme's wisdom-related characteristics, and its affective-warmth dimension with the positive inner-being cluster (Joy, Delight, Pleasure). Gladness may be the most dimensionally-distributed characteristic in M04 given its tov-root's breadth.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (G)

Incomplete — partial evidence suggests Delight's dimensional profile is the widest in M04, spanning affective-positive, volitional, moral-character, relational-disposition, and transformation dimensions simultaneously. This breadth is consistent with its five-sub-group structure and 247-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (G)

Incomplete; to be addressed in Session D.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (G)

Incomplete; to be addressed in Session D.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (G)

Not yet fully determinable. The partial evidence suggests Suffering-Joy's dimensional profile is largely shared with Joy but with suffering as the constitutive distinguishing dimension rather than a different set of dimensions. Suffering-Joy may not require a wholly separate dimension vocabulary but rather a contextual qualifier (suffering-context) applied to the Joy dimensions.

## T7 — Lexical, Literary, and Human Science Analysis

---

### T7

#### T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis

##### T7.1.1 — What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Primary terms and root meanings: (1) **gil_verb / gil** (H1523 / H1524A) — root associated with spinning or circular movement, capturing the kinetic energy of rejoicing; used in 36 of 83 verses in this corpus; (2) **su.s** (H7797) — to rejoice, exult, take delight; used in 22 instances; strong affective-volitional force; used of both God's and human exultation; (3) **re.na.nah** (H7445) — triumphing, ringing cry of joy; the sonic-expressive form of exultation (5 instances); (4) **cha.dah** (H2302) — to rejoice, be glad; less frequent (3 instances: Exo 18:9, Job 3:6, Psa 21:6); (5) **te.ev** (H2868, Aramaic) — to be glad (1 instance, Dan 6:23). No primary Greek terms in this corpus — M04-A is exclusively OT. The roots consistently emphasise physical movement (gil — spinning), intensity (su.s), and sonic expression (re.na.nah), revealing exultation as a characteristically kinetic and expressive inner state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Primary terms with root meanings: (1) **sa.mach** (H8055) — to rejoice, be glad; the verbal form used 147 times in M04-B; root meaning connotes brightness and happiness; the causative (hiphil) form frequently shows God as the one who makes people joyful; (2) **sim.chah** (H8057) — joy, gladness, mirth; nominal form, 89 instances in M04-B; the noun names the state that sa.mach produces; (3) **sa.me.ach** (H8056) — joyful, glad; adjectival form; the person characterised by the state; (4) **ma.s.vo.s** (H4885) — joy, exultation, rejoicing; nominal form; associated with festive, communal, bodily-expressive joy; (5) **sa.s.von** (H8342) — gladness, joy, exultation; 22 instances in M04-E; strongly restoration-linked; (6) **chairo** (G5463) — to rejoice, be glad; the primary NT rejoicing verb; 58 instances in M04-C; (7) **chara** (G5479) — joy; noun; 57 instances in M04-C; (8) **agalliao** (G0021) — to exult, rejoice greatly; 11 instances in M04-E-VCG-02; roots carry the sense of leaping or bounding exultation; (9) **sunchairo** (G4796) — to rejoice with, co-rejoice; M04-D; the syn- prefix makes shared participation constitutive; (10) **eufrosune** (G2167) — gladness, good cheer; 2 instances in M04-C.

Root-level summary: The Hebrew roots consistently connote brightness, inner gladness, and outward expression; the Greek roots connote active rejoicing (chairo), the resulting state (chara), and intensified leaping-joy (agalliao). The shared thread across all terms is an active, positive, inner-being brightening that moves outward.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **tov** (H2896A) — noun, adjective, and evaluative particle; the core goodness-root. Root meaning: pleasant, good, beautiful, beneficial; in its evaluative use it names the quality of what satisfies a standard of genuine excellence. 133 instances across M04-L (83) and M04-O (50). The root generates the noun tov (goodness, good thing), the adjective tov (good, better, best), and the verbal idiom "ki-tov" (for he is good) that forms the liturgical refrain; (2) **makarismos** (G3108) — blessing, blessedness; 3 NT instances in M04-O-VCG-04 (Rom 4:6, 9; Gal 4:15). Root: makarios (blessed, happy in divine favour); makarismos names the state of being declared blessed by divine pronouncement; (3) **sa.s.von** (H8342) — gladness, exultation, joy (22 instances in the overlapping M04-E-VCG-01 corpus that serves both Characteristics 2 and 3). Root related to the concept of brightness and joyful gladness; (4) The **ki-tov formula** — not a single term but a liturgical construction ("for he is good, for his steadfast love endures forever") functioning as a fixed doxological expression whose repetition across Psalms 100, 106, 107, 118, 135, 136 makes it a structural feature of Gladness's primary register.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **sha.a.shu.im** (H8191) — plural of intensity from sha.a root; root meaning: to delight, play, caress; the plural intensification names not a single act of pleasure but accumulated, multiple-faceted cherishing — the richness of God's treasuring of Ephraim (Jer 31:20), Wisdom's treasuring of humanity (Pro 8:31), the psalmist's treasuring of God's testimonies (Psa 119:24); (2) **sha.a** (H8173B) — verb: to delight, play, sport; root: carefree enjoyment, playing without threat; the nursing-child-over-cobra (Isa 11:8) and bounced-on-knees (Isa 66:12) images bring out the playful-carefree quality; (3) **a.nog** (H6026) — to be delicate, to luxuriate, to delight oneself; root: delicateness, soft/luxurious quality; the most physically-textured of the Delight terms — Deu 28:56's delicate woman, Isa 55:2's rich food, Isa 66:11's deep drinking from abundance; (4) **cha.phets** (H2654A) — to take delight in, to desire, to be pleased; root: to bend down/bow toward; the most volitionally-oriented verbal root — the bending of the will toward its object; (5) **che.phets** (H2656) — delight, desire, matter, affair; the nominal form of H2654A; (6) **cha.phets adj** (H2655) — delighting in (1Ki 13:33; 21:6 — "any who would"); (7) **eudokeo** (G2106) — to think it good, to be well pleased; from eu (well) + dokeo (think/seem); the NT equivalent that carries both the affective-approval quality and the cognitive-positive assessment; the Father's eudokeo in the Son is the deepest NT deployment; (8) **sunēdomai** (G4913) — to rejoice/delight together with; compound: sun (together with) + hēdomai (to be pleased/enjoy); the co-delight register of Rom 7:22 — the inner being delighting in God's law in solidarity with it; (9) **arestos** (G0701) — pleasing, acceptable; from areskō (to please); the compliance/acceptability register of M04-M; (10) **ni.cho.ach** (H5207) — soothing, pleasing (as an aroma); root: to rest/settle; the aroma that settles or soothes — used for the inner-being condition of correctness in worship (or its corruption).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **na.im** (H5273A) — pleasant, agreeable; root na.em — to be pleasant, comfortable, agreeable; the quality of what is fitting and agreeable to the inner sense; the root carries gentleness and ease without harshness; (2) **na.em** (H5276) — to be/experience pleasant; the verbal experience of pleasantness; (3) **no.am** (H5278) — pleasantness, beauty, graciousness; the noun naming the quality: God's own beauty (Psa 27:4), wisdom's character (Pro 3:17); (4) **na.a.man** (H5282) — pleasant (adj): Isa 17:10's "pleasant plants"; (5) **ni.cho.ach** (H5207) — soothing, pleasing (aroma); root nuach — to rest, settle, give rest; the quality of what causes to settle, calm, and rest; the soothing quality of the worship-aroma that causes God's regard to settle into receptive acceptance; (6) **a.nog** (H6026) — to be tender, delicate, to luxuriate; (7) **a.nog adj** (H6028) — tender, delicate; (8) **a.las** (H5965) — to exult, delight (in pleasure); (9) **ta.a.nug** (H8588) — daintiness, luxury; (10) **ed.nah** (H5730B) — pleasure, luxury, delight; (11) **tov** (H2896A) in the comparative register; (12) **thambeō** (G2284) — to be amazed (Mar 10:24). Root synthesis: the na.em root names gentle agreeableness; the nuach root of ni.cho.ach names settling/rest as the mechanism of worship-Pleasure; a.nog/ta.a.nug name delicate, luxuriant ease; a.las names exultant pleasure.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **pa.la** (H6381) — verb: to be extraordinary, surpass, be too difficult; root meaning: to be separated out, set apart from the ordinary; the fundamental semantic: Wonder arises at what is categorically distinct from normal reality; 47 instances; (2) **pe.le** (H6382) — noun: wonder, marvel; 7 instances; Exo 15:11; Isa 9:6 ("Wonderful Counselor"); Psa 77:11; 88:10, 12; 89:5; Isa 25:1; 28:29; 29:14; Lam 1:9; Dan 12:6; (3) **miph.la.ah** (H4652) — wondrous work, noun: Job 37:16; (4) **thambeō** (G2284) — to be seized with astonishment; root: thamb- — to seize, arrest; the bodily and inner arrest quality of Wonder; Mar 1:27; 10:24 (cross-assigned); 10:32; (5) **thauma** (G2295) — wonder, marvel (noun); 2Cor 11:14; Rev 17:6; (6) **thaumazō** (G2296) — to marvel, be astonished; Gal 1:6; Rev 17:6, 7 (also cross-assigned in M04-N-VCG-02). Root synthesis: pa.la/pe.le names Wonder as arising from what is categorically set apart from ordinary reality; thambeō names the inner seizure-quality of Wonder; thaumazō names the sustained state of marvelling.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Primary terms: (1) **agalliao** (G0021) — to exult, leap for joy, rejoice greatly; root: agan (very much) + hallesthai (to leap); the root's leaping-intensity quality captures the paradox: this is not mild comfort but intense, outward-moving exultation; 11 instances in M04-E-VCG-02; (2) **ba.lag** (H1082) — to smile, gleam, be cheerful; root: a gleaming or brightening; 3 instances in M04-F-VCG-01 (Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13) — the root's connotation is fragile, momentary brightening, the exact opposite of agalliao's intensity; (3) **mav.li.git** (H4010) — consolation, comfort; 1 instance (Jer 8:18) — root related to comfort and solace; used here negatively ("my joy/comfort is gone"); (4) **agalliasis** (G0020) — the noun form of agalliao; appears in Luk 1:14 (agalliasis = gladness alongside chairo); Luk 1:44 (the baby leaping in agalliasis); Heb 1:9 (oil of gladness — agalliasis). At definitional level: the agalliao/agalliasis root names an intense, superlative, leaping-quality exultation; ba.lag names its fragile, barely-attainable opposite in the human struggle.

---

##### T7.1.2 — What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the characteristic operates?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

**gil** functions as both a verbal root (H1523, gil_verb — 36 instances: the act of rejoicing as a dynamic event) and a noun (H1524A — 7 instances: joy/rejoicing as a state or quality). This grammatical dual-functioning reveals exultation operating as both an **act** (something done, commanded, chosen) and a **condition** (something present as an ongoing state). The verbal form's frequency over the nominal form confirms that exultation is primarily experienced as an active dynamic event rather than a passive condition.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**sa.mach** (H8055) is exclusively verbal — it always names an act of rejoicing, not a condition or quality. Its dominance (147 verbal instances) over sim.chah (89 nominal) reveals that Joy is fundamentally an act before it is a condition — the grammar of the Hebrew primary term names the characteristic as a dynamic event (something happens) rather than a static state (something is). **chairo** (G5463, 58 instances) is similarly verbal. **chara** (G5479, 57 instances) is the corresponding nominal form — the state that chairo produces. The near-equal frequency of verbal and nominal forms in the NT (58 vs. 57) suggests that Joy operates equally as act and state in the NT register. **sa.me.ach** (H8056, 21 adjectival instances) names the person defined by the state — the one who habitually is glad. Together the three grammatical forms (verb + noun + adjective) show Joy as: an event (sa.mach/chairo), a state (sim.chah/chara), and a character quality (sa.me.ach) — a fully developed inner-being characteristic across all grammatical registers.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

**tov** operates across three grammatical registers in this corpus: (1) **Adjectival / predicative** — "God saw that it was good" (Gen 1:4–31); "the Lord is good" (Psa 25:8; 100:5; Nah 1:7) — predicate adjective naming a stable quality; (2) **Comparative** — "better than" forms (Rut 4:15; 2Sa 18:3; Pro 8:11; 16:16; 17:1 — various) — the comparative form "tov min" (good from) names surpassing worth; (3) **Negated / substantive** — "not good" (Exo 18:17; 1Sa 2:24; Neh 5:9; Pro 17:26; Eze 18:18) — tov negated to name moral deficiency. The grammatical range reveals: Gladness is not primarily a verbal action (unlike Joy's dominant sa.mach verb) but a quality-assertion — it predicates goodness of persons, actions, circumstances, and God's character. The predicate form is the primary grammatical mode, confirming Gladness's status as a quality/condition rather than an act.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

**cha.phets** (H2654A) functions across all grammatical modes: (1) **Verbal** — Gen 34:19 (Shechem delighted in Dinah); Psa 40:8 (I delight to do your will); Isa 53:10 (it was the will of the Lord to crush him) — active volitional acts; (2) **Adjectival** (H2655) — 1Ki 13:33 ("any who would") — predicate adjective of willingness; (3) **Nominal** (H2656) — Psa 1:2 ("his delight is in the law"); 1Sa 15:22 ("has the Lord as great delight in burnt offerings") — stable nominal state or orientation; 2Sa 23:5 ("all my help and my desire"). The tri-form grammatical spread (verb/adjective/noun) reveals Delight as a characteristic that operates simultaneously as act (verbal), disposition (adjectival), and condition (nominal). This grammatical completeness distinguishes Delight from characteristics that operate primarily in one grammatical mode.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

**na.im** (H5273A) functions primarily as an **adjective** — it attributes the quality of pleasantness to persons, places, and circumstances (Psa 133:1 — "pleasant it is"; Job 36:11 — "years in pleasantness"; Song 1:16 — "truly delightful"). **na.em** (H5276) functions as a **verb** (2Sa 1:26 — "you have been pleasant to me"; Pro 2:10 — "knowledge will be pleasant"; Pro 9:17 — "bread eaten in secret is pleasant"). **no.am** (H5278) functions as a **noun** (Psa 27:4 — "the beauty of the Lord"; Pro 3:17 — "ways of pleasantness"). The adjectival-verbal-nominal spread of the na.em root covers: the quality itself (no.am), the attribution of that quality to something (na.im), and the experience of that quality by a person (na.em). This grammatical completeness reveals Pleasure as both an objective quality of what is pleasant and a subjective experience of pleasantness felt by the inner person.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**pa.la** (H6381) functions across four modes: (1) **Verb** — "God thunders wondrously" (Job 37:5); "who does great things and unsearchable, marvellous things" (Job 5:9); "the Lord will do wonders" (Exo 3:20; Jos 3:5); (2) **Niphal reflexive/passive** — "it is marvellous in our eyes" (Psa 118:23); "things too wonderful for me" (Job 42:3); "too difficult for you" (Deu 17:8; 30:11); (3) **Piel intensive** — "you have wondrously shown your steadfast love" (Psa 31:21); "God deals wondrously with you" (Joel 2:26); (4) **Nominal derivative pe.le** — used as a noun and as a component of the name "Wonderful Counselor" (Isa 9:6). The grammatical spread reveals pa.la as active in divine agent contexts (God does wonders), reflexive in human perceptive contexts (it is marvellous to us), and intensive in contexts of surpassing action (wondrously showing love). This grammatical range confirms Wonder as simultaneously a quality of divine acts (active pa.la) and a perceptive response by humans (niphal pa.la).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

**agalliao** (G0021) functions primarily as a **verb** — naming an event of exultation rather than a stable state. The 11 verbal instances in M04-E-VCG-02 show Suffering-Joy as primarily an act or event: Luk 1:47 ("my spirit rejoices"); Luk 10:21 ("he rejoiced"); Joh 8:56 ("Abraham rejoiced"); Act 16:34 ("he rejoiced"); 1Pe 1:6 ("in this you rejoice"); 4:13 ("rejoice insofar as"); Rev 19:7 ("let us rejoice"). **agalliasis** (G0020, noun) appears adjacent (Heb 1:9 — "oil of gladness") — naming the quality of the state. The verbal predominance reveals Suffering-Joy as primarily an event/act rather than a stable condition — consistent with its paradoxical character (genuine joy arising in and through the suffering event, not a settled state independent of the suffering context).

---

##### T7.1.3 — What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

**gil** (verbal and nominal) ranges across: (1) human rejoicing directed at God (primary: Psa 32:11; 35:9; 89:16; 97:1); (2) God's rejoicing over his people (Zep 3:17; Isa 65:19; Jer 32:41); (3) human relational rejoicing (Pro 23:24–25; Song 1:4; Isa 9:3); (4) creation's personified rejoicing (Psa 96:11; 97:1; Isa 35:1–2; 49:13); (5) inverted/absent rejoicing (Psa 13:4; Pro 24:17; Joe 1:16; Jer 48:33; Hos 10:5); (6) prohibited or illegitimate rejoicing (Hos 9:1; Pro 2:14; Pro 24:17). The full semantic range shows exultation as a comprehensive inner-being capacity that can operate in any direction, including corrupted ones.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**sa.mach** ranges across: (1) prescribed feast-joy (Deu 12:7; 16:11–15 — commanded worship context); (2) responsive-spontaneous joy (Exo 4:14 — heart-gladness; 1Sa 6:13 — joy at seeing the ark); (3) relational/parental joy (Pro 10:1; 23:24–25 — father's joy at wise son); (4) God-directed psalmist joy (Psa 5:11; 9:2; 14:7; 32:11; 40:16 — rejoice in the Lord); (5) inverted/corrupt joy (Pro 2:14; Eze 25:6; Hos 9:1; Jon 4:6 — rejoicing at evil or wrongly-directed); (6) God himself rejoicing (Isa 65:19; Psa 104:31; Jer 32:41 — divine joy). The range is broader than any other term in M04 — sa.mach covers every register of Joy from prescribed worship to personal gladness to divine inner life to corrupt misdirection.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

tov's semantic range is the widest of any M04 primary term: (1) **Divine character** — "the Lord is good" (M04-L-VCG-01 — intrinsic divine attribute); (2) **Moral quality** — "a good man" (M04-L-VCG-02 — human moral character); (3) **Evaluative judgment** — "better than" (M04-L-VCG-02, VCG-03 — comparative moral or wisdom assessments); (4) **Circumstantial benefit** — "good news," "it will be well with you," "good land" (M04-O — situational goodness); (5) **Covenantal promise-quality** — "good promises," "good hand" (M04-O-VCG-04 — divine reliable provision); (6) **Wellbeing** — "Saul was well" (1Sa 16:23 — experiential inner wellbeing). This breadth confirms tov as the programme's most foundational positive-quality term.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

cha.phets/che.phets ranges across: (1) **Divine sovereign will** — Psa 115:3; 135:6; Isa 44:28; 46:10; 53:10; 55:11 — God's cha.phets as his operative purpose; (2) **Divine relational delight in persons** — Psa 18:19; 37:23; 51:6; Jer 9:24; Hos 6:6; Mic 7:18; (3) **Human strong personal desire** — Gen 34:19; Psa 73:25; Job 13:3; 1Ki 9:1; (4) **Human volitional preference in practical/diplomatic contexts** — the entire M04-H-VCG-03 diplomatic idiom; (5) **Negated pleasure** — Psa 5:4; Heb 10:6, 8; Jer 6:10; Mal 1:10; (6) **Love's own readiness** — Song 2:7; 3:5; 8:4. Semantic range runs from the most transcendent (God's sovereign will) to the most mundane (diplomatic preference) through the most intimate (love's readiness). The range is unique in M04.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

na.im/na.em/no.am ranges across: (1) **Divine character** — Psa 27:4 (God's own beauty/pleasantness); (2) **Relational warmth** — 2Sa 1:26 (Jonathan's pleasantness to David); Psa 133:1 (brotherly unity's pleasantness); (3) **Wisdom's character** — Pro 3:17 (wisdom's ways as pleasantness); (4) **Speech** — Pro 15:26; 16:24 (gracious words as pleasant); (5) **Praise** — Psa 135:3; 147:1 (praise as pleasant); (6) **Creation** — Psa 16:6 (pleasant places); (7) **Negative** — Pro 9:17 (stolen bread appearing pleasant — the only morally negative instance within this vocabulary). The semantic range is primarily positive-relational and aesthetic, with the negative instance (Pro 9:17) being the exception that proves the rule.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

pa.la ranges across: (1) **Divine wonder-acts** — Exo 3:20; 34:10; Psa 78:4; 86:10; 136:4; (2) **Human Wonder-response** — Psa 118:23; 139:14; 119:18; (3) **Cognitive-limit naming** — Deu 17:8 ("too difficult"); 30:11 ("not too hard"); Gen 18:14 ("is anything too hard?"); Job 42:3 ("too wonderful for me"); (4) **Dark-Wonder** — Job 10:16 (wonders worked against Job); Deu 28:59 (extraordinary afflictions); Dan 8:24; 11:36; (5) **Extraordinary love** — 2Sa 1:26 (Jonathan's love as pa.la); (6) **Divine name-quality** — Isa 9:6 (Wonderful Counselor). Semantic range confirms pa.la as the most versatile Wonder term, covering positive, negative, cognitive-limit, and name-quality registers.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

agalliao ranges across: (1) **Mary's spirit-exultation** (Luk 1:47 — Spirit-joy in vulnerability); (2) **Jesus' Spirit-rejoicing** (Luk 10:21 — divine-human rejoicing in the Holy Spirit); (3) **Abraham's anticipatory faith-joy** (Joh 8:56 — prophetic exultation at Christ's day); (4) **The body's hope-residing** (Act 2:26 — tongue agalliao alongside bodily hope); (5) **Persecuted community's commanded joy** (Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23); (6) **Trials-joy** (1Pe 1:6 — alongside grieving trials); (7) **Suffering-glory orientation** (1Pe 4:13 — insofar as sharing Christ's sufferings); (8) **Faith-without-sight joy** (1Pe 1:8 — inexpressible and glorious); (9) **Coming-to-faith joy** (Act 16:34); (10) **Eschatological wedding joy** (Rev 19:7). The range shows agalliao operating across the full span from intimate-Spirit-joy to communal-eschatological-joy, always with the quality of intensity that distinguishes it from ordinary chairo.

---

##### T7.1.4 — Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes: (1) **gil** (act/condition — both forms) vs. **re.na.nah** (the sonic expression of exultation — the outward form); (2) **su.s** (the more volitional-affective, directed form) vs. **cha.dah** (the more responsive form — used for Jethro's spontaneous rejoicing); (3) nominal **gil** (H1524A — the exultation as a state: Psa 43:4 "God my exceeding joy"; Psa 45:15 "with joy and gladness") vs. verbal **gil** (H1523 — the exultation as an act). These distinctions allow the vocabulary to capture both the spontaneous and the cultivated, both the inner state and the outward expression of exultation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **sa.mach** (act) vs. **sim.chah** (state) vs. **sa.me.ach** (character) — grammatical distinctions between the event, the condition, and the person; (2) **sa.mach** (general Joy-act) vs. **agalliao** (intensified exultant Joy) vs. **sunchairo** (co-Joy) — the Greek terms distinguish degree of intensity and whether the Joy is solitary or shared; (3) **chairo** (act) vs. **chara** (state) — NT parallel of the OT sa.mach/sim.chah distinction; (4) **sa.s.von** (restoration-Joy, forward-oriented) vs. **sa.mach** (present Joy) — distinct sub-registers of the OT joy vocabulary.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: (1) **tov** (predicative — quality/condition) vs. **tov-min** (comparative — surpassing worth); (2) **lo-tov** (negated tov — moral deficiency and its condemnation: Exo 18:17; Neh 5:9; Pro 17:26 etc.) — the structural-opposite form built into the primary term; (3) **tov-lev** (compound: good-of-heart — Est 5:9's "glad of heart" — M04-B-VCG-04, cross-assigned to Gladness's relational-personal register: the inner-being compound confirming heart-location of circumstantial gladness); (4) **makarismos** (G3108 — the NT blessedness form, distinguishing declarative-status-gladness from experiential-circumstantial gladness).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes, across the full vocabulary: (1) **sha.a.shu.im** — the treasuring-cherishing aspect (multi-faceted, accumulated pleasure); **sha.a** — the playful-carefree aspect; **a.nog** — the luxuriating-resting aspect; **o.neg** — the noun of that luxuriating quality; these four together distinguish the affective-register's nuances; (2) **cha.phets** (verb) vs. **che.phets** (noun) vs. **cha.phets** (adj) — distinguish the act, the condition, and the disposition of volitional Delight; (3) **sunēdomai** — the solidarity-Delight aspect (delighting together with, in inner-being); (4) **arestos** — the acceptability/pleasing-compliance aspect; (5) **ni.cho.ach** — the soothing-aroma aspect (the quality of what rises from correct worship); (6) **ta.a.nug** — the daintiness/tender-parental aspect; (7) **che.med** — the covetous-lustful aspect of corrupt Delight; (8) **a.li.tsut** — the predatory-exultation aspect of corrupt Delight.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **na.im/na.em/no.am** — the relational-aesthetic pleasantness of persons, wisdom, and God's character; (2) **ni.cho.ach** — the worship-specific soothing-Pleasure at the divine-human worship interface; (3) **a.nog/ta.a.nug/ed.nah** — the luxury-sensory Pleasure of pampered ease and material comfort; (4) **a.las** — the exultant pleasure-delight at what one enjoys (distinct from the gentler na.em); (5) **tov better-than** — the wisdom-comparative moral-calibration of Pleasure. Together the terms distinguish five distinct aspects: relational-aesthetic (na.em), worship-receptive (ni.cho.ach), luxury-sensory (a.nog), exultant-pleasure (a.las), and wisdom-calibrated (tov).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **pa.la (verb)** — the active doing and passive experiencing of wonder; (2) **pe.le (noun)** — wonder as a substantive quality/reality; (3) **miph.la.ah** — the wondrous work as an object; (4) **thambeō** — the seizure-quality of sudden wonder-astonishment; (5) **thaumazō** — the sustained marvelling state; (6) **thauma** — wonder as a substantive noun (2Cor 11:14's "no wonder"). Together the terms distinguish: the act of doing/experiencing wonder (pa.la verbal), the quality of being wonderful (pe.le nominal), the object that produces wonder (miph.la.ah), the moment of seizure (thambeō), and the sustained state (thaumazō).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: (1) **agalliao** (verbal — the act of exulting) vs. **agalliasis** (nominal — the state of exultation or the quality of gladness as anointing); (2) **ba.lag** (fragile-attempted cheerfulness) vs. **agalliao** (Spirit-enabled intense exultation) — the two terms together name the full spectrum of Suffering-Joy from its fragile minimum to its Spirit-enabled maximum; (3) **mav.li.git** (comfort as desired but absent) vs. **agalliao** (joy present despite adversity) — the two terms frame Suffering-Joy's structural opposite (comfort-gone) against its fullest positive form.

---

##### T7.1.5 — Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Yes, by negation and antithesis within the corpus. The VCG-02 passages use the same terms (gil, su.s, re.na.nah) negated or inverted: Job 3:6–7 (night wished to be barren of re.na.nah); Joe 1:16 (joy and gladness — gil — "taken away"); Isa 16:10 (joy and gladness stripped from the fruitful field — gil). The structural opposite is expressed through the negation of the same vocabulary rather than a distinct antonym term.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes, by negation and by antonym: (1) **By negation** — "the Lord does not rejoice" (Isa 9:17 — sa.mach negated); "rejoice not" (Hos 9:1 — sa.mach prohibited); "let not your heart be glad" (Pro 24:17); (2) **By antonym** — mourning (Psa 30:11 — sackcloth removed; dancing given); sorrow (Joh 16:20 — sorrow → Joy); sighing (Isa 35:10 — sighing flees at Joy's arrival); grief (1Pe 1:6 — grief alongside Joy); darkness (Isa 24:11 — "all joy has grown dark"). The vocabulary does not have a single dedicated antonym term for Joy but uses the cluster of mourning/sorrow/sighing as its structural opposite across the corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: **lo-tov** (negated tov — "not good") appears 15+ times in M04-L-VCG-02 and M04-O contexts (Exo 18:17; 1Sa 2:24; 2Sa 17:7; Neh 5:9; Pro 17:26; 18:5; 20:23; 24:23; 28:21; Eze 18:18; 20:25; 36:31; Isa 65:2) — the structural opposite is built into the primary term's own negation. This is analytically distinctive: unlike Joy (whose opposites are separate terms: mourning, sorrow), Gladness's structural opposite is simply the negation of its own primary term. This confirms that Gladness is constitutively an evaluative characteristic — its presence and absence are measured by the same standard.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Yes: (1) **lo-cha.phets** — "does not delight / takes no pleasure" (negated cha.phets): Psa 5:4; 40:6; 51:16; Isa 1:11; Jer 6:10; Heb 10:6, 8 — the structural opposite built into the primary verbal form's negation; (2) **mav.li.git** (H4010 — Jer 8:18) — also appearing in M04-F (Suffering-Joy); the comfort/joy that is entirely gone; (3) **Moab as a vessel for which no one cares** — Jer 48:38 (lo-che.phets) — the total absence of desire/care as social-relational rejection. The negated forms of both the verbal (cha.phets) and nominal (che.phets) registers provide structural-opposite vocabulary.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **lo-ni.cho.ach** (negated ni.cho.ach) — Lev 26:31 ("I will not smell your pleasing aromas") — the structural opposite in the worship-Pleasure register: God's non-smelling = non-reception = absent worship-Pleasure; (2) **lo-a.las** (negated a.las) — Job 20:18 ("he will get no enjoyment") — the structural opposite of sensory Pleasure; (3) **Harshness** — implicitly the opposite of na.im/na.em's gentleness, though not a single dedicated opposite term.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Not a dedicated antonym, but: (1) **Forgetting as the structural opposite** — consistently named (Neh 9:17 — "not mindful"; Psa 78:11 — "forgot his works") rather than through a dedicated opposite-term; (2) **lo-pa.la** (negated) — Deu 30:11 ("this commandment is not too hard/wonderful for you") — the negation of pa.la indicating that something is not in the Wonder-category, accessible rather than exceeding; (3) **"No wonder"** — 2Cor 11:14 (thauma negated — "and no wonder") — the dismissal of Wonder by removing its unexpectedness.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes: **mav.li.git** (H4010 — Jer 8:18: "my joy is gone; grief is upon me; my heart is sick within me") — the comfort/joy that is gone when Suffering-Joy's fragile form is entirely overwhelmed. Additionally: the world's rejoicing over the prophets' deaths (Rev 11:10 — chairo in the evil sense) is the structural-opposite of Suffering-Joy — the world's gladness at the silencing of truth.

---

##### T7.1.6 — Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Not a distinct person-type term in this corpus. The closest is the characterisation of the one who exults "all the day" (Psa 89:16) and the one who "joyfully works righteousness" (Isa 64:5 — su.s) — these describe a person-type by their characteristic activity rather than by a specific noun designation.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: **sa.me.ach** (H8056, 21 instances) — the adjectival form naming the joyful/glad person as a type: 1Ki 4:20 ("Judah and Israel were… sa.me.ach"); 1Ki 1:40 ("rejoicing with great joy"); Pro 15:13 ("glad heart"); Isa 24:7 ("merry-hearted"). The NT equivalent is the one who "rejoices in the Lord" as a standing posture (Phili 4:4's commanded "rejoice always" produces a person-type: the one who habitually rejoices in the Lord).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Yes: **tov** used substantivally to name the person — "a good man" (ish-tov / ha-tov: Pro 12:2; 13:22; 14:14; 14:19; 15:3). The person-type is the "good man" — one in whom the evaluative-gladness faculty correctly operates and who lives accordingly. This is the person-type most directly generated by Gladness's moral-evaluative face.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Partially: (1) **The man who greatly delights in God's commandments** — Psa 112:1 (cha.phets adj — "greatly delights in his commandments") — this is a person-type: the blessed man who greatly delights; (2) **The eunuchs who choose the things that please Me** — Isa 56:4 (cha.phets) — persons defined by their volitional Delight-orientation; (3) **Those who delight in my righteousness** — Psa 35:27 (cha.phets adj) — a person-type defined by what their Delight is directed toward. These are descriptive person-type references rather than a single dedicated person-type term, but they constitute a functional person-type vocabulary.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Partially: (1) **The man of tender/refined living** (a.nog adj, H6028) — Deu 28:54 ("the man who is the most tender and refined among you") — a person defined by their orientation toward pampered ease; (2) **The cheerful of heart** — Pro 15:15 ("the cheerful of heart has a continual feast") — a functional person-type term; (3) **The one who gazes upon God's beauty** — Psa 27:4 — a functional person-type (the seeker of divine beauty) rather than a dedicated vocabulary term.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Not a dedicated person-type term, but functional person-types: (1) **The one who considers/meditates on wondrous works** — Job 37:14; Psa 119:27; 145:5 — a functional person-type defined by their Wonder-contemplative practice; (2) **The one who proclaims wonders** — Psa 71:17 ("I still proclaim your wondrous deeds") — the lifelong wonder-proclaimer as a person-type; (3) **The humble person** — Psa 131:1 ("I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvellous for me") — a functional person-type defined by their epistemic humility toward Wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

No dedicated person-type term for the one who habitually possesses Suffering-Joy appears in this corpus. The "blessed are those who are persecuted" (Mat 5:10 — makarismos, adjacent to Mat 5:12) is the closest: the persecuted person who rejoices is implicitly typed as blessed. But no single-word person-type term is evidenced.

---

##### T7.1.7 — Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Psa 51:8 ("let the bones that you have broken rejoice") is the closest to a seeking or supplicatory form — the psalmist asks that his broken exultation-capacity be restored. Psa 9:14 ("that I may rejoice in your salvation") frames future rejoicing as the hoped-for outcome of divine rescue. These are supplicatory uses of the exultation vocabulary — seeking the characteristic from God as gift.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Yes: Psa 51:12 ("restore to me the joy of your salvation") — the petitionary use of sim.chah (requesting the restoration of lost Joy); Psa 86:4 ("gladden the soul of your servant") — a direct petition for God to produce Joy; Psa 90:14–15 ("that we may rejoice and be glad all our days… make us glad for as many days as you have afflicted us") — intercession for Joy. These confirm Joy is something that can be sought from God as a gift.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Partially. Psa 86:5 ("for you, O Lord, are good and forgiving… abounding in steadfast love to all who call upon you") — "all who call upon you" frames seeking as the means of access to divine goodness. Lam 3:25 ("the Lord is good to those who wait for him, to the soul who seeks him") names seeking as the required orientation. These are not a dedicated seeking-term but the functional seeking-orientation that enables reception of Gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Partially. The M04-H-VCG-03 "if it pleases the king" / "if it seems good to you" formulas function as seeking-Delight language: they are the verbal acts of seeking the other person's inner pleasure as the condition for a request. Psa 37:4's "delight yourself in the Lord" functions as an implicit seeking command — orient yourself toward him as your object. Job 9:3 ("if one wished to contend with him") and Job 13:3 ("I desire to argue my case with God") express the desire to seek an encounter with God. These are functional seeking-expressions rather than a single dedicated seeking term.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 27:4** ("one thing have I asked of the Lord… that I may gaze upon the beauty of the Lord") — seeking divine Pleasure explicitly through petition; (2) **Psa 90:17** ("let the favor/pleasantness of the Lord our God be upon us") — communal supplication for divine no.am to rest on them; (3) **The cultic instruction** — Num 28:2 ("be careful to offer to me at its appointed time") — the Levitical instruction as the form of seeking to produce the pleasing-aroma relationship.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Yes: (1) **Psa 119:18** ("open my eyes, that I may behold wondrous things out of your law") — the explicit petition for God to enable Wonder-perception; (2) **Jer 21:2** ("perhaps the Lord will deal with us according to all his wonderful deeds and will make him withdraw") — the petition invoking God's wonder-works as the basis of request; (3) **Jeremiah's prayer** (Jer 32:17 — "nothing is too hard for you") — the confession-as-petition establishing the basis for God's wonder-acts.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Yes, in M04-F: Job 10:20 ("leave me alone, that I may find a little cheer") — a plea for the condition of ba.lag-cheerfulness; Psa 39:13 ("look away from me, that I may smile again") — the psalmist's petition for a brief brightening before death. These are seeking/supplication forms of ba.lag — seeking the comfort/cheer from God as a temporary respite.

---

##### T7.1.8 — What does the relationship between the OT Hebrew vocabulary and the NT Greek vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

This corpus (M04-A) contains no NT Greek terms. The NT dimension of exultation is carried by other sub-groups (agalliao in M04-E; chairo in M04-C). The absence of NT evidence in this corpus means the OT-NT continuity question cannot be answered from M04-A's evidence alone. Cross-characteristic synthesis (particularly with agalliao in M04-E) would be required to address this.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The OT-NT relationship shows both continuity and expansion: (1) **Continuity** — chairo/chara (NT) perform the same function as sa.mach/sim.chah (OT) — naming the inner-being act and state of rejoicing; the NT maintains the characteristic's essential character as active, directed, and heart-located; (2) **Expansion in the Spirit-register** — the NT adds the Spirit as a constitutive agent of Joy (Gal 5:22; 1Th 1:6; Rom 14:17) — a register absent from the OT's primary Joy vocabulary; (3) **Agalliao as bridge** — agalliao (M04-E-VCG-02) appears in both OT quotation contexts (Act 2:26 quoting Psa 16:9 with agalliao replacing sa.mach) and NT-original contexts (1Pe 1:8; Rev 19:7) — showing continuity of the intense-exultant register across testaments; (4) **Sunchairo as NT innovation** — the co-rejoicing term (M04-D) appears only in NT; the OT has communal joy but not the explicit shared-participation term.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The OT-NT relationship shows limited direct continuation: tov (OT) has no single NT equivalent — the NT uses agathos (good as moral quality) and kalos (good as beautiful/fitting), but neither appears in this corpus as a primary Gladness term. The makarismos instances (M04-O-VCG-04) represent the NT's most direct engagement with Gladness's experiential-blessedness register. The relative scarcity of NT terms in this characteristic's corpus (only 3 NT instances, all makarismos) is itself analytically significant: Gladness as characterized by tov is primarily an OT-constituted characteristic; the NT develops the joy and suffering-joy characteristics more than Gladness specifically.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The relationship shows both strong continuity and significant NT development: (1) **Continuity** — eudokeo in the NT continues the cha.phets register of divine sovereign pleasure (Mat 3:17; Col 1:19; Gal 1:16) and human willing-delight (Rom 15:26–27; 2Cor 5:8; 12:10); the divine-pleasure vocabulary is directly continuous from OT to NT; (2) **Development** — the NT concentrates the divine-Delight vocabulary on the Father-Son relationship (the baptism/transfiguration eudokeo series) in a way the OT does not; eudokeo in the Father's declaration over the Son is the NT's most distinctive Delight contribution; (3) **Reduction** — the rich OT sha.a.shu.im/sha.a/a.nog affective-register has no single NT equivalent; sunēdomai (Rom 7:22) is the closest NT equivalent for the affective-inner-being Delight, but it appears only once; (4) **New obedience-vocabulary** — arestos (G0701) as the M04-M obedience-pleasing term appears only in the NT, naming the obedience-orientation of Delight with a specifically Hellenistic term.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The relationship reveals limited NT development of Pleasure as a distinct characteristic: (1) **No NT equivalents for na.im/na.em/no.am** — the relational pleasantness vocabulary has no direct NT equivalents in this corpus; (2) **ni.cho.ach → NT fragrant-offering** (Eph 5:2 — not in corpus but the type) — the NT develops the OT ni.cho.ach typologically in Christ's self-offering, fulfilling and transcending the OT system; (3) **thambeō** (G2284, Mar 10:24) — the single NT contribution to M04-K is the disciples' amazement at Jesus' teaching; amazement/wonder is the NT's closest parallel to Pleasure in encountering the extraordinary; (4) The relative NT absence confirms Pleasure as an OT-dominant characteristic, with the ni.cho.ach system pointing typologically forward rather than being developed in NT positive-Pleasure vocabulary.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Continuity in theme** — both OT pa.la/pe.le and NT thambeō/thaumazō name the same inner seizure-quality of Wonder at the extraordinary; (2) **NT concentration on Jesus** — the NT Wonder-vocabulary (thambeō in Mark; thaumazō in Revelation) is focused on Jesus' teaching/authority and on apocalyptic visions; the OT Wonder is primarily focused on God's historical and creative acts; (3) **Shift from proclamatory to reactive** — the OT VCG-01's proclamatory wonder-tradition (Tell-Remember-Meditate) is absent from the NT's thambeō instances which focus on immediate response rather than sustained proclamatory practice; (4) **Dark Wonder expansion** — the NT's dark Wonder register (Gal 1:6; Rev 17:6, 7) is proportionally larger than the OT's, reflecting the NT's eschatological-conflict context.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The relationship shows typological development: (1) The OT ba.lag register (M04-F) represents the pre-Spirit form — the fragile, barely-attainable, mortal-under-suffering attempt at cheerfulness; (2) The NT agalliao register (M04-E-VCG-02) represents the Spirit-enabled, eschatologically-grounded form — intense, paradox-sustaining, community-extending exultation; (3) The continuity is typological: M04-F's OT sufferers (Job, the psalmist, Jeremiah) are the type of the NT's suffering community whose agalliao fulfils and transcends what ba.lag attempted. The OT sought a little cheer before death; the NT commands inexpressible joy filled with glory because of the resurrection.

---

##### T7.1.9 — Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (S)

Not evidenced in this corpus. See T7.1.8.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**Sunchairo** (G4796) is the most distinctive NT coinage for Joy — the syn- prefix making shared participation structurally embedded in the term itself rather than contextually implied. **Agalliasis** (G0020, the noun form of agalliao) also functions distinctively in NT contexts (Luk 1:14; Act 2:46; Jude 24) — it names an intense, overflowing gladness that is not precisely represented in the OT vocabulary. These coinages reveal that the NT extends Joy into the explicitly relational-shared domain (sunchairo) and into the intensified-eschatological domain (agalliasis).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (S)

No NT-coined term for Gladness is evidenced in this corpus. Makarismos appears in classical Greek before the NT and is not a new coinage. The relative absence of NT coinage for Gladness is consistent with the characteristic's primary location in the OT-tov corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (S)

No term uniquely coined in the NT period for Delight is evidenced in this corpus. Eudokeo and arestos both have pre-NT Greek usage. Sunēdomai is a compound with pre-NT antecedents. The NT deployment of eudokeo in the Father-Son declaration (Mat 3:17) is theologically new but not lexically new.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (S)

No NT-coined term for Pleasure is evidenced in this corpus. thambeō is pre-NT Greek. The NT does not develop new Pleasure vocabulary in this corpus.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (S)

No term uniquely coined for Wonder in the NT period is evidenced in this corpus. thambeō, thaumazō, and thauma are pre-NT Greek terms deployed in new theological contexts.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (S)

agalliao itself appears in classical Greek but the specific theological usage in suffering-paradox contexts (1Pe 1:6; 4:13; Mat 5:12) represents a distinctively NT deployment rather than a new coinage. No term is newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic; what is new is the theological-context deployment of an existing term.

---

##### T7.1.10 — What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The full OT vocabulary arc reveals exultation as a comprehensive inner-being capacity with kinetic (gil — movement), affective-volitional (su.s — directed delight), and expressive (re.na.nah — triumphing cry) components that operate across all registers of the inner being's life: the person's spontaneous response to divine acts, the cultivated habit of Godward orientation, the volitional choice in adversity, the cosmic-scale participation of all creation, and God's own inner exultation over his people. The vocabulary arc is entirely OT-Hebrew in this sub-group, with NT continuity requiring cross-characteristic synthesis.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The full vocabulary arc across sa.mach/sim.chah (OT primary), sa.s.von (OT restoration), ma.s.vo.s (OT festive-communal), agalliao/agalliasis (eschatological-intense), chairo/chara (NT primary), sunchairo (NT co-joy), eucharistia (NT thanksgiving within Joy), and euthumeō (NT cheerfulness) reveals Joy as a characteristic with: (a) a stable core (active inner rejoicing in response to divine reality — carried by sa.mach/chairo across both testaments); (b) a festive-communal register (ma.s.vo.s; sunchairo — the social form of Joy); (c) an eschatological-restoration register (sa.s.von; agalliao — Joy oriented toward the not-yet); (d) a Spirit-mediated register (NT additions: the Spirit as Joy-agent); (e) an adjacent thanksgiving register (eucharistia — the Godward-gratitude face of Joy). The arc shows Joy as semantically rich, multi-registered, and consistently oriented across all registers toward genuine participation in what is celebratable before God.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The vocabulary arc of tov (OT primary, spanning divine character, moral appraisal, circumstantial benefit, and wellbeing) combined with makarismos (NT blessedness) and the adjacent sa.s.von (restoration-gladness) reveals Gladness as: (a) the most ontologically-grounded of M04's characteristics — tov's root in the concept of genuine goodness as objective quality makes Gladness the characteristic most directly connected to reality's moral structure; (b) the most cognitively-constituted — tov's evaluative-predicative grammar makes Gladness an assertion about what is genuinely the case, not merely a subjective feeling; (c) an OT-dominated characteristic — the near-absence of NT primary terms shows that the NT concentrated its positive inner-being development in Joy (chairo/chara) and Suffering-Joy (agalliao) rather than in the evaluative-gladness register.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

The full vocabulary arc from sha.a.shu.im/sha.a/a.nog (affective-resting) through cha.phets/che.phets (volitional-sovereign) through arestos/ni.cho.ach (obedience-pleasing) through ta.a.nug (parental tenderness) through che.med/a.li.tsut (corrupt desire) reveals Delight as the most semantically complex and structurally comprehensive characteristic in M04. The arc spans from the most divinely transcendent (God's sovereign cha.phets declaring purpose — Isa 46:10) through the most intimately relational (Jer 31:20's sha.a.shu.im as God's cherishing of Ephraim-as-darling-child) through the most embodied (a.nog's luxuriating satisfaction) to the most corrupt (a.li.tsut's predatory elation). No other M04 characteristic spans this range.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The vocabulary arc reveals Pleasure as spanning the widest constitutional range in M04 (body to soul to God's inner being) through a diverse vocabulary: from the gentlest relational agreeableness (na.im — brotherly unity's pleasantness) through the worship-soothing mechanism (ni.cho.ach — the most technically specific worship-vocabulary in M04) through the bodily luxury-ease (a.nog — the most physically textured) through the wisdom-calibrated better-than (tov). The arc also reveals Pleasure as the characteristic with the largest worship-related technical vocabulary (the ni.cho.ach corpus of 38 verses), making it uniquely the characteristic most embedded in Israel's formal worship practice.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

The pa.la/pe.le → thambeō/thaumazō arc reveals Wonder as a characteristic whose lexical identity is remarkably stable across the Testaments: the semantic content (inner seizure before what is categorically extraordinary) is preserved across the Hebrew and Greek vocabularies. What changes is the primary object: the OT's dominant wonder-object is God's acts in Exodus and creation history; the NT's dominant wonder-object is Jesus himself — his teaching, authority, and advance. The arc reveals Wonder as moving from acts (OT) to person (NT): in the NT, encountering Jesus produces Wonder more directly than encountering his acts, pointing toward the revelation of the Wonderful Counselor as the fullness of all divine wonder.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The arc from ba.lag (OT fragile brightness) through mav.li.git (comfort-gone) to agalliao/agalliasis (NT Spirit-enabled intense exultation) reveals Suffering-Joy as a characteristic that exists in the OT in fragile, barely-attainable form and reaches its full expression in the NT through: (a) the Spirit's enabling; (b) the resurrection's eschatological grounding; (c) the Christ-pattern of suffering-to-glory as the normative trajectory. The characteristic is not an NT invention but the OT's barely-attempted cheerfulness brought to full, paradox-sustaining expression through the gospel.

---

#### T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation

##### T7.2.1 — What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

In Psa 35:9 ("my soul will rejoice in the Lord, exulting in his salvation"), the primary term (gil_verb — "rejoice" / su.s — "exulting") functions as the **main predicate** of the soul — it names what the soul will do as the culmination of the psalmist's hope and expectation. The terms are the syntactic and semantic peak of the verse: the soul as subject + rejoice/exult as predicate + "in the Lord" / "in his salvation" as the governed prepositional objects. The terms carry the full weight of the verse's inner-being claim.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

In Deu 16:11 ("And you shall rejoice before the Lord your God"), sa.mach functions as the **main predicate of a second-person command** — it is the central imperative of the verse, making Joy the required inner act of covenant participation before God. The "before the Lord your God" prepositional phrase gives the term its constitutive object and direction. The grammatical weight of the term as command-predicate across the Deuteronomic feast-corpus shows Joy as the defining inner act that covenant worship requires.

In Phili 4:4 ("Rejoice in the Lord always; again I will say, rejoice") — chairo functions as a repeated imperative with the unique intensification of double repetition ("I will say it again") — showing Joy's commanded standing as so fundamental that it requires insistence.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

In Mic 6:8 ("He has told you, O man, what is good; and what does the Lord require of you but to do justice, and to love kindness, and to walk humbly with your God?"), **tov** functions as the **object of divine declaration** — "what is good" names the content God has revealed. The term is the syntactic and semantic centre around which the verse's three requirements cluster as its definition. God's declaration establishes the good as a known, revealed reality — not a matter of human invention or preference — and the human person's task is to recognise it (evaluative Gladness) and live it (conscientiousness). The term's function as the object of divine declaration confirms Gladness's cognitive-receptive character: goodness is first known, then lived.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

In Psa 37:4 ("delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart"), **a.nog** (hitpael — reflexive: "delight yourself") functions as the **commanded reflexive volitional act** — the psalmist is commanded to direct the luxuriating delight faculty toward the Lord. The hitpael form is theologically significant: it names a self-directed action of the inner being — the person is to actively orient themselves toward God as the object of a.nog. The second clause ("he will give you the desires of your heart") shows the consequential divine response: Delight in God restructures the heart's desires in alignment with what God gives. The primary term functions as the pivotal inner-being act on which the whole verse's promise turns.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

In Psa 27:4 ("one thing have I asked of the Lord… to gaze upon the beauty [no.am] of the Lord"), **no.am** functions as the **object of the supreme desire** — the pleasantness/beauty of the Lord is what the psalmist most deeply wants to behold. The term names the quality of God that makes dwelling in his presence the soul's supreme pursuit. No.am here is not merely aesthetic — it is the totality of God's agreeable, beautiful, life-giving character that the soul seeks to gaze upon. The term's function as the object of the supreme petition reveals Pleasure in God as the highest form of the characteristic's operation.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

In Psa 118:23 ("this is the Lord's doing; it is marvellous in our eyes"), **pa.la** (niphal — "it is marvellous") functions as the **community's perceptive-evaluative declaration**: the niphal passive form names what is marvellous not as an objective quality claimed by God but as what is experienced as marvellous by the worshipping community ("in our eyes"). The verse structure: "this is the Lord's doing" (attribution) + "it is marvellous in our eyes" (inner perceptive response). The term's function confirms Wonder as a relational-perceptive response — something seen (perceptive) and recognised as extraordinary (evaluative) by the inner being of those who observe it.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

In 1Pe 1:8 ("though you do not now see him, you believe in him and rejoice [agalliate] with joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory"), **agalliao** functions as the **main predicate of the faith-community** — it names the primary defining act of the community in its unseen-Christ faith context. The term is qualified by two superlatives: "inexpressible" and "filled with glory" — both modifiers emphasising the quality's transcendence of ordinary affective categories. The term's function as the main predicate confirms Suffering-Joy as the defining inner-being act of the community under this characteristic: this is what they DO in faith, even amid trial (v.6).

---

##### T7.2.2 — What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form require for responsible interpretation?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The primary literary form is the **Psalm** — specifically the individual and corporate lament-praise psalm (Psa 13; 35; 51; 89) and the enthronement psalm (Psa 96; 97). Responsible interpretation requires: (1) attending to the emotional arc of the psalm (lament → trust → anticipated/experienced exultation); (2) reading the exultation as the climax of the psalm's movement rather than as an isolated statement; (3) recognising the corporate-liturgical function of many psalms — the exultation is performed and reinforced through communal use. The prophetic passages (Isa 25:9; 61:10; 65:18–19; Zep 3:17; Zec 9:9) require eschatological interpretation — the exultation is forward-oriented and conditionally promised.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Multiple literary forms carry the evidence, each requiring different interpretive care: (1) **Command / Legal-liturgical** (Deu 12:7; 16:11; Lev 23:40) — requires reading the commands as genuine formative directives, not mere regulations; Joy is prescribed because it is a necessary inner posture; (2) **Lament Psalm** (Psa 30; 51; 90; 126) — the Joy within lament is particularly significant: it is requested, anticipated, or recovered after mourning — reading Joy in lament requires attention to the journey from grief to gladness; (3) **Wisdom literature** (Pro; Ecc) — requires attention to the Ecclesiastes examination of joy's limits and commendation alongside wisdom's cautions; (4) **Prophetic** (Isa 35; 51; 55; 61; Jer 31; 33; Zec 8) — requires eschatological reading; the prophetic joy-promises are conditional on restoration and are not yet fully realised; (5) **NT Epistle** (Phili; 2Cor; 1Th; Jas) — requires situational reading (Paul's Joy in imprisonment, Paul's joy amid community conflict) that contextualises the commands.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Multiple primary forms: (1) **Liturgical/doxological** (M04-L-VCG-01 ki-tov Psalms) — requires reading as communal worship expression and memory-formation, not merely theological proposition; (2) **Wisdom/Proverbs** (M04-L-VCG-02, 03) — requires reading as formative instruction, not merely descriptive observations; the better-than comparatives are the wisdom teacher's guidance for the evaluative faculty; (3) **Prophetic/legal** (Mic 6:8; Exo 18:17; Neh 5:9; Eze 18:18) — requires reading as moral demand and accountability structures; (4) **Narrative** (M04-O-VCG-03 — Saul's wellbeing; David's men's goodness; Jonathan's advocacy) — requires reading as character evidence and moral exemplars; (5) **NT Epistle** (makarismos in Romans 4; Galatians 4) — requires reading within the Pauline argument about faith/righteousness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Primary forms: (1) **Psalmic instruction/promise** (Psa 37:4; 73:25; 84:10; Psa 119 series) — requires reading as both individual and communal guidance for the inner life, not merely descriptive; (2) **Prophetic oracle** (Isa 58:13–14; 62:4; Jer 9:24; Jer 31:20; Eze 18:23; Mic 7:18) — requires reading as direct divine speech about God's own inner dispositions — the most authoritative register for divine-Delight claims; (3) **Wisdom instruction** (Psa 1:2; Pro 8:30–31; Ecc 12:10) — requires reading as formative teaching about the inner life's proper orientation; (4) **Narrative** (1Sa 19:1; Gen 34:19; Est 6:6–11) — requires reading as character evidence showing Delight in operation; (5) **Epistolary** (Rom 7:22; 1Th 2:8; 1Jo 3:22; 2Th 2:12; Heb 10:38) — requires reading as instruction to specific communities facing specific challenges; (6) **Divine declaration** (Mat 3:17; 12:18; 17:5) — requires reading as the most theologically weighted statement of divine Delight — not simile or metaphor but direct divine speech.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Primary forms: (1) **Psalmic worship and praise** (Psa 27:4; 16:11; 36:8; 90:17; 133:1; 135:3; 147:1) — requires reading as both personal and communal expressions of the Pleasure-of-worship, not merely theological propositions; (2) **Levitical instruction** (Lev, Num ni.cho.ach corpus) — requires reading as formal cultic prescription where the term names the intended effect of correctly-offered sacrifice on the divine-human relationship; (3) **Narrative poetry** (2Sa 1:23–26 — David's lament) — requires reading as genuine grief expressing the felt loss of relational Pleasure; (4) **Wisdom instruction** (Pro 2:10; 3:17; 15:16, 17; 16:24; 19:10) — requires reading as formative teaching about the proper calibration of Pleasure; (5) **Song of Songs** (Song 1:16; 7:6) — requires reading as inspired celebration of relational and embodied Pleasure in love.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Primary forms: (1) **Hymnic/liturgical Psalm** — dominant: VCG-01's 61 verses are primarily from Psalms (Psa 9, 26, 31, 40, 71, 72, 75, 77, 78, 86, 88, 89, 96, 98, 105, 106, 107, 111, 118, 119, 131, 136, 139, 145); requires reading as communal worship-proclamation, not merely private reflection; (2) **Narrative dialogue** — Job's dialogue and God's whirlwind speech (Job 5, 9, 10, 37, 42); requires reading as genuine theodicy-wrestling; (3) **Legal-cultic instruction** — Deu 17:8; 30:11 (pa.la in the sense of "too difficult for local courts") — requires reading as practical legal-community instruction; (4) **Prophetic oracle** — Isa 9:6; 25:1; 28:29; 29:14; Jer 21:2; 32:17, 27 — requires reading as divine speech about future wonders; (5) **Narrative** — Exo 3:20; 34:10; Jos 3:5; Judg 6:13; 13:19; 2Ch 26:15 — requires reading as historical testimony to divine wonder-acts; (6) **Apocalyptic vision** — Dan 8:24; 11:36; 12:6; Rev 17:6, 7 — requires reading as symbolic-visionary literature where Wonder has dark registers.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Synoptic beatitude/command** — Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23 — the beatitude form requires reading as genuine promise and command, not merely idealistic aspiration; (2) **NT Epistle** — 1Pe 1:6–8; 4:13; Jas 1:2–4 — requires reading as practical instruction to real communities under real suffering; the commands are genuine, not performative; (3) **Gospel narrative** — Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21 — requires reading as historical-theological witness to actual inner-being events in Jesus and Mary; (4) **Wisdom poetry/lament** — M04-F (Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13) — requires reading as genuine expressions of inner struggle rather than theological propositions; (5) **Prophetic lament** — Jer 8:18 — requires reading as the prophet's own genuine grief at the people's ruin.

---

##### T7.2.3 — What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The dominant logical structure is: **Because God has done X → therefore exult in him.** Psa 48:11 — "Let the daughters of Judah rejoice because of your judgments" (causal: judgments → exultation). Joe 2:23 — "Be glad, O children of Zion, and rejoice in the Lord your God, for he has given the early rain" (causal: God's gift → commanded exultation). Isa 25:9 — "we have waited for him, that he might save us... let us be glad and rejoice in his salvation" (inference: salvation received → exultation follows). The characteristic is evidence-based in its argument: exultation is called for by the facts of God's acts, not as an arbitrary emotional demand.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Several key argument structures: (1) **Because God has done X, therefore rejoice** — Deu 16:11 (because God has blessed you); Psa 126:3 (because God has done great things for us → we are glad); Joe 2:23 (because God has given rain → rejoice); (2) **Rejoice because your reward is eschatological, not present** — Mat 5:12 (rejoice under persecution because your reward is great in heaven — the Joy is grounded in an eschatological reality, not the present circumstances); (3) **Joy is the goal of divine action** — Psa 85:6 (revive us → that your people may rejoice in you — Joy as the telos of revival); (4) **My joy is your joy** — Joh 15:11; 17:13 — the argument that Christ's own Joy is intended to be fully in the disciples; (5) **Count trials as Joy** — Jas 1:2 — the argument that trials, when rightly evaluated, yield Joy (through the tested faith → endurance → completeness chain).

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Key argument structures: (1) **Because God is good, therefore praise** — ki-tov formula (Psa 100:5; 106:1; 136:1) — the logical structure is character → commanded response; (2) **A is better than B because A has quality X** — wisdom-comparative form (Pro 16:8 — a little with righteousness better than great revenue with injustice; Pro 8:11 — wisdom better than jewels) — the argument evaluates competing goods against a standard of genuine value; (3) **This conduct is not good, therefore it is condemned** — the lo-tov verdicts (Pro 17:26; 18:5 etc.) — the standard of goodness is the premise; the falling-short is the condemnation; (4) **God's good promises have not failed, therefore trust** — Jos 21:45 — the historical evidence of promise-fulfilment grounds present and future trust; (5) **Blessedness is declared to the one who has faith counted as righteousness** — makarismos argument (Rom 4:6–9) — declarative logic: status is assigned by divine declaration, not achieved.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Key argument structures: (1) **Delight condition → divine response** — Psa 37:4 (delight yourself in the Lord → he will give you desires); Num 14:8 (if the Lord delights in us → he will bring us to the land); Isa 58:14 (call the Sabbath a delight → you shall take delight in the Lord → God exalts); (2) **God's inner character → God's action** — Jer 9:24 (I delight in these things → understand and know me); Mic 7:18 (delights in steadfast love → pardon iniquity); Eze 18:23 (no pleasure in death → so turn and live); (3) **Isa 53:10 — divine delight as atonement mechanism**: it was the Lord's will to crush him → his soul makes an offering → he sees offspring → the will of the Lord prospers; (4) **Negated Delight → judgment** — Isa 65:12; 66:4 (chose what I did not delight in → sword); Heb 10:38 (if he shrinks back → my soul has no pleasure); (5) **Law-Delight → formation** — Psa 1:2 (delight → meditation → like a tree planted by water).

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Key argument structures: (1) **Wisdom → Pleasure** — Pro 2:10 (wisdom enters heart → knowledge pleasant to soul); Pro 3:17 (wisdom's ways = pleasantness — definitional equivalence); (2) **Correct worship → divine Pleasure** — Gen 8:21 (offering → God smells → God resolves); Lev 1:9 (entrails washed, fully burned → pleasing aroma to Lord); the logical structure is: proper action → produced quality → divine receptive state; (3) **Better-than evaluation** — M04-K-VCG-03's comparatives: X (modest moral quality) > Y (abundant material goods) — the argument structure of wisdom's evaluative logic applied to Pleasure; (4) **Covenant faithfulness → pleasantness of years** — Job 36:11 (listen and serve God → complete days in prosperity → years in pleasantness).

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Key argument structures: (1) **Incomparability → Wonder** — Exo 15:11 ("who is like you… doing wonders?") — incomparability as the logical ground for Wonder; (2) **Remembering → not forgetting → faithfulness** — Neh 9:17 and Psa 78 provide the reverse argument: not-remembering wonders → rebellion; therefore remembering wonders → faithfulness (implied); (3) **Wondrous acts → therefore my soul keeps them** — Psa 119:129 (the wonderfulness of testimonies as the logical ground for the soul's obedience); (4) **Nothing too hard for the Lord → therefore pray** — Gen 18:14; Jer 32:17, 27 — God's unlimited wonder-capacity as the logical ground for petitionary prayer; (5) **Wonder upon wonder → wisdom of the wise shall perish** — Isa 29:14 — escalating wonder as the logical consequence of human wisdom's inadequacy.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Jas 1:2–4**: Command (count trials as joy) → grounds (faith-testing → steadfastness → completeness); (2) **1Pe 1:6–8**: State (you rejoice) ↔ parallel (though grieved) → purpose (tested faith → proved genuine → praise/glory/honour at Christ's revelation); (3) **Mat 5:12**: Command (rejoice and be glad) → grounds (great reward in heaven; the prophets were persecuted similarly); (4) **1Pe 4:13**: Conditional command (rejoice insofar as sharing Christ's sufferings) → purpose (that you may also rejoice at glory's revelation); (5) **Heb 12:2**: Example (Christ endured the cross) → mechanism (for the joy set before him) → result (seated at the right hand). The dominant argument structure across all five is: **command or description → eschatological grounds → eschatological goal**.

---

##### T7.2.4 — What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that setting reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Primary settings: (1) **Liturgical** — the Psalm settings are worship contexts; exultation is the inner state being formed and expressed in communal worship; (2) **Covenantal** — the Deuteronomic and prophetic passages (Deu 30:9; Jer 32:41; Zep 3:17) are explicitly covenantal; exultation is the covenantal inner state at its fullest; (3) **Eschatological** — Isa 65:18–19; 66:10; Zec 9:9 are eschatological; exultation is the characteristic that marks the age of restoration; (4) **Narrative** — Exo 18:9 and Dan 6:23 are narrative contexts where exultation is a character's immediate inner response to events. The diversity of settings confirms exultation as a characteristic that operates across all of life's contexts.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

(1) **Liturgical/festal** — M04-B-VCG-01 (feast-commandments) and M04-B-VCG-02 (sanctuary joy) reveal Joy as constitutive of Israel's covenant worship; joy belongs to the sanctuary encounter as its designed inner climate; (2) **Covenantal** — the Deuteronomic and prophetic settings (Deu 28:47; Jer 7:34; 31:13) reveal Joy as a covenantal diagnostic — its presence indicates covenant health, its absence indicates covenant failure; (3) **Apostolic pastoral** — M04-C-VCG-03 (Pauline relational and community joy) reveals Joy as the inner climate of the apostolic community; Paul's letters breathe Joy as the characteristic inner tone of the healthy community; (4) **Eschatological** — M04-E (sa.s.von; agalliao) and M04-C-VCG-04 (constant Joy) reveal Joy as eschatologically anchored — its fullest expressions are anticipations of the coming kingdom and marriage of the Lamb.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

(1) **Liturgical/worship** — M04-L-VCG-01 Psalms are primarily worship contexts; the ki-tov declaration is inherently liturgical; (2) **Wisdom/formation** — M04-L-VCG-02 and VCG-03 are the wisdom classroom; (3) **Prophetic/covenantal** — Mic 6:8 (judicial-covenantal context: what does the Lord require?); Neh 5:9 (communal covenant accountability); (4) **Narrative/historical** — M04-O's wellbeing narratives are embedded in historical contexts showing God's provision in the lives of individuals and communities; (5) **Covenantal promise** — M04-O-VCG-04 (Jos 21:45; Jer 29:10; 33:14) — God's word of promise as the framing context for trust-Gladness; (6) **NT theological argument** — makarismos in Romans and Galatians (the Pauline argument about justification by faith).

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

(1) **Covenantal address** (Psa 37; Deu 30:9; Jos 23) — God addressing his covenant people about the dynamics of their relationship; (2) **Theophanic/Christophanic declaration** (Mat 3:17; 17:5; Luk 3:22) — the most direct divine speech settings; (3) **Prophetic judgment and restoration** (Isa 58; 62; Jer 9; 31; Eze 18; 33; Mic 7) — Delight operating as the inner principle of judgment (withheld divine pleasure) and restoration (renewed divine pleasure); (4) **Psalmic worship and instruction** (Psa 1; 37; 40; 51; 73; 84; 111; 112; 119) — the liturgical and formative setting; (5) **Wisdom school** (Pro 8:30–31; Ecc 12:10) — the formation setting; (6) **NT epistle** (Rom 7:22; 1Th 2:8; 1Jo 3:22; Heb 10) — the apostolic instruction setting.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

(1) **Cultic/worship** (M04-K-VCG-01) — the dominant context: Israel's formal covenant-worship system; (2) **Lament/elegy** — 2Sa 1:23–26 (David's lament); (3) **Wisdom instruction** (Proverbs) — the formation context for calibrating Pleasure; (4) **Hymnic worship** (Psalms) — the praise and seeking contexts; (5) **Judgment and restoration oracles** (Eze 20:41; Lev 26:31; Isa 47:1) — Pleasure in the covenantal-consequence context; (6) **Love poetry** (Song of Songs) — the relational beauty context.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

(1) **Covenantal worship/liturgy** (VCG-01 dominant) — the Psalms and Chronicles worship tradition; the community gathered to remember and proclaim God's wonders; (2) **Theodicy** — Job (the individual wrestling with God's incomprehensible acts); (3) **Prophetic judgment and restoration** — Isa, Jer, Mic, Joel — divine wonder-acts as the mode of both judgment and restoration; (4) **Narrative history** — Exodus, Judges, Samuel, Chronicles — historical testimony to wonder-acts; (5) **Apocalyptic** — Dan, Rev — the dark and complex wonder of end-time events.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

(1) **Persecution/opposition** — Mat 5:12; Luk 6:23; Act 5:41; 1Pe 4:13 — the defining setting for commanded Suffering-Joy; (2) **Faith-trial** — Jas 1:2; 1Pe 1:6 — the testing of faith as the occasion for joy; (3) **Crisis/miracle-moment** — Act 16:34 — the jailer's crisis-and-faith as the setting for immediate agalliao; (4) **Incarnation/divine encounter** — Luk 1:47; Luk 10:21 — the most intimate divine-encounter settings; (5) **Extreme grief/mortality** — M04-F-VCG-01 (Job 9:27; 10:20; Psa 39:13; Jer 8:18) — suffering without resolution as the OT setting.

---

##### T7.2.5 — Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential character?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)
