Yes: **Psa 35:9** — "my soul will rejoice in the Lord, exulting in his salvation" — is the clearest single-verse expression of the characteristic's essential nature: (1) soul as the constitutional locus; (2) rejoicing and exulting as the inner acts; (3) "in the Lord" and "in his salvation" as the directed objects; (4) future-tense as the anticipation that sustains present trust. It concentrates the characteristic's core elements in a single verse. **Zep 3:17** is the clearest expression of the divine-exultation dimension: "he will rejoice over you with gladness; he will quiet you by his love; he will exult over you with loud singing."

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Several candidates: (1) **Phili 4:4** — "Rejoice in the Lord always; again I will say, rejoice" — the most concentrated NT expression of Joy as a commanded, standing, unconditional inner disposition directed at its proper object (the Lord). The double repetition signals this as the characteristic's defining command; (2) **Deu 16:11** — "And you shall rejoice before the Lord your God" — the OT feast-commandment that establishes Joy as Israel's fundamental covenant posture; (3) **Psa 16:11** — "in your presence there is fullness of joy" — the verse that names Joy's eschatological maximum and its constitutive source (God's presence). If one anchor is to be chosen, **Phili 4:4** is the candidate for the NT register and **Psa 16:11** for the OT register's deepest statement.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Two primary candidates: (1) **Mic 6:8** — "He has told you, O man, what is good; and what does the Lord require of you but to do justice, and to love kindness, and to walk humbly with your God?" — the most programmatic statement of what human goodness is, as declared and known content; it concentrates the evaluative-gladness faculty's content (what is the good?) and its relational orientation (walking humbly with God). Programme OBS-027 confirms this as the registry's definitional anchor; (2) **Gen 1:31** — "And God saw everything that he had made, and behold, it was very good" — the ontological foundation of goodness in Scripture; the divine evaluative act as the archetype for all evaluative-gladness.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Three candidates of near-equal significance: (1) **Psa 37:4** — "delight yourself in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart" — the most frequently cited and most programmatically comprehensive statement of Delight in the OT; it names the inner act (directed Delight), its object (the Lord), and its consequence (desires restructured); (2) **Rom 7:22** — "For I delight in the law of God, in my inner being" — the NT's most explicit constitutional-location statement for Delight; it names the deepest layer of the person (inner being/esō anthrōpos) as the seat of Delight in God's law, producing the Pauline inner conflict; (3) **Mat 3:17** — "This is my beloved Son, with whom I am well pleased" — the NT's most theologically weighted declaration of divine Delight; it names the Father's eudokeo directed at the Son as the trinitarian ground of all subsequent divine pleasure in persons.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Two primary candidates: (1) **Psa 27:4** — "one thing have I asked of the Lord, that will I seek after: that I may dwell in the house of the Lord all the days of my life, to gaze upon the beauty of the Lord" — the most comprehensive statement of Pleasure as the supreme soul-desire; it names the quality of God (no.am), the seeking posture, and the dwelling context as the fullest expression of what Pleasure's deepest register aspires to; (2) **Pro 16:24** — "gracious words are like a honeycomb, sweetness to the soul and health to the body" — the most explicit constitutional-scope statement for Pleasure, naming both soul and body as recipients, and providing the most vivid sensory metaphor for how genuine pleasant-speech Pleasure operates.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Two primary candidates: (1) **Psa 118:23** — "this is the Lord's doing; it is marvellous in our eyes" — the most precisely formulated statement of Wonder as perceptive-communal recognition of God's extraordinary act; it names the divine agency, the human perceptive response, and the communal ("our eyes") nature of genuine Wonder; it is also the NT's most explicitly quoted wonder-text (Mat 21:42); (2) **Job 42:3** — "things too wonderful for me, which I did not know" — the most explicit statement of Wonder as epistemological humility; it names what Wonder reveals about the human person: they have spoken of what exceeded their comprehension.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two primary candidates: (1) **1Pe 1:8** — "though you do not now see him, you believe in him and rejoice with joy that is inexpressible and filled with glory" — the clearest and most comprehensive expression of the characteristic in its Spirit-enabled form: faith without sight, agalliao with eschatological quality, in a context of trials (v.6); (2) **Jas 1:2** — "count it all joy, my brothers, when you meet trials of various kinds" — the most programmatic command to Suffering-Joy, with the most explicit formation-sequence following (v.3–4). If one anchor is chosen: **1Pe 1:8** for the experiential description; **Jas 1:2** for the formation command.

---

##### T7.2.6 — What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

Psa 35:9 reveals that exultation is **the soul's own act toward God** — not a body-function, not a communal event, not an external performance, but the soul itself as the exulting agent directed toward the Lord. The soul as the explicit grammatical subject of both "rejoice" and "exult" makes this the most direct constitutional-location statement in the corpus. Zep 3:17 uniquely reveals the **mutuality and tender intensity of divine exultation** — the pairing of "exult with loud singing" and "quiet you by his love" in the same verse shows that God's exultation over his people is not triumphalist but tenderly relational — the loud singing is the overflow of the same love that also quiets.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**Phili 4:4** uniquely reveals: (1) Joy as a standing, unconditional commanded posture — "always" removes any circumstantial qualification; (2) The double-command structure — "again I will say, rejoice" signals that this is the characteristic most needing insistence; Joy is the inner-being state most at risk of being conditional, so it requires the most emphatic command; (3) The Lord as the constitutive object — "in the Lord" is not circumstantially dependent; the command is to rejoice *in* God regardless of what is happening outside. **Psa 16:11** uniquely reveals that Joy reaches its maximum not in circumstances but in God's presence itself — "fullness of joy" is a statement about Joy's maximum capacity, which is found only in the direct encounter with God. No other verse names Joy's ceiling as unambiguously: the fullness of Joy is God's presence.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

**Mic 6:8** uniquely reveals that Gladness in its evaluative face is not a human construction or preference but **divinely declared content** — "he has told you what is good." The good is known because God has spoken it; the human evaluative faculty's proper operation is not autonomous but responsive to divine declaration. No other verse states so explicitly that the content of genuine goodness is known because God has declared it. **Gen 1:31** uniquely reveals that Gladness originates in a divine inner-being act (God's evaluative delight in his own creation) that precedes and grounds all human evaluative-gladness — the "very good" at creation is the ontological baseline from which all departures (the "not good" verdicts) and all returns (the ki-tov praise declarations) are measured.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

**Psa 37:4** uniquely reveals that Delight in God is the precondition for the proper operation of the heart's desires: the verse does not say "give up your desires and delight in God instead" but "delight in the Lord, and he will give you the desires of your heart" — Delight in God restructures desire rather than eliminating it. No other verse makes so explicit that the correction to disordered desire is not desire-elimination but desire-reorientation through Delight in the right object. **Rom 7:22** uniquely reveals the constitutional depth of Delight: the "inner being" (esō anthrōpos) as the deepest layer of the self that genuinely delights in God's law even while the flesh operates against it — this is the only verse locating Delight at the deepest constitutional layer and distinguishing it explicitly from the flesh's contrary operation. **Mat 3:17** uniquely reveals the trinitarian basis: divine Delight is first the Father's declared pleasure in the Son before it is God's pleasure in any human person; the divine inner life of Delight precedes and grounds all human participation in it.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

**Psa 27:4** uniquely reveals that Pleasure's highest expression is directed toward God's own character-beauty (no.am) as the supreme object of the soul's aspiration — not pleasure in created things, not pleasure in material ease, but the beauty of God himself as the soul's supreme desired pleasantness. No other verse makes so clear that genuine Pleasure at its fullest is specifically the experience of God's own agreeable, beautiful character. **Pro 16:24** uniquely reveals Pleasure's constitutional holism: the honey simile is the only verse in the corpus that explicitly names both soul AND body as recipients of the same instance of Pleasure from the same source (gracious words). No other verse demonstrates the full soul-to-body range of Pleasure's constitutional scope in a single sentence.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

**Psa 118:23** uniquely reveals Wonder as simultaneously perceptive ("in our eyes"), communal ("our"), and theologically certain ("this is the Lord's doing"). No other verse names all three simultaneously: the perceptive faculty, the communal nature of genuine Wonder, and the theological attribution of the marvellous to God as its exclusive source. **Job 42:3** uniquely reveals the epistemological register of Wonder that no other verse states so plainly: the person in genuine Wonder recognises they have exceeded their own comprehension — Wonder is not only astonishment at the external but is simultaneously a revelation about oneself (the limits of one's own knowledge and speech).

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

**1Pe 1:8** uniquely reveals: (1) The **faith-without-sight** structure of the characteristic — "though you do not now see him, you believe and rejoice" — Suffering-Joy is the form of joy that is specifically fitted to the period of not-yet-seeing; no other verse captures this so clearly; (2) The **inexpressible** quality — the agalliao is beyond the capacity of words to capture, revealing that Suffering-Joy at its fullest transcends ordinary affective categories and requires a category larger than human language; (3) **"Filled with glory"** — the present exultation already participates in the quality that belongs to the eschatological age; no other verse names this present-eschatological quality of the joy so directly.

---

#### T7.3 — Human Science Frameworks

##### T7.3.1 — Which human science framework (psychology, moral philosophy, developmental psychology, sociology, anthropology, or other) is most useful as an interpretive lens for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

**Positive psychology** — particularly the study of transcendent emotion, awe, and meaning-based positive affect — is the most directly useful framework. The research on transcendent positive emotions (Dacher Keltner's work on awe; Barbara Fredrickson's broaden-and-build theory of positive emotions) provides useful lenses for exultation as a high-intensity, object-directed positive inner state. Fredrickson's broaden-and-build theory — that positive emotions broaden the person's awareness and build lasting personal resources — is directly relevant to the evidence showing exultation producing security (Psa 16:9), sustained orientation (Psa 89:16), and agency (Isa 64:5).

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

**Positive psychology** is the primary useful lens, particularly: (1) Barbara Fredrickson's broaden-and-build theory — positive emotions (joy, love, contentment) broaden momentary awareness and build lasting personal resources; this maps onto Joy's evidence of building strength (Neh 8:10), generosity (2Cor 8:2), and resilience; (2) **Flow theory** (Csikszentmihalyi) — the state of full engagement with a valued activity; the feast-joy passages show a similar full-engagement quality of the whole community participating in worship; (3) **Wellbeing and hedonia/eudaimonia distinction** — the Ecclesiastes evidence (joy commended even under vanity) maps onto the eudaimonic dimension of wellbeing (life-meaning and engagement) rather than the hedonic (pleasure-seeking); (4) **Attachment theory** — the relational dimension of Joy (M04-D; M04-C-VCG-03) maps onto the secure-attachment register: persons who experience Joy in the context of secure relational bonds.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Two frameworks are useful: (1) **Moral philosophy / virtue ethics** — particularly Aristotle's concept of eudaimonia (flourishing-wellbeing as the good life for the human person) maps onto M04-O's wellbeing-gladness register ("it is well with the man who deals generously" — Psa 112:5; Lam 3:26–27 — the good of bearing the yoke). The evaluative question "what is good for the human person?" is Aristotle's question and Gladness's question; (2) **Cognitive appraisal theory** (Lazarus and others) — the psychological model in which emotion is constituted by cognitive appraisal of a situation maps directly onto Gladness's evaluative-cognitive structure: Gladness arises from appraising a situation/person/circumstance as genuinely good. This is the human-science analogue of Gladness's tov-evaluation.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Two frameworks: (1) **Self-determination theory** (Deci and Ryan) — the psychological framework distinguishing intrinsic motivation (doing something because it is inherently pleasurable and satisfying) from extrinsic motivation (doing it for external reward). Delight-in-God's-law (Psa 1:2; 40:8) maps precisely onto intrinsic motivation: the law is delighted in for its own inner satisfaction, not merely complied with for external reward. The framework illuminates why M04-M (obedience-Delight) is not mere compliance but a different quality of inner orientation; (2) **Attachment theory** — the psychological framework studying how persons form deep bonds of secure attachment to primary relationships. God's sha.a.shu.im in Ephraim (Jer 31:20), divine rescue from Delight (Psa 18:19), and the relational-naming of Zion (Isa 62:4) map onto secure attachment: the person whose primary bond is God-directed Delight is constitutively secure; the corrupt Delight of beast-captivation (Rev 13:3) maps onto anxious-disorganized attachment to a dangerous object.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Two frameworks: (1) **Aesthetics** — the philosophical study of beauty, taste, and sensory experience. Psa 27:4's "gaze upon the beauty of the Lord" and Song of Songs' celebration of the beloved's beauty engage aesthetics directly: the inner capacity for aesthetic appreciation, the experience of beauty as a distinctive form of pleasant inner response that is not merely preference but recognition of genuine quality; (2) **Positive psychology** — particularly Martin Seligman's PERMA model (Positive Emotions, Engagement, Relationships, Meaning, Achievement) and the study of hedonia (pleasurable experience) vs. eudaimonia (flourishing). The M04-K-VCG-03 wisdom-comparatives (integrity with modesty > corrupt abundance) map directly onto positive psychology's finding that hedonic adaptation (the treadmill of seeking more pleasure) produces less wellbeing than eudaimonic engagement with genuinely meaningful life.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Two frameworks: (1) **Philosophy of wonder** — primarily Aristotle's account (in the Metaphysics) that philosophy begins in wonder (thaumazein) — the inner state of puzzled astonishment that motivates inquiry; this maps directly onto M04-I-VCG-02's Wonder as the recognition of cognitive limits that begins genuine inquiry (Job 37:16 — "do you know the balancings of the clouds?"); (2) **Cognitive science of awe** — Dacher Keltner and Jonathan Haidt's research on awe as the emotion arising from vast stimuli that exceed existing cognitive frameworks, requiring cognitive accommodation (updating one's mental categories). This maps onto pa.la's "set apart from ordinary categories" and Job 42:3's "things too wonderful for me, which I did not know."

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Two frameworks: (1) **Post-traumatic growth theory** (Tedeschi and Calhoun) — the psychological research showing that some people experience genuine psychological growth through traumatic experiences, with positive changes in self-perception, relationships, and life philosophy. This maps directly onto Jas 1:2–4's tested-faith → steadfastness → completeness sequence; (2) **Viktor Frankl's logotherapy** — the finding that meaning-making in the context of suffering is the key to psychological resilience and even a form of inner flourishing. Frankl's concept of meaning found within unavoidable suffering maps onto the characteristic's eschatological-grounding mechanism: the suffering becomes meaningful when understood as participation in Christ's suffering-to-glory pattern.

---

##### T7.3.2 — Where the human science framework illuminates the verse evidence — making a finding more coherent or complete — what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The broaden-and-build framework illuminates the sequence trust → exultation → security → praise (Psa 16:9; 63:5): the positive emotion of exultation broadens the person's inner capacity (whole being rejoices, not just the heart) and builds lasting resources (flesh dwells secure; sustained Godward orientation). The research on transcendent awe and elevation — the inner state produced by witnessing virtue or moral beauty — illuminates the exultation-at-God's-judgments passages (Psa 48:11; 97:8): moral-beauty awe is the human-science analogue to the inner exultation produced by recognising God's righteous governance.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

Fredrickson's broaden-and-build directly illuminates the feast-joy formation logic: the prescribed feast-joy (Deu 16:11–15) broadens communal awareness and builds lasting inner resources (covenant faithfulness, community cohesion, sustained orientation toward God) in precisely the way the theory predicts positive emotions function. The evidence that Joy produces strength (Neh 8:10), generosity (2Cor 8:2), and continued proclamation (Act 8:39; 13:48) is fully consistent with the building function of positive emotions. The theory also illuminates why Joy under suffering (2Cor 8:2; 1Pe 1:6) produces more lasting resources than Joy in comfortable circumstances — it is the characteristic that, when grounded in the Spirit's work rather than circumstances, most fully demonstrates the broaden-build dynamic.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Cognitive appraisal theory illuminates why Gladness varies so much by circumstance and person: the same circumstance produces different Gladness-responses in different people (Num 14:3 — Israel evaluates the land as dangerous; Caleb and Joshua evaluate it as genuinely good) because their cognitive appraisals differ. The theory explains that forming the evaluative faculty (wisdom-formation in M04-L-VCG-02, 03) is fundamentally the same as forming the cognitive appraisal patterns that produce appropriate Gladness-responses. Virtue ethics illuminates Lam 3:26–27 (it is genuinely good — eudaimonic good — to bear the yoke in youth) by providing the framework for understanding why discipline and adversity are genuinely beneficial, not merely instrumentally useful.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Self-determination theory illuminates why Psa 40:8's "I delight to do your will" is constitutionally different from mere compliance: intrinsic motivation produces sustained, energised, self-generating engagement; extrinsic motivation produces resentful compliance that stops when the external pressure stops. The person whose Delight is in God's law (Psa 1:2) meditates day and night not because they must but because the inner pleasure sustains the engagement. Attachment theory illuminates Jer 31:20's God-Ephraim bond: God's sha.a.shu.im functions as a secure parental attachment that persists through discipline and rebuke — the child is safe precisely because the attachment is not withdrawn when the child fails. This explains why God's Delight-withheld (Mal 1:10; Heb 10:38) is so theologically serious: it represents an attachment threat — the secure bond at risk.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Aesthetics illuminates Psa 27:4: the "gaze upon the beauty of the Lord" is not passive looking but the active aesthetic-receptive engagement with a supremely beautiful object — what aesthetics calls the contemplative encounter with beauty. This illuminates why Pleasure in God's beauty requires "dwelling" (sustained presence) rather than a glance — genuine aesthetic experience of the most beautiful object requires time and attention. Positive psychology illuminates M04-K-VCG-03: the wisdom literature's consistent preference for modest-integrity-Pleasure over corrupt-abundance-Pleasure anticipates the research finding that relational and virtue-based wellbeing produces more durable positive experience than material wealth. Pro 15:17's "dinner of herbs where love is" maps onto positive psychology's finding that the quality of relational context determines the pleasantness of material experience more than the quality of the material itself.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Keltner/Haidt's awe research illuminates the VCG-01 corpus's emphasis on communal proclamation: awe research finds that awe is strongly pro-social — it leads people to cooperate, connect, and communicate; the Tell-Remember-Meditate-Declare pattern of VCG-01 is exactly what awe research predicts: the Wonder-response drives social sharing and communal identity formation. Aristotle's wonder-as-beginning-of-inquiry illuminates the VCG-02 corpus: the "is anything too hard for the Lord?" (Gen 18:14; Jer 32:17, 27) and Job's "things too wonderful for me" are precisely Aristotle's thaumazein — the puzzled astonishment that motivates continued seeking. The pa.la "too difficult" in legal contexts (Deu 17:8) is also thaumazein applied to practical wisdom.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Post-traumatic growth illuminates why Jas 1:3–4 is analytically plausible: the tested faith producing steadfastness → completeness is the theological articulation of a real psychological phenomenon. Frankl's logotherapy illuminates why the eschatological grounding is necessary — without the "joy set before him" (Heb 12:2) or the "reward in heaven" (Mat 5:12), the suffering has no meaning-structure that could generate genuine joy rather than mere endurance. The frameworks confirm that the verse evidence is psychologically sophisticated rather than mere wishful thinking.

---

##### T7.3.3 — Where the verse evidence and the human science framework diverge, what does the divergence reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The most significant divergence: human science frameworks treat positive emotions as produced by pleasant or beneficial stimuli and typically diminished by adversity. The verse evidence shows exultation transcending this pattern — Hab 3:18 exults in God despite total material loss; Psa 35:9 anticipates rejoicing in God's salvation from within affliction; Psa 31:7 rejoices in God's steadfast love within acknowledged distress. The divergence reveals that scriptural exultation has an object (God) that is entirely independent of circumstances — it is not stimulus-bound in the way that positive psychology's emotional architecture assumes. This is analytically significant: it points to exultation as a theologically-grounded rather than psychologically-automatic inner state.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The most significant divergence: (1) **Unconditional Joy** — Phili 4:4's "Rejoice always" and 1Th 5:16's "Rejoice always" command an inner disposition that positive psychology would not expect to be achievable or sustainable; the human-science framework predicts that Joy is circumstance-responsive; the command to Joy regardless of circumstances points to a theological grounding (in God as Joy's object) that makes Joy independent of the stimulus-response patterns positive psychology describes; (2) **Joy in suffering as a primary register** — positive psychology frames positive emotions as reduced by negative experiences; Characteristic 2 includes Joy in affliction (2Cor 8:2; 1Pe 1:6; Jas 1:2) as one of its defining expressions; the divergence reveals that Joy grounded in eschatological promise and Spirit-presence operates outside the stimulus-response model; (3) **Joy as commanded** — positive psychology treats positive emotions as products of circumstances or conditions; the command to Joy reveals that the Scripture's understanding includes Joy as a volitional act, not only an emotional product.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

The most significant divergence: cognitive appraisal theory treats the standard of goodness as constructed or culturally relative — "good" is what the appraisal-system has learned to value. The verse evidence treats the standard of goodness as **ontologically given** — God has declared what is good (Mic 6:8); the creation's "very good" (Gen 1:31) is not a cultural construction but an ontological declaration. The divergence reveals that Scripture's Gladness requires an objective standard of goodness (God's character and declaration) that human science cannot provide from within its own framework. The evaluative faculty in Scripture is trained toward a given standard; in cognitive appraisal theory, the standard is itself a product of learning and culture.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Self-determination theory treats intrinsic motivation as generated by the person's internal psycho-social processes. The verse evidence treats Delight in God as both the person's own genuine inner state (Rom 7:22 — genuinely the inner being's Delight) AND as given or restructured by God (Psa 37:4 — delight in the Lord → he gives the heart's desires; the desires being given are not the person's autonomous production). The divergence reveals that Scripture's Delight-in-God is simultaneously intrinsic (genuinely the person's own inner pleasure) and received (given and restructured by God) — a paradox that human science cannot account for within its framework of self-generated vs. externally-provided motivation. Attachment theory's primary divergence: secure human attachment depends on the attachment figure being consistently responsive; divine attachment (God's Delight) in the evidence is responsive to human faithfulness (Psa 37:23) but also precedes and grounds it (Jer 31:20's persistent cherishing). Divine attachment has no human analogue.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

The most significant divergence: positive psychology treats Pleasure as a natural human capacity optimised through the right life-conditions; the verse evidence treats Pleasure in God's beauty (Psa 27:4; 36:8; 16:11) as requiring divine enabling — God's own pleasantness must be disclosed before it can be enjoyed. The pursuit of divine beauty (Psa 27:4 — "that I may gaze") is not optimisable by human life-conditions alone; it requires God to be present and to allow the gazing. The divergence reveals that Pleasure in God specifically transcends what human science can provide as an account — it requires theology (the category of divine beauty and covenantal presence) not available within positive psychology.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Keltner/Haidt's awe research is entirely naturalistic: vast stimuli (nature, music, moral exemplars) produce awe as a social-psychological phenomenon. The verse evidence's Wonder is exclusively directed at God's acts and character — the truly marvellous in Scripture is always divine, not natural or social. Zec 8:6 ("should it also be marvellous in my sight, declares the Lord?") makes the divergence explicit: what is marvellous to humans (God's extraordinary acts) is not marvellous to God because God is not a creature encountering something greater than himself. Natural awe can be experienced by anyone at anything vast; biblical Wonder is specifically the creaturely response to the Creator's incomprehensible acts. The divergence reveals that Scripture's Wonder is theologically bounded in a way that naturalised awe is not.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

The most significant divergence: post-traumatic growth is not experienced by everyone and is probabilistic rather than commanded. The verse evidence commands Suffering-Joy (Mat 5:12; Jas 1:2; 1Pe 4:13 — imperatives). The divergence reveals that the characteristic's mechanism (Spirit-enabling) is not the same as the psychological mechanism (meaning-making through natural resilience): Scripture commands a Spirit-produced state that transcends natural psychological categories. The agalliao of 1Pe 1:8 ("inexpressible and filled with glory") explicitly signals that this transcends what human science can account for from within its framework.

---

##### T7.3.4 — Does the human science framework surface any aspect of this characteristic that the verse evidence has not yet addressed — and does that absence require further verse investigation?

**[CHAR-1] Exultation** (E)

The research on peak experiences (Maslow) and flow states (Csikszentmihalyi) surfaces the question of whether exultation has an optimal or peak-functioning register — a condition of fullest expression — that the verse evidence addresses but does not systematise. Psa 68:3's "jubilant with joy" and Isa 61:10's "I will greatly rejoice" suggest degrees of intensity in exultation, but the evidence does not systematically describe peak exultation. This is an analytically interesting gap — the verse evidence shows the range and conditions but not a developed phenomenology of exultation's most intensive expressions.

**[CHAR-2] Joy** (E)

The distinction between **hedonic** (pleasure-focused) and **eudaimonic** (meaning-and-flourishing-focused) wellbeing is useful: the Ecclesiastes evidence (commending Joy while acknowledging vanity) is more naturally eudaimonic than hedonic; Joy here is recommended as the fitting inner companion of mortal life rather than as pleasure-maximisation. The verse evidence does not use these categories but the human science distinction helps clarify what Ecclesiastes is doing — it is commending eudaimonic Joy rather than hedonic pleasure-seeking, which is what the Preacher rejects (Ecc 2:1–2). This surfacing does not require further verse investigation but provides a conceptual clarification useful for Session C output.

**[CHAR-3] Gladness** (E)

Virtue ethics surfaces the developmental trajectory of the evaluative faculty more systematically than the verse evidence does: Aristotle's account of how moral perception (phronesis/practical wisdom) is formed through habituation and experience provides a richer phenomenology of the evaluative faculty's development than the verse evidence explicitly offers. This developmental detail does not require further verse investigation but provides useful conceptual framing for the Session C treatment of Gladness's formation dimension.

**[CHAR-4] Delight** (E)

Attachment theory surfaces the developmental-trajectory question for Delight: human attachment research shows that secure attachment in early childhood shapes the capacity for Delight across a lifetime. The verse evidence names the content and direction of mature Delight (Psa 37:4; Rom 7:22) but does not systematically address how Delight is formed developmentally from childhood onward. Psa 22:9–10 (trusted from birth — adjacent developmental register) and Lam 3:27 (bearing the yoke in youth) suggest that formative development matters, but the verse evidence does not provide a systematic developmental account of how Delight is shaped. This gap does not require further verse investigation but is a useful framing note for the Session C treatment of Delight's formation dimension.

**[CHAR-5] Pleasure** (E)

Aesthetics surfaces the question of aesthetic education: if the inner capacity for genuine Pleasure in beauty must be cultivated (as aesthetics proposes), then the verse evidence's wisdom-formation for Pleasure (Pro 2:10; M04-K-VCG-03) is the theological equivalent of aesthetic education. The human science framework suggests asking: how is the capacity for genuine aesthetic Pleasure in God's beauty formed? The verse evidence doesn't fully answer this — it names the fact of wisdom-formation enabling Pleasure but does not provide a systematic account of aesthetic development. This is a useful conceptual gap for Session C treatment.

**[CHAR-6] Wonder** (E)

Awe research surfaces the developmental trajectory of Wonder-capacity: awe research finds that awe-capacity can be trained (through nature exposure, art, moral exemplars) and can diminish through habituation. The verse evidence names wonder-failure (Neh 9:17; Psa 78:11) as a moral-spiritual failure, but does not systematically address the developmental or habituation mechanisms. The human science framework suggests asking: how does the Tell-Remember-Meditate tradition of VCG-01 function as an anti-habituation practice — deliberately renewing Wonder that would naturally fade? This is a useful conceptual framing for Session C treatment of Wonder's formation dimension.

**[CHAR-7] Suffering-Joy** (E)

Post-traumatic growth research surfaces the question of **trauma specificity** — the finding that not all suffering produces growth; the type and context of suffering matters for the growth outcome. The verse evidence does not differentiate between types of suffering (Jas 1:2 says "trials of various kinds") but the human science finding raises the question of whether Suffering-Joy's formation potential varies by suffering-type. This does not require further verse investigation but is a useful conceptual note for the Session C treatment.

---
